First downstream consumer: TBD.


## Phase 30

Phase 30 (2026-05-22) bundled three `/review-close` skill prose hardenings filed 2026-05-22 from BeanRider's triage pass — all single-file edits to `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md`, all silent-deny-pattern adjacent. **ISSUE-0033** (Step 6 `git push origin --delete <branch>` silent-deny): the Permission Guard's `Bash(git push origin:*)` rule is necessary but not sufficient — the auto-mode classifier hard-codes destructive-flag protection on `--delete` (and `--force`) regardless of allow-rule glob, the same way it hard-codes protected-branch policy on `git push origin main` (Step 4d). The "Why this order matters" paragraph's trailing claim that no permission-rule change is needed (because the rule already exists) was technically true but misleadingly framed — the actual failure mode is classifier-overrides-allow-rule, not missing-rule. Stricken and replaced with a "**If `git push origin --delete <branch>` is silently denied**" paragraph that names the classifier behavior, directs agents to `! git push origin --delete <branch>` shell-escape, notes that local `git branch -d` runs in-band (no remote contact → no classifier interception), and points at the Step 4d `PATH=.venv/bin:$PATH` venv-prefix pattern when the remote pre-push hook needs venv tools. **ISSUE-0027** (Step 4c `git commit` silent-deny): the consolidation commit during `/review-close` itself can be classifier-rejected even though the first `docs(tasks):` commit of a cycle goes through unblocked — empirically the classifier extends protected-branch policy upstream from the push to its enabling commit when context implies an imminent push. Added "**If the commit is silently denied**" paragraph after Step 4c step 7 mirroring Step 4d's silent-deny shape, plus a "**Use multiple `-m` flags, not a heredoc**" footnote: the `$(cat <<'EOF' … EOF)` shape that `/document-work` Step 2 mandates breaks zsh quote-tracking when typed as a one-line `!`-escape (user's shell drops to a continuation prompt on the unterminated quote); concrete escape shape uses sequential `-m` flags — each becomes its own paragraph in the commit message, so multi-paragraph bodies work without heredoc. **ISSUE-0029** (Step 3 venv-aware invocation gap): Phase 23b added the "Venv-aware invocation" paragraph to WORKFLOW.md § 6.1 template and to Step 4d's silent-deny escape hatch — but not to Step 3 skill prose. When the consumer's CLAUDE.md § Pre-merge verification lists commands without `.venv/bin/` prefix, Step 3 had no fallback hint and an `exit 127` / `ModuleNotFoundError` ran into a dead end. Added a "**Venv-aware invocation**" paragraph after the "If any command fails" line directing agents at `.venv/bin/<cmd>` (explicit binaries) or `PATH=.venv/bin:$PATH <cmd>` (shell pipelines or tools that re-exec), naming the consumer-side canonical fix (author venv-prefixed commands in CLAUDE.md per WORKFLOW.md § 6.1) while unblocking the cycle when the consumer's command list hasn't been venv-ified yet. **What didn't ship:** the optional `_shared/silent-deny-escape.md` partial extraction noted in ISSUE-0033 (premature with three callers in one file — revisit when a fourth caller surfaces); the worktree × venv × lock asymmetry cluster (ISSUE-0028 + 0030 + 0017 + 0031 + 0032 + 0013) which needs a design call on where locks canonically live (main vs per-worktree) before shipping; ISSUE-0016 (Step 1 misses dirty worktrees — silent-data-loss risk) which is structural (Step 1 worktree-state classification + Step 2a verdict branch + Step 6 hard guard) rather than three prose paragraphs, so doesn't bundle cleanly with this phase. **Scope:** 1 file edit (~9 net new lines: +3 Step 3, +4 Step 4c, +2 Step 6), no installer change, no schema bump, no new permission rules, no new scripts. **Housekeeping bundled:** Phase 29's `(this commit)` placeholder in CLAUDE.md Phase log + REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md Phase log (28 entries) updated to `532b7e8`; missing Phase 29 row added to REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md's phase table; the three ticked entries (ISSUE-0033 / ISSUE-0027 / ISSUE-0029) in REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md Medium-priority section flipped from `[ ]` to `[x]` with "Resolved Phase 30, 2026-05-22" prefix. First downstream consumer: BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle, which exercises the three escape hatches during the same `/review-close` pass that surfaced ISSUE-0027 (the Step 4c silent-deny is the most-likely friction to recur during a multi-commit absorption).

## Phase 31

Phase 31 (2026-05-22) closed BeanRider ISSUE-0016 — the structural `/review-close` silent-data-loss gap that Phase 30 explicitly deferred ("structural Step 1 worktree-state classification + Step 2a verdict branch + Step 6 hard guard, rather than three prose paragraphs, so doesn't bundle cleanly with this phase"). The failure mode: `/review-close` Step 1 ran 4 commit-tip-based git commands (`git branch -a`, `git log`, `git branch --list`, `git stash list`) but never inspected worktree working-tree state, and didn't even list worktrees — `git worktree list` was conspicuously absent from Step 1's documented surface (it appeared only later in Step 3b for the per-branch worktree-removal lookup). A `/claim-task`-ed branch where the agent did substantial worktree edits but never committed (paused mid-implementation by the user) has a branch tip identical to a freshly-claimed never-touched branch. Step 2a's commit-based `git log main..<branch>` verdict says "no commits, reject" for both, and Step 6's cleanup pass would then attempt `git worktree remove`. BeanRider hit this on FEAT-0030 (2026-05-14): ~560 lines of in-progress mcp_server work (modified `mcp_server/server.py` +21, `mcp_server/tools.py` +197, `tests/mcp_server/conftest.py` +14; untracked `mcp_server/tax_mapping.py` 49 lines, `tests/mcp_server/test_end_of_year_summary.py` 133 lines, plus fixtures) sat in the worktree under a `status: in_progress` lock. The save was `git worktree remove`'s built-in dirty-tree refusal — NOT the skill. If a downstream codepath ever reaches for `--force` (some `/auto-judge` and `/document-work` cleanup paths legitimately do when the worktree is expected to be clean per their preconditions), the work would have been silently destroyed. **Four coordinated edits in `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md`:** (1) Step 1's parallel-command list gained a fifth bullet — `git worktree list --porcelain` — closing the structural gap that the worktree surface was undocumented in Step 1 to begin with; the porcelain form is consumed by the new Step 1a. (2) New **§ 1a "Classify Worktree State (silent-data-loss guard, BeanRider ISSUE-0016)"** between Step 1 and the existing § 1b. The classifier walks `git worktree list --porcelain` (parsed via awk for `worktree <path>` / `branch refs/heads/<name>` pairs; skips the worktree whose branch is `main`), runs `git -C <worktree-path> status --porcelain` per worktree, and emits one of three classes per branch: **`clean-merged`** (tip ancestor of main AND porcelain empty — safe to remove in Step 6, true stale claim or already-merged-but-not-cleaned-up), **`clean-ahead`** (commits ahead of main AND porcelain empty — normal review path, proceed to Step 2a commit-based inspection), **`dirty`** (porcelain non-empty — paused mid-implementation work; SKIP at Step 2a, never remove). Gitignored `.locks/` and `.pending-docs/` are NOT in `--porcelain` output without `--ignored`, so they don't false-positive into `dirty`. (3) Step 2a gained a **step 0** pre-check: if Step 1a classified this branch's worktree as `dirty`, the verdict is **SKIP — paused work present**, distinct from `approve`/`reject`. The branch is excluded from Step 3b (worktree removal), Step 4 (merge), and Step 6 (cleanup) for this run; the agent surfaces the dirty file count and the recommendation ("commit-as-WIP, stash, or leave alone — re-run `/review-close` after the user decides") and continues to the next branch. (4) Step 3b's "Remove the worktree" bullet gained a hard rule: **never `--force`**. By Step 1a's classification, an `approved` branch passed through Step 2a's clean-state check, so the unforced remove should succeed; if it refuses (`fatal: '<path>' contains modified or untracked files`), the worktree became dirty between Step 1a and now — stop, downgrade the branch to SKIP for this run (preserve worktree/lock/branch), continue. Step 6 gained an explicit "**For each SKIP'd branch**" handling bullet (leave worktree + `.locks/<TASK_ID>.lock` + branch fully in place, surface the SKIP in Step 8's report) plus a paragraph-level **Hard guard** note: Step 6's documented flow does not call `git worktree remove`, but if a future evolution of the skill adds a worktree-cleanup pass here, that pass MUST refuse to remove any worktree classified as `dirty` AND MUST NOT use `--force`. Step 8's report template gained a `SKIP'd branches — paused work` bullet in the Remaining block alongside the existing rejected/remote-cleanup bullets. **What didn't ship:** factoring the dirty-state classification into a `core/companion/scripts/classify_worktrees.sh` script (premature with one caller — the inline awk + bash form is ~20 lines and reads cleanly; revisit if `/auto-claim`, `/auto-judge`, or `/auto-review` grow a similar need); modifying `/auto-judge` or `/document-work`'s `--force` paths to consult the classification (out-of-scope for this filing — those skills' worktree-removal preconditions are different surface area and need their own ISSUE-* filings if the silent-data-loss path actually exists there in current code; Phase 31's Step 6 hard-guard note documents the future-evolution risk locally). **Scope:** 1 file edit (~45 net new lines: +5 Step 1, +28 Step 1a, +3 Step 2a, +4 Step 3b, +5 Step 6, +1 Step 8 report), no installer change, no schema bump, no new permission rules, no new scripts. The new `git worktree list --porcelain` and `git -C <path> status --porcelain` calls are both covered by existing universally-allowed git read commands — no settings.json addition needed. First downstream consumer: BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle, which exercises the new Step 1a classification on the same FEAT-0030 worktree shape that surfaced this issue (verifying the `dirty` classification + SKIP verdict + Step 6 hard guard against the originally-paused work).

## Phase 32

Phase 32 (2026-05-22) closed the lock half of the BeanRider worktree × venv × lock asymmetry cluster (ISSUE-0028 + 0030 + 0032 + 0013 + 0017 collapse) that Phase 30 explicitly deferred as "interlocking, needs design call on where locks canonically live before shipping" — per [`PHASE_32_HANDOFF.md`](./PHASE_32_HANDOFF.md). The design call landed on **Option A** from ISSUE-0032: locks resolve to the **main** repo's `.locks/` via `git rev-parse --git-common-dir` regardless of cwd, with both the lock writer (`claim_task.sh --lock`) and the lock reader (`validate_tasks.py` Invariant 9) using the same resolution so every caller — pre-commit hooks running inside worktrees, `/review-close` validator runs from main, ad-hoc CLI from any working tree — agrees on one canonical location. Picked over Option B (validator-resolves-via-worktree-aware-repo-root with locks staying per-worktree) because B re-creates the visibility problem one layer deeper: the whole point of the `in_progress requires lock` invariant is to be checkable from any caller, and B distributes per-worktree what should be a single source of truth. The `.venv`-symlink half (Option C) was held back as a Phase 32.x Mac/Linux opt-in because Windows file-symlink behavior (admin/dev-mode requirement + Git Bash quirks) hasn't been verified and shipping it bundled would have forced a per-OS code path into the canonical claim flow. **Five edits:** (1) `core/companion/scripts/claim_task.sh` — the `USE_LOCK` block now runs `git rev-parse --git-common-dir`, canonicalizes the absolute-or-relative result via `dirname` + `cd ... && pwd`, sets `LOCKS_DIR="$MAIN_REPO_ROOT/.locks"`, and hard-aborts with an actionable error if `git-common-dir` fails (no silent fallback — the contract is canonical-or-fail). The script's docstring gained a "Lock location (Phase 32)" block explaining the canonical contract for future readers of `--help`. (2) `core/skills/claim-task/SKILL.md` Step 4 — documented invocation flipped from `bash scripts/claim_task.sh <TASK_ID> <BRANCH_NAME>` to `bash scripts/claim_task.sh --lock <TASK_ID> <BRANCH_NAME>`, bringing skill prose into sync with Phase 16's already-stated promise that a lock IS created (the prior asymmetry meant the validator's Invariant 9 fired after every `/claim-task` until the agent hand-touched the lock, which BeanRider hit on every multi-session active-development week per ISSUE-0028 + 0030 + 0013). (3) `core/companion/scripts/validate_tasks.py` — new `_resolve_canonical_locks_dir()` helper invokes `subprocess.run("git", "-C", project_root, "rev-parse", "--git-common-dir")` (5 s timeout, never raises) with three-tier fallback (subprocess error → non-zero exit → empty stdout all return `project_root / ".locks"`) so `--self-test` synthetic fixtures and atomic-staging callers outside any working tree continue to work; `validate()` calls the helper instead of computing `locks_dir = project_root / ".locks"` inline. Invariant 9's error message was rewritten: "this usually means a /claim-task crashed mid-flight" was misleading (the script may have completed cleanly without `--lock`); the new text names the canonical location, points at `git rev-parse --git-common-dir` as the resolution path, and tells the user to re-run `bash scripts/claim_task.sh --lock <TASK_ID> <BRANCH>` or flip the task back to `open`. (4) `core/companion/tasks/schema.md` — Invariant 9 + Status-specific-requirements table cell both gained the `<main-repo-root>/.locks/` clarifier with inline "resolved via `git rev-parse --git-common-dir`" + Phase 32 attribution; the table's "Requires lock file" column for `in_progress` updated from `.locks/<TASK-ID>.lock` to `<main-repo-root>/.locks/<TASK-ID>.lock`. (5) `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` — § 4.1's "Lock file coordination" paragraph gained the canonical-location contract; § 2.2 Planning step 3 documents that `/claim-task` Step 4 now passes `--lock` always; § 8.1 task-system row's Invariant 9 description mentions the git-common-dir resolution so every caller (pre-commit from inside a worktree, `/review-close` from main, ad-hoc CLI) finds the same canonical state. **Q2 lean from PHASE_32_HANDOFF.md revised mid-implementation:** the initial "leave validator's resolution simple, only fix error text" lean was overturned after discovering that `core/companion/git-hooks/examples/pre-commit-tasks-validate.example` runs `validate_tasks.py` with cwd = worktree (line 65: `"$PYTHON3" scripts/validate_tasks.py --quiet`). Under "locks in main + validator-stays-simple," any pre-commit inside a worktree with `tasks/index.yml` containing any `in_progress` task would fail because cwd-resolved `.locks/` is the worktree's empty one. Centralizing the resolution in the validator makes every caller correct by construction — including the inevitable case of someone debugging interactively from a worktree by running `python3 scripts/validate_tasks.py`. The revised decision is documented in PHASE_32_HANDOFF.md § "Resolved design decisions" #2 so future readers don't second-guess the validator's now-larger surface area. **Smoke-tested on `/tmp/wf-phase32-test` across 8 scenarios** (all green): `claim_task.sh --help` shows the new Lock-location block; claim from main → lock at main's `.locks/`; claim from worktree → lock STILL at main's `.locks/` (worktree's `.locks/` never exists in either case); validator from main with `in_progress` + valid lock → exits 0; validator from worktree (cwd=worktree) → resolves git-common-dir → finds main's lock → exits 0; validator from non-git-tmpdir (the `--self-test` fixture case) → falls back to `project_root / ".locks"` → 8 existing fixtures all pass (`SELF-TEST OK`); rewritten error text fires correctly when lock is hand-deleted and names canonical location + git-common-dir + re-run command; worktree path computation (`${REPO_ROOT}/../...-${TASK_LOWER}`) is unchanged — peer-worktree placement still works whether invoked from main or from a worktree. **Phase 32.x deferred candidate:** `.venv` symlink for Mac/Linux (ISSUE-0031); opt-in via `claim_task.sh --symlink-venv` flag or separate `link_worktree_venv.sh` helper, with OS guard skipping on `MINGW*`/`CYGWIN*` and pointing at Phase 23b's `.venv/bin/<cmd>` prose workaround for Windows. Filed as a Medium-priority entry in REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md alongside the closed cluster. **Scope:** 5 files + REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md + CLAUDE.md + PHASE_32_HANDOFF.md (new), no installer change, no schema version bump, no new permission rules, no new scripts. **Housekeeping bundled:** the cluster checkbox in Medium-priority flipped from `[ ]` to `[x]` with "Resolved Phase 32, 2026-05-22" prefix; "Open BeanRider issues" paragraph at top of REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md updated (count of remaining Medium-priority dropped from five to four; ISSUE-0031 named as Phase 32.x carryover); CLAUDE.md Phase 31 row's `(this commit)` placeholder updated to `36ee6ef`. **First downstream consumer:** BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle, which exercises the new claim path on first `/claim-task` and confirms pre-commit hooks continue working inside worktrees with an `in_progress` task in `tasks/index.yml`.

## Phase 33

Phase 33 (2026-05-22) closed BeanRider ISSUE-0015 — `scripts/close_batch.sh` completed its inner sed-edits to `review_tasks.md` but the documented `docs: close Batch …` commit never landed. The diagnosis from the issue body, re-verified by inspecting the script: the commit step exists at `close_batch.sh:248–249` and was NOT missing — the failure mode is that `set -euo pipefail` (line 19) aborts the script silently mid-flow when `git commit` exits non-zero, most commonly a pre-commit hook failure (BeanRider hit this when the project's `bean-check` hook needed a venv-installed CLI that wasn't on the cwd `PATH`). The skill caller (`/review-close` Step 4b) treats the script's exit as authoritative, so the silent abort left `review_tasks.md` modified-but-uncommitted while the workflow proceeded to Step 4c — Step 4c's doc-consolidation commit then swept up the close-batch edits along with its own diff, folding both into one commit and breaking the documented "after merge but **before** doc consolidation" ordering. **Two-part fix per the issue's recommendation** (load-bearing change is script-side; skill-side is the trust-but-verify backstop): (1) `core/companion/scripts/close_batch.sh` lines 248–249 — wrapped the commit in explicit `if ! git commit -m "..."; then ... exit 1; fi` with an actionable stderr message (names the close-batch edits as still-staged, lists the two common causes — venv-prefix workaround + signing failure — and quotes the re-run command with the original batch list `CLOSED[*]`). Inline comment cites BeanRider ISSUE-0015 + Sysop Phase 33 so future readers see why `set -e`'s default behavior was specifically inadequate here. (2) `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md` Step 4b — added a one-line verify-check after the script invocation: `git log -1 --pretty=%s | grep -q '^docs: close Batch ' && git diff --quiet && git diff --cached --quiet`. Halt before Step 4c if the check fails; inspect the script's stderr output (most commonly a pre-commit-hook failure — Step 4d's venv-prefix pattern is the canonical workaround), fix the underlying cause, re-run `close_batch.sh` with the same batch list. **Smoke-tested on `/tmp/wf-phase33-{test,clean}` across three scenarios** (all green): (1) success path on clean repo — script emits "✅ Committed: docs: close Batch 1", working tree clean, skill verify-check exits 0; (2) failure path on artificial failing pre-commit hook — script emits the new "❌ git commit failed —" stderr block + exits 1, leaves `M  review_tasks.md` staged, skill verify-check exits 1; (3) re-run after the failed attempt — script correctly short-circuits ("ℹ️ Already Merged. Skipping.") but the stale staged change is still present, so the skill verify-check still exits 1 (correctly tells the agent "do not proceed until you've reconciled the prior failure"). **What didn't ship:** factoring close_batch.sh's commit step into a `_git_commit_or_loud_fail` shell helper (premature with one caller; the inline shape is 9 lines and reads cleanly — revisit if another script grows the same need); generalizing the pattern to `claim_task.sh`'s commit step (out-of-scope — `claim_task.sh` doesn't write a roadmap-touching commit on its own, and its failure mode is different surface area). **Scope:** 2 files (`core/companion/scripts/close_batch.sh` +15/-2, `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md` +9/-0), no installer change, no schema bump, no new permission rules, no new scripts, no new allow-rules (existing `Bash(bash scripts/close_batch.sh:*)` covers both success and failure paths; the new verify-check uses `git log` / `git diff --quiet` which are universally-allowed git reads). **Housekeeping bundled:** Phase 31's `(this commit)` placeholder in REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md phase table updated to `36ee6ef` (CLAUDE.md was already correct); Phase 32's `(this commit)` placeholder in both files updated to `5343602`; ISSUE-0015 in REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md Medium-priority flipped from `[ ]` to `[x]` with "Resolved Phase 33, 2026-05-22" prefix; "Open BeanRider issues" paragraph at top of REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md updated (count of remaining Medium-priority dropped from four to three; ISSUE-0015 moved to "Closed by Phase 33"). **First downstream consumer:** BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle, which exercises both halves of the fix — the script-side surfacing fires the next time a pre-commit hook trips during `close_batch.sh`, and the skill-side verify-check catches any other mid-flow `close_batch.sh` failure mode that surfaces in the wild (e.g., concurrent index lock, disk full, signing key removed).

## Phase 34

Phase 34 (2026-05-22) bundled the two `sysop-update.sh`-adjacent ergonomics filings from BeanRider's 2026-05-22 triage. Both touch the same code surface (the shim + install.sh's three interactive prompts), both are first-contact-friction class, and both ship cleanly without schema or permission changes. **ISSUE-0012** (non-interactive `/dev/tty` failure): `install.sh`'s three prompts (`prompt_target`, `prompt_packs`, `confirm`) all read from `/dev/tty` directly so the script can prompt even when stdin is redirected, but when an agent invokes the shim from a tool subprocess (no controlling terminal) the redirect itself fails with bash's cryptic `Device not configured` + a silent abort downstream. New `_require_tty_or_flag()` helper performs a non-destructive open check (`( : < /dev/tty ) 2>/dev/null` — the `[[ -r /dev/tty ]]` test is unreliable on macOS, where the device file passes readability even when no controlling terminal can actually open it) and emits an actionable per-prompt flag suggestion (`--yes` for confirm, `--packs <list>` for prompt_packs, positional `<target>` for prompt_target) before the `read` is attempted. Each prompt gates on this helper as its first action. Verified via three scratch-repo scenarios: confirm() under `--update` without `--yes` halts with the new error instead of silently aborting; prompt_packs() under fresh install without `--packs` halts with the `--packs` hint; prompt_target() under no-positional-target halts with the install.sh-positional hint. The `--yes` path under non-tty correctly bypasses the gate and completes the update. **ISSUE-0011** (`$SYSOP_SRC` discoverability): the shim has been ergonomically correct since Phase 14 (one-line entrypoint, all flags forward verbatim), but its hard precondition — `export SYSOP_SRC=/absolute/path/to/sysop` — was documented only in README.md prose and surfaced via the shim's error message after the user already hit it. Fresh agents (or new contributors) coming to a Sysop-installed consumer with no prior context hit the precondition error without knowing where to look for the path. **Fix:** `install.sh`'s fresh-install footer now prints a "Future updates" block with the literal `export SYSOP_SRC="$REPO_ROOT"` line for copy-paste — `$REPO_ROOT` is the Sysop source directory the installer is running from, so the printed path is always correct for the consumer's machine. Plus a recommendation of the shim as the entry point and the lower-level `bash $REPO_ROOT/install.sh $TARGET --update` form as the advanced escape hatch. The shim's three precondition error messages (unset env var, missing dir, missing install.sh) also gained one-line clarifications that the path names the **Sysop source clone** (not the consumer repo) plus a pointer back to the install-time bootstrap output. **Doc edits:** WORKFLOW.md § 8.2b's `$SYSOP_SRC` paragraph gained two sentences naming both Phase 34 surfacings; no installer flag, no new scripts, no new permission rules, no schema bump. **Scope:** 3 files (`install.sh` ~22 net lines: +12 helper + 3 prompts + 9 footer; `core/companion/scripts/sysop-update.sh` ~12 net lines for sharpened error wording; `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` 2 sentences) + this file's Status sentence/paragraph + phase log row + REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md two ticked checkboxes + Last-updated header + Open BeanRider issues paragraph. **First downstream consumer:** BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle — the ISSUE-0011 footer text only fires on fresh installs (so BeanRider sees the existing footer wording until it re-bootstraps), but the ISSUE-0012 prompt pre-checks fire the moment any agent invokes the shim or install.sh under non-tty stdin. The two remaining open Medium-priority BeanRider issues are ISSUE-0008 (`/review-close` manual-smoke pre-merge gate) and ISSUE-0031 (`.venv` symlink, Phase 32.x candidate).

## Phase 35

Phase 35 (2026-05-22) closed BeanRider ISSUE-0008 — `/review-close` had no path for honoring a feature's documented "manual smoke required" pre-merge gate. Symptom from the issue's original incident (BeanRider FEAT-0011, 2026-05-14): the feature's pending-doc carried a `## Manual smoke required before review-close` section with a 6-step browser smoke for a new Streamlit Queue tab; `/review-close` Step 3 ran `pytest` / `bean-check` (read-only, never `streamlit run`) and Step 5 (post-deploy smoke) was a no-op for the single-user local project with no deploy pipeline. The documented manual smoke was honored only because the user mentioned it in their `/review-close` invocation message — under `auto` mode that fails silently. **Design alignment** (asked before building; both recommended options confirmed): schema field `+` heading-scan with `AskUserQuestion` halt — combines REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md line 439's preference for schema-enforceable triggers with ISSUE-0008's heading-scan + 3-option-halt proposal. **Five-file scope:** (1) `core/companion/tasks/schema.md` task-fields table gained a `manual_smoke: bool` row + new "### Manual smoke" subsection documenting the contract (procedure location, validator behavior, skill behavior, `AskUserQuestion` shape) + new Invariant 12 (warn-only). (2) `core/companion/scripts/validate_tasks.py` — new module-scope `_MANUAL_SMOKE_HEADING_RE` (the same case-insensitive `manual\s+smoke|smoke\s+required` regex Step 3c uses, so an author who satisfies the validator's check also satisfies the skill's detection) + new `_check_manual_smoke()` function called inline from `_validate_tasks` after the body-existence check; non-bool `manual_smoke` is a hard error (type guard); `manual_smoke: true` + body missing a smoke heading is a warning. Two new self-test fixtures (`_build_manual_smoke_fixture` with three tasks exercising the warn-only matrix, `_build_manual_smoke_bad_type_fixture` exercising the type guard); all 10 fixtures pass `SELF-TEST OK`. (3) `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md` — new Step 3c between Step 3 and Step 3b (~90 lines): heredoc'd python runs from the repo root, scans `.pending-docs/*.md` bodies for the smoke heading regex (extracting each section from its heading line through the next heading-of-same-or-higher-depth) AND cross-checks `tasks/index.yml` for any task whose ID appears in a pending-doc's `roadmap_ids:`/`task_ids:` frontmatter (Phase 23a compat shim) AND carries `manual_smoke: true`, surfacing the body's smoke section from the task body file when the pending-doc didn't already carry it. Dedupe via case-folded substring check prevents double-counting the same section across the two sources. Output is `NO_SMOKE_REQUIRED` or `SMOKE_REQUIRED: N signal(s)` with `---SIGNAL---` blocks. The skill parses signals and calls `AskUserQuestion` per signal with three options ("I'll drive the smoke" → agent attempts via available MCP tools, halt on failure / "Already ran it manually — proceed" → trusted at face value / "Skip with waiver" → non-blocking, surfaced in Step 8). Step 8's report template gained a "Manual smoke" line. (4) `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` § 8.1 task-system row mentions `manual_smoke:` alongside `effort:`/`blast_radius:` + Invariant 12 (warn-only); § 2.8 Senior Merge step 3 mentions Step 3c gates on `manual_smoke: true` tasks and `.pending-docs/` smoke headings. (5) `install.sh` starter index commented example task gained `manual_smoke: false` line so the field is discoverable on fresh install. **Smoke-tested** on `/tmp/wf-phase35-smoke-{,clean,case}` across three scenarios (all green): both signals present with dedupe across the two sources working correctly; no smoke signals → `NO_SMOKE_REQUIRED`; BeanRider's actual ISSUE-0008 shape `## Smoke required before review-close` (case-insensitive heading variant) → correctly detected. Fresh install smoke also verified — `tasks/index.yml` starter contains the `manual_smoke: false` example and validates clean. **What didn't ship:** factoring Step 3c's heredoc into a standalone script (premature with one caller; revisit if `/auto-claim` or another skill grows a similar gate); enhancing `/document-work` to auto-carry the smoke section from task body to pending-doc (currently the gate fires on either source, so the carry-forward is nice-to-have not load-bearing); adding a `--bypass-smoke` flag (the "Skip with waiver" option already provides the escape hatch). No installer flag, no schema version bump (purely additive optional field), no new permission rules (existing `Bash(python3 -:*)` from Phase 16.1 covers Step 3c's heredoc). **First downstream consumer:** BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. The Step 3c gate fires the moment any pending-doc carries a smoke heading OR any `manual_smoke: true` task ships through a review-close cycle. The single remaining open Medium-priority BeanRider issue is ISSUE-0031 (`.venv` symlink, Phase 32.x candidate, Mac/Linux opt-in deferred until Windows behavior is verified).

## Phase 36

Phase 36 (2026-05-22) ported Claude Code 2.1.89's `PermissionDenied` hook capability into Sysop's settings.json template, closing the Filed-2026-05-22 Medium-priority entry that proposed eliminating the four `/review-close` silent-deny escape paragraphs Phase 30 had shipped. **Design pivot during build:** the original filing assumed the hook could auto-bypass the classifier via `{retry: true}`; agent research confirmed the hook can NOT bypass (retry just re-hits the same deny) but CAN inject `additionalContext` into the model's view of the denial. That's the load-bearing capability — it turns the classifier's silent halt into a halt-with-guidance, where the model sees the exact `!`-prefixed shell-escape command and the rationale without having to remember Phase 30's skill prose. **New script:** `core/companion/scripts/permission_denied_hook.py` (~190 lines, presence-tested across 9 patterns) reads the denial input on stdin, strips leading `cd ... && ` prefixes from skill-generated commands, and matches three classifier-override patterns: (1) protected-branch push `git push origin (main|master)` — emits the `! git push origin main` escape with venv-prefixed variant when `.venv/` is detected at the main repo root (resolved via `git rev-parse --git-common-dir` so worktrees inherit detection); (2) destructive-flag push `git push origin --delete <branch>` — emits the `!` escape + venv variant; (3) `git commit` while the current branch is `main` or `master` — emits the multi-`-m`-flag rewrite recipe (heredoc `$(cat <<'EOF' … EOF)` breaks zsh quote-tracking when typed as a one-line `!`-escape). Unmatched denials produce no output (denial stands silently, same as pre-Phase-36 behavior). Verification-command denials (Step 3 — `pytest`, `npm test`, etc.) are NOT covered because the vocabulary varies too widely per consumer; the prose in `/review-close` Step 3 stays as the load-bearing instruction there. **settings.json template** gained a `hooks.PermissionDenied` array referencing `python3 $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/scripts/permission_denied_hook.py` with `matcher: "Bash"`. **install.sh `install_permissions` extension:** existing-consumer merge logic now also union-merges `hooks.<event>` entries — keyed by hook script filename (`permission_denied_hook.py`), so consumer customizations of the same `PermissionDenied` event are preserved alongside Sysop's entry rather than being overwritten. The merge is idempotent (verified — second `--update` doesn't duplicate). **Skill prose collapse** in `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md`: the four Phase 30 silent-deny paragraphs (Step 3 verification denial, Step 4c commit denial, Step 4d push denial, Step 6 `--delete` denial) shrunk from ~4-line full instructions to ~2-line pointers that defer to the hook's authoritative phrasing — except Step 3's verification-denial paragraph, which is preserved in full because the hook doesn't cover verification commands. **WORKFLOW.md** § 8.2a gained a "Phase 36 — `PermissionDenied` hook surfaces escape guidance automatically" paragraph after the existing `AskUserQuestion` paragraph (documents the hook's three matched patterns, the can't-bypass-classifier constraint, the presence-keyed merge logic, and that sub-agent fire behavior is undocumented in Claude Code 2.1.89 and should be verified on first consumer absorption); the settings.json template sample in § 8.2a gained the `hooks` block; § 8.4 scripts table gained a `permission_denied_hook.py` row noting it is wired via `settings.json::hooks.PermissionDenied` (not directly invoked by any skill). **Smoke-tested on `/tmp/wf-phase36-{hook,install,merge}` across 12 scenarios** (all green): hook fires correctly on protected-branch push (no venv + with venv), destructive `--delete`, `git commit` on main, `cd <path> && git push origin main` (prefix stripping); hook stays silent on `git commit` on feature branch, unmatched `rm` command, non-Bash tool, invalid JSON stdin; install.sh fresh install lands the `hooks` block correctly; `--update` against a consumer with custom `PermissionDenied` entry + custom `PreToolUse` entry preserves all three (consumer custom + Sysop + unrelated event) and second `--update` is idempotent (no duplicate Sysop entry). **Scope:** 1 new script (~190 lines) + 5 edited files (`core/companion/.claude/settings.json` +13 lines, `install.sh::install_permissions` +30 lines, `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md` 4 paragraphs collapsed net ~-20 lines, `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` § 8.2a +14 lines + sample +13 lines + § 8.4 +1 row) + this file's Status + Phase log row + REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md (Last-updated + ticked entry + phase log row + Open BeanRider issues paragraph). No installer flag, no schema bump, no new permission allow-rules (the hook script isn't called from a skill — it's wired in via the hooks block which Claude Code invokes directly outside the auto-mode classifier). **First downstream consumer:** BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. The hook fires the moment any of the three matched patterns hits the classifier during a `/review-close` (or any other skill); the model receives the `additionalContext` automatically without needing to recall the skill prose. Outstanding verification deferred to that absorption: (a) does `PermissionDenied` fire for sub-agent Agent-tool bash calls (from `/claim-task` reviewer-executor or `/auto-claim` Phase 6e execution agent)? Claude Code 2.1.89 docs don't specify — surface as a `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` filing if it doesn't; (b) if a future Claude Code version surfaces the deny `reason` field in the hook input, the script can specialize the guidance per-reason rather than per-pattern. The Phase 30 prose paragraphs aren't fully deleted — they're collapsed to pointers that name the hook as the authoritative source, so readers grepping for "silently denied" still find the explanation thread.

## Phase 37

Phase 37 (2026-05-22) ported Claude Code's `SubagentStop` hook capability (specifically the `last_assistant_message` field — originally attributed to 2.1.41; corrected to 2.1.47 against the changelog in Phase 54) into Sysop's settings.json template, closing the Filed-2026-05-22 Medium-priority entry that proposed structurally parsing `/claim-task` + `/auto-claim` executor envelopes via hook instead of regex against the Agent return text. **Design posture (resolved up front via AskUserQuestion):** additive — JSON-first with regex fallback — because `SubagentStop`'s timing relative to the parent receiving the Agent tool's return is undocumented in Claude Code 2.1.x. The skill never depends on the hook winning the race. If the hook fires before the parent reads → JSON is used. If it fires after or crashes → the skill falls back to its existing regex parse of the Agent return text. Phase 7 envelope-recovery (`/auto-claim`'s filesystem check via `git log $PRE_EXEC_HEAD..HEAD` + `.pending-docs/<branch>.md`) stays as the deepest fallback and moves from "expected sometimes-fires" to "rare-edge-case-only" — fires only when no parser sees the envelope at all. **New script:** `core/companion/scripts/parse_subagent_envelope.py` (~225 lines) reads the SubagentStop hook input on stdin (`last_assistant_message`, `agent_id`, `session_id`, `agent_transcript_path`, `cwd`), finds the LAST fenced YAML block carrying both `TASK:` and `STATUS:` (matches the prompt's "LAST content in your final message" instruction so abort+restart sequences resolve last-wins), extracts the seven envelope fields (`TASK`, `STATUS`, `WORKTREE`, `BRANCH`, `ERROR`, `BLOCKER_QUESTION`, `PARKED_REASON`) plus the sealed `REVIEW_REPORT:` block at the TOP of the response, validates the TASK field against `<PREFIX>-<ID>` shape, and writes structured JSON to `<repo>/.subagent-envelopes/<TASK_ID>.json` (resolved via `git rev-parse --git-common-dir` so worktrees write to main's dir). The documented "none" sentinel in `BLOCKER_QUESTION:` / `PARKED_REASON:` / `ERROR:` maps to JSON null so downstream consumers don't need to special-case it. **Diagnostic path:** parse miss (no envelope found OR envelope present but TASK shape invalid) writes `_unparseable_<session>_<agent>.json` with a `parsed: false|true` flag, the failure reason, and the last 2000 chars of the assistant message — persists across runs intentionally for inspection. Empty stdin / malformed JSON / non-Bash tool / missing `last_assistant_message` → exit 0 with no file (hook never blocks the parent). All writes use the tmp+fsync+os.replace atomic pattern. **settings.json template** gained a `hooks.SubagentStop` array referencing `python3 $CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/scripts/parse_subagent_envelope.py` (no `matcher` field — `SubagentStop` is a session-lifecycle event, not a tool-call event, so the matcher is omitted). **install.sh extension:** `SYSOP_HOOK_FILENAMES` tuple grew from `("permission_denied_hook.py",)` to `("permission_denied_hook.py", "parse_subagent_envelope.py")` — the Phase 36 union-merge logic now preserves consumer customizations of both events keyed by hook filename. Idempotent across repeat `--update` runs (verified). **Skill prose updates:** `/claim-task` Step 8 rewritten to read `.subagent-envelopes/<TASK_ID>.json` first with explicit fall-back-to-regex contract + consume-and-delete semantics (the dir is for in-flight handoff only). `/auto-claim`'s rolling-window-refill paragraph + Phase 7 scope paragraph both updated to name the new read order. `_shared/adversarial-review.md` gained a new `## Envelope receipt — SubagentStop hook (Phase 37)` section documenting the additive contract and warning future maintainers not to change the envelope shape without re-validating the hook's parser. **WORKFLOW.md** § 8.2a gained a "Phase 37 — `SubagentStop` hook parses sub-agent envelopes structurally" paragraph after the Phase 36 one; the settings.json sample in § 8.2a gained the `SubagentStop` block; § 8.4 scripts table gained a `parse_subagent_envelope.py` row; § 8.6 runtime-directories table gained a `.subagent-envelopes/<TASK_ID>.json` row alongside `.locks/` and `.pending-docs/`. **Smoke-tested on `/tmp/wf-phase37-{test,install,merge}` across 11 scenarios** (all green): valid `/claim-task` EXECUTED envelope with REVIEW_REPORT at TOP (parses cleanly with both blocks captured), `/claim-task` BLOCKED envelope (`BLOCKER_QUESTION:` flows through to JSON), `/auto-claim` EXECUTED envelope (PARKED_REASON shape), multiple envelopes in one message (last-wins — FEAT-SECOND emitted, not FEAT-FIRST), no envelope at all (diagnostic file written), empty stdin (no file, exit 0), malformed JSON (no file, exit 0), TASK field with invalid shape `not-a-task-id` (diagnostic file with `task_id_valid: false`), fresh install lands both hooks correctly, merge against a consumer with three pre-existing hook events (custom `PermissionDenied` + custom `PreToolUse` + custom `SubagentStop` — all preserved alongside Sysop's two), second `--update` is idempotent (no duplicate Sysop entries). End-to-end: hook writes file, skill reads it, skill consumes-and-deletes; BLOCKER_QUESTION text flows through unchanged. **Scope:** 1 new script (~225 lines) + 5 edited files (`core/companion/.claude/settings.json` +10 lines, `install.sh` 1-line tuple extension, `core/skills/claim-task/SKILL.md` Step 8 rewrite ~+10 lines, `core/skills/auto-claim/SKILL.md` two paragraph updates, `core/skills/_shared/adversarial-review.md` +1 section ~+5 lines, `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` § 8.2a paragraph + sample + § 8.4 row + § 8.6 row ~+8 lines) + this file's Status + Phase log row + REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md (Last-updated + ticked entry + phase log row + Open BeanRider issues paragraph). No installer flag, no schema bump, no new permission allow-rules (the hook is invoked by Claude Code itself outside the auto-mode classifier, same as Phase 36). **First downstream consumer:** BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. The hook fires the moment any sub-agent finishes a `/claim-task` Step 7 reviewer-executor run; the JSON file lands at `.subagent-envelopes/<TASK_ID>.json` and the next /claim-task cycle's parent skill reads it. Outstanding verification deferred to that absorption: (a) does `SubagentStop` fire BEFORE or AFTER the parent receives the Agent tool's return — empirically observable from the first cycle; (b) does the hook fire for in-process teammates (Agent SDK pattern) or only for Agent-tool spawns — the AGENT SDK pattern isn't used in Sysop today but may matter for future skills. **Out of scope (deferred):** moving the envelope shape itself (Phase 29's `REVIEW_REPORT:` YAML + bottom envelope stays — the hook reads what the sub-agent emits); extracting the parser into a `_shared/` helper that both `/claim-task` Step 8 and `/auto-claim` Phase 6e can call inline (premature with two callers and the fall-back-to-regex path adding branching anyway); generalizing the hook to write JSON for any envelope shape (current parser is Sysop-envelope-specific by design — TASK + STATUS as the discriminator).

## Phase 38

Phase 38 (2026-05-23) extracted the Phase 1–29 prose history from this file into [`PHASE_LOG.md`](./PHASE_LOG.md) to shrink the always-loaded context. `CLAUDE.md` dropped from ~117KB to ~59KB (~49%). The Phase log table below remains the authoritative index (commit hashes for `git show <hash>`); recent-phase prose (30+) stays inline because it's most likely to inform current work; older phases land in `PHASE_LOG.md`. ## Phase 39

Phase 39 (2026-05-23) finished the redundancy cleanup that Phase 38 started. Phase 38 moved Phase 1–29 prose out of `CLAUDE.md` to shrink always-loaded context, but the same prose still lived in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`'s Phase completion log Notes column (for Phase 16 onward) and `CLAUDE.md` Status section retained inline prose for Phase 30–37 — three places carrying the same narrative for some phases. **Fix:** (1) appended Phase 30–37 prose to `PHASE_LOG.md` so it carries the full 1–38 narrative; (2) removed inline Phase 30–37 prose from `CLAUDE.md` Status section, replacing it with a 2-paragraph current-state summary that names `PHASE_LOG.md` as the single source of truth + states the going-forward convention; (3) shrank `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`'s phase log Notes column for every row whose Notes exceeded 500 chars (30 rows) to a first-sentence summary + pointer `(full prose in [PHASE_LOG.md](./PHASE_LOG.md))`. Sentence extraction was depth-aware (skipped periods inside `**bold**` or backticked code) and capped at 300 chars. **Result:** `CLAUDE.md` 59KB → 15KB (~74% further reduction; ~87% from pre-Phase-38 baseline). `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` 437KB → 341KB (~22% reduction). `PHASE_LOG.md` 59KB → 103KB (now the canonical home). **Going-forward convention:** authors of new phases write full prose in `PHASE_LOG.md` only; `CLAUDE.md`'s 3-col Phase log table gets the standard row (Phase | Commit | Done); `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`'s 4-col Phase completion log row gets a first-sentence Notes summary + the PHASE_LOG.md pointer. The convention is stated in `CLAUDE.md`'s Status section so future agents see it on every session start.

## Phase 40

Phase 40 (2026-05-23) shipped the `/sitrep` skill — a read-only situation report across the entire Sysop surface — plus the `Doc-Work:` git trailer that makes its lifecycle classification deterministic. The motivation: between `/claim-task`, `/auto-claim`, `/document-work`, and `/review-close`, multiple sessions can have multiple tasks in flight at once, and there was no single command that answered "where does each one stand, and what's the next move?" The use case that crystallized the need was cold-restart recovery — a Windows machine reboot drops every active session, and re-asking each agent where it left off is high-friction and incomplete (some agents don't know about other sessions' work). `/next-task` is single-task scoped; `/review-close` is an actuator on a single batch; neither answers the cross-cutting question.

**Design discipline: read-only, deterministic, no new mechanisms beyond one git trailer.** Three classification mistakes had to be avoided up front: (a) heuristic state detection that flips between "in progress" and "ready for review" depending on commit-message convention drift; (b) a parallel state-tracking file that can desync from filesystem reality; (c) an actuator-shaped skill that takes cleanup actions and turns a survey into a destructive operation. The chosen shape: each task's lifecycle state derives from filesystem + git facts only — lock presence at `<git-common-dir>/.locks/<TASK_ID>.lock` (Phase 32 resolution), branch existence, commits ahead of main, the `Doc-Work:` trailer on those commits, upstream-push state. No new state files, no new mechanisms beyond the trailer, no mutations of any kind. The actuators stay where they were: `/review-close`, `/document-work`, `cleanup_worktrees.sh`, manual git.

**The `Doc-Work:` trailer (prerequisite — single load-bearing change).** Without a deterministic "doc-work ran" marker, `/sitrep` would have to subject-regex-match commits to infer state — noisy, brittle to rebase/squash, conflates "this is the close-out commit" with "this commit happens to mention the task ID." The fix is a single git trailer (`Doc-Work: <TASK_ID>`) appended to every close-out commit, separated from the body by one blank line per RFC trailer format. Git's `interpret-trailers --parse` reads them natively; multiple trailer lines with the same key are natively supported for the rare multi-task close-out. Edits land in two places that produce close-out commits: `core/skills/document-work/SKILL.md` Step 2 (both interactive and `--non-interactive` paths) and `core/skills/claim-task/SKILL.md` Reviewer-Executor Prompt step 9 (the reviewer-executor sub-agent's single commit on the worktree branch). The `/auto-claim` execution agent delegates committing to `/document-work --non-interactive`, so editing those two skills covers all close-out paths. **`--non-interactive` trailer-amend path:** if `/document-work --non-interactive` enters with no uncommitted changes (the reviewer-executor already committed), it verifies the most recent commit carries `Doc-Work: <TASK_ID>` via `git log -1 --format=%B | git interpret-trailers --parse | grep -q "^Doc-Work: <TASK_ID>$"` and amends with `git commit --amend --no-edit --trailer "Doc-Work: <TASK_ID>"` if absent. Amend is safe here because the worktree branch has no upstream until `/review-close` Step 4a pushes it, and the reviewer-executor explicitly does NOT push (`/claim-task` SKILL.md § Reviewer-Executor Prompt step 9 hard constraint). For the common case where the reviewer-executor's commit already carries the trailer, the amend is skipped.

**The mental model that made the planning state deterministic.** The original design draft hedged the "planning" state behind a heuristic (branch has plan file but no execution commits — imperfect because plan files aren't reliably committed). Reading `claim_task.sh` and the Reviewer-Executor Prompt clarified the actual flow: `claim_task.sh` flips `tasks/index.yml § status: in_progress` and commits **on main** (not the worktree branch); the worktree branch starts at 0 commits ahead; the reviewer-executor's single commit IS the implementation. So planning collapses cleanly to "0 commits ahead of main," in progress is "≥1 commit, no `Doc-Work:` trailer found," ready-for-close is "any commit has `Doc-Work:` and branch pushed." No heuristic, no `~` markers needed for the primary states. The only `~` marker that remains is for pre-Phase-40 close-out commits — the survey script reads its embedded `PHASE_40_CUTOFF_ISO = "2026-05-23T00:00:00Z"` constant and applies a subject-pattern fallback (`<type>: ... (<TASK_ID>)`) only to commits older than that cutoff. Once all in-flight pre-Phase-40 branches close out, the fallback is dead code and can be removed.

**The survey script (`core/companion/scripts/sitrep_survey.py`, ~700 lines).** Pure-Python (matches `validate_tasks.py` / `review_index.py` precedent), PyYAML for lock + index parsing, subprocess for git plumbing, 15-second timeout per git invocation to bound runtime on large repos. Resolves the main repo via `git rev-parse --git-common-dir` so it works identically from any worktree (Phase 32). Reads: `<main-root>/.locks/*.lock` files (YAML format from `claim_task.sh`), `git worktree list --porcelain`, `tasks/index.yml` (via `yaml.safe_load`), `review_tasks.md` (minimal regex parser for batch headers + task lines — does not require `review_index.py` because that's a write-path index and adds dependency surface), per-branch `git log <main>..<branch>` with `--pretty=format:%H%x1f%s%x1f%aI%x1f%B%x1e` (ASCII 0x1f field separator + 0x1e record separator avoids subject/body collisions with the format string itself), per-worktree `git status --porcelain` for dirty detection. The trailer parser is in-process (`_extract_doc_work_trailers`) — splits the body on `\n\s*\n`, scans only the last paragraph, validates each `Doc-Work:` value against `TASK_ID_RE = ^[A-Z][A-Z0-9]*-[A-Z0-9][A-Z0-9-]+$` to reject malformed values, returns a deduplicated list. Bypasses `git interpret-trailers` to avoid one subprocess per commit on busy branches.

**Classification states (6) + discrepancy categories (5).** Each task lands in exactly one of: `claimed, no branch` (lock + no branch); `planning` (lock + branch + 0 commits ahead); `in progress` (≥1 commit, no `Doc-Work:`); `ready for /review-close` (`Doc-Work:` found + pushed); `doc-work done, unpushed` (`Doc-Work:` found + local ahead of upstream); `stale` (lock + no commit activity ≥ `--stale-days`, default 7). Discrepancy categories: stale lock (workspace missing), orphan worktree (no matching lock or index entry), orphan branch (task-shaped name with no lock/worktree/index), index drift (`status: in_progress` without a lock), and the implicit "abandoned claim" which surfaces as `state: stale` directly rather than as a separate discrepancy entry. Each discrepancy carries a `suggestion:` string with a specific investigation step — never an automated action. Review batches (`review_tasks.md`) get their own classification path: pending-not-claimed → claim, claimed-no-branch → recheck, in-progress with partial Doc-Work coverage → continue, all-Doc-Work + pushed → /review-close.

**Output: text by default, JSON via `--json` (reserved for orchestrators).** The text report has four sections — `ACTIVE WORK` (per-task line + indented `next:` action + any notes), `REVIEW BATCHES` (Doc-Work counts vs batch total), `DISCREPANCIES` (kind + detail + suggestion), `SUGGESTED ORDER` (numbered list ordered by ready-to-close → unpushed → in-progress → planning → triage). The suggested order is opinionated: ready-to-close tasks come first because they have the smallest remaining surface; planning resumption comes last because it's the highest cold-context cost. The script exits 0 on a successful survey regardless of discrepancy count — discrepancies are body content, not exit-code signal. Exit 1 means the script itself failed (corrupt YAML, no git repo, etc.). JSON mode emits the same data as a structured object with `suggested_order` as an array of strings; consumers can shape their own UI.

**The skill file (`core/skills/sitrep/SKILL.md`).** Thin wrapper around the survey script. Pre-flight permission guard checks for `Bash(python3 scripts/sitrep_survey.py:*)` plus the git read commands the script shells out to. Step 1 invokes the script. Step 2 surfaces the report verbatim — explicit instruction NOT to re-summarize because the human is reading the same screen and re-summarization adds latency without signal. Step 3 optionally offers to actuate the single highest-priority next move only when the `SUGGESTED ORDER` resolves unambiguously; never proceeds without explicit confirmation. Classification states and discrepancy categories are documented in a reference table at the bottom of the skill so consumers reading sitrep output know what each label means.

**Permission rule landed in the installer's settings.json template** (`core/companion/.claude/settings.json`): `Bash(python3 scripts/sitrep_survey.py)` and `Bash(python3 scripts/sitrep_survey.py:*)` joined the existing `validate_tasks.py` pair so the consumer's settings.json picks up the rule on next `--update`. No `.claude-plugin/plugin.json` edit (skills are auto-discovered from `core/skills/`) and no installer-script edit (the loop at `install.sh:1319` enumerates everything in `core/companion/scripts/` automatically).

**Smoke-tested on Sysop itself** — output identifies the existing orphan branch `feat/feat-custom-range-resolver` (no lock, no worktree, no index entry) and suggests `git branch -D` after investigation. Text and JSON modes both render correctly. Trailer extraction unit-tested with six fixtures: simple trailer; multiple trailers per commit; no trailer; trailer-only-in-body-not-last-paragraph (must be ignored); invalid task ID format (must be rejected); trailer-only commit with no prose body. All six pass.

**Deferred (explicit, named in the skill):** `--cleanup-stale` flag (actuate based on discrepancies — wait for 2–4 weeks of validated read-only use first); `--task <TASK_ID>` drill-down (today's per-task summary plus manual `cat`/`git log` is sufficient); telemetry log file (eyeballing the printed output is the first-pass signal; structured capture comes later only if eyeballing proves insufficient). GDP handoff is a separate follow-up pass by the user — Phase 40 lands the Sysop side only.

## Phase 41

Phase 41 (2026-05-25) backports two `/document-work` Step 2 hardenings that gdp surfaced during its Phase 40 absorption (gdp commit `e619bbe5`). Both edits land in a single file (`core/skills/document-work/SKILL.md`) and target the same hazard: Step 2 making assumptions about the world that hold inside the orchestrated `/claim-task → /document-work → /review-close` pipeline but fail when the skill is invoked from outside it. Phase 40's Step 2 text justified amend-safety via the pipeline invariant ("the worktree branch has no upstream until `/review-close` Step 4a pushes it") without ever checking for it — fine for the orchestrated path, silently destructive for any direct human invocation on a branch that already has an upstream.

**Upstream-probe hardening.** The trailer-amend path (Step 2 enters with no uncommitted changes, the most recent commit lacks `Doc-Work:`) now probes `git rev-parse --abbrev-ref --quiet '@{u}' >/dev/null 2>&1` before any `--amend`. Probe-fails (no upstream — the normal pipeline state) → amend as before with `git commit --amend --no-edit --trailer "Doc-Work: <TASK_ID>"`, safe because the worktree branch has no upstream until `/review-close` Step 4a pushes it. Probe-succeeds (the branch already tracks a remote — `/document-work` invoked outside the claim-task pipeline on a pushed branch, or mid-direct-commit-flow on `main`) → write a fresh trailer-only commit `git commit --allow-empty -m "chore: emit Doc-Work trailer (<TASK_ID>)" --trailer "Doc-Work: <TASK_ID>"` instead. `/sitrep` finds the trailer on either commit and classifies the branch identically; the new path costs one extra commit but rules out the rewrite-pushed-history failure mode entirely. The probe-then-branch shape converts a documented convention into a check.

**Trailer-paragraph warning.** Added an explicit paragraph after the Step 2 format fenced block stating that all git trailers must share one trailing paragraph — no blank line between `Doc-Work:` and `Co-Authored-By:` (or any other trailer). `git interpret-trailers --parse` only inspects the last paragraph of the commit message body; if `Doc-Work:` sits in a paragraph of its own above another trailer (or vice versa), parsing silently drops the orphan line and `/sitrep` will misclassify the commit as "in progress." gdp ran into this at merge time on the Phase 40 port commit itself, which had to place `Doc-Work:` adjacent to `Co-Authored-By:` for the parser to see both. The format example in Step 2 was also extended to show `Co-Authored-By:` in the same trailer block so the canonical shape includes both. Hand-written commit messages are the only hazard; `git commit --trailer "Doc-Work: ..."` and `git commit --amend --trailer ...` handle placement correctly because git appends to the existing trailer block automatically. The warning is one sentence in the skill, not a separate gate — readers see the canonical format and the rule for hand-writing in the same screen.

**Scope.** 1 file edit (~+10 net lines in `core/skills/document-work/SKILL.md` — opening paragraph + trailer-paragraph warning + replaced amend block) + this file's Phase 41 prose + CLAUDE.md Phase log row + REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md row and Last-updated paragraph. No installer change, no schema bump, no new scripts. No new permission allow-rules — the new `git commit --allow-empty -m "chore:..." --trailer ...` invocation, like the existing `--amend --no-edit --trailer ...` path Phase 40 shipped, may trigger a permission prompt under strict auto-mode allow-listing; the existing `git commit -m claim:*` / `git commit -m rollback:*` rules in the installer template don't match either form, and `/document-work` interactive commits already work this way. Same posture as Phase 40 — consumer can broaden the allow list if the prompt friction matters.

**Why not also add a permission rule.** The `chore:` subject doesn't match a documented allow-rule pattern in the template, and broadening to a wildcard like `git commit:*` would weaken the existing protection that keeps Sysop skills from emitting commits with arbitrary subjects through the auto-mode classifier. The right fix — if the friction is real — is to either add a narrower `Bash(git commit --allow-empty -m chore:*)` rule (waits for first real-consumer signal that the prompt is noisy enough to matter) or use the Phase 36 `PermissionDenied` hook to surface a `!`-escape escape hatch for this specific shape. Both are deferrable until the friction is real.

**First downstream consumer:** BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle absorbs the Step 2 prose change. gdp already has the upstream-probe hardening (Phase 40 absorption shipped it directly). No verification deferred to absorption — the change is prose-only on a single skill file; the behavioral surface is exercised the next time any consumer's `/document-work --non-interactive` enters Step 2 with no uncommitted changes (the common case from the `/auto-claim` execution-agent path).

## Phase 42

Phase 42 (2026-05-26) is a two-commit drift-detection backport from gdp-query-system. After Phase 41 landed, the user asked whether any Sysop skills had diverged significantly from gdp's parallel copies. A directory-by-directory `diff -rq` across the 12 shared skills (everything except gdp-only `daily-summary` / `db-status` / `db-sync` / `upcoming-releases`) surfaced three classes of drift: (a) gdp shedding code Sysop added (permission-guard.md references, defensive `worktree-state` classification in `/review-close`, the `## Pre-flight: Permission Guard` section in every skill — gdp now runs under `defaultMode: bypassPermissions` so the guards became no-ops there); (b) gdp hardcoding Sysop-generic prose to its own project (`scripts/run_ratchet_lint.sh`, `LAUNCH_LANE_PHASES = {6, 11}`, `../gdp-<task>` worktree paths, frontend npm + backend pytest as the verify command); (c) two narrow generic improvements gdp made that have backport value with no project-specific entanglement. Phase 42 lands the third bucket; the first two were explicitly judged not in scope.

**Phase 42a — `/auto-claim` heavy-solo invariant (`8bd57e9`).** gdp added a third Solo invariant to Step 2's batch-sizing rule on 2026-05-23 after `TECH-PYRIGHT-TESTS-BACKLOG-FIX` (a High + cross-module task, weight 4 × 2.5 = 10.0) was rejected by rule 3 with an empty batch — the candidate was simply too heavy to fit with anything else, but rule 3's "STOP-with-empty-batch" path treated that as "no batch possible," and `/auto-claim` refused to run. The new rule `c` fires when `candidate.weight > K=6` and the batch is empty: take the task alone, STOP. Same Solo-invariants semantics as rules `a` (architectural) and `b` (migrations), but the trigger is the math rather than a property of the task. Without it, the only escape was a manual `/claim-task`, which defeats the orchestrator's whole purpose for exactly the tasks (heavy + alone) where parallelization has nothing to offer. Worked Example G added to the existing fixtures (A–F) to demonstrate the path. Rule 3's commentary about the K=6 sum ceiling stays — the per-effort solo gate is still gone (per the long-standing 2026-05-21 drop), and the sum ceiling remains the throttle for the common case. The gdp-specific task ID (`TECH-PYRIGHT-TESTS-BACKLOG-FIX`) was scrubbed from the example prose; the Sysop version says "Without rule `c`, the candidate would be rejected by rule 3..." instead. Permission-guard section, gdp's `LAUNCH_LANE_PHASES = {6, 11}` hardcoding, and gdp's `scripts/run_ratchet_lint.sh` references were all explicitly NOT backported — Sysop's `current_focus: true` lookup (Phase 16 invariant) is the framework-agnostic shape, and the permission guards stay by design.

**Phase 42b — `/claim-task` Python schema validator + structured Step 4 (`9b4bf0b`).** gdp's 2026-05-25 rewrite of Steps 2, 3, and 4 had three independent improvements that bundle cleanly into one change. **Step 2** replaces the grep-style ID lookup (`python3 -c "import yaml; ... print(any(...))"`) with a full `python3 - <<'PY'` heredoc that loads `tasks/index.yml` via `yaml.safe_load` and validates, in order with typed exit codes: the index file exists (exit 2 — "consumer not bootstrapped or wrong cwd"), the task ID is present (exit 3 — "user mistyped or task in deferred/archive; suggest `/next-task`"), `status == "open"` (exit 4 — "if `in_progress`, check `.locks/` for owner before suggesting takeover; if `done`/`deferred`, the task is closed"), the `body:` field is set (exit 5), and the body file exists on disk (exit 6). The parent surfaces stderr verbatim and branches on the exit code without re-parsing — typed exits eliminate the "did Step 2 fail because of X or Y" guess. The script also prints structured `key=value` lines for downstream steps to consume (`id`, `title`, `status`, `phase`, `effort`, `branch`, `body`) so Step 3 and Step 5 don't need to re-read the index. **Step 3** now honors the index entry's `branch:` field ahead of the prefix-based auto-generation — matches the field `/auto-claim` Step 5 already reads, eliminating the divergence between manual and orchestrated claims when the consumer pre-chose a branch name in `index.yml`. **Step 4** splits the monolithic two-action block into 4a (flip status open → in_progress via PyYAML round-trip; mirrors `/auto-claim` Step 5.1 exactly) / 4b (`bash scripts/claim_task.sh --lock <ID> <BRANCH>`) / 4c (`python3 scripts/validate_tasks.py` to prove invariants — lock present, body resolvable, no ID collision, ref integrity — before the claim commit lands on `main`) / 4d (`git add tasks/index.yml && git commit -m "claim: ..."`). The new explicit Step 4c is the load-bearing addition — pre-Phase-42, a broken `index.yml` propagated from claim time into the worktree and only surfaced at `/review-close` Step 4b validate-check. Now it surfaces at claim time, while the worktree is uncommitted and rollback is one command. Rollback path documented as a separate paragraph: if 4b's script exits non-zero, or 4c's validator exits non-zero, undo 4a's uncommitted edit via `git checkout tasks/index.yml`, plus `bash scripts/cleanup_worktrees.sh --force` if 4b created an orphan worktree before failing.

**Permission-guard re-alignment (Phase 42b).** Since Step 2 and Step 4 changed invocation shapes, the Pre-flight Permission Guard list needed re-syncing: dropped the now-obsolete `Bash(python3 -c:*)` rule (Step 2 no longer uses `-c`; both Step 2 and Step 4a are `python3 - <<'PY'` heredocs covered by `Bash(python3 -:*)`), added `Bash(python3 scripts/validate_tasks.py)` + `Bash(python3 scripts/validate_tasks.py:*)` (4c — same pair `/auto-claim` and `/review-close` already require), and added `Bash(git add tasks/index.yml)` + `Bash(git commit -m claim:*)` (4d — exact patterns from `/auto-claim` Step 5.4). Each rule has an inline comment naming the step that needs it so future drift is easier to audit. The one-line reason text in the guard's hard-fail message extended to mention "runs the schema validator before committing the claim" so the rationale matches the new shape.

**Scope and what stayed in gdp.** Two file edits — `core/skills/auto-claim/SKILL.md` (+7 lines, the rule `c` block plus Example G) and `core/skills/claim-task/SKILL.md` (+160/-47, the Step 2 heredoc replacement + Step 3 branch lookup + Step 4 split + permission guard re-align + the cosmetic `../gdp-<task-lower>/` → `../<project>-<task-lower>/` Step 5 placeholder fix). No installer change, no schema bump, no new scripts, no new helper functions, no consumer-side files. Two separate commits (one per skill) for review hygiene — same shape as Phase 24a/24b. gdp deltas explicitly NOT backported: (a) permission-guard removal across every skill (gdp runs `bypassPermissions`; Sysop keeps guards by design for consumers running under stricter modes); (b) `/review-close` simplifications (gdp deleted ~100 lines including Step 1a worktree-state classifier, Step 1c archive-rotation drain warning, and the hardcoded-to-`npm + pytest` verify command — all multi-project flexibility Sysop needs); (c) `/document-work` frontmatter unification (gdp consolidated `roadmap_ids` + `review_task_ids` into one `task_ids` field — gdp-specific design call, not a bug fix; Sysop also has Phase 41 non-interactive-mode docs gdp hasn't backported yet, so it's a both-diverged not a Sysop-behind); (d) `_shared/adversarial-review.md` `SPEND_USD:` becoming mandatory (low value without cost-attribution wiring); (e) gdp's `.venv/bin/python3` paths (project-specific; Sysop's `python3` is the right framework-agnostic shape); (f) gdp's Phase 17-split-shape language and `scripts/run_ratchet_lint.sh` references (gdp's review-close hardening, not in scope here).

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider absorbs both edits via the next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. 42b exercises every `/claim-task` invocation on roadmap tasks (the heredoc fires Step 2; the rollback path tests on any 4b/4c failure). 42a exercises only when a heavy single-task candidate surfaces — rare; the worked Example G in the skill is the test case until a real consumer trips it. No verification deferred to absorption — both changes are prose + heredoc edits on existing skills, and the heredoc was lifted from gdp's actual production code (proven on gdp's TECH-PYRIGHT-TESTS-BACKLOG-FIX cycle).

## Phase 43

Phase 43 (2026-05-27) is a two-commit BeanRider feedback absorption — six open BeanRider ISSUE entries (`SYSOP_ISSUES.md` 0034–0039) folded back into Sysop. ISSUE-0033 (the seventh entry in the same date range) was already resolved by Phase 36's `PermissionDenied` hook and needed no upstream change. The split is 43a (skill + script bundle: four issues touching three files in `core/`) and 43b (beancount pack first population: two issues seeding two new files in `packs/beancount/companion/`). Both sub-phases share the same trigger — BeanRider hit each issue in a real `/review-close` or `/claim-task` cycle and filed the entry with proposed fix in the same session — so absorption is a high-confidence transcription rather than a design exercise.

**Phase 43a — skill + script bundle (`132104d`).** Four narrow edits, each closing one BeanRider ISSUE with a small surface change:

- **ISSUE-0034** (`/review-close` Step 4c routing table). The table's `Roadmap` column read `—` for `bugfix`, `ui-iteration`, and `adhoc` — but the heredoc immediately below it rounded-tripped every ID in `roadmap_ids` regardless of `type`. BeanRider closed BUG-0001 (`type: bugfix`, `roadmap_ids: [BUG-0001]`) and had to override the table by reading the prose; a strict table-reading would have left BUG-0001 stuck `in_progress` with its body orphaned under `tasks/open/`. Fix: replace every `—` in the Roadmap column with `if populated`, add a post-table paragraph stating the column is informational only and the round-trip is data-driven, naming ISSUE-0034 for traceability. Two judgment-call options existed — (a) make the column purely informational, (b) add a `tracked-bugfix` row that mirrors `feature` — and (a) won because splitting `bugfix` vs `tracked-bugfix` would force the pending-doc author to make a typing decision at write time, which is a needless cognitive load when the data (`roadmap_ids` populated or not) already drives the behavior.

- **ISSUE-0035** (`/review-close` Step 4c lock-file cleanup). BeanRider closed BUG-0001 cleanly but the per-task lock file `.locks/BUG-0001.lock` remained on disk afterward; `.locks/FEAT-0031.lock` and `.locks/FEAT-0036.lock` from prior cycles were also still sitting around (2+ cycles of accumulated detritus). The lock's lifecycle is `open → in_progress (claim_task --lock creates) → done (here)` but Step 4c had no `unlink` call. Fix: append a `Path(f'.locks/{t["id"]}.lock').unlink(missing_ok=True)` line inside the per-task body-move block in the heredoc, with `missing_ok=True` to tolerate pre-Phase-32 tasks whose locks were already cleaned by hand. Inline comment naming ISSUE-0035 explains *why* the unlink is here and not in Step 6. No stage, no commit — `.locks/` is gitignored. Two judgment-call options — (a) per-close removal in Step 4c heredoc, (b) a Step 6 janitor that enumerates `.locks/*.lock` and removes locks whose tasks are `done` — and (a) won because it's symmetric to the claim-time creation in `claim_task.sh --lock` (the same code path that creates the lock is now responsible for removing it). A janitor was deferred — the per-close fix handles steady state; existing stale locks from prior cycles can be cleaned by hand once or left to age out (operators see them when they `ls .locks/` and can remove them at will).

- **ISSUE-0038** (`/claim-task` Step 8 auto-mode chaining). After the reviewer-executor sub-agent returned `STATUS: EXECUTED`, the parent skill printed the handoff banner ending in "Run `/document-work` when done" and stopped — under auto-mode, the agent should chain directly into `/document-work` since that's the canonical lifecycle and auto-mode is already biased toward continuing. Fix: add an "Auto-mode chaining" paragraph immediately after the `EXECUTED` handoff banner that documents the chain (`/claim-task → /document-work` direct invocation under auto-mode), names the four skip conditions (BLOCKED, FAILED, pending UI verify, user-asked-to-pause), and explicitly does NOT extend the same chain to `/document-work → /review-close` — `/review-close` is the senior-reviewer merge gate and intentionally stays user-initiated. The skip-on-non-auto-mode preserves today's behavior for consumers running stricter modes. The non-extension to review-close is the load-bearing scope call: doc → close implies the documenter is also the senior reviewer, which is fine in solo BeanRider-shaped projects but not universal; that chain decision belongs to a per-project skill version, not the framework default.

- **ISSUE-0039** (`close_batch.sh` opacity + Step 4b recovery prose). During a 9-batch `/review-close` cycle, the script's commit-success / commit-failure banners were both missing from `tail -40` output and the next step's pre-flight grep flagged the missing close-batch commit. Two contributing causes (the issue author's investigation): (1) pre-commit hooks that print to stdout — pytest's per-test dot output on a ~500-test repo — push the banner past the operator's `tail` window; (2) the script's `set -euo pipefail` would silently abort on an unexpected mid-flow error, leaving `review_tasks.md` modified-but-unstaged. Fix: append a terminal one-liner at the very end of `scripts/close_batch.sh` (after the Summary block) that prints `── close_batch.sh completed — close-batch commit present: N`. The line's *presence* proves the script ran to completion without aborting; the `N` count proves the commit landed (`grep -c '^docs: close Batch '` against the tip subject). It's the LAST stdout line, so it survives `tail -N` truncation regardless of pre-commit-hook chattiness. Paired with Step 4b prose: when the pre-flight gate fires, the recovery is now spelled out as two ordered fallback paths — re-run the script (idempotent for `review_tasks.md` because sed substitutions are no-ops on already-Merged batches), and if that still doesn't commit, commit by hand with the canonical `docs: close Batch <N1>, <N2>, …` subject. Pre-Phase-43 the prose said "inspect git status and the pre-commit-hook output" which is true but leaves the exact recovery form to inference.

**Scope (43a).** Three files edited: `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md` (~+25 net lines across two regions — routing table + heredoc + Step 4b prose), `core/skills/claim-task/SKILL.md` (~+5 net lines — one new paragraph after the EXECUTED handoff banner), `core/companion/scripts/close_batch.sh` (~+12 net lines — terminal one-liner with a multi-line comment naming ISSUE-0039). No installer change, no permission allow-rule change, no schema bump, no new scripts. Backward compatible — the new lock-unlink uses `missing_ok=True`, the new terminal echo is purely additive, the routing-table column is text-only, and the auto-mode chaining note only fires when (a) the harness is in `auto` mode AND (b) the sub-agent returned EXECUTED cleanly, so non-auto-mode consumers and BLOCKED/FAILED paths see no change.

**Phase 43b — beancount pack first population (`4fdd1e1`).** ISSUE-0036 (parsers/*.sha256 baseline-hash files) and ISSUE-0037 (`data/<vendor>/README.md` carve-out) needed an upstream home but didn't fit cleanly into the existing python pack — the per-vendor data-dir layout and schema-baseline pattern are specific to vendor-ingest pipelines (personal-finance, small-business bookkeeping, any "raw download → normalized double-entry ledger" shape), not Python in general. The beancount pack has been a manifest-only placeholder since the marketplace was set up; the README explicitly says placeholder packs populate from real-project use, and BeanRider is Sysop's first vendor-ingest consumer. Phase 43b ships the first two real files under `packs/beancount/companion/`:

- **`convention_map.md`** (5 sections, ~60 lines). Covers `<vendor data dir>/**` (never-commit rule, no import-time enumeration, carve-out reference), `<vendor data dir>/<vendor>/README.md` (the lone committable file under the vendor data tree — synthetic content only, `.gitignore` carve-out paired in the same commit, cross-reference to the consuming parser), `<parsers dir>/*.py` (overlay on the python pack — `base_dir=` containment, explicit `encoding="utf-8"`, no source-file mutation, idempotency against re-ingest), `<parsers dir>/*.sha256` (single-line hex, reproducible generation command, hand-edit-only updates, 1:1 source-file pairing), and `<ledger>.beancount` (synthetic content in tracked ledgers, account-hierarchy stability, `bean-check` on every commit). Each section names its placeholder vocabulary in the header — `<vendor data dir>` and `<parsers dir>` are the two pack-specific placeholders; everything else inherits from python pack vocabulary.

- **`security_map.md`** (5 sections, ~50 lines). Mirrors the convention map with OWASP categories — `A02 Data Exposure` dominates (everything under `<vendor data dir>/` is PII; the README is the lone exception with strict synthetic-only enforcement), `A04 Insecure Design` covers the import-time enumeration ban and the no-source-mutation rule, `A03 Injection` covers parser input handling (defusedxml, no `eval`, bounded Decimal precision), `A05 Misconfiguration` covers explicit encoding + the baseline-hash hand-edit-only rule, `A08 Integrity` covers baseline 1:1 source-file pairing + Beancount account-rename consistency. Each section explicitly lists Skip categories so `/security-audit` doesn't waste attention on inapplicable concerns (parsers don't need A07 / A10; sha256 baselines are content-derived so most categories don't apply).

**Why beancount pack and not python pack.** Three options existed for where these patterns should live: (a) python pack with placeholders, (b) populate the beancount pack, (c) defer until a second consumer surfaces the same shape.
