Generalizing the `hooks/pre-commit` skeleton further (already at its Phase 2F.2 intended shape). Adding bash-script test coverage for the two newly-`cp'd` `.sh` files (already a filed low-priority entry from Phase 47).

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider, on its next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. Absorption is mechanical: Phase 24b's safety net currently has all five cp'd scripts flagged as preserved diverged paths; after Phase 51 lands, the upstream copies match BR byte-for-byte and a `--accept-upstream` cycle on those five paths produces clean trailing-newline-only diffs. The deferred pair (`archive_review_tasks.py` + `backfill_completed_dates.py`) and the partial-port (`parse_subagent_envelope.py`) remain flagged as diverged until the follow-up phase ships. The two real-fork entries (`run_checks_impl.py` shim, pre-commit + pre-merge-commit hooks) absorb on their own paths — `run_checks_impl.py` mechanically next cycle; pre-commit stays as-is (skeleton is the contract); pre-merge-commit stays diverged until its own follow-up phase lands.

## Phase 52 (executed 2026-05-27)

Phase 52 closes the HIGH-priority security finding Phase 51 filed against `core/companion/git-hooks/pre-merge-commit`. The shipped hook had two problems: (a) it unconditionally `source`d `$REPO_ROOT/.env` before invoking pytest — broad-blast-radius secret leak + RCE surface via shell metacharacters — and (b) it still carried gdp-shape paths (`agent/*.py`, `frontend/app/`, `migrations/*.sql`, `frontend/__tests__/`, `npm run build` against `frontend/`) that the 2F/2I generalization passes never touched. Phase 51 deferred the fix to its own phase because both halves want to be addressed together and the new example file deserves deliberate authorship. This phase ships the bundle as two commits — a pure rename of the gdp-shape original to `examples/pre-merge-commit-python.example`, followed by a new generic skeleton at the original path — keeping `git log --follow` traceback intact and mirroring exactly the shape Phase 2F.2 used for `pre-commit`.

**Commit 1 — pure rename (`0753021`).** Single `git mv` of `core/companion/git-hooks/pre-merge-commit` → `core/companion/git-hooks/examples/pre-merge-commit-python.example`, no content edits. Verification: `git log --follow --oneline core/companion/git-hooks/examples/pre-merge-commit-python.example` traces back through `0753021` → `5076074` (Phase 2A-2D restructure) → all the way to the pre-extraction Round-N commits in gdp's filtered history. The rename detection survives because the post-rename blob is 100% identical to the pre-rename blob; rename threshold is irrelevant. Splitting the rename out of the content-change commit is the documented Phase 2F.2 convention — the prior attempt of staging rename + content-edit + new-file all together collapsed git's diff-time rename detection (both old and new paths showed differing blobs, so the example became a "new file" instead of a rename). Reset, redid as two-commit sequence, history now clean.

**Commit 2 — skeleton + header (`17ec442`).** Two files touched: (1) `core/companion/git-hooks/pre-merge-commit` — new 106-line generic skeleton; (2) `core/companion/git-hooks/examples/pre-merge-commit-python.example` — 20-line header block prepended explaining gdp-derivation + a SECURITY NOTE on the retained `source .env` line. The skeleton's structure: `set -euo pipefail`, configurable `PROTECTED_BRANCH="main"` constant (was hardcoded `"main"` in the gdp-shape version), `TARGET_BRANCH` gate, `CHANGED` detection via `git diff --cached --name-only` with the same `HEAD~1` fallback as the original, two commented-out blocking-check templates (backend Python tests under `<backend dir>/`, frontend build under `<frontend dir>/`), one commented-out advisory section (test co-change warnings on `<backend dir>/`), the `FAILED=true` accumulator pattern, and the merge-blocked banner. Every concrete path or command is either `<placeholder>` form (matching the `convention_map.md` vocabulary) or commented out — the consumer uncomments and substitutes. The "Why this hook does NOT source .env" header block runs ~9 lines and names both failure modes (secret leak + RCE) so a consumer who later wonders "shouldn't this load DB_PASS?" sees the answer in the file they're editing, not buried in PHASE_LOG.

**Security note in the example.** The example file retains the `source "$REPO_ROOT/.env" 2>/dev/null || true` line verbatim because the purpose of an `.example` file is historical fidelity — operators studying the original gdp-shape implementation should see what was there, not a sanitized version. A SECURITY NOTE in the header explicitly flags that the source line is retained for reference and not recommended for adoption, with the same two-failure-mode rationale as the skeleton's header. This mirrors the convention `pre-commit-python.example` uses (concrete identifiers preserved, header note explains they're placeholder examples).

**Placeholder vocabulary.** Substituted `agent/` → `<backend dir>/`, `frontend/` → `<frontend dir>/`, kept `tests/test_*.py` (universal pytest convention) and `__tests__/` (universal JS test convention) as-is. Did NOT introduce a `<protected branch>` placeholder for the `main`-vs-other-branch check — instead exposed it as a configurable `PROTECTED_BRANCH="main"` constant at the top of the file because (a) consumers will want to edit it directly rather than think about substitution, (b) the value is a real git branch name not a structural placeholder, (c) leaving it as `<protected branch>` would require operators to also remember to update the echo-message string later in the file. Direct-edit constant is the lower-cognitive-load choice.

**Why not parameterize differently.** Considered making the blocking checks live by default (uncommented) with a `SYSOP_PRE_MERGE_SKIP=1` env-var escape hatch matching `pre-commit`'s `PRE_COMMIT_ADVISORY_ONLY=1` pattern. Rejected: pre-commit's blocking checks are universal (anti-patterns that have caused bugs in any Python/TS code); pre-merge-commit's blocking checks are project-specific (which test command to run, which build dir to cd into, which env vars to set). Shipping commented-out templates that the consumer uncomments matches the actual configuration boundary — there's no useful default the skeleton could ship that wouldn't immediately fail for a brand-new consumer's first merge.

**Verification all green.** `bash -n` syntax check on both files passed. Full 274-test pytest suite passes in 0.67s post-Phase-52 (no test changes — the hook isn't covered by Python tests; that's the open low-priority bash-test-coverage entry from Phase 47). `git log --follow` on the example file confirms history traces through the pure-rename commit `0753021` back to `5076074` and earlier. `chmod +x` set on the new skeleton (`install.sh`'s `install_git_hooks()` copies as-is so executable bit needs to be source-side; verified the original also had `+x` so this preserves the contract).

**Install pathway unchanged.** `install.sh:1368` iterates `core/companion/git-hooks/*` for top-level files only (`[[ -f "$f" ]]` skips the `examples/` directory). `core/companion/scripts/install_hooks.sh:31` arms only the explicit allowlist `pre-commit pre-merge-commit pre-push`, so the `.example` file would not be armed even if it lived at the top level. Both safeguards mean the example file is delivered nowhere — it lives only in Sysop's own repo as documentation. Consumers see the new generic skeleton at `scripts/hooks/pre-merge-commit` on their next `bash install.sh --update` cycle.

**Out of scope (intentionally).** Bash-script test coverage for `pre-merge-commit` / `install_hooks.sh` / `batch_work.sh` etc. (already a filed low-priority Phase 47 follow-up). Adding example variants for other stacks (Node-only, Go, Rust) — wait for actual consumer demand. Generalizing `pre-commit` further (already at its 2F.2 intended shape). Adding a structural test that asserts skeleton hooks have no concrete-project identifiers — would be useful but wants its own design pass.

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider, on its next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle. BR already dropped the `source .env` line independently (Phase 51's audit noted BR's pre-merge-commit was the inverse-direction reference for what Sysop should ship), so BR's preserved-divergent version will now match the upstream shape closely enough that an `--accept-upstream scripts/hooks/pre-merge-commit` will produce a clean diff (BR's paths differ — `parsers/`, `streamlit_app/` — so a full byte-equal absorb isn't expected; the consumer will need to re-apply their concrete paths once on top of the upstream skeleton, which is the intended adoption model).

## Phase 53 (executed 2026-06-08)

Phase 53 ships `/pr-dependabot`, **Sysop's first GitHub-touching skill** — every prior skill is local git only. It is a client-side replacement for GitHub's native auto-merge, which is gated behind Pro/Team/Enterprise for private repos (`enablePullRequestAutoMerge`); on the Free plan it silently stays off and passing Dependabot PRs pile up (gdp had a ~15-PR manual sweep on the day this phase was built, and an open `TECH-DEPENDABOT-AUTOMERGE` task documenting the blocker). Rather than pay or rework gdp's broken `dependabot-automerge.yml`, the skill makes the *agent* the merge actor: list open Dependabot PRs via `gh`, classify each by ecosystem + semver bump, and merge the safe ones with a normal authenticated `gh pr merge --squash` (no `--auto`), which works on Free. The skill is GitHub/Dependabot-specific **by design** — Renovate or GitLab would be siblings (`pr-renovate`, …), not a rename — and is the first of an intended `pr-*` family (a later `pr-review` covers human PRs). It is scoped narrowly on purpose: bot dependency PRs have clean, machine-decidable rules; human PRs do not.

**Prototype-first, validated against real history.** Before writing any skill file, the classification rules were prototyped and replayed against gdp's last ~50 real Dependabot PRs (`--validate` mode survives in the shipped script). The replay caught two design rules that a from-scratch spec would have gotten wrong, and confirmed the core classifier reproduces every real merge/close decision. The two corrections:

1. **Supersession must be scoped to the currently-open set, never to history.** Computed over the 50-PR history, the supersession check throws ~17 false "superseded" flags — the same package (`@types/node`, `vitest`) is bumped repeatedly over weeks, each PR merging before the next opens, so a history-scoped check false-flags every earlier bump. `mark_superseded()` only fires when ≥2 PRs for the same package+directory are open *simultaneously*. (The `--validate` output still shows these as `XX` mismatches precisely because it runs over `--state all`; the note in the output explains why.)
2. **Dependabot already auto-closes its own superseded PRs** ("Looks like X is up-to-date now, so this is no longer needed" — confirmed on the two patch/minor PRs that were the only apparent classifier misses; both were Dependabot self-closes, not human rejections). So `close-superseded` is a safety net for the race window, not a primary job, and can stay conservative.

**Two deliberate improvements over a naive auto-merge** (and over gdp's broken GHA): (a) **majors are held even from trusted publishers** — gdp's GHA had a trusted-publisher allowlist that merged a *major* Action bump (`gitleaks 2→3`) because it ignored semver; here semver wins, any major is held; (b) **github-actions auto-merge requires a trusted publisher** (`TRUSTED_ACTION_PUBLISHERS`, a constant consumers edit) because a malicious Action update runs in CI with repo secrets — a higher-stakes supply-chain surface than an npm devDependency. Untrusted-publisher Action bumps surface for human review.

**The validated merge policy** (chosen by the human from a tradeoff menu — "patch + minor auto"): npm/docker patch|minor → merge (gated on green CI + `MERGEABLE`); github-actions patch|minor from a trusted publisher → merge; any major → hold; pip/`chore(deps)` → close (Python deps owned by the pip-compile workflow, and pip security updates bypass dependabot.yml's ecosystem exclusion so this rule is live, not vestigial); superseded duplicate → close; grouped/unparseable version → surface.

**Files.** `core/skills/pr-dependabot/SKILL.md` (dry-run default, `--execute` gated behind an explicit human confirm after the dry-run, since a merge squashes to `main` and is hard to walk back). `core/companion/scripts/pr_dependabot.py` (~430 lines: pure classification core + `gh` shell-out + executor that re-polls `mergeable`/CI at merge time and skips any non-green or non-`MERGEABLE` PR rather than force-merging). `tests/test_pr_dependabot.py` (+39 tests over the pure core — `semver_bump`, `ci_state`, `classify` every branch, `mark_superseded` open-set behavior; the `gh` boundary is deferred to manual/dry-run verification per the suite's convention; 274 → 313 passing). `core/companion/.claude/settings.json` gains the first `Bash(gh pr ...)` rules (`list`/`view`/`merge`/`close`) plus `python3 scripts/pr_dependabot.py:*` — a conscious permission-surface expansion, the first time Sysop's allow-list reaches beyond local git + project scripts.

**The GitHub boundary, called out.** This is the notable architectural fact of the phase: Sysop has been 100% local-git until now. `/pr-dependabot` introduces a hard dependency on `gh` (installed + authenticated) and a new permission surface. That is deliberate and contained to the one skill — the permission guard names exactly the `gh` rules it needs, Step 0.5 checks `gh auth status` and refuses to authenticate on the human's behalf, and the skill writes nothing to the filesystem (its only side effects are PR merges/closes under `--execute`).

**Verification.** Full suite 313 passing in 0.68s (274 prior + 39 new). `pr_dependabot.py --validate --repo wade-cms/gdp-query-system` replays the real history with the documented open-set-supersession artifact and otherwise-clean deterministic classes. Dry-run against the (now-empty) live backlog prints "No open Dependabot PRs. Nothing to sweep." `settings.json` re-parses as valid JSON. Did **not** execute any real merge/close during the build — the live backlog was empty, and `--execute` is human-gated regardless.

**Out of scope (intentionally).** `pr-review` for human PRs (different problem — judgment, not semver — earns its way in from real use). Scheduled/unattended sweeps via `/loop` or `/schedule` (keep the human in the loop until the policy runs clean across a few weeks of real backlogs). Renovate / non-GitHub hosts (siblings). Docker *digest* bumps with no semver in the title (currently `surface`; revisit if a consumer's digest volume makes it toil). Retiring gdp's broken `dependabot-automerge.yml` — the skill replaces it, but deleting the dead workflow is gdp's own follow-up, not a Sysop edit.

**First downstream consumer.** BeanRider and gdp both. gdp is the immediate beneficiary — its `TECH-DEPENDABOT-AUTOMERGE` blocker is resolved by running `/pr-dependabot` instead of paying for Pro or hand-sweeping. On BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle the new skill + script + `gh` permission rules land; BR adopts it once it accumulates its own Dependabot backlog.

## Phase 54 (executed 2026-06-10)

Phase 54 closes both 2026-06-10 changelog-sweep filings in one bundle: the Phase 37 envelope-hook upgrade and `disallowed-tools` read-only guards.

**The headline finding is a correction, not a feature.** Before implementing, the sweep's version attributions were re-verified against the changelog itself (`raw.githubusercontent.com/anthropics/claude-code/main/CHANGELOG.md`) — and every one except `additionalContext` (2.1.163 ✓) was wrong: `last_assistant_message` dates to **2.1.47** (sweep said 2.1.156; Phase 37 said 2.1.41), `agent_id` + `agent_transcript_path` to **2.0.42** (sweep said 2.1.162), `disallowed-tools` to **2.1.152** (sweep said 2.1.170). The fields the sweep framed as "new capabilities to consume" all predate Phase 37 — whose script already consumed all three. Lesson for future sweeps: a capability filing should quote the changelog line *with its version header verified by grep*, not from memory of the scroll. The wrong versions were load-bearing — they made already-shipped code look like pending work.

**What actually shipped in the script.** `parse_subagent_envelope.py` previously exited silently when `last_assistant_message` was absent, leaving only the parent's regex fallback. It now falls back to reading the LAST assistant message from the sub-agent's own JSONL transcript at `agent_transcript_path` (tolerant of garbage lines, string-or-list content shapes, missing files — any failure degrades to exit 0 as before), and every written payload (envelope, both diagnostic shapes) records `message_source: hook_input | agent_transcript` so a dogfood run can verify which path fired. +8 tests (321 total green).

**The caveat retirement.** Phase 37's posture rested on "SubagentStop's timing relative to the parent receiving the Agent tool's return is undocumented — the fallback keeps the read race-free." The hooks docs now document the SubagentStop input schema and lifecycle; the synchrony argument is structural: SubagentStop supports `decision: "block"` (which prevents the sub-agent from stopping), so the hook necessarily completes before the parent receives the Agent tool's return. No verbatim single-sentence ordering guarantee exists in the docs — the prose cites the lifecycle + blocking-decision argument rather than overclaiming a quote. Fallback justification downgraded from "race guard" to "defense in depth" in `_shared/adversarial-review.md` § Envelope receipt, `WORKFLOW.md` § 8.2a Phase 37 paragraph, and the script docstring. The 2.1.163 `additionalContext` option (hook injects the parsed envelope in-band) was declined for v1 per the filing's own lean — the file handoff is race-free under documented ordering, so it buys nothing until a consumer hits a file-handoff failure.

**`disallowed-tools` guards.** `disallowed-tools: Edit, Write, NotebookEdit` added to `/sitrep` and `/next-task` frontmatter — the Phase 36/37 promotion pattern (prose convention → harness structure) applied to the read-only claim. Each skill's intro gained a note documenting the honest scope: `Bash` must stay allowed for the git/python reads, so shell redirects remain possible — the guard removes the dedicated write tools, it does not sandbox. `/triage` excluded (legitimately writes `review_tasks.md`; no per-path granularity). Installer impact: none — `install.sh::install_skills` copies skill dirs verbatim, and non-Claude-Code agents read SKILL.md frontmatter as inert prose. `WORKFLOW.md` § 8.2a gained a Phase 54 paragraph alongside the Phase 36/37 hook paragraphs.

**Dogfood owed (not blocking).** One BeanRider `/claim-task` cycle on a current harness verifying envelope receipt with `message_source: hook_input` — fold into the next BR absorption rather than a dedicated trip.

## Phase 55 (executed 2026-06-10)

Phase 55 is the installer YAML-layer bundle: BeanRider ISSUE-0042 (concat-merge drops YAML comments on id-collision) and ISSUE-0041 (placeholder substitution garbles markdown section headers), shipped together because both live in `install.sh`'s concat pipeline — exactly the pairing both filings recommended.

**The headline design call: the filed ruamel.yaml recommendation was tested and rejected.** ISSUE-0042's filing recommended swapping pyyaml for `ruamel.yaml` round-trip mode with "merge logic itself doesn't change." A scratch-venv experiment before implementation showed the naive ruamel splice **fails the filing's own acceptance test**: a `# OVERRIDE (...)` comment *above* an overriding rule does not travel with the spliced entry (ruamel attaches pre-item comments to the *preceding* sequence item's metadata, not to the item itself — only eol/intra-entry comments follow the entry), and the round-trip re-indents the whole file (2-space sequence indent collapsed), churning every absorption diff. ruamel would also have been a new install-time dependency on every consumer's python — extending `pick_python_with_yaml()`'s contract and colliding with the open runtime-vs-dev requirements question Phase 47 deliberately left unresolved. The shipped approach needs neither.

**ISSUE-0042 — text-level collision merge.** The collision path in `concat_files()` no longer does a structural pyyaml round-trip. Instead, a python heredoc removes the colliding entries from the upstream-assembled body **line-wise**: top-level `checks:` entries are located by minimum dash indent, each block's `id:` is read, colliding blocks are removed with trailing blank/comment lines trimmed off the block end (so a section-header comment introducing the *next* entry survives), and the result is validated (must still `safe_load` AND contain none of the colliding ids) before an atomic tempfile + `os.replace` write. Then the whole project file is header-stripped and text-appended — exactly the no-collision path, so the two branches converge and the consumer's file (comments included) lands byte-faithfully. The structural round-trip survives as an explicit **fallback** (exit-3 signal from the removal script) for assembled bodies the line parse can't confidently handle — flow-style entries, no dash lines, ids it can't locate — with a `⚠ ... falling back to structural merge (comments will be lost)` note. Trade-off, documented in WORKFLOW.md § 8.2c: overridden entries take the project-file position (end of merged file) rather than the upstream position. The duplicated awk header-strip (now needed in three places) was factored into a `strip_yaml_leader()` helper.

**ISSUE-0041 — substitution scoped to `paths:` values in checks.yml.** `apply_substitutions()` now early-returns for any dst that isn't `*/checks.yml`, and the heredoc applies a line-state machine instead of whole-file `.replace()`: inline `paths: [...]` lines substitute on the spot; block-form `paths:` keys open a mode that substitutes subsequent deeper-indented `- ` items until dedent. Markdown maps are never substituted — their placeholder tokens (`<auth module>`, `<api module>`) are accurate upstream documentation, and the old whole-file substitution rewrote section headers into junk (`## __disabled_no_op__/*.py — Auth`, the BR incident). This is the filing's option A in intent, but implemented as **line-scoped text replacement rather than the suggested YAML round-trip** — a round-trip would have destroyed comments in the assembled body, silently reintroducing the ISSUE-0042 bug through the substitution pass. The substitution write is also atomic now (tempfile + `os.replace`). Knock-ons: the dry-run "would substitute" note only fires for checks.yml; the stale-token report names the narrowed scope and its grep hint targets `paths:` lines; keys that only ever matched markdown prose now correctly surface as stale.

**Tests.** New `tests/test_install_concat.py` (+10, suite 321 → 331): integration tests that scaffold a scratch git consumer in tmp_path and invoke the real `install.sh` (the merge/substitution logic lives in bash heredocs, so subprocess-level coverage is the only honest test; `python3` resolves to the pytest interpreter via PATH prefix so `pick_python_with_yaml()` finds pyyaml). Covers: OVERRIDE-comment survival at fresh install AND across two `--update` cycles (the actual BR regression shape), consumer-wins entry replacement with unique-id parse validation, the text-level note firing (and the structural fallback NOT firing), no-collision append comment preservation (existing-behavior guard), sentinel confined to `paths:` lines, markdown maps token-verbatim, and stale-vs-used key reporting. The structural fallback path itself is not integration-covered (it requires an assembled body the line parser rejects, which Sysop's own fragments never produce) — it is the previously-shipped code, demoted to fallback.

**Verification.** Full suite 331 passing. Live smoke on `/tmp/wf-phase55-smoke` (BR-shaped consumer: override entry with `# OVERRIDE (TASK-0315):` annotation + substitutions file with one used + one stale key): fresh install + two `--update` cycles all keep the comment with exactly one `logger-fstring` entry; 14 path-token replacements land only on `paths:` lines; both markdown maps clean of the sentinel and keep `<api module>` verbatim; stale report names only the stale key; dry-run announces the scoped substitution.

**Dogfood owed (not blocking).** BeanRider's next `bash scripts/sysop-update.sh` cycle re-adds the TASK-0315 annotation to `.claude/checks.project.yml` and verifies it survives the regeneration — plus checks that BR's `substitutions.project.yml` keys all still match `paths:` values (any markdown-only keys will newly surface in the stale report and should be dropped).

## Phase 56 (executed 2026-06-10)

Phase 56 splits the resolved/historical record out of `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` into a new `REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`. The checklist had grown to 427KB — past the harness's single-`Read` limit — and a size audit showed ~85% of it was historical: 133 ticked `- [x]` entries (~165KB), the seven `## Resolved — Phase N` narrative sections (~68KB), a single 64KB running "**Last updated**" paragraph accumulating per-phase summaries since Phase 7, and fully-applied "Proposed quick fixes" batches. The genuinely open items totaled ~41KB. Every session that obeyed CLAUDE.md's "always read REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md first" rule paid grep/sed archaeology before it could see the queue. Same disease, same cure as Phase 38's CLAUDE.md → PHASE_LOG.md extraction.

**What moved (verbatim, no rewriting):** all `## Resolved — Phase N` sections; every top-level `- [x]` entry from the High/Medium/Low buckets (each carried into a mirrored `## <bucket> — resolved entries` section); one unchecked-but-superseded entry (the pre-Phase-29 `/auto-claim` port plan, "preserved for traceability" — traceability is the archive's job); the entire `### Filed by …` tail of "Proposed quick fixes" (every remaining unchecked item there was a *(verified clean)* audit record, not work); and the 64KB "Last updated" narrative, replaced in the checklist by a one-paragraph pointer. **What stayed:** all open items in their buckets, watch-only records whose job is being seen before someone repeats work (the changelog-sweep "confirmed negatives" entry), resolved *sub-items* under still-open parents (two in "Decisions to revisit later" — moving them would orphan the parent's narrative), "Decisions to revisit later" wholesale, the quick-fixes heading + format blockquote (the active intake point for review sessions), and the Phase completion log (part of the Phase 38/39 triple-update convention).

**Mechanism:** a deterministic Python splitter (throwaway, `/tmp`) rather than hand-editing a 430KB file — section-level classification plus block-level `- [` parsing within buckets (a block runs to the next top-level `- [` or heading, so indented sub-bullets and bare `- **…**` continuation bullets travel with their entry). Two safety assertions: a line-conservation check (every nonblank original line must appear in exactly one output — the splitter refuses to write otherwise) and a zero-top-level-`[x]`-remaining check on the new checklist. The first run caught a real subtlety: four `- [x]` occurrences that *shouldn't* move (indented sub-items under open parents), which tightened the assertion from substring-count to line-anchored. Writes were atomic (tempfile + `os.replace`) per the repo's data-integrity convention.

**Cross-reference handling:** archived entries keep their original "filed below" / "the entry above" phrasing; the archive header documents that positional references describe the pre-split layout (open targets → checklist, resolved targets → archive). The one positional reference between two still-open entries (telemetry ↔ auto_claim_miner deferrals in Low priority) kept its relative order, so it stays correct.

**Going-forward convention (the durable part):** when a phase resolves a checklist item, the entry — with its resolution note — moves to `REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md` in the same commit that resolves it. Ticked entries no longer accumulate in the checklist. Encoded in three places: the checklist's header blockquote, the Phase completion log's update-protocol paragraph, and CLAUDE.md's "Update REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md as you go" bullet. The review-session edit boundary is unchanged: review sessions still write only `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`; the build session owns archive moves.

**Result:** checklist 427KB → 82KB (81% smaller), readable in one pass again; archive 348KB. Not `git mv`-based — it's a content split like Phase 38, and the checklist keeps its own history; `git log -p REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` still recovers any archived entry's filing/resolution sequence.

## Phase 57 (executed 2026-06-17)

Phase 57 reconciles a contradiction between two Sysop artifacts on *when a review finding becomes an enforceable convention* — the first of the pre-public roadmap phases (57–61). `WORKFLOW.md` §3.5 promoted on an **in-round** threshold ("3+ occurrences across different files" within a single review round); the public monograph `docs/workflow.html` §IV asserts **cross-round** recurrence ("recurs across two review rounds," reinforced by Fig. 5's `round N+1 · N+2` label). These are different rules on different axes — in-round breadth vs. across-round persistence — not a wording slip. The in-round burst promotes fast but over-promotes on a noisy round; cross-round survival is higher-precision but slower.

**Decision (ratified 2026-06-17): cross-round survival.** Higher precision is the right trade for a high-signal 78-entry map where every prose bullet costs per-prompt context on every future generation/review pass; it matches the public monograph centerpiece (the one artifact a reader judges the workflow by); and it unifies with the deferred C3 audit loop, which is inherently cross-round ("a glob accrues no-test decisions AND *later* throws bugs").

**Reconciliation shape (option #2, two-stage — not full replacement).** The 3+-occurrence signal is **kept as the in-round *extraction/noticing* heuristic** (what makes something a candidate worth recording); **promotion is gated on cross-round survival** (the candidate's pattern must also be present in an earlier round before it becomes an enforceable rule). Full replacement — striking the 3+ signal entirely — was rejected: it discards a real breadth signal that does useful work at the candidate stage. Two-stage preserves §3.5's existing Extraction→Promotion split and only moves the *promotion trigger*.

**Compute over maintain (the precondition the rule rests on).** Cross-round recurrence is *computed* each round from the durable record — round-attributed `convention_map.md` entries plus archived `review_tasks.md` rounds — not maintained as a carried-forward watch-list. A candidate that doesn't clear the gate is simply left unpromoted; *this* round's attributed findings become part of the record from which a *later* round recomputes recurrence. The new `> Why cross-round survival` note in §3.5 makes the dependency explicit: if that prior-round record stops being durably queryable, the gate silently degrades to in-round. This keeps the loop a derivation, not an agent-memory ledger the reviewer carries between sessions.

**Scope grew beyond the two filed artifacts — by necessity.** The checklist framed the scope as "edit `WORKFLOW.md` §3.5 + `docs/workflow.html` §IV." A repo-wide sweep during execution found the in-round rule encoded in **six** sites across **four** files, and — critically — two of them are the *operational* skills that actually execute promotion: `core/skills/codebase-review/SKILL.md` and `core/skills/security-audit/SKILL.md` (Step 9). Reconciling only the spec docs would have shipped the decision half-applied — spec says cross-round, tool still does in-round. So the cross-round gate was added to both skills' Step 9 (their Step 8 *extraction* correctly keeps the 3+ in-round heuristic), and the in-round phrasing was reconciled across `WORKFLOW.md` (§2.5 steps 8/9, §3.5 extraction + promotion + the "what makes a good candidate" bullet + the §5.1 ASCII loop + the §"prevention convention" descriptive line) and the human-readable `WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md` (two sites). A `> Why cross-round survival` rationale note now sits in §3.5 beside the existing `Why promotion runs in-session` / `Why mechanical-first` notes.

**`docs/workflow.html` needed no edit.** It already asserted cross-round recurrence cleanly (the §IV lede + Fig. 5); a sweep confirmed it carries *no* in-round 3+ language anywhere. The HTML was the artifact the others had drifted *from*, so reconciliation moved everything else toward it rather than touching the public monograph.

No code changed; 331 tests stay green (the suite asserts nothing on this prose). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention.

## Phase 58a (executed 2026-06-17)

Phase 58a is the first of the two plan-layer-hardening additions (B) and addresses a *live* defect class: plan steps that call drifting external SDK methods — the `google.generativeai`→`google.genai` churn and `anthropic` SDK reshaping the `llm` pack already documents (`GenerateContentConfig`, `response.text`, etc.). A plan written from memory cites an API surface that may no longer exist, and nothing in the review loop caught it.

**Done-condition: flag, not verify.** The deliberate scope is to *flag an external call as unverified*, not to *verify it against live docs* — at plan time the agent may have no web access. The reviewer is asked only to confirm an **in-repo precedent** (an existing same-project call site using the method the same way, cited `file:line`) or, failing that, to require the call be marked `unverified — no in-repo precedent`. An external call that is neither precedent-cited nor flagged is the finding.

**No `source_map` file — by design.** A static "which APIs are real" map was explicitly rejected: it rots the instant the SDK ships a release and becomes the exact liability it was meant to catch. The check rides on in-repo precedent (which moves with the code) instead of a maintained list.

**Two edits, dimension-only enforcement.** (1) A new **dimension #9** appended to the 8-item numbered list in `core/skills/_shared/adversarial-review.md`'s Prompt Template, with the seeded anti-rationalization clauses folded directly into the appended prompt text so the reviewer reads them — seeded from *observed* review-round rationalizations ("the SDK is well-known, the method must exist" · "I've called this before" · "the signature probably hasn't changed" · "types/autocomplete would catch it" · "close enough to the documented shape"). (2) An **External SDK/framework call check** paragraph added to the `## Constraints & Risks` preamble spec in `core/skills/claim-task/SKILL.md`, cross-linked to dimension #9.

**No new deterministic check in `/plan-review` Step 2 (ratified this session).** Step 2's deterministic preamble check works because "is there a `## Constraints & Risks` heading + ≥1 bullet" is structurally unambiguous; "does this plan call an external SDK method without precedent" is not — it needs the reviewer's reasoning. Forcing it into the deterministic gate would be brittle (false-negatives on any unusually-phrased call) and would contradict the flag-not-verify framing. Enforcement therefore rides entirely through dimension #9; Step 2 is untouched.

**Future enhancement (filed, not built).** The session-available `context7` MCP server could later verify external calls against live docs — graduating the check from "flag unverified" to backed verification — once that path is proven on a real consumer.

Independently shippable, zero downstream. No code changed; 331 tests stay green (the suite asserts nothing on this prose). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention.

## Phase 58b (executed 2026-06-17)

Phase 58b is the second plan-layer-hardening addition (B). Where 58a made the adversarial reviewer *flag* unverified external calls, 58b makes the planner *record* a deliberate test decision for the work — the durable, plan-time answer to "how do we know this works?" — so that Phase 59's `/review-close` verify step has a recorded claim to check against. The convention: every claimed task's body carries a `## Test decision` section reading either **`test <X> proves <Y>`** (the regression test that pins the changed behavior) or **`no test because <Z>`** (the explicit, reviewable rationale when no automated test is added).

**The body is the durable home.** The plan composed in `/claim-task` Step 6 is ephemeral (fed to the reviewer-executor and discarded); the task body file (`tasks/open/<TASK-ID>.md`) persists. 58b puts the decision in the body so it survives to close time. The Step 6 instruction tells the planner to add a plan step writing the section into the body; the reviewer-executor persists it during implementation.

**Warn-only validator check — `in_progress`-scoped (the load-bearing design call).** New Invariant 13 in `validate_tasks.py` (`_check_test_decision`) mirrors the Phase 35 `manual_smoke` heading-scan: a module-scope `_TEST_DECISION_HEADING_RE` (`^#{1,6}\s+.*test\s+decision`, case-insensitive, MULTILINE), warn-only, never blocks. The judgment call was the **trigger**: `manual_smoke` is gated on a self-declared bool field, but a test decision has no natural gating field — and gating it on one would be *toothless* (a forgetful author who skips the decision also skips the field, so no warn fires). So the check fires by **status** instead: `in_progress` only. That is the post-claim window where the plan — and therefore the decision — should exist. `open` is un-planned backlog (warning there is pure noise on a fresh consumer's queue); `done`/`deferred` are terminal or parked (warning there would flood every legacy task). Warn-only because the read-and-verify gate is Phase 59 (`/review-close`); the validator is a backstop, never a merge gate. The scope is reversible — easy to widen later if real use shows `in_progress` is too narrow.

**Explicitly NOT a "test-file-touched" blocking gate.** The phase framing (and the STAGED_TESTS investigation behind it) ruled out promoting a proxy like "a test file was touched" to a hard gate: it's gameable, false-positives on refactors/config/docstring changes, and erodes gate culture. There is also no functioning test-gate anywhere in the repo to "promote" — `STAGED_TESTS` at `WORKFLOW.md:906` is a declared-but-unused variable in the §6.4 pre-commit skeleton, and the shipped `pre-merge-commit` has its test co-change advisory commented out. 58b is clean-slate authoring of a recording convention, not enforcement.

**Reconcile with adversarial finding #7 (no collision).** `_shared/adversarial-review.md` finding #7 ("Missing invariant tests") gained a clause positioning it as the *review-time scrutiny* counterpart to 58b's *plan-time recording*: the reviewer consults the `## Test decision` record and judges whether a `no test because Z` rationale is *sound* (pure rename/move, config/docs-only, a path an existing named test covers, a `manual_smoke:`-only behavior) rather than flagging the mere absence of a test — flagging only a hand-wave `Z`, an untested load-bearing invariant with no sound rationale, or a missing section on behavior-touching work. Author records; reviewer judges the record.

**Edits.** `validate_tasks.py` (regex + `_check_test_decision` + call site + self-test fixture, with the unused `task` param dropped to keep pyright clean); `tasks/schema.md` (conventional body layout gains a `## Test decision` section, a new "### Test decision" subsection, Invariant 13); `claim-task/SKILL.md` Step 6 (record-in-body instruction parallel to 58a's SDK check); `_shared/adversarial-review.md` finding #7 (reconcile clause); `WORKFLOW.md` §8 file-map row (invariant count 12 → 13 + the new warn-only clause — a factual-drift fix, since the count is canonical). Tests: +3 pytest cases in `test_validate_tasks.py` (warns on in_progress missing the section / no-warn when present / no-warn for open) plus a validator self-test fixture. Full suite **334 passing** (was 331); self-test green. Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention. **Feeds Phase 59.**

## Phase 59 (executed 2026-06-17)

Phase 59 closes the test-decision arc (C1). 58b made the planner **record** a `## Test decision` in the durable task body (`test <X> proves <Y>` / `no test because <Z>`) and left a warn-only validator backstop; Phase 59 builds the **read-and-verify gate** that consumes that record at merge time. The whole arc is deliberately graduated: 58a *flags* (adversarial dimension), 58b *records + warns* (body convention + Invariant 13), 59 *verifies* (review-close gate). One new step — **Step 2d in `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md`** — plus a Step 8 report line and a parallel mention in `WORKFLOW.md` §2.8. No code; the change is skill/doc markdown only.

**Verify the record, don't re-judge.** This is the load-bearing framing. Step 2d reads the recorded decision and checks it against the branch diff in exactly the two forms the record can take: `test-proves` → *"plan said test X — is it here?"* (does the diff actually add/modify the named test?); `no-test` → *"plan said no-test-because-Z — does Z still hold?"* (does the diff's character still match the stated rationale?). It does **not** form a fresh opinion that a test *ought* to exist — that judgment is the adversarial plan reviewer's "Missing invariant tests" dimension (`_shared/adversarial-review.md` finding #7), applied at plan time. The division of labor set up in 58b holds end-to-end: **author records (claim-task Step 6) → validator backstops (Invariant 13, warn) → reviewer judges the rationale's soundness (finding #7, plan time) → review-close verifies record-vs-reality (Step 2d, merge time).** The "does Z still hold" check carries inherent judgment residue; that's acknowledged and bounded — it's a record-to-diff match, not a coverage audit.

**Placement: Step 2d, within "Review Pending Work."** The step needs two inputs already in hand in Step 2 — the task body (resolved from `tasks/index.yml`'s `body:` exactly as Step 2a step 3 does) and the branch diff (`git diff main..<branch>`, already computed in Step 2a/2b). It forms part of the per-branch verdict, so it lives beside the diff review (2a) and the prevention-convention check (2b). Appended as **2d** after the existing 2c (Unpushed Main Commits) so no existing sub-step is renumbered — a grep confirmed no numeric cross-references to "Step 2c" exist outside the heading itself, but appending is still the lower-risk move. The step is scoped to **approved** feature branches; unpushed main commits (2c) carry no `/claim-task` record, so an empty approved set makes 2d a clean no-op.

**Sibling of the Step 3c manual-smoke gate — same shape, reused deliberately.** Both are per-task body conventions that the validator warns on and `/review-close` enforces; both halt via `AskUserQuestion` one task at a time. Step 2d reuses the established verify-state shape (a deterministic classification like Step 1a's worktree verdict, carried into a verdict) and the AskUserQuestion-on-mismatch pattern from 3c, so it adds no new control-flow vocabulary.

**"Hold for fix" reuses the reject disposition — the key integration call.** A mismatch offers three choices: *record holds — proceed* (stays approved), *waive — proceed with noted waiver* (stays approved, logged for Step 8), or *hold for fix — don't merge this run*. The third demotes the branch from **approved** to **rejected** for the run. This is the deliberate design economy: a rejected branch is *already* handled correctly everywhere downstream with zero new code paths — Step 3b/Step 4 skip it (only approved branches merge), Step 6 leaves its worktree, lock, and branch intact for follow-up, and Step 8 reports it under "Remaining." So the spec's "1 step" stayed literally one step: no edits to Steps 3b/4/6 were needed. (The alternative — minting a new "held" disposition — would have forced edits to all three downstream steps and risked a future reader mishandling the new state. Reusing reject is both smaller and safer.)

**Per-branch doc-only skip.** A test decision over a doc-only change is incoherent (nothing to pin), so a branch whose diff touches no code files (the same code-file set Step 3 already uses for its doc-only skip) is skipped with a one-line note. Scoped per-branch, not globally — a cycle may mix a code branch and a doc branch.

**Missing record is surfaced, not silently passed.** Invariant 13 already warns at plan time when an `in_progress` body lacks the section; Step 2d treats a missing/placeholder record as a discrepancy so the gap reaches the merge gate rather than dissolving. Consistent with the arc's intent that the record is the contract.

**Verification.** Markdown-only change — no executable path touched — so the existing suite is the regression proof: **334 passing** (unchanged from 58b), confirming nothing in the Python surface moved. No new tests added (no new code to cover; the skill-prose convention is not unit-testable, same as every prior skill-only phase). Applying 58b's own discipline reflexively, the test decision for Phase 59 is *"no test because the change is skill/doc markdown with no executable code path; the 334-test suite is run to confirm no regression."* No new permission rules (Step 2d introduces no new Bash commands — `git diff` is already used; `AskUserQuestion` is not gated). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention. **Closes the 57–58–59 plan-layer/test-decision sequence; 60 (`/intake`) and 61 (coverage gate) remain.**

## Phase 60a (executed 2026-06-17)

Phase 60a builds the **planning front door** — the `/intake` skill, a new `core/skills/intake/SKILL.md`. It closes a structural gap verified at the start of the pre-public roadmap: *nothing in Sysop creates a populated task queue.* `install.sh` seeds an empty scaffold (`tasks: []`); `/codebase-review` and `/security-audit` write to a separate `review_tasks.md`; every other lifecycle skill mutates an `index.yml` that already has entries. Before `/intake`, the first real task was authored by hand. `/intake` is also Sysop's **first instructional skill** (it runs a conversation, not a procedure) and its **first bulk task-writer** (it owns its write path into `index.yml` + bodies, gated by `validate_tasks.py`). 60a is the spine; the calibrated **decomposition rubric + BeanRider dogfood is Phase 60b** — held deliberately provisional here (see below).

**No new marketplace/pack/installer surface.** The core plugin exposes `./skills/` and `install_skills()` globs `core/skills/*/`, so a new `intake/` directory auto-ships via both install paths with zero manifest or `install.sh` edits — verified against both before authoring.

**The spine, against the A.1–A.7 brief.** (A.1) **Intent layer** — two durable on-disk artifacts, `tasks/vision.md` (the *why + what*) and `tasks/decisions.md` (the technical-decisions record, the planning-side analog of the convention map). Coherence is **detection, not prevention**: on re-entry `/intake` reads them, checks each new decision against the committed record (a contradiction is surfaced, not auto-resolved), and runs a **staleness sweep** — if the vision or a decision has drifted since the roadmap was derived, the affected `open`/`in_progress` tasks are flagged for re-check rather than silently rewritten (the same discipline a stale convention-map entry imposes on code that cited it). (A.2) **Interaction loop** brain-dump → playback → sounding-board → phases/decisions → priority → emit, explicitly built as *a few rich conversational turns, not micro multiple-choice rounds* — `AskUserQuestion` is reserved for a genuine load-bearing fork, everything else is prose the human corrects. (A.3/A.4) **Sounding-board + boundary discipline** as compact anti-rationalization blocks modeled on `adversarial-review.md` dimension #9: have opinions on stack/schema/sequencing and *argue against your own strong call at the moment you commit it*, with seeded rejections of "the human said so" / "it's obvious" / "we can change it later"; **never adjudicate venture worth** (judge the plan, not the business); **self-check against hype drift** (does this trace to the v1 vision, or did it get pulled in because it's trendy?). (A.5) **Built for parallelism** — emit an actionable phase-one backlog, keep later phases *coarse* (title + one-line intent + rough effort, no task list), re-enterable so a later pass decomposes the next slice against what shipping the current one actually taught. (A.7) **Two-leg done** — `validate_tasks.py` is the **floor** (well-formedness only; a single 40-hour `FEAT-EVERYTHING` task passes it), a human reading the roadmap + sample bodies is the **ceiling**; the skill stops at the floor and hands over the ceiling, which is *why* it leaves the slice uncommitted.

**Two decisions ratified in-phase (both as recommended).** (1) **Intent-artifact location** → `tasks/vision.md` + `tasks/decisions.md`. Co-located with the queue they govern; the validator's orphan check scans only `open/`/`deferred/`/`archive/`, so root-level `tasks/*.md` is never orphan-flagged (verified in `_validate_orphans`); and `install.sh`'s tasks handler only ever writes `schema.md`/`README.md`/`.gitkeep`/`index.yml`, so the two intent files are consumer-owned **by absence** — the installer never creates them, so nothing can overwrite them (an adversarial-review correction: this is *not* the skip-if-exists guard `index.yml` carries; the SKILL + `tasks/README.md` both now state the mechanism accurately so no future reader assumes a guard exists). (2) **Emit + commit** → the skill leaves the emitted slice **uncommitted** and adds **no new permission rules** — it writes via the `Write`/`Edit` tools (not Bash-gated) and runs only `validate_tasks.py` (already allow-listed, bare + `.venv` variants). `companion/.claude/settings.json` untouched. Leaving it uncommitted is the A.7 ceiling: the commit is the human's sign-off on the decomposition, not the skill's sign-off on the floor.

**The write path (60a) vs. the decomposition rubric (60b).** 60a ships the *mechanism*: per-task bodies via `Write` (first heading `# <TASK-ID>`, no `## Test decision` — that's `/claim-task`'s to record at plan time, ownership boundary preserved), `index.yml` via `Write` on a fresh project (with a compact validator-valid skeleton inlined) or surgical `Edit`-append on re-entry (never clobber an existing entry or `sprint_note`; refuse to reuse an `id`; keep exactly-one `current_focus`). The *quality* rubric — what makes a task atomic, how to calibrate `effort`/`blast_radius`, what's a real blocker — is fenced in a blockquote marked provisional with "Phase 60b replaces this," giving only schema-grounded sizing so the spine produces valid output without pre-empting 60b's curated-exemplar derivation.

**Adversarial review + emit-path proof.** Ran Sysop's own fresh-eyes discipline (a `general-purpose` Opus reviewer with zero authoring context) against the validator, schema, `install.sh`, `settings.json`, and the 60a/60b scope boundary. It traced every emit field as validator-valid, confirmed the permission claim, found no internal contradiction, no scope creep into 60b, and correct `## Test decision` non-ownership — surfacing **one real finding**: the original `consumer-owned` wording implied installer-awareness that doesn't exist (fixed in `SKILL.md` + `tasks/README.md`). It also flagged one minor correctness clause (a task's `phase:` must match a defined `phases[].number`), added to Step 7. The skeleton's validity was then **machine-confirmed** end-to-end: a throwaway `tasks/` tree built verbatim from the skill's skeleton + intent files at root validates `OK: 1 tasks across 2 phases, 0 errors, 0 warnings`.

**Edits.** New `core/skills/intake/SKILL.md`; `README.md` (lifecycle line "from intent to merge" + `/intake` mention; new **Prior art** section crediting the `interview-me` pattern from Addy Osmani's agent-skills, MIT — pattern credit only, prose written from scratch); `core/companion/tasks/README.md` (skills-table `/intake` row + an intent-layer section). Markdown-only — `/intake` *consumes* `validate_tasks.py`, it doesn't modify it — so the existing **334 tests stay green and unchanged**, and the validator self-test is clean. Test decision for this phase: *"no test because the change is a new skill plus doc markdown with no executable code path; the emit skeleton is verified against the real validator out-of-band, and the 334-test suite confirms no regression."* Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention. **60a complete; 60b (decomposition rubric + BeanRider dogfood) and 61 (coverage gate) remain before public.**

## Phase 60b (executed 2026-06-17 — rubric leg; greenfield dogfood pending — re-pointed off BeanRider 2026-06-22)

Phase 60b is the *product* half of `/intake`: the **calibrated task-decomposition rubric** that 60a held provisional. 60a shipped the planning-front-door spine with only schema-grounded sizing fenced behind a "Phase 60b replaces this" blockquote; 60b derives the real rubric — what makes a task correctly atomic, how to calibrate `effort`/`blast_radius`, what a true `depends_on` edge is, what counts as a real blocker — from **curated, cross-queue-surviving exemplars**, and gives it a durable home. This entry covers the **rubric-authoring leg**; 60b's own definition of done also requires a **real BeanRider `/intake` dogfood** (dogfood-in-consumer-before-ship), which a meta-repo session can't perform — so the rubric **ships provisional** and the dogfood is the remaining gate (see end).

**Measure-twice: curation before authoring.** The roadmap warned "curate the good ones — a scrape inherits their decomposition debt." Two parallel `general-purpose` curation agents read the two real queues — a large multi-service product queue (241 `done` tasks) and the small single-user consumer queue (25 `done`) — and returned *raw evidence* (field values + body excerpts + per-candidate assessment) rather than verdicts, so the final curation call stayed with the build session. The index metadata was itself rubric evidence: the natural `effort`×`blast_radius` cells (modal `Medium/single-module` + `Low/single-file`; the rare corners `Low/architectural`, `High/single-file` where sizing judgment actually lives) became calibration anchors before a single body was read.

**The promotion gate, dogfooded on the rubric itself.** A rule earns **promotion-grade** only by surfacing *independently in both* queues — Sysop's own cross-round-survival promotion semantics (WORKFLOW.md §5.1), applied reflexively to the rubric's construction. Six cleared it: the one-sentence done-condition atomicity litmus; `effort`⊥`blast` (each queue produced its *own* matched calibration set — the strongest possible signal); `depends_on` = physical impossibility; `user_action` = a human-only *action* (a gradient with a canonical mis-flag); body-quality ≠ decomposition-quality; and deferral-quality-as-decomposition-tell. Six more are **candidate** (strong in one queue, uncontradicted): consolidation-is-also-decomposition (the *coherent reviewable surface* is the unit — sometimes lump, sometimes flat-fan-out); scope-boundary prose as the written marker of discipline; the **un-owned seam** rule (stated firmly because it holds *by construction*); `surfaced_by` ≠ `depends_on`; `on_hold_until` ≠ `user_action`; and the small-consumer portability contrast (a flat fan-out of template instances is healthy, not under-modeled).

**The teaching anchors** (recorded here with real provenance — meta-doc, not shipped): the `effort`⊥`blast` triangle from the consumer queue (`FEAT-0034` templated `Low/single-module` parser → `FEAT-0036` PDF parser `High/single-module` *same surface, harder work* → `FEAT-0042` `source-row-hash` cross-cutting contract `High/architectural` *same effort, wider surface*); the product queue's pyright triad (one cleanup sliced by error-category: ~7 errs→Low, ~45→Medium, ~65→High, blast fixed) and its `High/single-file` proof (`…-ORCHESTRATOR-WARNINGS`, a risky 1,400-line refactor of one function); `BUG-0001` (matcher + capture-UI both closed `done`, feature non-functional — the un-owned seam); and the `FEAT-0045` mis-flag (research-the-agent-can-do encoded as `user_action: true`). The shipped rubric generalizes every one of these to a recognizable archetype — no `FEAT-*` or gdp-service identifier crosses into consumer content (verified by the adversarial pass).

**Home: `_shared/`, referenced (ratified this session via `AskUserQuestion`).** New `core/skills/_shared/decomposition-rubric.md`, referenced by `/intake` Step 6 — mirroring the `_shared/adversarial-review.md` precedent exactly (the decomposition rubric is the planning-side analog of the correctness-review rubric). Chosen over inline-in-Step-6 (bloats an already-long step; the literal reading of the provisional note) and skill-local (forecloses reuse): `/plan-review`'s adversarial pass has **no decomposition dimension today** (verified — `adversarial-review.md` stops at dimension #9), a real gap the shared home leaves open to fill in a follow-up. Auto-ships via both install paths — `install_skills()` globs every `core/skills/*/` subdir including `_shared/`, verified before authoring — so **no manifest or installer edit**. Step 6's provisional blockquote was replaced by a pointer + a tight four-test gist (atomic? sized? ordered? blocked?) plus the lifted un-owned-seam rule.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass — clean.** A `general-purpose` Opus reviewer with zero authoring context verified every field-semantics claim against `schema.md` (no drift on `effort`/`blast_radius`/`depends_on`/`surfaced_by`/`user_action`/`on_hold_until`/`schema_version`), confirmed the `WORKFLOW.md §5.1` citation, the install-path reference form, faithful Step 6 integration, and **zero project-identifier leakage**. **No blockers.** It surfaced two low-priority clarity wobbles in the promotion/candidate/provisional labeling vocabulary — both disclosed, neither required — and both were tightened anyway (the rubric *teaches* a labeling discipline, so its own labels must be crisp): "promotion-grade" and "provisional" now named as separate axes (evidence-a-rule-generalizes vs the-rubric-has-been-dogfooded), and the un-owned-seam rule reframed as candidate-by-evidence-but-firm-by-construction.

**Verification.** Markdown-only (a new `_shared/` doc + a Step 6 edit; the rubric *consumes* the schema, modifies no executable) → **334 tests green, unchanged**. Test decision for this phase: *"no test because the change is skill/doc markdown with no executable code path; the rubric's factual claims are verified against `schema.md` out-of-band by the adversarial pass, and the 334-test suite confirms no regression."* No new permission rules. Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention.

**Remaining leg — the `/intake` greenfield dogfood.** *(Re-pointed 2026-06-22: the target is a real **new** project, not BeanRider — BeanRider is past planning and can only exercise /intake's secondary re-entry mode, not the greenfield front-door path that matters; and the dogfood is now **non-blocking for public** — a recommended pre-ship validation rather than a hard gate, since /intake is already structurally validated + adversarially reviewed.)* 60b's rubric **ships provisional** until a real greenfield planning session runs `/intake` end-to-end against the rubric and the decomposition holds up (the dogfood-in-consumer-before-ship rule, a standing memory). That session validates the calibration on a live brain-dump → emit cycle and may surface refinements (a follow-up commit — exactly what the rubric's own "provisional" marker anticipates). Until then: rubric authored, reviewed, shipped; calibration provisional. **61 (crown-jewel coverage gate) remains after.**

## Phase 61a (executed 2026-06-18 — glob-scoped coverage measurement, C2 part 1)

Phase 61a builds the *measurement* half of the crown-jewel coverage gate: a new `run_checks` stage that reports test-coverage gaps on **changed lines inside a few carved "crown-jewel" globs**, leaving the hard-fail gate to Phase 61b. Sysop had **zero coverage infrastructure** before this (verified). The build is deliberately narrow — scoped to the carved globs, not the whole tree — so consumer-CI weight stays small and C3's general coverage infra is *not* dragged forward.

**The stage.** New `core/companion/scripts/run_checks/coverage.py` (`_run_coverage` dispatcher + `_run_diff_cover_check` + the `_path_in_critical` glob matcher). It shells out to `diff-cover` and parses its `--format json` `src_stats[*].violation_lines` (the changed-but-uncovered lines), filters each file to the check's `critical_path` globs, and emits the same `(check_id, file_line, msg)` tuples as every sibling stage — so baseline matching, `--mode` filtering, and (eventually) `--fail-on-blocking` apply uniformly. It reuses the verified-reusable subprocess→JSON→tuple contract exactly: 300s timeout, `FileNotFoundError` graceful skip, defensive `json.loads`, plus two coverage-specific inert paths (no `critical_path` globs → skip; `report:` file absent → skip, the same posture semgrep takes when `.claude/semgrep/` is missing). The dispatcher wraps each check in `try/except` so one malformed entry can't kill the stage.

**Ratified design — both legs route through `diff-cover`.** The spec named "`diff-cover` (Python) / `c8`|`istanbul` (frontend)"; 61b defines its gate as "changed lines must be **diff-covered**." Those point in different directions for the frontend, so the call was put to the human via `AskUserQuestion` and **ratified: both legs route through `diff-cover`**. `diff-cover` is language-agnostic over coverage report formats — Cobertura XML from `pytest-cov`, lcov from `c8`/`istanbul` — so one parser yields uniform *diff* coverage (exactly what 61b's gate consumes) and `c8`/`istanbul` are the frontend report *producers*, never invoked by the stage (just as `run_checks` never runs pytest to make `coverage.xml`). The alternative (shell out to c8 directly → absolute coverage) would have mixed diff-vs-absolute semantics, needed a second parser, and left 61b a separate frontend story. Two check IDs, `coverage-diff-python` (default report `coverage.xml`) and `coverage-diff-frontend` (default `coverage/lcov.info`), each with a consumer-overridable `report:` field.

**The new schema capability — `critical_path`.** Before 61a the checks schema had only check-level `blocking`. 61a adds **`critical_path`**: the crown-jewel globs that scope coverage measurement (a bare directory glob `"billing/"` matches everything beneath it, via the `_path_in_critical` matcher — which correctly *includes* `billing/charge.py` and *excludes* the sibling-prefix `billings/x.py` through its `startswith(gdir + "/")` guard). Crucially, `critical_path` is **consumer-authored and never installer-substituted**: `install.sh`'s `apply_substitutions` is anchored `^(\s*)paths:` and gated to `checks.yml` only, so it can't rewrite a `critical_path:` line — verified. Because of that the two coverage entries **omit `paths:` entirely** and use `critical_path:` as their sole scope field (nothing in `run_check`/`filter_checks`/`_validate_check` requires `paths`; only `id` is required). The same capability is what 61b's gate will consume as a block.

**Wiring + measurement-only.** `cli.py` collects mode-filtered `coverage-*` check *dicts* (not just ids — the stage needs each check's `critical_path`/`report`) and runs the stage in both the main path and the `--update-baseline` path. Both fragment entries ship `blocking: false` (`used_by: [codebase-review]` — a testing/quality concern, so `--mode security` drops them); the coverage entries are also a verified no-op in the grep loop (no `pattern:` → `run_check` returns `[]`), so they never produce spurious findings even though the main loop passes every check through `run_check`. The stage **never blocks** — 61b wires the gate.

**Verification.** New `tests/test_run_checks_coverage.py` — 23 tests (parser shape, the glob filter actually *dropping* a non-crown-jewel file, every skip path asserting `mock_run.call_count == 0` for the pre-subprocess short-circuits, the frontend default-report path inspected in `call_args`, the dispatcher, the `_path_in_critical` include/exclude edge cases, and the registry contract). Full suite **357 passed** (334 baseline + 23, zero regressions). End-to-end smoke on a scratch consumer repo confirmed the three real-world states: inert when no report, graceful warn-and-skip when a report exists but `diff-cover` is absent, and correct drop from `--mode security`. The new module auto-ships via `install.sh`'s Phase 49 subdir recursion — no installer or manifest edit.

**Test decision for this phase (58b discipline):** *"test `test_coverage_*` proves the parse + glob-scope + five-skip-path contract via canned diff-cover JSON over a mocked subprocess; no test exercises a real `diff-cover` binary because it's absent in CI and the stage's value is the parse/filter/skip logic the canned path covers fully — a real-binary integration test is filed alongside the existing eslint/pip-audit integration follow-up."* Every test's individual "proves" line is recorded in `tests/PORT_LOG.md`.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass — SHIP.** A `general-purpose` Opus reviewer with zero authoring context checked the glob matcher (confirmed `billing/` includes / `billings/` excludes, no double-emit on overlapping globs), the defensive JSON parse, all six skip paths, spec fidelity (measurement-only, no general-infra creep, sibling-pattern match), the `cli.py` wiring in both paths, schema-parse + installer-substitution safety, the no-op-in-grep-loop guarantee, gdp-identifier cleanliness, and test substance. Ten concerns cleared, two cosmetic NITs (both "no action needed"). Verdict **SHIP**. One self-review fix applied pre-review: an "answer-generation path" example in the fragment comment (gdp-domain-echoing) genericized to "the data-integrity path."

**Edits.** New `core/companion/scripts/run_checks/coverage.py`; `cli.py` (import + dispatcher + `--update-baseline` branch); `run_checks_impl.py` (shim re-exports); `core/companion/checks.yml.fragment` (two `coverage-*` entries + comment block); `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` §6.5 (header, `critical_path`/`report` fields-table rows, "Coverage findings" subsection, scripts-inventory stage line); new `tests/test_run_checks_coverage.py`; `tests/PORT_LOG.md` (Phase 61a section). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention. **61a done; 61b (crown-jewel hard gate) + the BeanRider `/intake` dogfood (60b) remain before public.**

## Phase 61b (executed 2026-06-18 — crown-jewel critical-path hard gate, C2 part 2)

Phase 61b arms the gate 61a measured. 61a shipped the `coverage-*` stage `blocking: false` — it reported changed-but-uncovered lines inside the `critical_path` globs but never failed CI. 61b makes an uncovered crown-jewel line a **hard fail**. The substance is small because 61a built the plumbing to be uniform: coverage findings already flow through the same `(check_id, file_line, msg)` shape, and `cli.py` already routes a `blocking: true` check into `blocking_ids` → `new_blocking_hits` → `--fail-on-blocking` exit 1. So 61b is three moves — flip the shipped entries to blocking, carve coverage out of the baseline, and make the failure message coverage-correct — plus docs and tests.

**The gate flip.** Both shipped fragment entries (`coverage-diff-python`, `coverage-diff-frontend`) move to `blocking: true`. The reasoning that resolves "ship blocking-on by default vs. opt-in": `critical_path` *is* the crown-jewel scope, and there is no measurement-only-critical-path concept in Sysop today (C3's general coverage signal is deferred). Marking a path crown-jewel **is** the opt-in to gating it; the spec's carve-out ("a real finding here is a launch-time credibility event, too costly to catch later") would be inverted if the gate didn't block on exactly those paths. The shipped entries stay **inert** until a consumer (a) replaces the placeholder globs (`<critical path module>/`) — `critical_path` is never installer-substituted, so the placeholder survives install untouched — and (b) produces a coverage report; absent either, the stage returns `[]`. A consumer who wants the 61a measurement posture instead keeps `blocking: false` — that path still works end to end (finding emitted, never counted), preserving the measurement-only fallback.

**Coverage bypasses the baseline — the spec's defining constraint.** The spec: the gate "consumes the coverage number directly as a block, **not through the audit loop**" — the audit loop being Sysop's baseline tech-debt-acceptance mechanism. A coverage finding's key is `coverage-…|path:line`, but the line number is *diff-relative* (it shifts every commit), so a baselined coverage gap would never re-match on the next PR — and, worse, `--update-baseline` would become an escape hatch: run it, commit the baseline, merge the uncovered crown-jewel line. That is exactly what the carve-out exists to forbid. So coverage is excluded from **both ends** of the baseline, centralized in `baseline.py`: `is_baseline_suppressed()` returns `False` for any `coverage-` id (a blocking coverage gap always counts, baseline or not), and `write_baseline()` never persists a `coverage-` finding (so the baseline file can't even *describe* an accepted coverage gap). The two are defense-in-depth: the write-side keeps the baseline clean; the read-side means even a stale or hand-edited baseline entry can't smuggle a gap past the gate. The legitimate escape for a genuinely-untestable line is a **coverage pragma** (`# pragma: no cover`, `/* istanbul ignore */`) at the report-producer layer — it drops the line from the report so it's not a violation at all — while the task's `## Test decision` record (Phase 58b) documents *why*. The record does **not** itself clear the gate; that division is deliberate (the record is human-facing rationale, the pragma is the mechanical signal).

**Coverage-correct failure message.** The generic `--fail-on-blocking` error tells the consumer to "regenerate the baseline with `--update-baseline`" — dead-end advice for a coverage gap (proven by the smoke: after baselining, the gate still fails). `main()` now counts `new_coverage_hits` alongside `new_blocking_hits` and, when any coverage gap blocked, appends a note: these are NOT baselineable; cover the line or pragma-exclude it. This was a self-review catch — the gate is useless if its own failure message routes consumers down a path that can't work.

**Why this isn't "just flip a flag."** The baseline bypass is the meaningful code of the phase. Without it, `--update-baseline` is a documented back door around the crown-jewel gate; with it, the gate honors the spec's "not through the audit loop" literally. The carve-out lives in `baseline.py` (one `_is_coverage` predicate, two call sites) so the policy has a single home, matching the file's existing ownership of `finding_key`/`load_baseline`/`write_baseline`.

**Verification.** `tests/test_run_checks_coverage.py` gains the Phase 61b section (+10 tests, and the 61a `test_coverage_entries_are_measurement_only` flips to `test_coverage_entries_are_blocking`): five `main()`-level tests drive the **real** `cli.main()` over a one-coverage-check scratch repo (non-coverage stages patched to `[]`, the `diff-cover` subprocess mocked, `--repo-root` passed so no git) — the gate blocks (exit 1) with coverage-correct guidance, passes without `--fail-on-blocking`, **still fails even with a matching baseline entry** (the bypass), stays exit-0 when `blocking: false`, and writes zero coverage keys on `--update-baseline`; four unit tests pin `is_baseline_suppressed` (coverage never suppresses; non-coverage still suppresses only when blocking AND baselined) and `write_baseline` (coverage excluded); one pins the `_is_coverage` predicate. Full suite **367 passed** (357 + 10, zero regressions). A real-process end-to-end smoke on a scratch repo with a **stub `diff-cover` on PATH** confirmed the four states as an actual subprocess (not in-process `main()`): dirty line → exit 1; clean → exit 0; `--update-baseline` → "Wrote 0 baseline finding(s)" + zero coverage keys; and **after baselining, the dirty line still fails** — the no-escape-hatch property the spec demands. The real-`diff-cover`-binary integration test remains filed alongside the existing eslint/pip-audit follow-up (same gap 61a recorded; `diff-cover` is absent in CI).

**Test decision for this phase (58b discipline):** *"the `test_gate_*` + `is_baseline_suppressed`/`write_baseline` tests prove the gate + baseline-carve-out contract by driving the real `cli.main()` and baseline functions over canned `diff-cover` JSON; no test exercises a real `diff-cover` binary (absent in CI; the gate/baseline logic under test is in `cli.py`/`baseline.py`, fully covered in-process) — the real-binary integration test stays filed with the eslint/pip-audit follow-up."* Per-test "proves" lines recorded in `tests/PORT_LOG.md`.

**Edits.** `core/companion/scripts/run_checks/baseline.py` (`_is_coverage` + `is_baseline_suppressed` + `write_baseline` carve-out); `cli.py` (helper import, emit-loop via `is_baseline_suppressed`, `new_coverage_hits` + coverage-correct error note, `--update-baseline` count honesty, stage comment); `coverage.py` (module docstring); `run_checks_impl.py` (shim re-exports `_is_coverage` + `is_baseline_suppressed`); `core/companion/checks.yml.fragment` (both entries → `blocking: true`, comment block + `notes:` + `description:` rewritten for the gate / baseline-bypass / pragma escape / measurement-only opt-out); `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` §6.5 (`blocking` + `critical_path` field rows, "Coverage gate" paragraph); `tests/test_run_checks_coverage.py` (+10, one rename); `tests/PORT_LOG.md` (Phase 61b section). Markdown-and-Python only, no installer/manifest edit (auto-ships via Phase 49 subdir recursion). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention. **61b done; the BeanRider `/intake` dogfood (60b) is the last item before public.**

## Phase 62 (executed 2026-06-22 — convention-demotion path, Tier 1: backward staleness sweep at Step 2a)

Phase 62 answers the convention-rot critique filed 2026-06-22: Sysop has a richly-instrumented convention *promotion* pipeline (extraction → cross-round survival gate → mechanical-first enforcement → sweep → `Promotion summary:` trailer) and **zero symmetric demotion pipeline** — conventions can enter the maps but never leave. The filed plan tiers the response; Phase 62 builds **Tier 1 only**, the cheap, static, unambiguous slice. Tier 2 (the FP-verdict ledger → interactive Step 9 retirement prompt, which addresses the expensive blocking-mechanical cost) stays spec'd-and-triggered in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`; Tier 3 (periodic prose-relevance + dependabot-hooked version re-confirmation) stays don't-build. The demotion item therefore remains **open** in the checklist with its Tier 1 leg marked done.

**What Tier 1 is.** Both review skills already run a `Step 2a: Map Coverage Audit` that diffs the maps against `git ls-files` in the **forward** direction — three checks that all detect *under*-coverage (a code file no map section governs). Tier 1 adds the **backward** direction (map → code: which map content has lost its referent), catching the two staleness modes that are *statically detectable*:
- **Mode C — removed category:** a `## <glob> — <Section>` section whose glob matches **zero** tracked files (`git ls-files -- <globs>` empty). The scoped surface is gone.
- **Mode B — dead reference:** a bullet citing a concrete in-repo helper (`_sanitize_log`, `useAbortableFetch`, `isSafeHref`) whose symbol no longer appears in tracked code (`git grep -nw` → 0 hits). The helper was renamed/moved/deleted.

It catches these **at the moment the symbol dies** — no telemetry, no schedule, every round. The sweep is the *detection* half of convention demotion, symmetric to the promotion lifecycle in WORKFLOW.md §3.5.

**The load-bearing design calls.** (1) **Step 2a, not Step 9.** Step 9 (convention promotion) only fires "if Step 8 produced candidates," so folding the backward sweep there would skip it on quiet rounds — exactly the rounds where slow code drift accumulates. Step 2a runs unconditionally. (2) **Detection only — flag, never auto-retire.** Tier 1 surfaces candidates and offers to apply only the *low-stakes map hygiene* (refresh a renamed citation, update a relocated glob). Retiring a *promoted convention* (deleting a CLAUDE.md § Prevention Conventions bullet) is a judgment call routed to a deliberate, human retirement step — the interactive Step 9 retirement prompt is Tier 2, designed but **not yet built**; until it ships the human retires using the map's round attribution. The prose nowhere implies Tier 2 exists. (3) **Refresh ≠ retire, and Mode G ≠ staleness.** A dead citation usually means the rule is still valid and only the helper name changed (refresh); an empty section usually means the category is gone (retire). But an *over-broad-from-birth* glob (Mode G) — one that never matched much — presents identically to a removed category, so the prose steers the runner to **tighten the glob, not retire the rule**, and to infer retirement only when the category genuinely existed and was removed. (4) **Low-FP discipline, borrowed from Phase 58a's dimension #9:** skip angle-bracket placeholders (`<api module>`), skip un-substituted globs, skip library/framework identifiers (no in-repo definition by design), distinguish *relocation* (forward pass found the files in a sibling location → update glob) from *removal* — and "when you cannot tell, leave it unflagged." The security skill adds a security-specific default: a dead citation on a sanitizer/auth-guard/redactor defaults to *refresh*, confirming the protection still exists somewhere before any retirement is even considered.

**Why markdown-only.** Step 2a is pure skill-runner prose — no script backs it (the runner parses headers, runs `git ls-files`/`git grep` inline). The filed plan's "modest script tweak" was speculative; there is no map-coverage script to tweak. So the change is four markdown surfaces and no executable path: both skills' Step 2a, WORKFLOW.md §3.6 (forward/backward split + check 4) and §5.3 (the feedback loop now runs in reverse too), and `docs/workflow.html`'s convention-rot explainer — which previously asserted "nothing in the workflow prunes a stale entry automatically," now corrected to the honest state (detection automatic via the backward sweep; the retirement *decision* still manual; the harder FP-driven demotion of blocking rules still spec'd-not-built).

**Verification.** Markdown-only, no executable code path changed → the full suite is the regression proof: **367 passed**, unchanged. A fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context) walked all six plan constraints (Step-2a-not-9 placement, detection-only/no-Tier-2-overclaim, no staleness-mode overclaim, the Mode-G guard, the low-FP guards, gdp-identifier cleanliness) plus sub-step renumbering integrity, forward-check preservation, command correctness, and HTML tag balance: verdict **SHIP**, no blockers/should-fixes.
