Both cosmetic NITs were applied — the §2.5 step-3 and §2.6 step-2 one-line summaries now mention the backward sweep, and the security skill's dead-citation guard was harmonized with the codebase skill's "only test in-repo identifiers" clause. The reviewer empirically confirmed `git grep -nw _sanitize_log` matches the bare helper without false-matching the substring inside `_sanitize_logger` — the rename-discrimination the prose relies on.

**Bundled correctness fix (pre-existing, discovered while editing §3.6).** Two cross-references read "§ 2.6 step 3" for the security review's map-coverage audit, but that audit is **step 2** of §2.6 (step 3 is the security grep checks). One was on the §3.6 "When it runs" line this phase rewrote; the other was §5.3's Detection line. Both corrected to "§ 2.6 step 2" rather than knowingly ship a doc with a wrong cross-reference while holding the pen two lines away.

**Test decision for this phase (58b discipline):** *"no test because the change is skill/process-doc markdown with no executable code path — Step 2a is runner-executed prose, not a script. The sweep's factual claims (command correctness, no Tier-2 overclaim, Mode-B/C-only scope) are verified out-of-band by the fresh-eyes adversarial pass, and the unchanged 367-test suite confirms no regression."*

**Sub-step renumbering.** codebase-review: forward `2a-1/2a-2/2a-3` → new `2a-4` (staleness sweep) → `2a-5` (offer, was 2a-4). security-audit: forward `2a-1/2a-2` → new `2a-3` (staleness sweep) → `2a-4` (offer, was 2a-3). No downstream references to the old offer-step numbers.

**Edits.** `core/skills/codebase-review/SKILL.md` (new 2a-4 + offer renumber); `core/skills/security-audit/SKILL.md` (new 2a-3 + offer renumber + security-default refresh caveat); `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` (§3.6 forward/backward split + check 4 + "Why it matters" rewrite; §5.3 reverse-direction note; §2.5 step 3 + §2.6 step 2 summaries; two `§ 2.6 step 3`→`step 2` corrections); `docs/workflow.html` (convention-rot explainer). Markdown-only, no installer/manifest/test edit, no new permission rules. Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention. **Phase 62 (Tier 1) done; demotion-path item stays open in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` for Tier 2 (triggered) and Tier 3 (noted-future). The BeanRider `/intake` greenfield dogfood (60b) remains the last recommended pre-public validation.**

## Phase 63 (executed 2026-06-25 — `/review-close` config-gated merge policy: PR-route a protected `main`)

Phase 63 resolves the **HIGH** item from the 2026-06-24 gdp→Sysop backport assessment. The assessment (three parallel agents over ~3 weeks of upstream workflow commits) surfaced that `/review-close` Step 4d ends with an unconditional `git push origin main` — and Sysop's own `main` became PR-protected 2026-06-24 (`required_status_checks: [pytest]` strict, `enforce_admins: true`, **no admin bypass**, verified via the protection API). A bare direct push is now rejected for everyone, so the shipped skill's merge path is genuinely broken for any protected-main project. (Sysop's meta-repo close-out is inline, not via `/review-close`, which masks it locally — but the skill ships to consumers.) Upstream gdp solved the same break in `b02a1517` (TECH-WADEFLOW-PR-ONLY-MAIN), but its solution assumes GitHub-Pro **native auto-merge** (`gh pr merge --auto`), which Sysop lacks (`allow_auto_merge: false`, private repo) — so this is an *adaptation*, not a port.

**The design fork (ratified via `AskUserQuestion`): config-gated dual flow.** A `§ Merge policy` line in `<project>/CLAUDE.md` (the same "consumer declares its shape" pattern as `§ Pre-merge verification`), default **`direct`**:
- **`direct`** (default) — the historical flow: merge onto `main`, `git push origin main`. A consumer who never configured a policy keeps today's behavior with **zero regression** (BeanRider and any unprotected-main project are untouched).
- **`pr`** — `main` is never written directly. Everything is assembled on a throwaway integration branch cut from **fresh `origin/main`** (so the PR's required checks run against the live base), with local-only `main` commits (claim flips + Step 1b doc saves) swept onto it via a `git rev-list --reverse origin/main..main` cherry-pick loop. The branch is pushed and squash-merged through a PR with a **non-`--auto` `gh pr merge --squash --delete-branch`** — the same client-side merge shape `/pr-dependabot` already standardizes on, which works on Free-plan private repos where native auto-merge is unavailable. A stuck PR (failing required check / `mergeStateStatus: BLOCKED`) → **report the PR URL + STOP**, never force-merge, never fall back to a direct push; Step 6 cleanup is deferred until the PR confirms `MERGED` so a stuck close leaves branches/worktrees/locks recoverable.

The two rejected alternatives: **PR-only** (gdp's shape) would break every consumer without a protected main or without `gh`; **auto-detect** (probe `gh api .../branches/main/protection`) would add a network + `gh` dependency to the previously git-only default path and fail offline.

**Stripped from gdp** (the genericness discipline): native `--auto`/auto-merge, the admin-bypass migration runbook and ruleset ID `18084254`, and `run_ratchet_lint.sh` (no such script in Sysop — the `pr` path leans on the PR's required check as the authoritative gate). A grep re-scan confirmed zero leakage (every `--auto` occurrence is an explicit "non-`--auto`" callout).

**Surfaces.** `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md`: Step 0 permission guard gains a **conditionally-required** `gh pr create/checks/view/merge` + `git fetch/cherry-pick/reset --hard/branch -D` block, gated on `pr` policy so a `direct` consumer isn't blocked for their absence; new **Step 4-pre** reads the policy and sets `$MERGE_TARGET` (+ cuts/sweeps the integration branch under `pr`, with an inline HEAD-guard); **4a/4b** are parametrized by `$MERGE_TARGET` (always `--force` on `close_batch.sh` under `pr`); **4d** splits into a `direct` push (with a "switch to `pr` if rejected" hint) and a `pr` push→PR→squash-merge with a **4d-1 stuck-PR report+STOP**; **Step 6** gains a merge-policy cleanup gate (defer until `MERGED`; re-sync local `main`; `-D` the integration + squash-merged branches) plus a lock-as-real-time-signal invariant note. `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md`: §2.8 step list (5/6/8/10) reframed for both policies + §6.1 `## Merge policy` table row and template.

**The `pr`-path mechanics worth recording.** `git branch -d` → `-D` for squash-merged feature branches (a squash makes the branch a non-ancestor of `main`, so `-d` would refuse "not fully merged" — the content is provably in the squash). Step 6 re-syncs local `main` with `git reset --hard origin/main` because the swept claim/doc commits are now folded into the squash and would otherwise leave local `main` diverged. The lock removal (Step 4c, working-tree unlink) happens before the PR merges under `pr` policy — safe because the task is `in_progress` (never claimable) throughout the in-flight window; the only effect is a transient `/sitrep` "in_progress without lock" drift flag that clears on merge.

**Verification.** Markdown-only (no executable path) → the full suite is the regression proof: **367 passed**, unchanged. A fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context) returned **SHIP WITH FIXES**; all applied: **B1** (blocker — the integration-branch `git push -u origin` would not match the `Bash(git push origin:*)` allow-rule because `-u` breaks the prefix; dropped `-u`, since tracking isn't needed), **S1** (`$MERGE_TARGET`/`$INTEGRATION_BRANCH`/`$RUN_ID` are set in 4-pre but referenced in later sub-steps the runner executes as *separate* shell calls — added a variable-persistence note: re-export, and HEAD is recoverable as the integration branch through 4a–4c), **S2** (`gh pr merge --delete-branch` removes the local branch too once HEAD leaves it, so the later `git branch -D` was made tolerant with `2>/dev/null || true`), **S3** (a reassurance that re-running after a stuck PR is idempotent — the next run re-cuts a fresh branch and re-sweeps the still-unpushed commits). N1 (zero-checks `gh pr checks` exit code — the `|| true` wrap already handles it) and N2 (`close_batch.sh` hard-codes `main` in its ancestry check — the bold "always `--force` under `pr`" prose neutralizes it) needed no change; N3 confirmed the `-d`→`-D` reasoning. Strip-list re-scanned clean. The reviewer also confirmed the dry-run boundary is airtight (all `pr`-path `gh` side-effects live in Step 4, which `--dry-run` skips) and `direct` is a verified no-op vs `git show HEAD`.

**Not fully done — recommended-not-blocking pre-ship validation.** The `pr` path has never run against a real protected-main repo; it is reasoned-through, not exercised. Per the dogfood-in-consumer-before-ship convention, the honest move is one real run before declaring it shippable — and Sysop's own `main` is now protected, so it can serve as the dogfood (set `§ Merge policy: pr` here and drive one `/review-close` through the integration-branch → PR → squash-merge). The other three (Medium) backport items from the assessment remain open. Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; the HIGH checklist item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Filed under two commits — the assessment filing (`1a602ba`) and this phase — landing via branch → PR → squash-merge because `main` is protected.

## Phase 64 (executed 2026-06-26 — `_shared/main-push-guard.md`: HEAD-hijack + autonomous-writer races)

Phase 64 resolves the **first of the three remaining Medium** items from the 2026-06-24 gdp→Sysop backport assessment — a generic-win port of gdp's `_shared/main-push-guard.md` (gdp `66ef2a5f`), and the natural sibling of Phase 63. Phase 63 removed direct `main` writes from `/review-close`'s `pr` path; Phase 64 guards the HEAD-hijack race on **every remaining commit/push path**. The guard closes two races on any commit/push to `main` (or an integration branch destined for it) **from the shared primary worktree**: (1) **local HEAD-hijack** — git keeps one `HEAD` per worktree, so a concurrent Sysop loop (`/auto-claim`'s parallel batch, a separate `/claim-task` session) or a manual `git checkout` can move `HEAD` off the expected branch mid-flow and land commits on the wrong branch; (2) **remote autonomous writer** — on an unprotected `main` with GitHub auto-merge (Dependabot — Sysop's own `/pr-dependabot` standardizes this), `origin/main` advances at unpredictable times and a direct push can collide with a merge landed since the last fetch.

**The central adaptation: Rule B kept and reframed, not dropped.** The filed item recommended "drop or heavily caveat Rule B" (gdp's direct safe-push), reasoning that Sysop's *own* `main` is protected so a direct push can't work here. But that conflates the meta-repo with the **product**: Phase 63 ships `direct` as the **default** merge policy for unprotected-main consumers (BeanRider), and that `git push origin main` path had **zero** safe-push hardening (bare push + "confirm it succeeded", no fetch / no rebase-if-advanced / no exact-SHA verify). So Rule B is genuinely live for Sysop — **scoped to the `direct` merge policy** — as the canonical safe shape, not gdp's obsolete break-glass fallback. It is dormant for Sysop's own runs (which use `pr`) but load-bearing for `direct`-policy consumers, exactly where the autonomous-writer race bites. The three rules as shipped: **Rule A** (assert the branch before every commit/push; expected = `main` for direct/claim-flips, the integration branch under `pr`, and the inverted "not `main`" for `/document-work`'s feature push); **Rule B** (safe direct push, `direct` policy only); **Rule C** (never force-push `main` or an integration branch).

**Wiring beyond the filed scope (two extra sites, justified by the item's own premise).** The filing scoped "new file + `document-work` Step 5 + references from `review-close`," but its premise names `/auto-claim` + `/claim-task` as the same-race carriers — and line-level inspection confirmed both commit the `open → in_progress` claim-flip **on `main` from the shared primary worktree** (`/claim-task` Step 4d, `/auto-claim` Step 5.4, the latter in a parallel-batch loop). Shipping a guard that names them in its premise but doesn't protect them would be a half-measure, so both got a one-line Rule A assert (fix-on-the-spot rather than file-a-gap). Total: 5 consumer skills. `/review-close`'s pre-existing inline guard (the one that literally read *"a future phase extracts this into `_shared/main-push-guard.md`; until then it lives inline here"*) was replaced by a pointer to the now-extracted partial — Phase 64 **is** that future phase.

**Stripped from gdp** (genericness discipline): the ruleset ID `18084254`, the `pg8000` / dated-incident specifics (kept the incident *shape* as a generic failure example), the `run_ratchet_lint.sh` reference (generalized to "re-run review-close Step 3, the project's § Pre-merge verification commands"), the `operations.md` runbook pointer, and the entire `TECH-WADEFLOW-PR-ONLY-MAIN` migration preamble (gdp has fully moved to PR-only with no bypass; Sysop keeps the dual `direct`/`pr` model, so the preamble's premise is false here).

**Bundled backward-staleness fix (Phase-62-class catch).** While wiring the WORKFLOW.md §8.3 partials enumeration, the count read "**Three** partials are present" but **four** files already existed — `decomposition-rubric.md` (Phase 60b) was never added to the list. This is exactly the lost-referent staleness Phase 62's Step-2a backward sweep targets, surfaced here at the moment of editing. Fixed the count to **five** and added both the missing rubric bullet and the new guard.

**Verification.** Markdown-only (no executable path) → the full suite is the regression proof: **367 passed**, unchanged. A fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context) returned **SHIP WITH FIXES** — no blockers; all six findings applied. **S1** (the high-value catch): Rule B's final verify used strict equality (`origin/main == PUSHED_SHA`), which **false-positives on exactly the autonomous-merge race Rule B targets** — a Dependabot merge landing between the push and the confirming fetch fails strict equality even though the push landed cleanly; switched to containment (`git merge-base --is-ancestor "$PUSHED_SHA" origin/main`), which still catches a push that silently didn't land while tolerating a later autonomous merge. This corrects a latent bug gdp's original shipped too. **S2**: under `pr` policy the variable-persistence note recovers `$INTEGRATION_BRANCH` from `HEAD`, so `HEAD == $INTEGRATION_BRANCH` collapses to `HEAD == HEAD` — a tautology that silently disables the guard against the precise hijack it advertises (Phase 64's HARD RULE newly propagated that to all 4a–4c sites); fixed by asserting against the fixed `merge/review-close-*` **pattern** (HEAD-independent) in the HARD RULE, the Step 4d-pr block (where it doubles as a safe recovery of `$INTEGRATION_BRANCH`), and a guard's Rule A "dynamic expected-branch" note, plus a caveat in the variable-persistence note. Nits all applied: N1 (acknowledged in WORKFLOW.md that `main-push-guard` is the first partial to inline a short assert one-liner at its call sites while keeping the canonical *rules* in the partial), N2 ("review-close Step 3" instead of bare "Step 3" inside a numbered block), N3 (noted Rule B runs as one atomic shell block so the step-1 assert covers the step-4 push), N4 (table label `git push origin main` → "safe push to `main` (Rule B)").

**Test decision for this phase (58b discipline):** *"no test because the change is skill/process-doc markdown plus one shared partial with no executable code path — the bash snippets are runner-executed instructions, not a shipped script. Correctness (the Rule B git sequence, the HEAD-independent pr-policy assert, the direct-only scope claim) was verified out-of-band by the fresh-eyes adversarial pass; the unchanged 367-test suite confirms no regression."*

**Edits.** New `core/skills/_shared/main-push-guard.md`; `core/skills/review-close/SKILL.md` (HARD RULE 462 → pointer + pattern-assert; Step 4d `direct` → Rule B; Step 4d `pr` assert → pattern-guarded recovery; variable-persistence caveat); `core/skills/document-work/SKILL.md` (Step 5 inverted assert); `core/skills/claim-task/SKILL.md` (Step 4d Rule A); `core/skills/auto-claim/SKILL.md` (Step 5.4 Rule A); `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` (§8.3 partials enumeration: stale count fix + two new bullets + inline-exception clause). Markdown-only, no installer/manifest/test edit, no new permission rules (`_shared/` auto-ships via `install_skills()`). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; the Medium checklist item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). **Two of the four 2026-06-24 backport items now resolved (HIGH in Phase 63, this Medium in Phase 64); the model-sunset tooling + park-verdict-archive Medium items remain open.** Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge because `main` is protected — which also dogfoods Phase 63's `pr` path on a real protected-main repo (its one recommended-not-blocking validation).

## Phase 65a (executed 2026-06-26 — `/auto-claim` park-verdict central archive: the standalone data-loss fix)

Phase 65a resolves the **park-verdict-archive** Medium item (the third of the four 2026-06-24 backport items), porting only the standalone, telemetry-free slice of gdp `64e0ab80` and **declining the telemetry subsystem** the rest of that commit rides on. The gdp change had three parts: (1) a `parked_reason` field captured into a `task_outcome` JSONL telemetry event, (2) a central park-verdict archive that survives worktree cleanup, (3) an append-only overlap allowlist in `analyze_auto_claim.py`. Parts (1) and (3) are **blocked** — they layer on gdp's `TECH-AUTO-CLAIM-TELEMETRY` subsystem (`_shared/telemetry.md` + `analyze_auto_claim.py` + a JSONL event stream) that was never ported to Sysop, so there is no substrate to attach them to (porting that subsystem stays a separately-filed, recommended-**declined** Low-priority item). Part (2) is portable standalone and **fixes a real data-loss bug present in Sysop today.**

**The bug.** `/auto-claim` Phase 6d, on a `blocker` finding, parks the task and writes the plan-only agent's plan + the adversarial verdict to `$WORKTREE_PATH/.auto-claim/plan.md` + `review.md` — byte-for-byte gdp's pre-change shape, with an explicit "the orchestrator does NOT commit these files" note. That worktree scratch is the **only** record of why the task parked. A parked task is by definition resumed *later*, and `cleanup_worktrees.sh --force` removes the worktree wholesale (verified: the script's `--force` branch runs `git worktree remove --force` on every non-`MAIN` worktree and never touches the primary worktree). So the verdict the human needs to resume the task is destroyed exactly when they come back for it.

**The fix.** Phase 6d now mirrors the plan + verdict to a **project-root** archive at `.auto-claim/parked/<TASK_ID>__<timestamp>.md` — the project root is where the `/auto-claim` orchestrator runs (it claims on `main` from the primary worktree), so the archive outlives any worktree and survives `--force`. Step 8's resume guidance and the v1 success criteria now point at the durable copy when the worktree is already gone. **Adaptation from gdp:** gdp keyed the archive filename on `$CYCLE_ID` (a telemetry construct absent from Sysop); per the filed item's instruction this is replaced by a `date -u +%Y%m%dT%H%M%SZ` UTC timestamp — a task parks at most once per cycle and cycles run minutes apart, so `<TASK_ID>__<timestamp>` is unique per park. The archive carries the plan + verdict only; gdp's `## Park reason (one-line)` section and the `parked_reason`/`task_outcome` emit are **omitted** as the telemetry coupling we declined.

**Gitignore + the latent dirty-tree trap.** `.auto-claim/` joins `.locks/` and `.pending-docs/` in Sysop's own `.gitignore` and in WORKFLOW.md §8.6's runtime-directories table. This is not just hygiene: an un-ignored project-root `.auto-claim/` on a consumer's `main` would surface as untracked in `git status --porcelain` and trip `/review-close` Step 1a's "any porcelain line → dirty" classification — the same false-positive class as BeanRider ISSUE-0043 (`.venv` symlink). The §8.6 entry is the consumer's documented gitignore contract (Sysop's installer doesn't manage `.gitignore`, consistent with how `.locks/`/`.pending-docs/` are handled).

**Test decision for this phase (58b discipline):** *"no test because the change is skill-runner markdown (the bash snippet in Phase 6d is a runner-executed instruction the orchestrator substitutes real values into, not a shipped script) plus `.gitignore` + a WORKFLOW.md doc row. Correctness — that `cleanup_worktrees.sh --force` removes only non-main worktrees and leaves the project-root archive intact — was verified by reading the script; the unchanged 367-test suite confirms no regression."*

**Edits.** `core/skills/auto-claim/SKILL.md` (Phase 6d central-archive write + Step 8 resume note + v1 success-criteria line); `.gitignore` (`.auto-claim/`); `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` (§8.6 row). Markdown + gitignore only, no installer/manifest/test edit, no new permission rules. Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; the Medium checklist item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). **Three of the four 2026-06-24 backport items now resolved (HIGH=63, Medium=64, Medium=65a); only the model-sunset tooling remains — landing next as Phase 65b.** Part of the Phase 65 branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 65b (executed 2026-06-26 — model-sunset migration tooling: guard Sysop's own skill model pins)

Phase 65b resolves the **last** of the four 2026-06-24 backport items — gdp `5c25516b`'s model-sunset tooling, the one the assessment flagged as a "generic win" that fills a verified gap. Sysop ships **23 model pins** across 12 skill files (the `check_skill_models.py --list` count — *more* than the assessment's hand-grep estimate of "~17," which is itself the rationale: a hand-grep misses sites). Model aliases (`opus`/`sonnet`/`haiku`) are bare string literals the harness reads with no templating layer, so when Anthropic sunsets a model every pin for that tier must move — and the Fable sunset already proved a hand-grep-and-replace misses sites. This makes the next sunset mechanical.

**The two scripts (ported near-verbatim from gdp).** `migrate_skill_model.py` — tier-safe pin migrator (`--from/--to`, dry-run default, `--apply` writes); it keys **strictly** on `re.escape(from_alias)` so the other tiers are structurally untouchable (you cannot hit the wrong tier by construction), rewrites operative pins (whole-line frontmatter `model:` + inline quoted `model: "<alias>"`), and **flags** freeform prose mentions for human rewording rather than robo-editing English. `check_skill_models.py` — fails (exit 1) if any pin names an alias absent from the `served_models.txt` allowlist, reusing the migrator's `extract_model_pins`/`iter_skill_files` by import (no duplicate regex). New data file `core/companion/.claude/served_models.txt` lists the served aliases (`opus`/`sonnet`/`haiku`) with the sunset runbook in its header.

**The porting crux: dual-context path resolution.** Sysop companion scripts are written for the **installed** layout — at `<consumer>/scripts/foo.py`, `Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent` is the consumer repo root, so `REPO_ROOT/.claude/skills` + `REPO_ROOT/.claude/served_models.txt` are the installed skill tree + allowlist (matching gdp's defaults verbatim, and the `next_task.py`/`validate_tasks.py` convention). In the **Sysop source tree** the same expression resolves to `core/companion/` — which is exactly where the shipped `served_models.txt` lives (so the default allowlist resolves correctly here too), and the source-tree skills are reached with an explicit `--root core/skills`. Verified working in both contexts: a real scratch `install.sh` then `cd <target> && scripts/check_skill_models.py` (zero args) resolved `.claude/skills` + `.claude/served_models.txt` and passed; `--root core/skills` passes in-source.

**Adaptations from gdp (genericness discipline).** Paths `.claude/skills/` → `core/skills/` (via `--root`) and `scripts/` → `core/companion/scripts/`. **Dropped** gdp's `.claude/checks.yml` `argparse-without-shared-cli` exclude-list registration — that lint rule has no Sysop counterpart (removed at the Phase 45a port), so there was nothing to register. **Generalized** all gdp-perspective prose: the migrator's "do these by hand" checklist no longer names gdp's `feedback_subagent_model.md` memory file or says "Sysop keeps SEPARATE copies" (inverted correctly — Sysop is the *source*; consumers hold installed copies that pick up a migration on the next `sysop-update.sh`); `served_models.txt`'s tier comments read "the conventional Sysop tiers; a consumer may differ." **Did NOT port** the pin-value churn around the commit (gdp's opus→fable→opus flips) — Sysop already sits at the opus end-state; only the tooling was wanted.

**Delivery + wiring.** New `install_served_models()` in `install.sh` delivers `served_models.txt` to the consumer's `.claude/` (unconditional — model pins are stack-neutral, so all consumers get it; managed-overwrite via `copy_file`, the right call for an allowlist that must refresh on a sunset, with the Phase 8 divergence check warning before any consumer-edited copy is overwritten). The two scripts auto-ship via the existing `install_companion_scripts()` loop (no installer edit needed for them). pre-commit wiring is a new drop-in fragment `git-hooks/examples/pre-commit-model-pins.example` (modeled on the sibling `pre-commit-tasks-validate.example` — same git-common-dir→`.venv`→system-`python3` resolution, gated on staged `.claude/skills/` or `.claude/served_models.txt`), kept as its own fragment rather than crammed into the topically-mismatched `pre-commit-python.example`.

**The real CI value: a Sysop-own guard test.** Beyond porting gdp's 17 tests (11 migrate + 6 check), `tests/test_check_skill_models.py::test_sysop_own_skills_all_served` asserts every pin in Sysop's own `core/skills/` is served against the shipped `served_models.txt` — so a future edit that introduces a stale pin, or a sunset that updates the allowlist without migrating the skills, **goes red in Sysop's CI** (the pytest GHA workflow) before it can ship. This is the concrete answer to "the Fable sunset already missed sites." +1 more original test (`test_main_missing_allowlist_is_usage_error`) → **19 new tests, 386 passing** (was 367). The gdp tests' `APP_ENV`/`sys.path.insert` boilerplate was dropped (Sysop's `pyproject.toml` `pythonpath` + bare import); per-test classification in `tests/PORT_LOG.md`.

**Test decision for this phase (58b discipline):** *"tested — the two scripts are pure / `tmp_path`-testable with no DB or network, so they get real unit coverage (regex extraction, tier-safe migration, allowlist parsing, exit-code contracts) plus the Sysop-own CI guard. The `--apply` write branch is a thin `path.write_text` over the unit-tested `migrate_text` return; covered indirectly. Proven: 386 passing, plus a real scratch-`install.sh` smoke in both the installed and source-tree layouts."*

**Verification.** 386 tests green; scratch `install.sh` delivers `served_models.txt` + both scripts and the installed-layout check passes with default paths; `--update` re-delivers idempotently (managed-overwrite, no spurious divergence flag); a regex cross-check over `core/skills/` confirmed the extractor catches all 23 operative pins with zero misses/false-positives and the two prose alias-mentions are correctly flag-not-rewrite. **Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP** — no blockers, no should-fixes. Both NITs applied: (1) a caveat in `migrate_text` that `inline_quoted_re` rewrites any quoted from-alias (broader than `extract_model_pins`'s `model`-prefixed match — intrinsic to gdp's design, guarded by dry-run-default + the printed diff); (2) reworded the WORKFLOW.md §8.4 `check_skill_models.py` row so consumers aren't pointed at the Sysop-internal `tests/` (which the installer doesn't ship) as their CI hook. The reviewer's one **out-of-scope finding** — 5 shipped skills still reference gdp's private `feedback_subagent_model.md` (a pre-existing strip-class identifier leak, made visible *because* 65b's `served_models.txt` generalizes the same tier-rationale concept correctly) — was **filed** as a Low-priority identifier-scrub item rather than bundled here (the reviewer correctly scoped it separately).

**Edits.** New `core/companion/scripts/migrate_skill_model.py` + `check_skill_models.py`; new `core/companion/.claude/served_models.txt`; new `core/companion/git-hooks/examples/pre-commit-model-pins.example`; new `tests/test_migrate_skill_model.py` + `tests/test_check_skill_models.py`; `install.sh` (`install_served_models()` + pipeline wiring); `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` (§8.4 two rows). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; the Medium checklist item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). **All four 2026-06-24 gdp→Sysop backport items now resolved (HIGH=63, Medium=64, Medium=65a, Medium=65b) — the assessment is closed.** Landing as the second commit of the Phase 65 branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 66 (executed 2026-06-26 — strip the `feedback_subagent_model.md` identifier leak from shipped skills)

Phase 66 closes the Low-priority strip-class identifier leak that Phase 65b's fresh-eyes reviewer surfaced and deliberately filed out-of-scope. Six references across five shipped skill files (`review-close`, `auto-review` ×2, `auto-judge`, `codebase-review`, `security-audit`) justified their `model: "opus"` pin with the phrase "per `feedback_subagent_model.md`" — gdp's *private* memory file, which exists only in the original author's local store and is never delivered by the bash installer or the plugin. A consumer reading an installed skill therefore hit a dangling reference to a file they cannot see. Same strip-class as the internal-identifier leaks the 2026-06-22 sterilization pass caught (a hardcoded prod-DB name and an internal batch ID); missed by the Phase 2I scrub because it lives in model-rationale prose, not a path.

**The fix is a pointer swap, not a deletion.** Phase 65b's own new `core/companion/.claude/served_models.txt` (delivered to every consumer via `install_served_models()`) already carries the generalized form of exactly this rationale — its **Tier semantics** block: `opus — adversarial-review / audit / judge tier + review-skill frontmatter`; `sonnet — cheap mechanical tier (e.g. auto-review fix agents)`. Each reference was reworded "per `feedback_subagent_model.md`" → "per the served-models tier semantics (`.claude/served_models.txt`)" — a **consumer-relative** path (no leading slash) that resolves in the installed layout; citing the source-tree `core/companion/.claude/...` path would have been a *new* leak of the same class (that path doesn't exist in a consumer checkout). The pins themselves never changed — only their justification pointer. The negative case (auto-review's "Opus is *reserved* for adversarial review; do NOT set it on these mechanical fix agents") points just as cleanly, because `served_models.txt` literally names `auto-review fix agents` as the sonnet example.

**Scope discipline.** The strip is confined to shipped content. A repo-wide grep confirms `core/` + `packs/` are now 100% clean of `feedback_subagent_model`; the four remaining hits are all meta-repo narrative (`CLAUDE.md`, `PHASE_LOG.md`, `REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`, `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`) that *describe* the 65b decision and this filing — accurate history, not consumer-facing, and not delivered by the installer (only `core/`/`packs/` ship).

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix.** The CLAUDE.md Phase-log table and the REVIEW_CHECKLIST Phase-completion-log table both still carried `_squash-merge pending_` in the Commit column for Phases 64/65a/65b — stale since those landed via PR #5 (`49598a2`) and PR #6 (`6c2e47e`, the squashed 65a+65b). Filled in the six cells (three per table) with the real merge commits.

**Test decision for this phase (58b discipline):** *"no test because the change is six one-line prose rewordings in skill-runner markdown (plus six phase-log table cells) — no executable path. Correctness was verified mechanically: a repo-wide `grep` confirms zero `feedback_subagent_model` references survive in shipped `core/`/`packs/` content, `check_skill_models.py --root core/skills` still exits 0 (all 23 pins served — the prose change doesn't touch the pins), and the unchanged 386-test suite confirms no regression."*

**Edits.** `core/skills/{review-close,auto-review,auto-judge,codebase-review,security-audit}/SKILL.md` (6 references → generalized pointer); `CLAUDE.md` + `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` (6 stale phase-log Commit cells). Markdown-only, **386 tests green** (unchanged); no installer/manifest/test/permission edit. Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): **SHIP**, no blockers/should-fixes — NIT 1 applied (review-close nested-parens `))` → "in `.claude/served_models.txt`)"); NIT 2 (a pre-existing tension between auto-review's "use the default model" and `served_models.txt`'s "sonnet … pinned not inherited", made newly discoverable by the reword) **filed** as a Low-priority follow-up rather than bundled — the reviewer correctly scoped it as a behavioral-reconciliation concern, not part of this cosmetic strip. Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; the Low-priority leak item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 67 (executed 2026-06-26 — convention-demotion Tier 2: the FP-driven retirement loop)

Phase 67 builds **Tier 2** of the convention-demotion plan, closing the long-open Medium item ("Sysop has a richly-instrumented promotion pipeline and zero symmetric demotion pipeline — conventions can only enter the maps, never leave"). Tier 1 (Phase 62) shipped the *static* detection half — a backward map-staleness sweep at Step 2a that flags map sections whose glob matches no file (removed category) and bullets citing a deleted helper (dead reference). Tier 2 is the *behavioral* half: it retires the **blocking-mechanical rules** (`checks.yml` regexes, `semgrep` rules, `pre-commit` letters) whose false-positive cost the map sweep cannot see — the rules that keep halting commits on things that are no longer violations because the underlying convention moved (a default changed, a category migrated, a dependency bump mooted the check). That stale-blocking-rule cost — each FP recurs on every touch of the scoped code, and the second-order cost is alert fatigue → a `--no-verify` suppression reflex that erodes the whole gate — is the user's actual pain the spec named. Tier 3 (periodic prose-relevance + dependabot-hooked version re-confirmation, for the no-static-signal change events) stays explicitly don't-build, so **the whole demotion item now resolves**.

**The asymmetry the design had to solve.** Promotion's cross-round gate is *computable* because a true positive becomes a durable task in `review_tasks.md` — recurrence is recomputed from that record each round, "compute over maintain," no carried-forward watch-list. A *stale* positive becomes **nothing**: the runner triages a prescan hit, judges it a non-violation, and the verdict is discarded. So demotion's signal — "this rule keeps firing on non-violations" — has no durable home unless one is made. That is the exact gap the spec identified ("demotion's gate needs a per-rule fire ledger Sysop doesn't keep").

**The build (prose-only mirror of the promotion machinery, + one regression test).**
- **Capture (both skills' Step 2b triage):** when a mechanical-rule hit is judged a *systemic* stale-FP — the rule is moot, not a one-off legitimate exception (which stays a baseline/`# nosemgrep` matter) — record a **stale-verdict**. Tier-1-class anti-FP guards: "rule moot vs. instance exception," "when you cannot tell, do not record," and (security skill) "confirm the protection moved, not vanished."
- **Ledger (new Step 5e):** a single `## Convention fire ledger` section in `review_tasks.md`, `| Round | Rule ID | Mechanism | Verdict | Why |`, one row per (rule, round). **Placement is load-bearing:** the section sits *outside* every `## Round` block, because `archive_review_tasks.py` relocates only `## Round` batch blocks — a per-round subsection would be silently dropped on archival (`build_archive_block` copies only header + batches), a BeanRider-class data-loss bug. A standalone bottom-of-file section bounds every round range, so the archiver never touches it. The ledger is a *maintained accumulator* (the one principled asymmetry vs. promotion's recompute — disclosed honestly in WORKFLOW §3.5b), bounded because every Step 9b disposition clears the adjudicated rule's rows.
- **Decision (new Step 9b: Convention Demotion, Interactive):** runs **every round, independently of Step 9** (Step 9 fires only on promotion candidates — folding demotion there would skip it on quiet rounds, the exact reasoning that put Tier 1 at Step 2a). Recompute per-rule stale-verdict recurrence; a rule stale in **2+ distinct rounds** (exact mirror of promotion's cross-round survival gate) → prompt `[retire / demote-to-advisory / tighten / keep]`. Retire removes the rule + its convention-map reminder; demote-to-advisory flips `blocking: true → false` (de-fangs the halt, keeps the signal — the lower-regret middle); tighten narrows an over-broad-from-birth rule (Mode G); keep overrides. Every disposition clears the rule's ledger rows (bounds the ledger; prevents a "keep" re-prompting forever). Emits a `Demotion summary: <N> retired` trailer, grep-auditable via `git log --grep "Demotion summary"`, mirroring `Promotion summary:`.
- **WORKFLOW.md:** new **§3.5b Convention demotion lifecycle** (the canonical spec, mirroring §3.5's depth: change-event taxonomy A–G, the capture→ledger→gate→decision→trailer pipeline, the principled-asymmetry and cost-concentration rationale blocks); §3.6 check 4, §5.1, §5.3, and §2.5/§2.6 updated from "Tier 2 designed, not yet built" to "now active." `docs/workflow.html`'s convention-rot explainer corrected likewise.
- **One regression test** (`test_archive_leaves_convention_fire_ledger_in_place`): proves the archiver leaves a `## Convention fire ledger` section intact (round range stops at the first following `## ` section; ledger neither moved to the archive nor deleted with the round) over the realistic `## Round` → `## Statistics` → `## Convention fire ledger` layout. The archiver itself is **unmodified** — the test locks the placement contract Step 5e/9b depend on. **387 tests green** (was 386).

**Decision ratified (via `AskUserQuestion`):** ledger lives **in `review_tasks.md`** (not a new dedicated file) — true mirror of how promotion recomputes from the review record, zero new artifact to bootstrap/install/archive. The build refined "per-round subsection" → "standalone section" once the archiver read proved per-round subsections would be dropped (same choice, archiver-safe realization).

**Test decision for this phase (58b discipline):** *"tested where there is an executable contract, prose elsewhere. The skill/WORKFLOW changes are runner-executed markdown (no code path) — the unchanged-then-+1 suite is the regression proof. The single new behavioral claim with a code dependency — that the archiver preserves the out-of-round ledger section — IS tested (`test_archive_leaves_convention_fire_ledger_in_place`), because it's a real integration assumption that a future archiver change could silently break (data loss). The archiver was not modified, so no other code test applies."*

**Edits.** `core/skills/codebase-review/SKILL.md` + `core/skills/security-audit/SKILL.md` (Step 2b capture + Step 5e ledger + Step 9b demotion + Step 2a routing note now-built); `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` (§3.5b + §3.6/§5.1/§5.3/§2.5/§2.6 updates); `docs/workflow.html` (rot-explainer corrected); `tests/test_archive_review_tasks.py` (+1 regression lock). **387 tests green.** Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): **SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — all 5 should-fixes applied: **SF1** (Tier-1→Step 9b hand-off was a dead end for *pure-prose* removed-category retirement — no ledger row, no decision venue → added an un-gated static-candidate clause to Step 9b step 1 in both skills, bypassing the 2+-round gate since a zero-match section is already unambiguous), **SF2** (`docs/workflow.html` still said FP-driven demotion was "spec'd rather than built" — a Phase-62-class staleness miss, corrected), **SF3** (codebase-review Step 9b cited a "Step 2a-4 security caveat" that exists only in security-audit's 2a-3 — a mirror-copy artifact, reworded), **SF4** (§3.5b/§5.1 cited non-existent "§2.5/§2.6 step 2b/9b" sub-steps → added a demotion clause to §2.5 step 9 / §2.6 step 5 and repointed the refs at the review skills' steps), **SF5** (test mislabeled "Phase 66" — it's 67); NITs N1 (shared-ledger note parity) / N2 (trailer counts retirements only, clarified) / N3 (test extended to the realistic Statistics+ledger layout) applied; N4 (the ≥2-round gate vs. the spec's loose "~3" — a deliberate exact-mirror reconciliation) noted, no change. **Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 66's own `_squash-merge pending_` cell in both phase-log tables with its merge commit (`6480692` #7). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; the Medium demotion item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md) (Tier 1 ✓ P62 + Tier 2 ✓ P67 + Tier 3 don't-build = item closed). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Rename round 1 (executed 2026-06-26 — `wade-flow` → `jig`)

> Section added by Phase 116 (2026-07-16). ## Phase 68 (executed 2026-06-26 — `run_checks/` package backport + `_log.py` single-source decision)

Phase 68 closes the Medium **"fresh-consumer correctness bug"** filed from the BeanRider `119279c→877e0b1` reconciliation, and resolves the entangled `_log.py` factoring decision the user chose to settle in the same phase ("All four + resolve `_log.py` now"). The `run_checks/` package — invoked in production via `run_checks.sh` → the 71-line `run_checks_impl.py` re-export shim → the package (Phase 49 split) — is what every package-first consumer actually runs. But sysop HEAD's package lacked four fixes BeanRider's preserved 937-line monolith carries (BR diagnosed them in `tasks/open/TECH-0005.md` + `SYSOP_ISSUES.md § ISSUE-0045`, commit `5ea6029`). BeanRider deliberately kept its monolith (TECH-0005's port-then-swap sequencing), so the bug is invisible in the one live consumer but ships to the next.

**The crux (fix #1 — PyYAML `safe_load`).** `config.py::parse_checks_yml` hand-rolled a line-by-line parser that only understood inline `["a", "b"]` lists. A block-style list —

```yaml
paths:
  - src/api/
  - src/core/
```

— set `paths` to the empty string `""` (the `:`-partition fell through to the plain-string branch) and then **silently skipped** each `- src/...` continuation line (the parser excluded lines starting with `-`). So every grep check using a block-style `paths:` was disabled with **no error and no finding** — a latent correctness bug for any consumer authoring block-style lists. BeanRider escaped it only because its `checks.yml` happens to be 100% inline `paths: [a, b]` (22 inline, 0 block → finding parity held 44==44). The fix replaces the hand-rolled parser with `yaml.safe_load` (the established `validate_tasks.py` house-style import guard: `try: import yaml / except ImportError: …; sys.exit(2)`). `_validate_check` flips from line-number- to index-based addressing and gains the **list-shape assertion** that is the other half of the fix: a `paths:`/`include`/`exclude`/`used_by` that arrives as a scalar (e.g. a misindentation collapsing a block list) now noisy-fails with a `ValueError` instead of silently no-opping. Proven end-to-end at the real shim entry point: a scratch block-style check that produced 0 findings under the old parser now fires `[no-eval-block] HIGH src/api/danger.py:1`.

**Fixes #2–#4.** **#2 `_sanitize_log`** (ANSI/control-char strip on exception interpolation) is applied at every exception-interpolation print site in the package — `lint.py:73` (the `FrontendDirAmbiguous` handler, the site BR's own `[semgrep-sanitize-exception-interp]` self-finding names), `cli.py`'s two `warn: check … failed` sites, `coverage.py`'s defensive handler, and the new `grep.py` warn. (sysop does **not** ship the `sanitize-exception-interp` semgrep rule — that's a BR-side convention — so #2 here is single-sourcing + convention-consistency hygiene, not clearing a sysop-shipped self-finding.) **#3 `_classify_checks(checks, active_token=None)`** is a new shared helper in `cli.py` that buckets checks by id-prefix, feeding **both** the `--mode` path and the previously-duplicated `--update-baseline` path. The central adaptation: BR's monolith `_classify_checks` returns only `(grep, lsp, semgrep, blocking)` — it predates sysop's lint/pip-audit/coverage stages — so porting it verbatim would have **silently dropped** the eslint/pip-audit/coverage classification. The sysop helper returns a **7-tuple** `(grep_checks, lsp_ids, semgrep_ids, lint_ids, pip_audit_ids, coverage_checks, blocking_ids)` covering all six stages (coverage returns full dicts because `_run_coverage` needs `critical_path`/`report`). **#4 grep `rc >= 2`** (a real grep error — unreadable file, malformed regex — vs. `1` = no-match) now surfaces a sanitized `warn: grep failed (rc=…)` line instead of being swallowed behind a clean "0 findings."

**The `_log.py` decision — resolved (path a: ship the module).** New `core/companion/scripts/_log.py` is the single source of truth for `_sanitize_log`. The package modules + `backfill_completed_dates.py` import it (`from _log import _sanitize_log`, which binds the name into each module namespace so the existing `bcd._sanitize_log` test-patch path keeps resolving). `validate_tasks.py` and `next_task.py` **keep their inline copies on purpose** — BR's deliberate carve-out, because both run from the pre-commit hook before the project venv (and a reliable `sys.path`) is wired up, so they must stay standalone. The import invariant — `from _log import _sanitize_log` resolves because `_log.py` sits beside the `run_checks/` package and is therefore importable wherever the package is — was verified empirically in **all four** contexts: the production shim (`python3 scripts/run_checks_impl.py`, script-dir = `sys.path[0]`), `python -m run_checks` from the scripts dir, `python -m run_checks` from a foreign cwd via `PYTHONPATH=scripts` (the case where cwd ≠ package dir), and pytest (`pythonpath = ["core/companion/scripts", "scripts"]`). `_log.py` is a depth-1 file under `core/companion/scripts/`, so `install_companion_scripts` auto-ships it — no installer or manifest edit. Verified by a real `install.sh` round-trip: `_log.py` lands in the consumer's `scripts/`, `backfill`'s inline def is gone, and the installed package reports `config._sanitize_log is _log._sanitize_log` → `True`.

**Deliberately scoped OUT (documented boundaries).** (a) The **atomic-rewrite / defensive-parse** wins for `backfill_completed_dates.py` + `archive_review_tasks.py` (the separate archive/backfill Medium item) — a distinct *durability* axis, not the *dedup* axis the `_log.py` decision settles; folding it in would balloon the phase with two scripts' worth of atomic-write logic + tests. That item shrinks to "atomic-rewrite + defensive-parse only; `_log` decision done, `backfill` migrated." `archive_review_tasks.py` is untouched (it has no `_sanitize_log` today — it gains one only with that backport). (b) BR's **additional "no valid `paths:` exist" run_grep warn** — it would fire on every check on a fresh install with un-substituted placeholder paths (`<api module>/`), regressing sysop's deliberate quiet-on-placeholders behavior (Phase 5). Only the `rc >= 2` half of BR's run_grep change is fix #4.

**Behavior-preservation of the `_classify_checks` refactor.** The old main path ran `run_check` on every mode-filtered check (relying on `run_check` to no-op the stage-prefixed ones that lack a `pattern:`); the new path runs `run_check` on grep-bucketed checks only. Findings, the `blocking_ids` set, the "No checks found" early-exit, and the summary `total_checks` count are all equivalent — verified, and the reviewer independently scanned all six shipped fragments to confirm no stage-prefixed check also carries a `pattern:`/`position_check:` (the one case that could diverge). The `--update-baseline` path's Phase 61b coverage carve-out (coverage findings never baseline) is preserved verbatim; round-trip smoke confirmed exit 1 (blocking) → write → exit 0 (baseline-suppressed).

**Tests.** New `tests/test_run_checks_yaml_parser.py` (+19) locks all four fixes at the package boundary: the block-style→list regression (proven non-tautological — the reviewer confirmed the old hand-rolled parser yields `paths=""` so reintroducing it fails this test), inline-still-works, mixed shapes, the real shipped core-fragment parse, the stricter-validation error paths, `_sanitize_log` single-source identity (`is`), the six-bucket `_classify_checks` contract incl. `active_token` filtering + blocking-across-buckets, and the grep `rc 0/1/≥2` warn behavior. **407 green** (was 387).

**Test decision for this phase (58b discipline):** *"this is a code change with executable contracts, so it is tested directly, not via the prose-mirror route. Every one of the four fixes has a boundary test that would red on regression; the crux (block-style→list) is proven non-tautological against the old parser's actual output; the refactor's behavior-preservation is proven by the unchanged 387 + the update-baseline round-trip smoke. The reviewer's SF1 added the one missing executable lock — the assembled-file single-`checks:` invariant `safe_load` now depends on."*

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers. **SF1** — the PyYAML switch removed the old structure-blind parser's *immunity* to a malformed assembly with duplicate top-level `checks:` keys (on dup keys `safe_load` silently keeps only the last mapping → would drop every fragment but the last, e.g. the whole core fragment, with no crash and no failing test). The assembly is correct today (`strip_yaml_leader` strips every fragment's `checks:` leader after the first — verified: the real 4-pack install yields exactly one `checks:` and all fragments survive), but the fix removed the safety net without a lock → added `tests/test_install_concat.py::test_assembled_file_has_one_checks_key_per_fragment_survives`, asserting exactly one `checks:` leader AND that both a core-fragment-only id (`todo-vs-deferred`, first) and a pack id (`logger-fstring`, later) survive — so a future `strip_yaml_leader` regression fails loudly here instead of silently disabling checks. **NIT 2** — stale `cli.py` module docstring still claimed "(no PyYAML dependency)"; corrected to "via PyYAML's safe_load." Both applied → **407 green**.

**Edits.** New `core/companion/scripts/_log.py`; `core/companion/scripts/backfill_completed_dates.py` (drop inline `_sanitize_log` → import `_log`); `core/companion/scripts/run_checks/{config,grep,lint,coverage,cli}.py`; `core/companion/scripts/run_checks_impl.py` (shim re-exports `_classify_checks`); new `tests/test_run_checks_yaml_parser.py` (+19); `tests/test_install_concat.py` (+1 SF1 lock). **407 tests green** (was 387). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; the Medium correctness item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md), and BR's TECH-0005 now shrinks to "adopt the shim" (its steps 1 — port the four fixes — are now upstream). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 69 (executed 2026-06-29 — model roles: role→model indirection so the workflow scales to better models)

Phase 69 answers the user's launch-prep concern — *"we need to be able to scale with better models… make it easy to select which model does what"* — surfaced by the Fable 5 glimpse that forced a hand-sweep of every Opus pin. It promotes Sysop's **implicit** three-tier convention (the `served_models.txt` comment already named opus/sonnet/haiku tiers) into a **first-class role→model config**, and closes two filed items in one phase: the long-deferred **"User-configurable model selection"** (`REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`, filed 2026-05-15, deferred "until public visibility" — now arrived) and the Phase-66-filed **auto-review "use the default model" vs. "pinned not inherited" contradiction**.

**The reframe.** Before Phase 69 the role and the model were the *same string*: `opus` meant both "the deep-reasoning tier" and "claude-opus-4-8." That conflation is exactly what made the Fable scare painful — and the Phase 65b migrator only made the rewrite *mechanical*, not *unnecessary*. The fix separates a stable **role** (the thing a skill pins) from a swappable **model** (what a config maps it to). The user's "roles" instinct beat the filed item's per-skill granularity: three roles (**`reasoning`** / **`mechanical`** / **`quick`**) capture N cases, vs. N per-skill knobs. Role names deliberately are **not** model names — "opus-as-a-role-label" is the trap.

**The constraint that shaped the mechanism.** A `claude-code-guide` probe confirmed the harness reads the skill-frontmatter `model:` field **literally** (a trailing `# comment` on that line is undocumented/risky), and — the load-bearing find — that the field *already* accepts full ids, Bedrock ARNs, Vertex names, and meta-values (`best`/`inherit`/`opusplan`). So (a) the role binding rides in a **body HTML-comment marker** the parser never sees, not in frontmatter; and (b) the harness is *already* provider-capable — Sysop treats a role's value as an opaque string, so the format is provider-neutral for free. Because the harness has no templating layer, role→model resolution happens at **install/update time** via the substitution layer the installer already owns (Phase 25/55), not at runtime.

**The mechanism.** `core/companion/.claude/served_models.txt` → `served_models.yml` (`git mv`), now `roles:` (reasoning→opus, mechanical→sonnet, quick→haiku) + `served:` (the allowlist that makes a sunset loud). Skills carry a file-level marker `<!-- sysop:model-roles frontmatter=<role> inline=<role> -->` after the closing `---`, with an optional trailing `<!-- sysop:role=<role> -->` per-pin override for a mixed-role file. `_model_roles.py` (shared primitives: marker parse, config load+merge, `resolve_text`, `find_role_violations`) backs both `resolve_skill_models.py` (the install/update-time rewriter, wired into `run_install_pipeline` after skills+scripts+config are present) and the rewritten `check_skill_models.py` (the role guard). **Under the default mapping the resolver is a byte-for-byte no-op** (reasoning→opus is already the shipped literal), so a default install does not diverge from source; it does real work only when a consumer remaps a role. A consumer's picks go in **`served_models.local.yml`** — never overwritten by Sysop, layered on top (local wins), so sunset fixes to the Sysop-owned defaults keep flowing (the established `checks.yml`/`.project.yml` split). A structural error (undefined role) makes the resolver write **nothing** — skills keep shipped defaults, so it can only degrade gracefully.

**The mixed-role file + the `:48` resolution.** `/auto-review` is the one file with two roles: the fix agents (mechanical) and the verification pass (reasoning). The fix agents' old prose — "Do **NOT** set `model: "opus"` — use the default model" — *was* the filed contradiction; Phase 69 makes them the explicit **`mechanical`** role (default `sonnet`, configurable), aligning the skill with `served_models`'s already-documented "pinned not inherited" intent. The behavior delta is neutral-or-cheaper (on an Opus session the fix agents move opus→sonnet, which the prose already wanted; on a Sonnet session, identical), and a consumer who prefers cost-follows-session sets `mechanical: inherit` locally. The verification pass stays `reasoning`→opus via the file default; the per-pin marker overrides only the fix-agent line.

**Tooling shift.** `check_skill_models.py` evolves from "is this literal in the allowlist?" to three role checks (un-roled pin / undefined role / role resolves to a non-served model — the last is the loud-sunset signal: drop a model from `served:` and any role still mapped to it goes red). `migrate_skill_model.py` is demoted to the **rare** role-vocabulary-change path — the common sunset is now a one-line `served_models.yml` edit, not a tree sweep.

**Decisions ratified (via `AskUserQuestion`).** (1) **Scope:** build the role layer Claude-only now but make the config format provider-neutral (role values opaque) — opening to other providers is a later data change, not a redesign; full multi-provider wiring deferred. (2) **Interview skill:** deferred — config + default first, matching Sysop's spine-before-ergonomics convention (intake 60a→60b); a `/configure-models` interview (or a single install-picker prompt) is a thin later layer, valuable only for the overriding consumer. (3) **Config home:** evolve `served_models.txt` (already the tier-semantics source) into the role map, rather than a new file or a Claude-Code-coupled `settings.json` block. (4) **Role names:** `reasoning`/`mechanical`/`quick` (user-picked over `deep`/`fix`/`trivial`).

**Test decision (58b discipline):** *this is a code change with executable contracts (resolver, checker, parsers, install pipeline), so it is tested directly. The load-bearing guarantees each have a lock: default config is a byte-for-byte no-op (zero divergence), a remap rewrites, the mixed-role file resolves per-pin, the resolver is idempotent and accepts full ids, a structural error writes nothing, the three guard failure modes each fire, local override layers, and a real `install.sh` round-trip resolves a pre-seeded override at install time. The renamed CI guard `test_sysop_own_skills_all_roles_served` runs the real check against `core/skills` + the shipped config — red on any un-roled/undefined/sunset pin.*

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers. **SF1** — the `served_models.yml` override *example* itself failed the guard: it remapped `mechanical: inherit` but omitted `inherit` from `served:` (meta-values are not exempt — the resolver writes `inherit` happily but the checker requires it in `served:`), so a consumer copy-pasting it verbatim got a red `check_skill_models.py` on first try; fixed the example (+ a `test_meta_value_is_not_exempt_from_served` regression locking that meta-values must be served, no special cases — the provider-neutral choice). **SF2** — the Phase 8 `--update` divergence net false-fired for override consumers: `reconstruct_old_install` ran the OLD installer against a fresh shadow that never received the consumer's `served_models.local.yml`, so the shadow resolved with the *default* mapping and every role-overridden skill was misreported as a committed local edit (non-destructive — skills are re-copied + re-resolved — but it undermined the safety net for exactly the customizing consumers this phase serves); fixed by seeding the consumer's `served_models.local.yml` into the shadow before the OLD installer runs, so it resolves identically (preserves genuine-edit detection, unlike blanket-skipping skills). **N1** (broad inline value regex over-match footgun → added the caveat `migrate` already carries) and **N2** (PyYAML-absent skip silently dropping an override → the skip note now warns loudly when a `served_models.local.yml` is present) applied; **N3** (a `PORT_LOG.md` historical `served_models.txt` reference — accurate as Phase-65b history) left as-is. The reviewer verified no `served_models.txt` survives in shipped content, the `_shared/adversarial-review.md` marker sits outside the verbatim-copied Prompt Template, and all 23 source pins resolve to served. **435 green** (was 407).

**Edits.** `git mv served_models.txt → .yml` (+ rewrite to roles+served+override doc); new `core/companion/scripts/{_model_roles,resolve_skill_models}.py`; rewritten `check_skill_models.py`; demoted `migrate_skill_model.py` (docstring/paths); markers in 12 skill files (`_shared/adversarial-review.md` + 11 SKILL.md), with auto-review's fix-agent prose reworked to the mechanical role; `install.sh` (served_models `.txt`→`.yml`; new `resolve_skill_models` pipeline step; SF2 shadow-seed; N2 skip-note); `pre-commit-model-pins.example` (role framing + PyYAML caveat + broadened path watch); `WORKFLOW.md` (script-table rows + a Model-roles note); `tests/PORT_LOG.md` (Phase 69 supersession block); new `tests/{test_model_roles,test_resolve_skill_models,test_install_model_roles}.py` + rewritten `tests/test_check_skill_models.py`. **435 tests green** (was 407). Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; items `:94` (User-configurable model selection) and `:48` (auto-review contradiction) moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). **Deferred (recommended, non-blocking):** the `/configure-models` interview skill and real multi-provider wiring (the format is ready). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

---

## Phase 70 (executed 2026-07-06 — `/roadmap`: a read-side queue-strategy skill, the "what's left, and in what order?" front door)

Phase 70 builds `/roadmap`, closing the Medium item filed 2026-07-06 during the tester-round-prep workflow-gap evaluation. It is the launch-prep answer to a recurring lived pattern: Wade repeatedly steps out of execution and asks, in plain chat, *"what's still outstanding in the roadmap?"* — and consistently wants the same shape back: the outstanding work grouped by kind, plus a proposed order of attack, ideally two or three alternative paths depending on what's prioritized. By Sysop's own promotion logic (a recurring pattern → promote it), that request is over the gate.

**The gap is structural, not a `/sitrep` deficiency.** Sysop had four skills that touch the queue, and none read it back at portfolio level. `/sitrep` is deliberately *execution-state* — a deterministic lifecycle classification of the *active* artifacts (locks, worktrees, branches, review batches) plus one routing recommendation, a fixed contract you can trust reflexively on cold resume. `/next-task` is a deterministic single-task resolver. `/intake` *writes* the queue. What nothing did was answer "where does the project stand against its `vision.md`, what's open by category, what are the `user_action` tasks waiting on me for, and what's a sensible order to attack it?" That was ad-hoc chat — the exact demo beat between `/intake` (the queue now exists) and `/auto-claim` (execute it).

**Why a new skill, not a `/sitrep` flag.** `/sitrep`'s value is precisely its *mechanical* classification — folding judgment (grouping, ordering, trade-offs) into it would blur the contract that makes it safe to invoke without wondering "did that just do something?" So `/roadmap` is a **sibling, not folded in**: the judgment layer over the backlog, where `/sitrep` is the deterministic layer over the in-flight work. They **compose** — `/roadmap --in-flight` overlays `/sitrep`'s survey — without merging.

**What it reads and produces.** `/roadmap` reads `tasks/index.yml` and the Phase-60a intent layer (`tasks/vision.md`, `tasks/decisions.md`), tolerating absence (a consumer may have run `install.sh` but not `/intake` — empty queue routes to `/intake`; missing vision drops the "against its vision" framing). It carries the read-only structural guard (`disallowed-tools: Edit, Write, NotebookEdit`, Phase 54) and the **`reasoning`** model role (Phase 69 marker; it's judgment work like `/intake`, not a deterministic printer like `/next-task`). The base path is **pure `Read`** — no scripts, no git — so it needs **no new permission rules** and runs on any agent, including bash-installer/non-Claude consumers. Output is three blocks: **Standing** (phase K of M vs the v1 done-definition; status buckets that partition, readiness sub-counts that are orthogonal), **Outstanding work grouped by kind** (derived from the ID-prefix vocabulary actually present — `FEAT-`→feature, `DATA-`→data-ops, `TECH-`→infra, etc.) with per-task **readiness flags** (🔒 `user_action` / ⏸ `on_hold_until` / ⛔ dep-blocked / ▶ in-flight / ✅ ready), and **1–3 proposed orderings**.

**The three orderings** are the distinctive output — not one "correct" order but the genuinely different paths, each with the trade-off that makes it the right pick, computed from real schema signals and **presented only when materially distinct** (never padded to three): **unblock-the-human-first** (lead with `user_action` tasks so the human clears credentials/console while agents work the rest — dropped entirely when the queue has none), **foundation-first** (a topological order over `depends_on`, tie-broken toward higher `blast_radius` and higher unlock-count — builds the base before what sits on it), and **ship-fast** (lowest `effort` first — land a visible win). The `--in-flight` flag makes one Bash-tool call (`python3 scripts/sitrep_survey.py --json`, the same survey `/sitrep` runs) to reconcile the strategy view against live execution reality; it reuses only the survey-script allow-rule and degrades to the index-only view when absent.

**Delivery.** The new `core/skills/roadmap/` directory **auto-ships** via the existing `install_skills()` directory glob — no `install.sh`, `marketplace.json`, or `plugin.json` edit. The Phase 69 resolver leaves the skill **byte-for-byte identical** at install time (the `reasoning`→`opus` default is a no-op). Two doc surfaces gained `/roadmap` beside `/sitrep`: the "Navigating the queue: helper skills" list in `WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md`, and the skill→reads/writes table in `tasks/README.md`. `WORKFLOW.md` § 8.3's skill table was left alone deliberately — it's the curated core-loop subset (`/sitrep` and `/intake` aren't in it either), so forcing `/roadmap` in would be inconsistent.

**Verification & dogfood.** Markdown-only, so the existing suite is the regression proof: **435 tests green** (unchanged; the Phase-69 role-guard CI test `test_sysop_own_skills_all_roles_served` accepts the new roled skill). The role guard passes over both the source tree and a real scratch `install.sh` target, where the diff confirms the resolver no-op. The skill's *logic* was dogfooded against BeanRider's real `tasks/index.yml` (a throwaway trace mimicking the skill's field reads + grouping + ordering): every field parses, kind-grouping works on real `FEAT-`/`TECH-` prefixes, readiness flags are correct, and the orderings compute — including the real "collapse when not materially distinct" case (BeanRider's queue has no dependency structure, so foundation-first ≈ ship-fast, exactly what the skill tells the runner to detect). The output it would produce is genuinely useful: *all three agent-ready tasks are `TECH-`; the two `FEAT-` tasks are 🔒 blocked on the human* (folder-scan needs a real folder, Coinbase needs a research PDF).

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — all four should-fixes applied, all real correctness gaps the BeanRider trace couldn't surface (its queue had no cycles, no deferred-deps-of-open-tasks, and every task carried `blast_radius`):
- **SF1** — "topological order" had no cycle guard, and the reviewer confirmed `validate_tasks.py` Invariant 6 is reference-integrity only with **no cycle detection**, so a fully-valid `index.yml` can hide an A→B→A cycle over which a topological sort is undefined. Added a detect-and-surface-as-data-defect clause (don't emit a broken order; flag the inconsistency; order only the acyclic remainder).
- **SF2** — `blast_radius` is *optional* at `schema_version: 1`, which is what `install.sh` ships, and the skill leaned on it three times with no fallback. Added explicit render-only-when-present + order-on-`effort`-alone-when-absent handling.
- **SF3** — a `deferred` dependency was silently treated as satisfied (neither `open` nor `in_progress`, so it failed the dep-blocked test and got flagged ✅ ready even though its prerequisite is parked). Now only a `done` dependency counts as met; a `deferred` prereq blocks.
- **SF4** (+ **N1**) — the `--in-flight` permission block claimed parity with `/sitrep`'s allow-rules but listed a *different, smaller* git set, and the whole git block was superfluous: `/roadmap` only ever calls `python3 scripts/sitrep_survey.py`, and the git reads are subprocesses *inside* that already-approved process that never hit the `Bash` gate (`_shared/permission-guard.md` § Notes explicitly says don't list read-only git). Trimmed the required set to the single `sitrep_survey.py` rule and replaced the hard-stop-then-continue contradiction (N1) with a one-line degrade-don't-halt note. **N2** (Standing counts could double-count on-hold-and-open tasks → partitioned status buckets vs. orthogonal readiness sub-counts) and **N3** (intro "never executes" reconciled with Step 5's "not without confirmation") also applied.

**Deliberately scoped out** (filed as a Low-priority follow-up in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`): wiring `/sitrep`'s `RECOMMENDED NEXT` cascade (Phase 44) to route to `/roadmap` at priority 7 ("no active work but ≥1 open roadmap task"). That touches `sitrep_survey.py`'s *tested* `_recommended_next` contract, so it stays out of this markdown-only phase rather than ballooning it into a Python + test change — consistent with the item's "cheap: prose skill + existing plumbing" framing.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix.** Filled Phase 69's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell with its real merge (`e9b2922`, #14) in both phase-log tables, and added Phase 69's missing `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` phase-completion-log row (Phase 69's close-out had skipped it).

Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; the Medium queue-strategy item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 71 (executed 2026-07-06 — `/report-issues`: the friction-log transport half, tester-round prep)

Phase 71 builds `/report-issues`, closing the Medium item filed 2026-07-06 (tester-round prep). It answers a launch-critical gap: Sysop's friction log (`SYSOP_ISSUES.md`, Phase 13) is a validated *capture* mechanism — BeanRider filed ~45 structured entries and a large fraction became Sysop phases — but the *collection* half only ever worked because the maintainer owns both repos and reads the consumer file directly. For an **external tester** the file is a dead end: the seeded template's own `Status:` enum anticipates `Filed to Sysop`, but nothing performs the filing, and `.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/` is unconnected to it. A tester round's single most valuable output — the install / permission-setup / first-`/intake` friction — would strand in a local file nobody upstream ever sees. `/report-issues` is the bridge.

**What it does.** Reads `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` at the consumer-repo root, classifies each entry by `Status:` (eligible = `Open`/`Prompt-ready`; `--include-resolved` also surfaces `Fixed in <consumer>` entries; `Filed to Sysop`/`Fixed in Sysop` skip), renders each eligible entry as the **exact** GitHub issue that would be filed — title `[<consumer>] <title>`, `bug` label, a body mapped onto the repo's `bug_report.md` template shape — gets **mandatory per-entry human consent**, files the consented ones with `gh issue create` **against the upstream Sysop repo** (`getsysop/sysop` by default, `--repo` for forks — *not* the consumer's own repo, the one place a `pr-*`-family skill points away from the current repo on purpose), then flips each filed entry to `Status: Filed to Sysop` and inserts a `**Filed:** <url> (<date>)` back-reference. **Dry-run is the default**; `--execute` is required to file, and even then nothing leaves the machine without an explicit pick. It's the second GitHub-touching skill after `/pr-dependabot` (Phase 53), whose gh-CLI pattern it mirrors (permission-guard Step 0, `gh auth status`, dry-run/`--execute`, the `reasoning` model role + Phase-69 marker).

**The architectural call: a skill, not a `report_issues.py` script.** Unlike `/pr-dependabot` (which shells to a script because classifying ~50 PRs needs deterministic rules), this has no classification problem and a deliberately *loose* input — the seed template explicitly invites "you can restructure freely." A rigid regex parser would silently choke on a tester's reformatted log, the exact failure mode Phase 68 just removed from the check-config loader (hand-rolled YAML parser silently dropping block-style lists). Agent-read markdown is the robust tool; the one irreversible side effect (`gh issue create`) is human-gated regardless. A structured `report_issues.py` is recorded as the escape hatch if a future consumer's volume makes the manual render tedious — filed as a revisit, not built.

**Earlier-capture half (the zero-code slice only).** Friction is captured today only at `/review-close` Step 7, but a tester's densest friction happens *before any review-close cycle exists*. Phase 71 ships the cheap mitigation the item scoped as pre-round: a "log friction as it happens, then `/report-issues`" note in `CONTRIBUTING.md` (a new "Reporting friction from real use" section) + a README line + a `/review-close` Step 7 pointer closing the capture→transport loop. The *structural* prompts (a nudge in `install.sh`'s closing summary and at the end of `/intake`) are the item's own "optional, later" bucket — **deferred and filed** as a new Low-priority follow-up rather than folded in.

**Delivery.** The new `core/skills/report-issues/` directory **auto-ships** via the existing `install_skills()` directory glob — no `install.sh`, `marketplace.json`, or `plugin.json` edit. Two permission rules were added to the `.claude/settings.json` template — `Bash(gh issue create:*)` + `Bash(gh issue list:*)` (the skill's guard Step 0 requires exactly these; read-only `gh auth status`/`gh repo view` are auto-approved and not listed, per `_shared/permission-guard.md` § Notes; the `Edit` to `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` needs no Bash rule). Doc surfaces: `WORKFLOW.md` §8.2b (transport half named) + the §8.1 friction-log table row, `WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md` helper-skills list, README, CONTRIBUTING. The Phase-69 resolver leaves the skill byte-for-byte identical at install (`reasoning`→`opus` default is a no-op).

**Verification.** Markdown + JSON only (plus one heredoc-text line in `install.sh`), so the existing suite is the regression proof: **435 tests green** (unchanged; the Phase-69 role-guard CI test accepts the new roled skill). Role guard passes over both the source tree and a real scratch `install.sh` target (resolver no-op confirmed). Install round-trip: skill ships to `.claude/skills/report-issues/`, both `gh issue` rules land, installed `settings.json` valid JSON, and the seed enum interpolates correctly (`Fixed in <consumer> <date>`).

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES** — one real blocker, three should-fixes, four nits, all applied:
- **BLOCKER** — the prescribed `gh issue create --body "<body>"` inlined arbitrary friction-log markdown into a *double-quoted* bash string, but the seed template **mandates** backticks and raw error text in exactly the body sections — so bash would run backtick/`$()` substitutions, break on stray quotes, and (worst case) **execute approved text as a shell command**, silently filing something different from what the human approved and breaking the shown-equals-filed privacy promise. Fixed: render the body to a temp file (`Write` tool) and use `--body-file`; single-quote the `--title` and render a clean equivalent if it carries shell-hazard chars. No new permission needed (`Bash(gh issue create:*)` already covers it).
- **SF2** — a single `AskUserQuestion` multiSelect enumerating one option per entry breaks past ~4 entries (the option cap) and overflows labels with full titles, and it diverged from the sibling one-at-a-time convention. Fixed: per-entry consent (or ≤4-entry batches, `ISSUE-NNNN` id as the short label).
- **SF3** — `--include-resolved` made `Fixed in <consumer>` entries eligible, but Step 5 only flipped `Open`/`Prompt-ready`, so a filed resolved-entry kept its status and a re-run would re-surface and double-file it. Fixed two ways: Step 5 now flips *any* successfully-filed entry to `Filed to Sysop`, and Step 1 treats any entry already carrying a `**Filed:**` line as ineligible regardless of status (belt-and-suspenders backstop).
- **NIT (label)** — auto-picking `enhancement` for pack/convention proposals produced a `bug_report`-shaped body on an `enhancement` issue; simplified to `bug`-only for v1 (maintainer relabels on triage), removing the shape mismatch.
- **NIT (dup search)** — searched the title *with* the `[<consumer>]` prefix, whose brackets weaken GitHub phrase matching; now searches the plain title.
- **NIT (body)** — the body dropped the entry's `### Workaround in <consumer>` section (useful upstream signal); now included when present.
- **NIT (Phase-62-class staleness, bundled)** — the `install.sh` seed-template `Status:` enum omitted `Fixed in <consumer> <date>` even though `/review-close` Step 7 writes it and this skill reads it (my `--include-resolved` made the gap load-bearing); added it to the seeded enum.
- **External reminder** — the default `getsysop/sysop` target requires the GitHub repo rename (Batch F, still-pending user action) to exist; added a `--repo`/404 caveat to Step 0.6 so a tester on a pre-rename clone gets a clean message rather than a loop.

Inline close-out per the meta-repo convention; the Medium transport item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md), and the deferred structural-capture prompts filed as a new Low-priority follow-up in [`REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`](./REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 72 (executed 2026-07-06 — `/daily-summary`: the retrospective/reporting leg, ported from GDP)

Phase 72 builds `/daily-summary`, closing the Low-priority item filed 2026-07-06 ("Port GDP's `/daily-summary` skill into `core/skills/` — sysop ships no retrospective/reporting leg"). It fills the one hole in Sysop's lifecycle coverage: the workflow spans plan (`/intake`) → strategize (`/roadmap`) → select (`/next-task`) → execute (`/claim-task`, `/auto-claim`) → document (`/document-work`) → review (`/review-close`) → audit (`/codebase-review`, `/security-audit`), but nothing was **backward-looking** — no "what happened over period X?" reporting skill. It's the direct sibling of Phase 70's `/roadmap`: `/roadmap` answers *what's left*, `/daily-summary` answers *what happened*, and together they cover a human's two standing questions about any project. It's also the most **tester-legible** of the launch-prep candidates — standup/async-update output is one of the features an outside audience reads at a glance.

**What it does.** A read-only, git-log-driven retrospective.
