It computes a target day (default: yesterday) and a week window, runs `git log` over both ranges (commits, `--shortstat`, `--name-only`), classifies the target day's commits by conventional-commit prefix, cross-references them against tasks closed that day in `tasks/index.yml`, enriches descriptions from any changelog/status/phase-log docs the project keeps, and emits a two-part report: **Yesterday in Detail** (commits by category, tasks closed, notable files, stats) + **Past Week** (a text activity heatmap, key themes, milestones grouped by phase, weekly stats). Flags: `--date YYYY-MM-DD`, `--days N`, `--week-only`, `--yesterday-only`; weekend/gap-aware (a zero-commit target day scans backward up to 3 days and reports the shift). It mutates nothing.

**The port — what was generalized off GDP.** GDP's `daily-summary` is deeply GDP-shaped; the port stripped every project-specific assumption. (1) **Date portability — the gate.** GDP's `date -v-1d` / `date -j -f` are BSD-only and silently fail on Linux; the filed item explicitly required a POSIX/GNU fallback "same treatment `claim_task.sh` got in Phase 50." Replaced with three portable helpers (`_days_ago` / `_date_minus` / `_day_name`), each **BSD form first (`-v` / `-j -f`) then GNU fallback (`-d`)** — the Phase-50 pattern. The third (epoch) fallback claim_task.sh carries is deliberately omitted and the omission justified inline: it existed there only for the sub-day `+4H` expiry; whole-day arithmetic is cleanly expressible in *both* BSD and GNU, so two forms suffice. (2) **In-model index parse, not a Python heredoc.** GDP `source .venv/bin/activate`'d and ran a `yaml`-parsing heredoc; the port has the agent `Read` + filter `tasks/index.yml` in-model (ISO `completed_date` strings sort lexicographically, so the `WEEK_START <= d <= TARGET_DATE` window is a plain string compare) — matching `/roadmap`'s in-model index read, dropping the `.venv`/Python dependency, and keeping the skill script-free and portable. (3) **Doc-enrichment sources generalized** off GDP's hardcoded `PROJECT_STATUS.md` Section 6 + `changelog.md` to "auto-discover a changelog / status / phase-log doc if present; all optional; the report is complete from git + `index.yml` alone." (4) **The `docs:`-commit filter softened from rule to judgment** — GDP hardcodes "filter out docs commits, this project pairs every code commit with a docs commit"; the port notes the pairing convention (Sysop's own `/document-work` produces it) but tells the agent to *judge* from the actual 1:1 shape and always surface docs as a distinct **count** rather than erasing them. (5) All GDP `product_roadmap.md`-migration cruft, the `.sql`-migration assumption, and Section-6 references dropped.

**Role + guard.** Carries the `reasoning` role (Phase-69 `<!-- sysop:model-roles frontmatter=reasoning -->` marker, `model: opus`) — the git-log→classify core is mechanical, but the value is in the **synthesis** (enriching descriptions, naming key themes the way a human would in standup), judgment work in the same class as `/roadmap` and `/report-issues`, the two other human-facing read-report siblings. The one deliberate judgment call worth flagging: `reasoning` vs `quick`. `/next-task` and `/sitrep` are `quick` (haiku) as *trivial* read-only surveys; `/daily-summary` isn't trivial (theme synthesis + enrichment), so `reasoning` fits — and the choice is cheaply reversible per-consumer: Phase-69's role→model indirection lets anyone remap `reasoning` (or this skill) to a lighter model via `served_models.local.yml` for lower standup-run cost. Read-only enforced with `disallowed-tools: Edit, Write, NotebookEdit` (Phase 54), partial by design — `Bash` stays for the `git log`/`date` reads. **No new permission rules** and no Step-0 guard: every op (`git log`, `date`, `Read`) is read-only, which `_shared/permission-guard.md` § Notes says is auto-approved and must not be listed.

**Delivery.** The new `core/skills/daily-summary/` directory **auto-ships** via the existing `install_skills()` directory glob — no `install.sh`, `marketplace.json`, or `plugin.json` edit. Doc surfaces: `WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md` helper-skills list (beside `/roadmap`) + `tasks/README.md` skill table. The Phase-69 resolver leaves the skill byte-for-byte identical at install (`reasoning`→`opus` default is a no-op).

**Verification.** Markdown-only, so the existing suite is the regression proof: **435 tests green** (unchanged; the Phase-69 role-guard CI test accepts the new roled skill). Role guard passes over both the source tree and a real scratch `install.sh` target (source == installed — resolver no-op confirmed), with **zero** new permission rules in the installed `settings.json`. Both data paths dogfooded: the git-driven core ran against Sysop's own history on macOS/BSD (portable helpers + git-log commands + heatmap counts all produce correct output), and the `tasks/index.yml` milestone-filter input shape was confirmed against BeanRider's real consumer queue (25 `status: done` rows with ISO `completed_date` + a `phases:` `number`/`title` list — exactly what the in-model filter and phase-title map consume); Sysop itself has no `index.yml`, so that path degrades gracefully here (a Step-7 edge case).

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES** — no blockers; the highest-risk part (the date portability that gated the port) was independently verified **correct on both platforms**, with the `||` fallback confirmed safe in *both* directions (on BSD the GNU forms return empty so the correct BSD form wins first; on GNU the BSD forms exit non-zero/empty so the GNU form fires — no silent-wrong-non-empty case). Findings:
- **SHOULD-FIX** — the Step 5 / Step 6 heatmap *example* labeled its dates `Mon–Fri`, but those 2026 dates are actually `Tue`–`Sat`, and it self-contradicted the Step 1 weekend example (which correctly has 07-04 = Saturday inactive, 07-03 = Friday active). Fixed both blocks to the real 2026 weekdays (`Tue 06-30` … `Sat 07-04`, with 07-04 = 0 and 07-03 = 2 to match Step 1) and added a "use the real weekday via `_day_name`, don't hardcode Mon–Fri" instruction so the output can't reproduce the slip.
- **NIT (window honesty)** — `--days 7` covers 8 inclusive calendar days (7 prior + target); the "week-lookback window (default 7)" wording now says so explicitly.
- **NIT (flag symmetry)** — Step 5 skips on `--yesterday-only` but there was no parallel `--week-only` skip on Steps 3–4 (harmless, just wasted classification work); added the symmetric skip note to Step 3.
- **NIT (git day-boundary)** and **NIT (permission-classification reliance)** — both marked "no change needed" by the reviewer (negligible, inherited from GDP / consistent with the read-only principle); left as-is.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 71's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`fe410da` #21) in both phase-log tables. Inline close-out; the Low-priority `/daily-summary` port item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 73 (executed 2026-07-06 — two small follow-up debts from Phases 70/71: `/sitrep`→`/roadmap` routing + earlier friction-capture)

Phase 73 knocks out the two small Low-priority follow-up debts that Phases 70 and 71 deliberately filed rather than fold in — both launch-prep tidy-up, bundled into one phase because each is a few lines on an independent surface.

**73a — `/sitrep`'s `RECOMMENDED NEXT` cascade routes to `/roadmap` for deep queues (the Phase-70 follow-up).** Phase 44's priority cascade in `sitrep_survey.py::_recommended_next` had a priority-7 rule — "no active work but ≥1 open roadmap task in `tasks/index.yml`" — that unconditionally recommended `/auto-claim`. But when the queue is deep and nothing is in flight, the better next move is often a *strategy view* (`/roadmap`, Phase 70: see the work grouped by kind + a proposed order of attack) than jumping straight to blind batch execution. 73a splits priority 7 by **queue depth**, anchored to a principled boundary rather than a magic number: `/auto-claim` caps a batch at N=4 tasks (WORKFLOW.md § 2.4b), so a new module constant `_AUTO_CLAIM_MAX_BATCH = 4` is the natural threshold — **more than one batch's worth (`n > 4`) → `/roadmap`** (strategize first); **a queue that fits one batch (`n ≤ 4`) → `/auto-claim`** (grab it in one go). The `/roadmap` recommendation carries `clear_nudge=False` — it's a read-only reasoning skill with no fan-out, unlike the `/auto-claim`/`/auto-review`/`/auto-judge` recommendations whose always-on `/clear` nudge exists because they spawn parallel/Opus agents. Surfaces: the P7 branch in `sitrep_survey.py` (+ the priority-order docstring), the `Recommendation routing rules` table in `sitrep/SKILL.md` (row 7 → 7a/7b), and — the reviewer's catch — the shipped `/roadmap` skill's own "Future wiring (not built here)" note, which described *exactly* this wiring as unbuilt (a Phase-62-class cross-reference rot the filed scope-list missed) → rewritten to "Wired (Phase 73a)". **The `_recommended_next` contract had zero direct test coverage** (the 38 existing `test_sitrep_survey.py` tests cover low-level helpers only — the same gap the still-open Medium `_find_discrepancies`/`_classify_review_batches` item names), so 73a adds **+7 tests** that lock the new routing where there was none: both branches, the boundary at exactly 4 (→`/auto-claim`) vs 5 (→`/roadmap`) written as `range(_AUTO_CLAIM_MAX_BATCH)` / `+1` so they *track the constant* rather than hardcoding 4, idle→`None`, the `detail_lines` "+N more" sample formatting, `clear_nudge` values both ways, and a precedence guard proving an in-progress P5 task still wins over a six-deep roadmap (P7 can never mask live work). **Deliberately a count threshold, not a weight one:** `open_roadmap_ids` carries no effort weights, the filed item asked for a count threshold, and the proxy errs toward `/auto-claim` for the few-but-heavy case (a small count is manageable to eyeball) — recorded as a known simplification, no change.

**73b — earlier friction capture (the Phase-71 follow-up).** Phase 71 shipped the friction-log *transport* half (`/report-issues`) + a zero-code capture note in CONTRIBUTING/README, but deferred the *structural* prompts as its own "optional, later" bucket. The gap they close: friction is prompted for only at `/review-close` Step 7, yet a tester's earliest and densest friction — install, first permission-rule setup, first `/intake` — happens *before any `/review-close` cycle exists*. 73b adds a capture nudge at those two earlier moments: (1) a **fresh-install-only** line in `install.sh`'s "Next steps" block ("Hit Sysop friction …? log it in `SYSOP_ISSUES.md`; `/report-issues` files the keepers upstream") — verified to sit in the `UPDATE_MODE=0` branch so it never fires on `--update`/`--adopt`/`--check`/`--dry-run` (a returning consumer isn't re-nudged); and (2) a one-line closing nudge in `/intake`'s completion message. The `/intake` addition is deliberately **inside the fenced completion summary the skill already prints** — not a new `AskUserQuestion` turn — because `/intake` is judgment-heavy and its turn budget is precious; an out-of-fence author note records that constraint so no future edit promotes it to an interactive turn. Both point at artifacts that exist post-install (`SYSOP_ISSUES.md` is seeded on fresh install; `/report-issues` ships).

**Verification.** **442 tests green** (was 435 — the +7 sitrep routing tests; the rest markdown/bash). Role guard green (source + installed). Install round-trips all clean: fresh (exit 0, nudge present in Next steps), update (exit 0, nudge absent), adopt (exit 0), check-with-`--source` (exit 0, "up to date"). Both the sitrep behavioral routing (n=0→None, n≤4→`/auto-claim`, n>4→`/roadmap`) and the fresh-install nudge placement were confirmed by real invocation.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES** — no blockers; the risky bits (fresh-install-only gating, precedence, the `clear_nudge` call, the boundary tests) all verified clean. One SHOULD-FIX (the `/roadmap` "not built here" staleness above — applied) + one NIT (a stale `§ Decision rules` docstring cross-ref that the diff already touched → `§ Recommendation routing rules`, applied); two NITs left per the reviewer (the count-vs-weight threshold simplification, recorded above; and close-out bookkeeping, which is this commit).

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 72's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`951324f` #22) in both phase-log tables. Inline close-out; both Low-priority follow-up items (filed by Phases 70 and 71) moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 74 (executed 2026-07-06 — `/auto-claim` + `/next-task` unblocker-first candidate ordering)

Phase 74 closes the Medium item filed 2026-07-06 (workflow-gap evaluation follow-up): make `depends_on` a **scheduling signal**, not only a gate. Before this phase both selectors — `/auto-claim` Step 1 (which forms a batch) and `/next-task` (which resolves one task) — used `depends_on` solely in the `ready()` filter, then sorted the survivors by `(effort asc, id)`. A task that five other open tasks are waiting on and a leaf that unblocks nothing sorted identically. The fix computes an **`unlock_count`** per candidate and sorts **`(unlock_count desc, effort asc, id)`** — unblocker-first — so claiming a foundational task now enlarges the pool the next cycle draws from.

**`unlock_count` definition (identical in both implementations).** `unlock_count[id]` = the number of tasks that are `status: open` **and** in the active/focus phase **and** list `id` in their `depends_on`. Three deliberate design calls, all matching the filing:
- **Direct count, not transitive** — a transitive count overweights long chains whose tails are far off anyway; the direct count is a clean "how foundational is this" proxy.
- **Phase-scoped** — the claimable pool is already phase-scoped (`/auto-claim` Step 1 and `/next-task` both filter to the `current_focus` phase), so only a *same-phase* dependent becoming ready enlarges the *next* pool. A cross-phase dependent doesn't count.
- **The simple direct count** — a dependent still blocked by *other* unmet deps is counted anyway. Refining to "only dependents whose sole remaining blocker is this task" would be more precise but needs a graph walk for marginal gain; the filing chose the simple count and this preserves it. `user_action` dependents count too (the filing's literal "open tasks listing `id`") — unblocking one still moves human work forward, and excluding them would add a special case for no real benefit.

**Scope decision — bundle `next_task.py` (ratified with Wade via `AskUserQuestion`).** The filing left open whether `/next-task`'s deterministic resolver (`next_task.py:pick_next_task`, Phase 45a) should get the same tie-break "for resolver consistency … acceptable as a follow-up." Bundled, for three reasons that emerged on measurement: (1) **consistency** — `/next-task` and `/auto-claim` both answer "what next?"; a divergent lead task between them is a latent confusion bug; (2) **near-zero regression cost** — `next_task.py`'s base test fixture (`_BASE_INDEX`) has *no* `depends_on` edges, so every `unlock_count` is 0 and the new sort reduces to the old `(effort, id)` → **all 41 existing `test_next_task.py` cases stay green untouched**; the change is additive-only test churn; (3) **it is the only way to get automated coverage** — `/auto-claim` Step 1 is an inline `python3` heredoc inside `SKILL.md` (markdown), unreachable by the pytest suite, so the shared unblocker-first logic would ship untested without the `next_task.py` leg. The two implementations are intentional parallel copies (same pattern as `_sanitize_log` duplicated across `next_task.py`/`validate_tasks.py` — the heredoc must stay self-contained for a consumer running it from their project root).

**Surfaces.**
- `core/skills/auto-claim/SKILL.md` — Step 1 heredoc gains the `unlock_count` computation + the new sort key + an `unlocks=N` field in the candidate report; the post-heredoc prose explains the ordering and carries `unlocks` forward; Step 4's "Proposed Batch" table gains an **Unlocks** column (surfaces the ordering rationale at the one human gate); the Step 2 worked examples get a preface note (A–G assume `unlock_count` = 0, so they read as before) plus a new **Example H** working through the reorder — including the case where it only changes the batch *set* under a binding ceiling (`N=2`), and the tradeoff that unblocker-first may take a heavier unblocker ahead of a cheap leaf, with the explicit note that the solo invariants + ceilings are unchanged by the sort.
- `core/companion/scripts/next_task.py` — `pick_next_task` computes `unlock_count` and sorts both the agent pool and the user-action fallback pool by `(-unlock_count, effort, id)`; the module docstring (Step 2a spec) and the `pick_next_task` docstring updated.
- `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` — the `/next-task` selection rules (§ 2.4) reworded: the sort is now unblocker-first, and the **stale claim "the primary sort key remains `effort:` for now" was corrected** (a Phase-62-class rot the change would otherwise have left behind); the `blast_radius`-as-future-secondary-sort note is preserved (it's a different axis than `unlock_count`). The `/auto-claim` Step 1 description (§ 2.4b) gains the unblocker-first ordering.
- `tests/test_next_task.py` — **+7 tests**: unblocker outranks lower effort, effort breaks an unlock tie, id breaks an equal-unlock-equal-effort tie, deferred dependents don't count (open-only), cross-phase dependents don't count (phase-scoped), a dependent still blocked by *other* unmet deps is counted anyway (the "simple direct count" decision — added by the adversarial pass's NIT 3), and the user-action fallback pool is unblocker-sorted too.

**Not a gate change → not gated on the GDP loosen experiment.** This reorders which *equally-safe* batch forms first; it touches no safety surface (the K=6 sum ceiling, cross-module cap, and solo invariants are unchanged), so unlike K / cross-module-cap tuning it does **not** wait on GDP's `TECH-AUTO-CLAIM-LOOSEN-GATE-EXPERIMENT` data. **Honest expected-impact caveat** (GDP telemetry, the 2026-06-30 report): 81% of GDP's solo batches were *math-limited*, not supply-limited, so pool enlargement alone wouldn't have converted most of them — the value is (a) pool *variety* feeding the gate (a bigger pool raises the odds a compatible low-weight partner exists under the cross-module cap), (b) the 19% supply-limited solos addressed directly, and (c) its clearest win: greenfield `/intake` queues, which the decomposition rubric emits `depends_on`-shaped, where unblocker-first ≈ a topological order with a max-width frontier — exactly what a human scheduler picks, and exactly the newcomer/launch audience.

**Verification.** **449 tests green** (was 442 — the +7 `next_task.py` unblocker-first cases; all 442 prior stayed green). The `/auto-claim` Step 1 heredoc — untestable by the suite — was hand-verified by running its exact python verbatim against a scratch `index.yml` modeling Example H plus the two filter edge cases: it emitted `TECH-C  …  unlocks=3` first, then the two `unlocks=0` leaves, with the cross-phase dependent (phase 7) and the deferred dependent both correctly excluded from the count, and the three blocked dependents excluded from candidates — matching `next_task.py`'s logic exactly (the two parallel implementations agree).

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP** — no blockers, no should-fixes. It re-derived Example H by hand (arithmetically exact) and confirmed the two implementations compute an identical `unlock_count` + sort for all schema-valid data. Four NITs, two applied: **NIT 1** — the heredoc's *missing*-`effort` fallback defaulted to `High` (weight 2) whereas `next_task.py` sinks a missing key to 9, a latent crack in the "parallel copies must agree" contract (pre-existing; only reachable on schema-invalid data the validator rejects) → heredoc changed to `order.get(t.get("effort"), 9)`, and a direct harness confirmed both selectors now order a missing-`effort` task identically (`MMM-UNBLOCK, ZZZ-HIGH, AAA-NOEFF` in both). **NIT 3** — the documented "simple direct count" decision (a dependent still blocked by *other* unmet deps is counted anyway, no graph walk) had no test → added `test_pick_next_task_unlock_counts_dependent_still_blocked_by_other_deps` (a "sole-remaining-blocker" implementation would fail it). NIT 2 (two tie-break tests don't independently discriminate a broken always-0 count — the suite discriminates collectively via the other five) and NIT 4 (this very note originally pre-recorded the verdict — a process smell, now reconciled to the actual outcome) acknowledged, no code change.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 73's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`85f8e3f` #23) in both phase-log tables. Inline close-out; the Medium unblocker-first item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 75 (executed 2026-07-06 — `install.sh` stack auto-detection: the Caliper `init` idea, onboarding polish for the tester round)

Phase 75 closes the **"framework auto-detection"** leg of the Caliper competitive-analysis item (Low-priority, filed 2026-06-24 — three ergonomics ideas worth borrowing from `getcaliper.dev`; the other two, real-time post-turn convention checks and the three-tier enforcement framing, remain open). It was chosen as the next builder phase (over the two Medium test-coverage/durability items) because the next real gate is a **private tester round**, and `install.sh` is the very first thing a tester touches — a smooth, low-friction first impression is what converts a tester into a repeat user, and stack auto-detection is Sysop's clearest onboarding gap versus a polished competitor. Caliper's `npx caliper init` auto-detects the stack in one command; Sysop's `install.sh` had only an interactive comma-separated pack picker with no detection.

**What it adds.** A new `detect_packs()` (plus two helpers, `_detect_has_file` and `_detect_manifest_mentions`) scans the target tree for high-precision stack signals and echoes a CSV of the detected **populated** packs (python, postgres, nextjs-react, llm, beancount). Three wiring surfaces:
- **`--packs auto`** — non-interactive detection (agent/CI-friendly, and the automated test seam: the interactive picker reads `/dev/tty` and is un-testable, so `auto` is the pytest-reachable path for the same machinery). Translated **centrally** in `main()` right after `validate_target` (before mode dispatch) so fresh + adopt share it; `cmd_check` reads packs from the lock, so detection is skipped under `--check`.
- **Interactive picker** — on a fresh install, `prompt_packs` pre-scans the target and offers the detected set as the **blank-default** ("Detected in your project: python, nextjs-react"); typing `none`/`core`/`-` forces core-only, an explicit list overrides, and no-detection preserves the historical blank = core-only behavior.
- **`PACKS_PROVIDED` flag** — a latent-correctness fix bundled in: an explicit `--packs ''` (or a `--packs auto` that detects nothing) now installs core-only instead of silently falling through to the interactive prompt (which, non-interactive, would abort with a TTY error). Previously `--packs ''` on a non-TTY errored.

**Detection design — precision over recall** (a wrong pre-selection is worse than none, since it undermines the "polished" first impression the feature exists to create): marker-file probes first (`pyproject.toml`, `alembic.ini`, `next.config.*`, `*.beancount`), file-content globs (`*.py`, `*.tsx`) only as depth-bounded (`-maxdepth 2/4`), vendor-pruned (`node_modules/`, `.venv/`, `venv/`, `.git/`) fallbacks. Postgres requires an **explicit** Postgres marker (`alembic.ini`, a compose file naming postgres, or a `migrations/*.sql`), never "any `.sql`". LLM tokens are **boundary-anchored** so a substring like `coherence`/`@coherentglobal` doesn't false-trip on `cohere`. Dependency resolution (postgres/beancount → sysop-python) is left to the existing `resolve_packs`, so detection outputs the raw pre-dependency set and the plan summary shows the resolved topological set.

**Scope.** Fresh install + the explicit `--packs auto` path; `--adopt` is deliberately **excluded from the interactive default** (it asks which packs were *originally* installed — a different question from the current stack), and `--update` continues to take packs from the lock.

**Surfaces.**
- `install.sh` — `detect_packs` / `_detect_has_file` / `_detect_manifest_mentions` (new); `prompt_packs` rewritten (detection-aware default, `ADOPT_MODE`-gated, case-folded core-only keywords); `main()` central `auto` translation + combined-`auto` rejection + `PACKS_PROVIDED` gate on both the fresh and adopt prompts; `--packs auto` arg + `PACKS_PROVIDED` in arg-parse; usage/`--help` text (documents `auto`/`''`, new example).
- **Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** the usage text **and** the picker menu both listed `beancount` as a *placeholder* pack, but Phase 43b populated it — moved to the "populated" line in both spots.
- `tests/test_install_detect.py` — **new**, 25 integration tests driving the real installer in `--dry-run --packs auto` against scratch git consumers (plus one non-dry-run lock-record test and one rc-2 combined-`auto` test): positive detection per pack + deps resolved, the precision negatives (vendored `node_modules`/`.venv` pruned for *all* probes, stray root `.sql` ≠ postgres, react-free `package.json` ≠ nextjs, `coherence` ≠ llm, `langchain-cohere` *is* llm), the Compose-v2 `compose.yaml` name, and the `PACKS_PROVIDED` gate (explicit `''` and empty-`auto` both core-only, no prompt).
- `README.md` (×2) + `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` § 8.2b — document detection + `--packs auto` + the `--adopt` exclusion.

**Verification.** **474 tests green** (was 449 — +25 in the new detection suite; all 449 prior stayed green). Detection smoke-tested end-to-end across all five populated packs + the precision negatives; a real (non-dry-run) `--packs auto` install exits 0 and records the **resolved** packs in `.claude/sysop.lock`. Role guard green (source), 13 manifests parse, leak-scan clean over the shipped diff. `bash -n` clean.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES** — one real blocker, all findings applied:
- **B1 (BLOCKER)** — `cmd_adopt` calls the *shared* `prompt_packs`, which unconditionally ran detection and flipped the blank-default from core-only to accept-detected, so interactive `--adopt` would record the *current* stack instead of what was *originally* installed (corrupting the lock's `packs` field for future `--update`) — and directly contradicted the shipped WORKFLOW.md text. **Fix:** gate detection in `prompt_packs` behind `ADOPT_MODE -eq 0`; adopt keeps the historical core-only default and shows no detection line.
- **S1** — the LLM SDK regex was an unbounded substring, so a `coherence`/`@coherentglobal` dependency false-tripped `cohere` → `llm`. **Fix:** boundary-anchor the tokens (`(^|[^a-z0-9])(…)([^a-z0-9]|$)`); empirically verified it rejects `coherence`/`coherent` (under `-i` too) while keeping `cohere`/`langchain-cohere` and every other real SDK name.
- **S2** — `_detect_manifest_mentions` and the postgres-migrations `find` pruned only `node_modules`/`.git`, not `.venv`/`venv`, so a developer's gitignored on-disk `.venv/` could be walked (latent, throttled by the depth bounds) — and the shipped doc promised all probes prune vendored dirs. **Fix:** add `.venv`/`venv` to both prune sets.
- **NITs, all applied:** N1 — case-fold the picker's `none`/`core`/`-` keywords so `None`/`NONE` also force core-only (was falling to the verbatim branch → `resolve_packs` hard-error). N2 — `--packs auto,python` now fails loud with a clear "auto must be used on its own" error instead of dying inside `resolve_packs` on "unknown pack: auto". N3 — match the Compose v2 default filename (`compose.yaml`/`compose.yml`), and switch the compose probe to `find -exec grep` to avoid a two-glob `ls` partial-failure bug (and handle spaces in paths). N4 — guard the empty-`hits` array expansion (`(( ${#hits[@]} ))`) so the final `printf "${hits[*]}"` is safe under `set -u` on bash < 4.4. N5 — skip the `auto` scan + echo under `--check` (read-only; it reads packs from the lock). N6 — added the negative tests the reviewer noted would have caught S1/S2 (vendored `.venv` manifest ≠ llm, `.venv` migrations ≠ postgres, `coherence` ≠ llm) plus the N2/N3 cases.

**Discovered during work, filed not fixed (out of scope):** `--adopt` into a target with **no pre-existing `.claude/` directory** tracebacks on the lock write (`FileNotFoundError` on `.claude/sysop.lock`, because the adopt flow computes `managed_paths` via a dry-run pipeline that never creates `.claude/`, then tries to write the lock into it). **Confirmed pre-existing** — reproduces identically on `main`'s `install.sh`, so it is unrelated to Phase 75 (my `--adopt` detection-gate works: detection ran and resolved correctly; only the downstream lock write fails). Adopt is documented as a backfill for *existing* installs (which already have `.claude/`), so this is a robustness gap on a misuse path rather than a broken supported flow — filed Low-priority in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 74's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`9059c1a` #24) in both phase-log tables. Inline close-out; the Caliper item's auto-detection leg marked done (the other two ideas remain open). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 76 (executed 2026-07-06 — guided (teaching) mode: the thin slice + tester onboarding)

**What & why.** Launch-prep, tester-round. The recruiting question "who is Sysop *for* — technical or non-technical?" surfaced that the workflow assumes a "competent engineer" (the workflow.html Audience section says so) but never states it — and, more interestingly, that a genuinely useful **safe mode for newer / less-senior builders** is possible *without* lowering the review bar. Guided (teaching) mode is that overlay: at every point a skill would halt and ask the human to approve / choose / promote, it (1) states the decision plainly, (2) adversarially reviews its *own* recommendation (the primitive Sysop already applies to plans), and (3) triages the call — **A** genuine values tradeoff → honest pros/cons, human owns it; **B** false choice (security hole / data-loss / broken invariant) → collapse to the right answer, don't offer the wrong option as a peer; **C** real-but-un-weighable → conservative default, log why, don't ask. **Load-bearing rule:** the adversarial layer is *allowed to conclude "this isn't your call"* — the failure mode to design against is **false balance / diligence theater** (a wrong answer dressed as a 50/50), which is worse than not asking. Generalizes `/intake`'s "argue the decomposition, never adjudicate venture-worth" boundary from planning to every gate.

**Thin slice (shipped) + full build (deferred).** Ratified scope: ship a real installed artifact + defer the ergonomics until the incoming tester gives signal (dogfood-before-build). Shipped: `core/skills/_shared/guided-mode.md` (the canonical protocol partial — pin-less prose, no role marker, auto-ships via the `install_skills()` `_shared/` glob, zero CI impact; the **sixth** partial), activated via a `## Guided mode` stanza in the consumer's `CLAUDE.md` (always-loaded → honored by all skills with **no per-skill wiring**; the **inline** stanza was chosen over a bare pointer for gate-fire reliability during the dogfood). Deferred + spec'd in `tools/GUIDED_MODE_SPEC.md`: per-skill wiring at each decision gate, a `/teach-me` toggle command, an install-time `--guided` flag, the toggle-home decision (person-not-project → leans user-level), and the `workflow.html` Audience revision (the original trigger). Filed as a Medium open item.

**Tester onboarding (bundled).** `docs/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` (private, round-scoped, removed at public launch): install → guided-mode-on → a focused spotlight set with one pointed question each (guided mode; `/intake`; the `/claim-task → /review-close` core loop; `/roadmap` + `/daily-summary`; `/auto-claim`; "anything missing") → the layered feedback ladder (friction log `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` → `/report-issues` → Discussions for open-ended → Issues → PRs) → cadence. GDP telemetry pulled to frame `/auto-claim` honestly: **safe** (≈117 parallel merges, 0 reopened/abandoned, no batch-caused conflicts) but **never measured faster** — the batch wins twice (parallel generation + one `/review-close` sitting instead of per-task setup overhead) yet each sitting is bigger to hold in your head, so the sweet-spot curve is exactly what the tester can measure. Premise corrected along the way: GDP already runs K=8 (not 6), the K=12 "loosen" never ran, and Sysop itself ships K=6.

**Docs.** WORKFLOW.md §8.3 (five → six partials + a `guided-mode.md` bullet noting it is *not yet cited from inside the skills* — the thin-slice activation is always-loaded CLAUDE.md prose), §6.1 (optional `## Guided mode` row in the required-sections table + the inline stanza template).

**Feedback infra (found already built).** The layered model the tester doc documents was already shipped by Phase 71: friction log + `/report-issues`, issue templates, the issue-before-PR norm, and a `config.yml` `contact_links` route to Discussions. The one gap is off-repo: **enable GitHub Discussions** (the `config.yml` link 404s until then) — flagged, not a code change.

**Follow-ups filed** (REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md): guided-mode full build (Medium); fresh-session `→ /review-close` handoff guidance + GDP parity (Medium — `/review-close` is designed context-independent, so running it in a bloated implementation session biases the review with the implementer's rationalizations; reword the two handoff messages to recommend `/clear`-then-`/review-close` with a one-line why); public `docs/getting-started.md` tutorial (Medium — the missing Diátaxis quadrant; markdown not a second HTML file, for staleness + discoverability); K=6→8 backport (Low, evidence-backed, skip-unless-wanted).

**Verification.** Markdown-only → **474 tests green** (unchanged from Phase 75); guided-mode.md is a pin-less partial so the role guard is untouched. **Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero context): SHIP** — no blockers / should-fixes; verified the "inert / not-yet-cited" framing is consistent across all three files, the §6.1 stanza and the protocol agree (A/B/C + the "not your call" rule verbatim), the anonymized `/auto-claim` stat is a safe subset of README's provenance framing and doesn't over-claim speed or imply the tester's K is raised, all links / step-refs resolve, and the partial count is right. 3 NITs applied (guided-mode.md coverage claim hedged for cold-context sub-agent gates; SPEC "defaulted ON" → "tester pastes the stanza"; SPEC toggle-home "ideal" → "leans" to match the open deferred decision); 1 context flag (the `getsysop/sysop` clone / Discussions / report-issues URLs 404 until the Batch-F repo rename lands — do the rename before handing the doc to the tester). Inline close-out. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 77 (executed 2026-07-06 — relocate tester onboarding out of the shipping tree: mirror-leak fix)

**What & why.** Phase 76 created `docs/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` without checking the existing tester apparatus in `tools/` — a placement bug caught when the launch plan came up. The public/tester mirror (`tools/make_public_mirror.sh`) does `git archive HEAD` then removes a fixed exclude list (`REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`, `REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`, `HANDOVER.md`, `CLAUDE.md`, `*_HANDOFF.md`, `PHASE_47_SPEC.md`, the auto-claim miner, and `rm -rf tools/`) — but **not `docs/`**. So `docs/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` would ship into both the private tester mirror (`wade-cms/jig-tester`) AND the public repo at launch — a doc literally titled "private tester round," referencing `getsysop/sysop` where the tester repo is `wade-cms/jig-tester`, and duplicating the pre-existing internal `tools/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` (the paste-ready note). The leak-scan greps would **not** catch it (no internal identifiers / home paths / gdp refs; it is not on the exclude list), so it would have shipped silently — exactly the mirror-drift class the leak-scan can't see.

**Fix.** (1) **Deleted `docs/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md`.** (2) **Folded its genuinely-new content into the internal `tools/` apparatus** (never ships — `tools/` is `rm -rf`'d by the mirror): `tools/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` (the paste-note) now carries the guided-mode-on instruction, the spotlight skills with one pointed question each (guided mode / `/intake` / `/claim-task`→`/review-close` / `/roadmap`+`/daily-summary` / `/auto-claim` / anything-missing), the honest `/auto-claim` framing (safe but never-measured-faster), and the layered feedback channels — all with the correct `sysop-tester` URLs (including `/report-issues --repo wade-cms/jig-tester`). (3) **`tools/TESTER_MIRROR_RUNBOOK.md`** gains a step to **enable Discussions** on `sysop-tester` (the open-ended channel; Issues stay for concrete bugs) + send the onboarding note + brief on guided mode. (4) Fixed the forward-looking `docs/`→`tools/` references in `tools/GUIDED_MODE_SPEC.md` and the two Phase-76 REVIEW_CHECKLIST open items. Phase 76's historical records are left verbatim (they accurately record what Phase 76 did; this entry records the correction).

**Product content unaffected.** The shipped guided-mode *feature* (`core/skills/_shared/guided-mode.md` + WORKFLOW §6.1/§8.3) is product content and correctly ships; `tools/GUIDED_MODE_SPEC.md` is internal (already in `tools/`, never ships). Only the misplaced onboarding doc moved.

**Verification.** Re-grepped for `TESTER_ONBOARDING` — no `docs/`-tree tester-round doc remains that the mirror would ship, and no dangling `docs/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` reference outside the Phase-76 historical records. Markdown-only → **474 tests green** (unchanged). Inline close-out. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 78 (executed 2026-07-06 — convention-promotion writes land in the consumer overlay, not the regenerated base; + fresh-context `/review-close` handoffs)

Two Medium launch-prep items, bundled. The lead is a **latent correctness bug in Sysop's headline feature** (the convention-promotion loop); the rider is a small handoff-hygiene reword that the same tester round wants.

**The bug (item A — base-map clobber).** `/codebase-review` + `/security-audit` Step 9 promote a recurring review finding into an enforceable rule by writing to `.claude/convention_map.md` / `.claude/security_map.md` / `.claude/checks.yml`. In a **consumer install** those three are **concat-managed base files** that `install.sh`'s `run_install_pipeline` regenerates from Sysop's core + pack sources on **every `sysop-update.sh`** (WORKFLOW §8.2c) — so a promotion written only to a base file is silently regenerated away on the consumer's next update. The Phase 24a/24b preservation machinery protects the `.project.*` suffix files and `scripts/*`+`scripts/hooks/*`, **not** the base maps — and no skill prose anywhere named `.project.*` as a promotion target. Doesn't bite the extraction source (gdp authors maps in place, never regenerates). Same class as the known absorb-pattern trap, never reconciled for the *promotion* path specifically.

**Dogfood result (honest — the bug is real but latent).** Verify-first per the "dogfood in the consumer before ship" rule: BeanRider (the one live consumer, has `.claude/sysop.lock` + overlays) **loses nothing today**. Five of six local-looking reminder ids in its base `convention_map.md` (`shell-mute-stderr`, `semgrep-sanitize-exception-interp`, `semgrep-subprocess-bare-except`, `open-without-encoding`, `semgrep-raise-from-none-outside-except`) resolve to **0** pack/core sources — they are BeanRider-local — **but they live in its hand-authored `.project.*` overlay** (`convention_map.project.md`=richly authored, `checks.project.yml`=their checks), which the concat re-appends into the base every update (the base's local reminders sit *after* the overlay-region boundary at line 142, i.e. in the appended region — safe). BeanRider dodged the bug by **hand-authoring its overlay at bootstrap** instead of ever running the Step 9 promotion loop to completion + updating. So the bug is latent: it bites the first consumer (or tester) who actually runs `/codebase-review` Step 9 (writes to base) then `sysop-update`s. The fix redirects the loop's output to exactly where BeanRider's hand-authored content already correctly lives.

**Fix (option (a) — redirect promotion writes to the overlay in consumer installs).** New canonical partial **`core/skills/_shared/promotion-write-target.md`** (the **7th** shared partial; auto-ships via the `install_skills()` `_shared/` glob — no manifest/installer edit; pin-less → zero role-guard impact), cited by both review skills. Consumer install is detected by the presence of **`.claude/sysop.lock`** (the installer writes it; absent in Sysop's own tree and any author-in-place repo). There, promotion/demotion **dual-writes**: the base file (live effect *this* round + the cross-round recurrence gate reads round-attributed base-map entries, before the next update runs the concat) **and** the never-managed `.project.*` overlay sibling (durable across update; re-appended for markdown, re-merged by `checks[*].id` for YAML). No duplication — `concat_files` truncates + rebuilds the base from upstream only (strips the in-place copy) *before* re-appending the overlay copy, so the entry lands exactly once. A new `.claude/semgrep/*.yaml` file, a `scripts/hooks/pre-commit` letter, and a `CLAUDE.md` prose bullet need **no** overlay mirror (the installer never overwrites an unshipped semgrep filename; `scripts/hooks/*` is a preserved managed path; `CLAUDE.md` is the consumer's own file). Source repo (no lock) writes base-only as before. Demotion (Step 9b): retire a locally-promoted rule from the overlay (base-only retirement resurrects it on the next update); suppress a `checks.yml`-mechanism core rule via a `checks.project.yml` override (`paths: ["__disabled_no_op__"]`); a core semgrep/pre-commit rule routes retirement upstream (no consumer-side suppression). **Surfaces:** both skills' Step 9 intro + checks.yml sub-cycle + reminder options b/c + the Step 9 & 9b commit `git add`s + the Step 2a coverage-hygiene note + commit; WORKFLOW §3.5 write-target note + §8.3 (six→seven partials). **Test:** new `tests/test_install_concat.py::TestPromotionOverlayDurability` drives a real `install.sh --update` ×2 and asserts a promoted `checks.project.yml` entry AND a `convention_map.project.md` reminder section both reappear in the **regenerated base** maps — locking the overlay-survival mechanism the dual-write relies on (the markdown text-append path was previously untested). **475 green** (was 474, +1).

**Item B — fresh-context `→ /review-close` handoffs.** `/document-work` Step 6 end-message and `/auto-claim`'s "Next steps" both handed off to `/review-close` without telling the user to start a clean session. `/review-close` is designed context-independent (reconstructs from committed branches, `## Test decision` records, `.pending-docs/`; heavy per-branch reading happens in spawned sub-agent windows), so running it in a session bloated with one task's implementation gives zero benefit and biases the merge gate with the implementer's own rationalizations. Both messages now recommend **`/clear` (or a new session), then `/review-close`**, with the one-line *why* — extends the Phase-73 `/clear`-nudge pattern; `/claim-task → /document-work` stays same-session (docs need the fresh implementation context). **GDP parity (the item's same-in-both requirement) is the remaining leg** — the two rewords must mirror to GDP (a separate repo); the item stays open in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` with the Sysop leg ✓.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 76's + 77's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cells (`1cc5903` #27; `07d6efd` #28) in both phase-log tables.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — the duplication / data-loss / override-suppression / demotion-resurrection failure modes were all verified against the real `install.sh` and BeanRider's live overlays and cleared. One **SHOULD-FIX** applied: the partial mis-listed a `security_map.md` reminder as a *Step 9* artifact and put `security_map.project.md` in the Step 9 git-add, but both skills write Step 9 reminders to `convention_map.md` (BeanRider confirms: 7 reminders in `convention_map.project.md`, 0 in `security_map.project.md`) and their Step 9 git-adds correctly omit it — the canonical partial would have re-seeded the exact clobber class it fixes; corrected to state security-audit's Step 9 reminders go to the convention map, and `security_map.project.md` is the durable home for security-map *sections* staged by the Step 2a / 9b commits. Three NITs applied (scoped the `__disabled_no_op__` override to checks.yml-mechanism rules in the partial + both skills; softened the test comment's "would be dropped" over-claim; fixed `/document-work`'s "reviews *all* pending branches" → "this branch and any others awaiting close" for the single-task skill). Markdown + one-test-file change → **475 tests green**, role guard + manifests + leak scan clean. Inline close-out; the Medium base-map clobber item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md), the handoff item kept open with its GDP-parity leg. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 79 (executed 2026-07-06 — public `docs/getting-started.md` tutorial: the missing Diátaxis quadrant)

Closes the Medium launch-prep item filed 2026-07-06 by Phase 76. Sysop shipped a Quickstart (README), reference (`WORKFLOW.md`), and explanation (`workflow.html`) but **no permanent public *tutorial*** — the hand-held install → `/intake` → `/claim-task` → `/document-work` → `/review-close` → "you shipped" walkthrough. The internal tester onboarding note (`tools/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md`) was a round-scoped superset that could seed it.

**Chosen next over the two live alternatives** (`sitrep_survey.py` test-coverage backfill; any-agent portability validation), ratified with the user via `AskUserQuestion`: the next real gate is the private tester round, and a permanent tutorial is the highest-leverage launch-prep artifact — the tester note can point at it for mechanics and stay focused on "what we want feedback on," and it's the one Diátaxis quadrant the docs lacked. Low-risk markdown, needed regardless.

**Shape (per the filing's ratified recommendation): markdown, not a second HTML monograph.** A step-by-step walkthrough names exact commands and outputs — the most staleness-prone content there is (the Phase-62 rot problem) — so it belongs in the cheapest-to-keep-accurate format, and readers look for a linked "Getting Started," not a separate `.html`. New `docs/getting-started.md` (ships publicly — `tools/make_public_mirror.sh` excludes only `tools/` + the internal-tracking files, so `docs/` lands in both the tester and public mirrors), linked as the first **README "Read next"** bullet. **Claude-Code-primary by necessity** (the lifecycle skills are Claude-shaped slash commands) with an honest closing *Running on another agent* section that frames portability as **design intent, not an earned record** — aligns with the still-open any-agent validation item, so the tutorial can't over-claim ahead of it. A light pointer added to `tools/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` "Start here" (the filing's anticipated seed relationship).

**Grounding.** Every command/skill-behavior claim traced to the real skills + `install.sh` before writing: the `/intake` brain-dump→playback→sounding-board→phases→priority→emit loop and its three artifacts (`vision.md` / `decisions.md` / `index.yml`+bodies, left uncommitted); `/claim-task`'s lock + sibling worktree + convention lookup + adversarial plan review; `/document-work`'s commit + deferred-doc + push + the Phase-78 `/clear`-before-`/review-close` handoff (quoted from `document-work/SKILL.md:351`); `/review-close`'s survey-all-branches + `direct`/`pr` merge policy; the one-line blurbs for `/next-task` / `/roadmap` / `/daily-summary` / `/sitrep` / `/auto-claim` / `/report-issues`.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — every relative link resolved, zero identifier leaks, skill descriptions substantially accurate. All 4 should-fixes + 3 NITs applied:
- **SF1 (real correctness bug):** the step-1 install commit (`git add .claude/ SYSOP_ISSUES.md`) was incomplete — `install.sh` also writes `scripts/`, `WORKFLOW.md` / `WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md`, and the `tasks/` scaffold to the repo root (confirmed against WORKFLOW §8.7 Port checklist), and the reviewer **empirically** confirmed the sharp edge: a `git worktree` only carries *committed* files, so an uncommitted `scripts/` is absent from the worktree `/claim-task` creates — silently breaking any later hook/check step that runs from there. Fixed the tutorial (`git status` review + `git add .claude/ scripts/ WORKFLOW.md WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md tasks/ SYSOP_ISSUES.md` + the "What landed" list), and **bundled** the identical incomplete `git add` in the **README Quickstart** (line 14) for consistency.
- **SF2:** the worktree/session choreography was unstated (a first-timer would run `/document-work` from `main` and see nothing) → step 3 now names the printed `Work in: <path>` and that follow-ups act on the task branch in the same session; step 5 clarifies `/review-close` runs from the main checkout because it surveys all pending branches.
- **SF3:** the `bash 4+` prerequisite was omitted (macOS ships 3.2 → immediate hard stop at `install.sh:39`) → added to "Before you start."
- **SF4:** the inline `## Merge policy: pr` form diverged from the two-line template (`WORKFLOW.md` §6.1) → shown as the canonical heading-then-`pr` block.
- **NITs:** guided-mode + merge-policy now note "create `CLAUDE.md` if you don't have one" (the installer writes none); `/claim-task`'s "runs the deterministic checks" softened (the `run_checks.sh` gate fires at `/review-close`, not claim-task — reinforces the "review is the gate" thesis); `/next-task` ordering corrected to unblocker-first primary / cheapest-effort tiebreak (Phase 74's real `(unlock_count desc, effort asc, id)` sort).

**Scoped OUT (filed Low-priority):** the README install-section's own `git add .claude/settings.json .claude/sysop.lock SYSOP_ISSUES.md` (line 66) carries the same incompleteness but is a deliberate "contract files" statement in dense launch prose — reworking it is a separate call, not a tutorial-phase drive-by.

**Gate:** markdown-only → **475 tests green** (unchanged); public-mirror leak-scan clean (no internal identifiers, no absolute paths, no `wade-flow` residue in the new doc); all four relative-link targets resolve on disk. Inline close-out; the Medium getting-started item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 80 (executed 2026-07-07 — `/test-audit` standing test-quality assessment skill + `test-assessment-rubric.md`)

Closes the Medium item filed 2026-07-06 (main-session), decisions ratified 2026-07-07. Builds the skill the [`tools/TEST_AUDIT_SPEC.md`](./tools/TEST_AUDIT_SPEC.md) spec (filed the same morning, commit `ba69ead` #37) designed and the 2026-07-07 ratification (all 7 decisions on their spec recommendations) unblocked.

**The gap it closes.** Every test mechanism in Sysop is **forward-facing / diff-anchored**: `## Test decision` (58b) covers the current task, adversarial #7 judges the current plan, `/review-close` Step 2d verifies the current diff, the coverage gate (61a/61b) measures **only changed crown-jewel lines** by design, and `/codebase-review`'s "Test Coverage Gaps" is per-file/reactive. Two capabilities had **no home**: (1) *standing* coverage assessment — a module 0%-covered for a year but never in a diff produces zero findings anywhere; (2) *existing-test health* — obsolete / redundant / hollow tests, flagged today only by one reactive `/codebase-review` bullet. `/test-audit` is the structural replacement for the ad-hoc "occasionally ask Opus to look for weak testing" practice — and, like `decomposition-rubric.md` / `adversarial-review.md`, **the value is the calibrated rubric, not the skill shell.**

**Built (the 60a→60b pattern: spine + provisional rubric together, then calibrate from runs).** **Leg A — the spine** `core/skills/test-audit/SKILL.md`: read-only (`disallowed-tools: Edit, Write, NotebookEdit`, Phase 54), `reasoning`-role (Phase-69 marker; judgment work like `/roadmap`/`/intake`, opus default, resolver no-op), `/roadmap`-shaped. Reads the source + test trees (`Read`/`Grep`); the crown-jewel globs by parsing the `critical_path:` entries of `.claude/checks.yml`'s `coverage-*` checks (the authoritative crown-jewel signal — *not* CLAUDE.md — with an explicit **placeholder guard**: the shipped fragment's `<critical path module>/` angle-bracket globs mean the consumer hasn't designated crown jewels, so treat the signal as absent and fall back to CLAUDE.md § Scope mapping / `convention_map.md` headers, exactly as `/codebase-review` bounds its surface); and — *optionally, if already on disk* — a whole-repo coverage artifact (`coverage.xml` / `lcov.info`) as enrichment only. Default scope **crown-jewel-first** (the same signal that says "gate this path" says "audit this path hardest"), then outward by exposure; whole-repo is an explicit `--all` opt-in (a standing judgment audit over a very large suite risks the context window → per-module-chunked + no-silent-caps "what was reached / not reached"). Flags `--path` / `--all` / `--tier1` / `--tier2`. Output: a ranked report per weak surface (why load-bearing, the recommended test or the retire/keep verdict, a confidence), closing with an offer to route accepted recs into `/intake` — **informs, does not actuate** (never writes a test, claims a task, or mutates the queue). **Leg B — the calibrated rubric** `core/skills/_shared/test-assessment-rubric.md` (the **8th shared partial**, pin-less prose → no role marker, auto-ships via the `install_skills()` `_shared/` glob, zero CI impact). Ships **provisional** (calibration-pending blockquote): **Tier 1** (worth a new test — load-bearing-invariant vocab reused from adversarial #7 [guards, error/exception paths, boundaries, security/data-integrity, parsers], the *covered-but-hollow* tell a coverage % can't see, and the **negative discipline** — don't manufacture busywork tests for trivial glue/config/re-exports); **Tier 2a** (provably-dead — production referent gone via `git grep -nw`, deprecated path, indefinite skip/xfail: static, immediate, high-confidence, fires first run, with the Phase-58a-#9 FP guard for dynamic-dispatch/string-keyed/re-exported referents + "a conditional skip is not a dead skip"); **Tier 2b** (judgment retirement — redundant/brittle/hollow, each carrying a confidence label + the specific named sibling / observable-behavior evidence + keep-when-unsure). The **scoping nuance** made explicit: only the Tier-2b judgment dimensions calibrate over runs; **Tier 1 + 2a fire correctly on the first run** (obsolescence-by-dead-referent is a fact, not a judgment) — nothing about the feature waits for N rounds.

**Decisions realized** (all 7 ratified per their spec recommendation): new skill not a `/codebase-review` bolt-on (Decision 1) **but single-source the judgment** — `/codebase-review`'s "Test Coverage Gaps" dimension re-pointed at the shared rubric (the `/plan-review`→`adversarial-review.md` pattern); name `/test-audit` (2); judgment-first + optional enrichment (3); read-only prose report routing to `/intake` (4); **Tier 1 + 2a + 2b all shipped** — 2b was cheap to bundle (markdown-only, read-only, confidence-labeled) so it did not fast-follow (5); provisional-then-calibrate scoped to 2b only (6); `(C3)` reconciled as the automated always-on signal that becomes this skill's optional `--report` enrichment if ever built, kept separately deferred (7).

**Delivery (all auto-ship; no installer/manifest edit):** skill + rubric via the `install_skills()` directory loop; **no new permission rules** (base path pure `Read`/`Grep`; the optional coverage-artifact read is a file read; per `_shared/permission-guard.md` § Notes read-only ops aren't listed). Docs: WORKFLOW.md §8.3 (7→8 partials + the new bullet) + a §6.5 "Standing test assessment" paragraph after the coverage-gate para (the gate is diff-scoped; `/test-audit` is the standing complement; they form a loop); WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md helper-skills list + `tasks/README.md` skill table (beside `/roadmap`/`/daily-summary`). Spec status line flipped to BUILT.

**Gate:** markdown-only → **475 tests green** (unchanged; the role-guard CI accepts the new roled skill); role guard green **source + installed**; leak-scan clean; 13 manifests valid; **install round-trip** ships both files with the Phase-69 resolver a byte-for-byte no-op (reasoning→opus default). **Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — every load-bearing cross-reference verified against the real files (coverage gate genuinely diff-scoped; crown-jewel signal genuinely `critical_path:` not CLAUDE.md; `/codebase-review` dimension genuinely per-file; adversarial #7/#9 + permission-guard § Notes + the placeholder-glob strings all byte-exact; read-only contract holds; rubric genuinely actionable not platitude). **SHOULD-FIX (a real leak):** the `--all` bullet used "**GDP-scale**" as an unframed size unit — a strip-class internal identifier in shipped launch-facing content (violates the no-gdp-identifiers rule; distinct from WORKFLOW's *framed* GDP worked-examples) → genericized to "a large monorepo (tens of thousands of lines)." **3 NITs applied:** the bare `(C3)` checklist-ID reframed to "a deferred automated coverage signal (tracked as `(C3)` in Sysop's own roadmap)" so an external reader isn't puzzled (heading + all 3 uses); "fall back to step 3" disambiguated from Step 3 → "item 3 below"; "demotion-style audit loop" softened to "an audit loop" (`(C3)` isn't the Phase-62/67 demotion loop). Post-fix re-grep confirms zero GDP/gdp residue in shipped `test-audit/` + rubric; role guard re-green.

**Follow-up (recommended, non-blocking):** the rubric's cross-suite **calibration** (Sysop's own 475-test suite + `PORT_LOG.md` classifications, BeanRider, GDP) — only the Tier-2b judgment dimensions need it; the 60b move for this rubric. Filed as the open calibration leg. Inline close-out; the Medium `/test-audit` item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 81 (executed 2026-07-07 — `/contribute-convention`: the convention give-back transport)

Closes the Low-priority candidate item filed 2026-07-06 (main-session, "can they submit convention findings back?"). Chosen by Wade over the two other buildable launch-prep candidates (`/release`; hardening) via `AskUserQuestion`, with the command name (`/contribute-convention` over `/propose-pack`) and the issue-grouping unit (one issue per target pack) both ratified the same way.

**The gap it closes.** Sysop's whole pack model is "grow your own pack from real use" — conventions earn promotion from recurring review findings and land in the never-managed `.claude/*.project.*` overlay (the Phase 78 promotion write target). But the give-back was **asymmetric**: `/report-issues` (Phase 71) transports *friction* upstream, and nothing transported the more valuable contribution CONTRIBUTING.md names first — a locally-promoted convention or a grown pack. That give-back — the loop the open-source thesis depends on, and a clean differentiator vs. the closed, Claude-Code-only Caliper — was a hand-authored GitHub issue, exactly the manual step the transport skills exist to remove.

**Built.** One new skill `core/skills/contribute-convention/SKILL.md` (468 lines), the **third GitHub-touching skill** after `/pr-dependabot` and `/report-issues`, mirroring `/report-issues`' transport shape closely (permission guard → `gh auth` → resolve upstream repo → render → per-item consent → `gh issue create` → annotate the source → report). `reasoning`-role (Phase-69 marker, opus default, resolver no-op). Flow: **read** the never-managed overlay (`convention_map.project.md` / `checks.project.yml` / `--include-security` `security_map.project.md`) — consumer-only (`.claude/sysop.lock` present); never the Sysop-shipped base maps (already upstream); **parse** into candidates, excluding suppression/override checks + verbatim-upstream restatements + already-contributed markers; **discover provenance** from `review_tasks.md` cross-round survival (the earn-their-way bar, shown not asserted; refuses to fabricate a recurrence count when the overlay was hand-authored — the human attests instead); **generalize** each rule to placeholder vocabulary the packs already teach (the value-add + the reason it's a reasoning task, with a "don't gut the rule / exclude-if-you-can't-generalize" discipline); **classify + group one issue per target pack** (existing populated / placeholder-to-populate / new-pack-skeleton); **render** the exact `pack_or_convention`-shaped body (label `enhancement`) — **shown-equals-filed** repurposed as the *no-fingerprints* contract; **consent** per pack (dry-run default, `--execute` required); **file** upstream to `getsysop/sysop` (`--repo` forks + Batch-F 404 caveat) with the body written to a temp file **outside the repo** + `--body-file` + single-quoted title (the exact RCE hazard `/report-issues` Step 4 fixed — convention text is dense with backticks/`$`); **annotate** the source overlay per candidate as the double-file backstop.

**Skill, not a script** — same rationale as `/report-issues`: the overlay is deliberately loose consumer-restructurable markdown, and generalizing a rule into fingerprint-free placeholder vocabulary without gutting it is judgment, not parsing. **Scope OUT (v1):** auto-opening PRs, auto-editing `packs/`, any Sysop-repo write beyond an issue.

**Delivery (all auto-ship):** skill via the `install_skills()` directory loop (no installer/manifest edit); **no new permission rules** — reuses the `Bash(gh issue create:*)` + `Bash(gh issue list:*)` rules Phase 71 already added to the `settings.json` template; the `pack_or_convention.md` issue template (label `enhancement`) already exists. Docs: CONTRIBUTING.md § "Contributing conventions and packs" (the primary pointer, mirroring the "Reporting friction" shape), WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md helper-skills list (beside `/report-issues`), WORKFLOW.md § promotion-write-target note (the overlay is also the give-back read source), README.md § project-specific extensions.

**Gate:** markdown-only → **475 tests green** (unchanged; the role-guard CI accepts the new roled skill); role guard green **source + installed**; leak-scan clean (two illustrative examples that carried a consumer flavor genericized); **install round-trip** ships the skill with the Phase-69 resolver a byte-for-byte no-op (reasoning→opus default). **Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES** — one real **BLOCKER (B1)**: Step 2's "skip bullets verbatim in the base map" self-defeated because `install.sh` appends the consumer's `.project.md` **verbatim** into the base `convention_map.md` (WORKFLOW §8.2c) — so *every* overlay bullet also sits in the base map's appended region, and a naive check would exclude 100% of candidates (verified against BeanRider's real 244-line base map, overlay appended at lines 138–244) → fixed by scoping the comparison to the base map's **upstream region** (subtract the appended overlay first). Four **SHOULD-FIXES**, all applied: **S1** the no-provenance human attestation was collected at consent (Step 7), *after* the body was shown — breaking shown-equals-filed and bypassing generalization → moved to a Step 3 conversational turn *before* render, flowing through Step 4 generalization; **S2** section-level annotation + section-level ineligibility permanently stranded a partly-contributed section's remainder → made the backstop **per-candidate** (a `— filed: <subjects>` list), so a re-run can send the remainder; **S3** `checks.project.yml` had no working dedup marker (`>` is a YAML block-scalar indicator, not a comment) → checks use a `# Contributed upstream:` comment; **S4** the checks suppression-exclusion only caught the exact sentinel `["__disabled_no_op__"]` and missed `used_by: []` disables + sentinel-with-extra-paths + overrides of ids already in the base `checks.yml` → match the sentinel by **containment** + skip any entry whose `id` already exists in the base (verified against BeanRider's real `logger-fstring`/`todo-vs-deferred` overrides). Two **NITs** applied (Step 0.6 "Step 6"→"Step 8" cross-ref; **bundled** a Phase-62-class staleness fix — CONTRIBUTING.md still listed `beancount` as a placeholder pack, populated since Phase 43b, which the new skill's Step 5 contradicted → moved to populated); **N3** ($TMPDIR mechanics, faithful to the sibling) left as-is per the reviewer. Post-fix re-gate green; the backstop marker strings verified matching between the Step 2 read sites and the Step 8 write sites.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 80's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`2c47968` #38) in both phase-log tables. Inline close-out; the Low-priority `/contribute-convention` candidate item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 82 (executed 2026-07-07 — `/sitrep` cross-check coverage: the two functions Phase 48 deferred)

Closes the Medium hardening item filed 2026-05-27 by Phase 48 — the two multi-source cross-check functions in `core/companion/scripts/sitrep_survey.py` (`_find_discrepancies`, `_classify_review_batches`) that Phase 48's `/sitrep` test pass left uncovered because both "demand a stack of mocks deep enough to be more test-fixture than test." Chosen by Wade over three other launch-prep candidates (`/release`; the `<project>/CLAUDE.md` schema doc; the any-agent portability audit) via `AskUserQuestion`, as the one piece of pure builder work fully in-session with no external dependency (no non-Claude agent, no greenfield project, no tester signal). The next real gate is the private tester round, and `/sitrep` is load-bearing for cold-resume — the survey a tester leans on to answer "what was I doing?" — so a regression net under its two blind spots de-risks that round.

**The deferral's premise turned out softer than feared.** Each function isolates a *single* subprocess boundary, not the deep fixture stack Phase 48 anticipated: `_find_discrepancies` shells out once (`_git(["branch", "--list", …])`) and otherwise runs pure logic over `Lock`/`Worktree`/`index` plus a real `Path.is_dir()` for stale-lock detection; `_classify_review_batches` has two (`_git` rev-parse for branch existence + `_commits_ahead_of_main` for the Doc-Work trailer tally). So the tests mock only those boundaries — `_git` via a `side_effect` that keys on `args[:2]`, `_commits_ahead_of_main` via a branch→commits map, workspace existence driven with real `tmp_path` dirs — and let every load-bearing loop, the `_derive_task_id_from_branch` suffix-uppercase fallback, the `batch_task_ids & all_dw_ids` intersection, and the `done vs total` classification run for real.

**+20 tests** (`tests/test_sitrep_survey.py`, all Sysop-original): 9 for `_find_discrepancies` (stale lock present/absent/empty-workspace, orphan worktree, worktree→index-drift isolated from the index-scan double-emit via a non-`in_progress` status, worktree+branch+lock all-clean, orphan branch, the non-task-shaped/in-index skips, the orphan-branch *lock* skip distinct from the `wt_branches` short-circuit, index-scan drift with a locked-negative fold, empty-inputs) and 11 for `_classify_review_batches` (terminal-status skip, pending flagged→`/auto-judge` / unflagged→`/triage` / the 55-char flag truncation incl. the `rstrip()` space-before-ellipsis path, claimed-no-branch, empty batch, ready-for-`/review-close`, in-progress partial, in-progress zero-trailer, the `has_lock`-True fall-through, and both `has_branch` signals — worktree membership *and* the rev-parse fallback). **495 tests green** (was 475). Purely **additive** — no source change, so the prior 475 stay green and the phase is behavior-preserving by construction.

**Surfaced, not fixed (kept the diff additive):** `_find_discrepancies` carries three dead parameters — `stale_days` is never referenced in the body, and `classified` feeds only a `by_id` dict that is itself never read (a leftover from a removed abandoned-claim check, per the `# … already surface as state='stale' above` comment). Removing them would ripple to the `run_survey` call site and cross the line from "test coverage" into "signature refactor," so it's **filed Low-priority** rather than bundled; the test helper passes `[]`/`7` for them, which is harmless since they're ignored.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — the reviewer hand-traced every branch and ran the suite, confirming the tests are **non-tautological** (delete any discrepancy-emit branch or flip any classification comparison and a specific test goes red), the mock signatures match the real callables exactly (positional args + `cwd`/`check` kwargs, `args[:2]` slicing), and no real subprocess leaks. One real **SHOULD-FIX (SF1)**: the in-progress-partial test supplied a commit whose `doc_work_ids` were a strict subset of the batch's own task ids, so a plausible bug — `done = len(all_dw_ids)` (count *every* branch trailer, ignoring batch membership) — would have survived the whole suite → strengthened by adding a stray `TASK-99` trailer absent from the batch, which under the bug flips `done` to 2 → `done == total` → "ready" and fails the test. Three **NITs** applied, each covering a genuinely distinct branch the initial set missed: (1) a `has_lock`-True Pending batch (proves the claimed-Pending fall-through, not `pending (not claimed)`); (2) a lock-backed branch *not* in a worktree (the orphan-branch-loop `l.branch == b` skip, which the all-clean test never reached because `b in wt_branches` short-circuits first); (3) a `flag_reason` whose 55th char is whitespace (exercises `flag_reason[:55].rstrip()`, whose purpose — no `" …"` artifact — the whitespace-free inputs never triggered). NIT5 (a docstring that overclaimed the lock-skip coverage) corrected in the same pass. The reviewer independently confirmed the dead-param observation above.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 81's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`1a8add5` #39) in both phase-log tables. Inline close-out; the Medium `/sitrep`-coverage item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md), the dead-param cleanup filed Low. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 83 (executed 2026-07-07 — `/release`: the release-authoring skill)

Closes the Medium candidate filed 2026-07-06 by the main-session launch-prep gap analysis (REVIEW_CHECKLIST line ~52) — chosen by Wade this session, and offered (declined) in the Phase 81 and Phase 82 `AskUserQuestion` rounds before that. The gap it fills is real and structural: pressure-testing the positioning line *"Sysop gives one builder and an AI the engineering discipline of a full team, from first idea to a verified deploy"* surfaced that Sysop had **no release-management leg**. `/review-close` Step 5 verifies a *single* deploy (waits on the pipeline + runs a post-deploy smoke), but nothing managed a *release* — no versioning, no changelog, no notes across the **many** review-close cycles a release bundles. `/daily-summary` is close kin but windows by **date**, not by release boundary, and is read-only. So a release is a genuinely distinct cadence → a distinct skill, not a `/review-close` bolt-on.

New `core/skills/release/SKILL.md` — the **write-side sibling of `/review-close`** (no `disallowed-tools` guard: it writes `CHANGELOG.md`, creates/pushes a git tag, and can publish a GitHub Release), `reasoning`-role (Phase-69 marker `<!-- sysop:model-roles frontmatter=reasoning -->`; opus default; the resolver leaves it byte-for-byte no-op). It is a **layered join**, not "just git logs": (1) window anchor = **last git tag → HEAD** (this is what makes it *release* management vs. `/daily-summary`'s day-window; first-release fallback to full history); (2) commits → **`/daily-summary`'s conventional-commit classifier**, reused verbatim (the category table is kept in sync as deliberate parallel copies; `/release` additionally flags breaking-change markers for the bump); (3) `tasks/index.yml` → the **human-readable layer** — done-since-tag tasks joined by real titles, ID-prefix categories, and `blast_radius` as a highlights signal, because a commit subject is terse where a task title is meaningful; (4) **PR links via `gh`** only under `pr` merge policy (optional enrichment, degrades silently); (5) **a proposed semver bump** from commit types (`feat`→minor / `fix`→patch / `BREAKING`→major), human-confirmed. Output artifacts (v1, all human-gated): a Keep-a-Changelog `CHANGELOG.md` entry, an annotated `git tag`, and — opt-in — a GitHub Release. Deliberately **lightweight**: staged rollout / canary / feature-flag orchestration / rollback runbooks are the *operations* band Sysop holds the line on (chasing it turns Sysop into Datadog/PagerDuty territory and dilutes the convention-ratchet identity) — that's the deferred **(D) rollback / staged-rollout** sibling; this skill is release *authoring/recording*, that one is release *operating*.

**Two decisions ratified via `AskUserQuestion`** (both recommendations accepted):

- **Version source = tag-based, manifest read-only.** Base version = the last tag, or a **read-only** field from a *detected* manifest (`package.json` / `pyproject.toml` / `plugin.json`) if no tag, or `0.0.0`. The skill **never rewrites a manifest** — it prints the new version so the human bumps it through their own flow. This matches the filed artifact list (changelog + tag, no manifest write) and is the honest default given Sysop itself is deliberately unversioned. Manifest-writing is a filed v2 deferral. (Alternatives declined: tag-plus-manifest-write — stack-specific, riskier arbitrary-manifest parsing; tag-only-ignore-manifests — gives no starting version to manifest-versioned projects with no tags.)
- **Outward reach = local + tag push by default; GitHub Release opt-in.** Dry-run is the default (renders the full plan, writes/creates nothing). `--execute` writes the changelog + creates and pushes the tag, each human-confirmed. The public GitHub Release needs a **second** explicit `--github-release` opt-in. (Alternatives declined: full-release-under-`--execute` — larger default outward footprint; local-artifacts-only — most conservative but finishes the release by hand.)

**A load-bearing design call (mine, documented in the skill): the changelog is written but left uncommitted.** Committing it would need either a direct push to `main` (rejected under `pr` merge policy, where `main` is protected) or a whole PR flow — scope that belongs to `/review-close`, not a lightweight release skill. So `/release` writes the entry and hands the commit to the human's merge policy; the **tag** is the durable release marker (it points at already-shipped code on `origin/main`), and the changelog documents it and lands right after. Release hygiene preconditions (Step 2) enforce that the tag marks *shipped* code: on the release branch (default `main`), HEAD already contained in `origin/<branch>` (else "run `/review-close` first"), and a warn on a dirty tree.

**Delivery:** auto-ships via the `install_skills()` dir-glob (no installer/manifest edit). **+2 permission rules** in the `core/companion/.claude/settings.json` template — `Bash(git tag:*)` and `Bash(gh release create:*)`; the tag push reuses the existing `Bash(git push origin:*)`, and read-only `gh release view` / `git fetch` / `gh auth status` are unlisted per `_shared/permission-guard.md` § Notes. Step 0's guard requires rules **conditionally** (nothing on the dry-run path; `git tag`+`git push origin` under `--execute`; `gh release create` under `--github-release`) — the same policy-gated shape as `/review-close`'s `pr`-only requirement. Docs: WORKFLOW_GUIDE helper-skills list, `tasks/README.md` skill table, and a `CHANGELOG.md` row in WORKFLOW.md's project-files table (mirroring how `/report-issues` registered `SYSOP_ISSUES.md`).

**Gate:** markdown + JSON only → **495 tests green** (unchanged; the role-guard CI test accepts the new roled skill). Role guard green source + installed (`release/SKILL.md:5 reasoning -> opus`); leak-scan clean; `settings.json` valid; fresh `install.sh` round-trip rc 0 — ships the skill, both new rules land in the installed allow-list, and the Phase-69 resolver leaves the installed skill byte-for-byte identical to source.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES.** One real **BLOCKER (B1)**: Step 8.3 inlined the auto-generated tag message into `git tag -a … -m "<summary>"`, but that summary is synthesized from commit subjects + task titles that routinely carry backticks, `$`, and quotes **by design** — bash would run command/variable substitution and, worst case, **execute approved release-note text as a shell command** (the exact hazard `/report-issues` Step 4.2 fixed with `--body-file`, and which *this skill already avoided* for the GitHub-release notes in Step 9). Fixed to write the summary to a temp file via `Write` and pass `git tag -a … -F <file>` (git ≥ 2.x; verified available). Two **SHOULD-FIXES**: **S1** — the Step-2 branch/tip guarantee is stale by the time the tag is created, because the Step-8.1 `AskUserQuestion` version gate is an arbitrary pause during which a concurrent Sysop loop or manual `git checkout` can move `HEAD` in the shared primary worktree (exactly what `_shared/main-push-guard.md` Rule A guards) → re-assert the branch **and** `git merge-base --is-ancestor HEAD origin/main` immediately before the `git tag` write; the subsequent tag *push* needs no HEAD re-assert (a tag is an immutable ref already created on verified-pushed code, unlike a branch push). **S2** — `git describe --tags --abbrev=0` returns the most-recent reachable tag regardless of shape, so a consumer's date tag (`2026-07-01`), a name tag (`beta`), or **Sysop's own `wade-flow-extract-base`** would feed garbage into "strip the prefix" → added a semver-shape guard that falls through to the first-release path with a clear note (`pass --as X.Y.Z`).
