Four **NITs**, all applied: the classifier-parity claim overstated identity (table is identical, but `/release` adds breaking detection — reworded to "mirror the table, not the breaking-detection"); the changelog release date used the tip-commit date behind an inaccurate "can't call `date` reliably" claim (→ portable `date +%Y-%m-%d`, since plain formatting has no BSD/GNU divergence, with the tip-commit date as fallback); a one-line note that `0.y.z` collapses breaking and `feat` into the same minor bump (the human sets the exact number at the Step-8.1 gate); and the "as portable as `/daily-summary`" claim scoped to exclude the optional `gh pr list` enrichment (which relies on the existing `Bash(gh pr list:*)` rule and degrades silently). **N5** (`git fetch` in dry-run) confirmed no-change — read-only w.r.t. the remote and consistent with the siblings. A bundled coherence fix followed B1: Step 7's dry-run "show the exact `git tag -a` command" was reworded to reflect the `-F` file form.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 82's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`1c6604e` #40) in both phase-log tables. **Filed Low-priority (discovered, not fixed):** WORKFLOW.md §8.2a's permission JSON block + rule table is a stale *partial* mirror of the real `settings.json` template — it lists none of the `gh` family (`gh pr` / `gh issue` / `gh release`), nor `next_task.py` / `sitrep_survey.py` / `pr_dependabot.py` / `git tag`; the three prior `gh`-adding phases (53 / 54 / 71) never synced it, so the established precedent is "update the real template, leave §8.2a." Rather than half-sync a single `gh` rule into a `gh`-less block, I followed that precedent and filed the drift (resync fully, or reframe §8.2a explicitly as an illustrative core subset). Inline close-out; the Medium `/release` candidate moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 84 (executed 2026-07-07 — bash script lifecycle test coverage)

Closes the long-open Phase-47 **"Bash script test coverage"** item (filed 2026-05-27): Sysop's seven lifecycle shell scripts had **zero** automated coverage. Chosen by Wade over two other in-session launch-prep candidates (Caliper's real-time post-turn convention checks; a tester-facing polish bundle) via `AskUserQuestion`, as the highest-leverage way to de-risk the imminent private tester round — `install.sh` is already integration-tested (`test_install_*.py`), but the scripts a tester actually exercises through `/claim-task` → `/review-close` (`claim_task.sh`, `close_batch.sh`, `cleanup_worktrees.sh`, `batch_work.sh`, `install_hooks.sh`, `run_checks.sh`, `sysop-update.sh`) were untested. A regression there breaks a tester's first lifecycle cycle — exactly the fragility this phase removes.

**Harness.** The filed item speculated a `bats`-or-shellcheck harness; instead the tests reuse Sysop's **existing** integration pattern (`tests/test_install_detect.py` / `test_install_concat.py`): python-subprocess drives the real script against a scratch `git init` repo in `tmp_path` and asserts on exit code / stdout / stderr / filesystem. This keeps CI a single `pytest` invocation with **no new dependency** (no `bats`, no shellcheck in the matrix). Seven new files, one per script, each with a local `_git` / repo-builder helper (matching the per-file-duplication convention the install tests set). Scripts operating on their CWD's repo (`install_hooks`, `run_checks`, the review scripts) run with `cwd=repo_root`; `run_checks`/`sysop-update` success paths are stubbed (a fake `run_checks_impl.py` argv-echo; a fake `install.sh` in a git repo) so the wrapper contracts are locked without the real heavy machinery.

**What's locked.** The cheap, high-certainty guard/refusal paths first (they fire before any heavy setup): not-a-git-repo, unknown-flag + `${1:?}` usage, missing `SYSOP_SRC` (and its four sub-guards), absent `scripts/hooks/`, absent `review_tasks.md`. Then the crown-jewel safety invariants that are these scripts' reason for existing: `cleanup_worktrees.sh` **never removes the primary worktree** under `--force` (and `--clean` skips ACTIVE/dirty worktrees, uses non-force `git worktree remove`, deletes branches with safe `-d`); `close_batch.sh` **aborts loudly with exit 1 on commit failure** (BeanRider ISSUE-0015 — proven via a failing `.git/hooks/pre-commit`) and `--dry-run` leaves the file **byte-identical** and git history unchanged; `claim_task.sh` **never overwrites a live lock** and, from inside a linked worktree, resolves `.locks/` under the **main** repo via git-common-dir (the Phase-32 canonical-location invariant) with a populated `expires:` (anti-malformed-lock); `install_hooks.sh` **allowlist** — only `pre-commit`/`pre-merge-commit`/`pre-push` ever land in `.git/hooks/`, so a stray `.DS_Store`/`README.md`/`evil` dropped into `scripts/hooks/` is rejected — plus atomic install, executable bit, and backup-on-differ / no-backup-on-identical. The two review-driven scripts are tested against hand-authored `review_tasks.md` fixtures with **no `scripts/review_index.py`**, forcing the fragile pure-grep / bash-regex fallback (the code most worth locking).

**Two bundled fixes for a silent-abort bug class the coverage surfaced.** Writing the `close_batch.sh` tests immediately reddened on a Pending batch with no `**Branch:**` line: the `BRANCH_NAME=$(sed … | grep -o … | sed …)` pipeline has no `|| true`, so `grep`'s no-match (exit 1) under `set -euo pipefail` aborts the whole command-substitution assignment — **silently, rc 1, empty stderr** — defeating the script's own explicit "No branch metadata found. Proceeding" fallback three lines below. The sibling greps (task-count, Grand Total) already carry the `|| true` guard the ISSUE-0044 hardening added; this one was missed. Fixed with the same one-liner (verified by repro that `||` binds to the whole pipeline, masking only the grep no-match — `BATCH_START`/`BATCH_END` are always valid line numbers by this point, so nothing else in the pipeline can fail). The fresh-eyes review then confirmed the **identical** class at `batch_work.sh` L182 (`batch_end=$(… | grep -n '^##' …)` inside the directly-called `claim_batch`, where `set -e` is active — unlike `close_batch`'s `find_batch_range`, which is called under `if !` so `set -e` is suppressed). It is narrower (reachable only on the on-main auto-claim path: on main + clean tree + a reachable origin + the Pending batch being the file's last section with no trailing `##`), so I initially filed it — but the reviewer argued to bundle the proven one-liner rather than leave a known silent-abort of the exact class one file over, and I agreed. It ships **fixed + regression-tested** via a new claim-on-main test that also fills the previously-untested auto-claim-commit happy path; mutation-verified (removing the guard reddens the test, restoring it passes).

**Gate.** **558 tests green** (was 495; +63); `bash -n` clean on all seven scripts; tests deterministic across repeated runs (no leaked worktree/lock state). **Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — the reviewer empirically confirmed every crown-jewel test goes red under the obvious script mutation (non-tautological), the `close_batch` fix is correct/minimal/load-bearing (4 tests depend on it), and the `batch_work` scoping accurate in both directions (L182 reachable-but-narrow; L175 genuinely safe because the batch's existence is pre-verified by `parse_batches`). All findings applied: the SHOULD-FIX (bundle + lock the `batch_work` one-liner) and 2 NITs — added `close_batch.sh` `--force`-accept + unmerged-skip refusal tests (a path a tester hits), and hardened all commit-making fixtures against a contributor's global `commit.gpgsign` (added `commit.gpgsign=false`) and `core.hooksPath` (pinned in the commit-failure test so a global override can't neutralize the failing hook). Also tightened the MAIN-never-removed assertion to the exact `Force-removed 1 worktree(s), 0 failed.` message so the guard-removal mutation reddens it directly, not incidentally via rc. No new REVIEW_CHECKLIST items were filed — the reviewer's NITs were all addressed inline rather than deferred.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 83's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`960debb` #41) in both phase-log tables. Inline close-out; the Phase-47 bash-coverage item moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 85 (executed 2026-07-07 — launch-prep polish bundle: four accumulated low-priority fixes)

Chosen by Wade over three other in-session candidates (the `<project>/CLAUDE.md` schema doc; the post-turn convention-check feature; a data-integrity backport) via `AskUserQuestion`, as the highest tester-friction-removed-per-effort work ahead of the private tester round. The bundle closes **four** accumulated Low-priority items, one of them a *confirmed first-timer breakage*.

**Fix A — README Installation `git add` completeness (filed Phase 79, `REVIEW_CHECKLIST:50`).** The Installation section's post-install line (`README.md:67`) told the user to `git add .claude/settings.json .claude/sysop.lock SYSOP_ISSUES.md` — but `install.sh` also writes `scripts/`, `WORKFLOW.md`/`WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md`, and `tasks/` to the repo root (WORKFLOW §8.7), and a `git worktree` (what `/claim-task` creates) only sees **committed** files, so a first-timer following that line literally gets a worktree missing `scripts/` and the workflow docs → later hook/check steps break. Phase 79 fixed the tutorial + the README **Quickstart** but explicitly left this Installation-section line as a separate call (it's dense "these three are the *contract* files" prose, not a complete commit instruction). Reworded to commit the **whole payload** — `git add .claude/ scripts/ WORKFLOW.md WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md tasks/ SYSOP_ISSUES.md && git commit -m "chore: install Sysop"` (now byte-identical to the Quickstart at `:14` and `docs/getting-started.md:45`) — while **preserving** the contract-file framing as a "worth knowing by name" note (settings.json = harness contract, sysop.lock = `--update` contract, SYSOP_ISSUES.md = friction record). The reviewer confirmed via a real core-only install that the six `git add` entries are *exactly* what lands at the target root — no omission, no extra.

**Fix B — WORKFLOW.md §8.2a stale permission mirror (filed Phase 83, `:48`).** The illustrative `.claude/settings.json` JSON block + rule table at §8.2a was a **stale partial mirror** of the real template (`core/companion/.claude/settings.json`): three prior `gh`-adding phases (53/54/71) + Phase 83 (`git tag`) each updated the real template but left §8.2a untouched, so it listed **none** of the `gh` family, `git tag`, the `.venv/bin/python3` variants, or the `sitrep_survey.py`/`next_task.py`/`pr_dependabot.py` rules. Rather than a full resync that would just re-accrue drift on the next `gh`-adding phase, **reframed** it (the durable option the filed item offered): the intro now marks the block an "illustrative core subset" and names the installed file authoritative; a new note after the table enumerates the additional families the template carries + instructs "add new rules to the template — this subset is deliberately **not** kept in lockstep." The reviewer's programmatic set-diff confirmed the block is a genuine 27-of-48-rule subset (no phantom rules) and the enumeration covers exactly the 21 missing rules. One reviewer NIT applied: the `git add review_tasks.md` gloss was tightened from a loose "/codebase-review / /document-work" pairing to the accurate mapping (`git add review_tasks.md` → the four review skills; `git commit -m docs:*` → the `Doc-Work` shape) after `grep` confirmed `/document-work` does *not* `git add review_tasks.md`.

**Fix C — `install.sh --adopt` bare-target traceback (filed Phase 75, `:54`).** `install.sh <target> --adopt` on a target with **no** pre-existing `.claude/` crashed with a raw python `FileNotFoundError` (reproduced on HEAD before the fix). The filed diagnosis ("DRY_RUN writes nothing → `.claude/` never created") was incomplete — the real mechanism is `ensure_dir`'s `KNOWN_DIRS` **memo poisoning**: `cmd_adopt` runs `run_install_pipeline` under `DRY_RUN=1` to compute `managed_paths`, during which `ensure_dir "$TARGET/.claude"` caches the dir as *known* without mkdir'ing it; the later real `write_lock_file` → `ensure_dir` sees the memo hit and early-returns, so the mkdir never runs and the lock write opens a file in a nonexistent dir. This DRY_RUN-flip-within-one-process is **unique to `cmd_adopt`** (verified: the `saved_dry`/`DRY_RUN=1` pattern appears nowhere else). The fix is *not* a silent `mkdir` (that would mint a lock referencing phantom paths the dry-run never wrote) — adopting a target with no `.claude/` means there's **nothing to adopt**, so it's a graceful pre-check: absent `.claude/` → actionable error ("No existing Sysop install found … run a normal install first") + exit 1, placed after the lock-exists guard and before the crash site. Legit adopt (target *with* `.claude/`, no lock) is unaffected — the memo early-return is harmless once the dir exists on disk. **+2 integration tests** (`tests/test_install_adopt_sh.py`, the `test_install_*.py` subprocess pattern): the graceful-error case (rc≠0 + pointer + **no** `Traceback`) and a **non-tautological over-block guard** (real install → delete only the lock → adopt succeeds + rewrites the lock). The reviewer independently reproduced the pre-fix traceback via a guard-stripped copy, proving the guard load-bearing.

**Fix D — `_find_discrepancies` dead params (filed Phase 82, `:46`).** `core/companion/scripts/sitrep_survey.py::_find_discrepancies` carried three dead constructs surfaced by Phase 82's coverage work: `stale_days` (never referenced in the body), `classified` (fed only an unread `by_id = {…}` line), and the `by_id` line itself (assigned-never-read — a leftover from a removed abandoned-claim check). Dropped all three from the signature + the single `run_survey` call site + the Phase-82 test helper `_run_discrepancies` (which passed `[], stale_days` positionally). Purely a signature cleanup — no behavior change; the 65 sitrep tests stay green. The reviewer grep-confirmed `by_id` is empty repo-wide and no other caller exists.

**Gate.** **560 tests green** (was 558; +2 adopt integration tests; the sitrep signature change kept its 65 green). `bash -n install.sh` clean; leak-scan over the diff clean (the pre-existing README-provenance + WORKFLOW §6.2/6.3 worked-example gdp paths are untouched history, not in-diff); no manifest/role-guard impact (no skills touched). **Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP** — no blockers, no should-fixes; the one cosmetic NIT (the §8.2a `review_tasks.md` gloss) applied. Reviewer empirically verified each of the four fixes (real install enumeration for A; programmatic 48-vs-27 rule set-diff for B; guard-stripped traceback repro for C; repo-wide `by_id` grep for D) and confirmed the new adopt tests are non-tautological.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 84's stale `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`2a51f5f` #42) in both phase-log tables. Inline close-out; all four Low-priority items moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 87 (executed 2026-07-08 — `/intake` adopting mode: mature-project onboarding thin slice + ONBOARDING_SPEC)

Triggered by a design conversation this session. Wade asked whether `/intake` is only for greenfield scoping/vision or is also set up for **mid-project feature dev** — the recurring GDP pattern of *"I look at the site, it'd be good to have a button that does X → iterate a conversation → settle constraints → emit tasks into the roadmap."* The answer: `/intake`'s **re-entry** mode already covers mid-project feature work (Step 0 branches on it; Step 7 has a dedicated append path; the intent-layer coherence/staleness machinery exists precisely to make repeated mid-project invocations safe). But a check of GDP's *real* state exposed a Step-0 classifier seam: GDP has a 155 KB `tasks/index.yml` (~116 tasks) but **no** `tasks/vision.md` / `tasks/decisions.md` (it predates `/intake`, Phase 60), and Step 0's fresh-vs-re-entry branch keyed **only on the intent layer** — so a mature project with a populated queue but no intent files misreads as **"fresh"** and gets the greenfield *"tell me everything"* interview over a product that already exists. The conversation widened into a design for full mature-project onboarding; Wade said *"do both now"* — ship the small Step-0 fix and write the spec.

**The design (three capabilities, not one feature).** Captured in `tools/ONBOARDING_SPEC.md` (internal; `tools/` ships nowhere): (1) **intent-layer establishment** on a project with none; (2) **evidence-seeded reconstruction** — read code/git/docs to *draft* the intent layer rather than interview from a blank page; (3) **backlog import** — an existing roadmap/tracker → `index.yml` + bodies so the adopter runs `/next-task`/`/auto-claim` day one. They separate cleanly (import without reconstruct, and vice versa). The make-or-break correctness property is the **fabrication guard**: reconstruction infers a *rationale* that was never recorded (observing Postgres in the code is fact; *"chosen because transactional integrity over analytical throughput"* is a guess — and the `Rationale`/`Rules out` fields of a `decisions.md` entry are exactly where a confident hallucination lands) → **reconstruct observations high-confidence; render inferred rationale as a draft the human confirms** — the existing Step-2 playback discipline pointed at an evidence source. Vision is interview-*assisted*, not interview-*replaced* (code says *what* was built, never *who it's for* or *what v1's done-line was*). Placement: **detect + offer at Step 0** (shipped); the heavy seam is **in-repo vs external-tracker** (in-repo = pure `Read` + Phase-71's existing `gh issue list` rule, staying inside `/intake`'s zero-new-permissions envelope; Jira/Linear/Notion = new permission surface → separate module, the `/sitrep`↔`/roadmap` sibling precedent), **not** reconstruction-vs-import.

**The thin slice shipped (markdown-only, `core/skills/intake/SKILL.md`).** Step 0 rewritten from a two-case (fresh / re-entry) into a **three-case** classifier that reads `vision.md`, `decisions.md`, **and** `index.yml`: **fresh** (neither intent file, empty queue — plus a light *"is there real source beyond the Sysop scaffold?"* guard that confirms greenfield-vs-adopting instead of blindly interviewing), **re-entry** (either intent file present — load what exists, and if exactly one is missing author only the missing file, **never overwriting** the one that exists), **adopting** (neither intent file but the queue already lists tasks — name what you see → honest pros/cons → establish the intent layer by interview, **evidence-seeded only when the human hands over a doc** → rejoin re-entry, using a freshly-written vision as a lens to spot queued tasks that no longer serve it). An explicit **deferral blockquote** states that systematic code/git archaeology and backlog import are *planned, not built* — the skill never scans or imports on its own — and (Phase-77/86 mirror-leak discipline) **does not cite the internal `tools/` spec path**. The `description:` line was extended for discoverability. Deliberately scoped out (deferred to the spec): any code scan, git-history read, or task import; the fuzzy empty-queue-but-existing-codebase *detection* heuristic.

**Gate.** **560 tests green** (unchanged — markdown-only, no executable surface); role guard green source + installed (`reasoning=opus` marker untouched); leak-scan clean; no `tools/` reference in the shipped skill. **Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — one **SHOULD-FIX** (the classifier treated "intent layer present" as binary, but it's *two* files: a project with only `vision.md` **or** only `decisions.md` matched no case cleanly and, read as adopting, could **re-author/overwrite** the file that already exists → redefined presence explicitly: *either* file present → **re-entry**, author only the missing one, never overwrite) + 3 NITs all applied (the existing-codebase guard clarified as a light *presence* check, not the deferred *"never scans your code"* reconstruction; the `vision.md` artifact-shape parenthetical extended to cover adopting; the *"skip straight to decomposing"* path given a concrete landing — a scoped brain-dump, not the greenfield opener, then Steps 5–8 as re-entry). One edge I'd already fixed pre-review (an empty-queue project routed from the fresh-guard hitting adopting's populated-queue framing) reconciled cleanly with the SHOULD-FIX.

**Follow-up filed (Medium, non-blocking):** the deferred heavy build — evidence-seeded reconstruction (systematic) + in-repo backlog import + the external-tracker module + empty-queue adopting detection — **sequenced to let the private tester round calibrate it** (dogfood-before-build; the round is the ideal place to watch real mature-project onboarding friction before building the archaeology engine). Converges with the open any-agent portability item and the greenfield `/intake` dogfood (Phase 60b) — all three want a real new/existing project to exercise. **Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix:** filled Phase 86's `_PR pending_` Commit cell (`10a1578` #44) in both phase-log tables. Inline close-out. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 88 (executed 2026-07-08 — `/onboard`: the mature-project onboarding engine — evidence-seeded reconstruction + backlog import)

Triggered by Wade this session: the tester repo is live, and testers will be **onboarding existing projects** — so the Phase-87-deferred heavy build had to precede the round rather than be calibrated by it. That deliberately flips `tools/ONBOARDING_SPEC.md`'s "defer until tester signal" sequencing: the round now calibrates a shipped v1 instead of a design. Scope ratified via `AskUserQuestion`: a **new dedicated `/onboard` skill** (over expanding `/intake` inline — both legs are guided multi-step flows that would have roughly doubled a 233-line skill for a minority path; the `/sitrep`↔`/roadmap` sibling precedent), shipping **legs 1+2** (reconstruction + in-repo import), name **`/onboard`**; external trackers (leg 3, new permission surface) and empty-queue auto-detection heuristics (leg 4) stay deferred.

**The skill (`core/skills/onboard/SKILL.md`, `reasoning`-role, auto-ships via the `install_skills()` dir-glob — the 21st skill).** Two independent legs behind a Step-0 scope conversation, governed by two rules: **opt-in always** (detection/offers free; scans and imports only after an explicit yes — the consent block deliberately quotes no item count, since counting requires the read the yes gates) and the **fabrication guard** (observations recorded as fact; every inferred `Rationale`/`Rules out` marked `(inferred — confirm or correct)` and walked individually — no batch-accept; unadjudicated inferences stay `(unconfirmed)`, never silently promoted; three anti-rationalization blocks incl. "any reasonable engineer would have chosen X" = *your* rationale, not theirs). **Leg A — reconstruction:** presence-check-only evidence enumeration (README/docs≤depth-2 vendor-pruned/CHANGELOG/ADRs/manifests/git-log subjects — the Phase-75 scan-bounding heuristics), consent, then a **skeleton** draft (3–5 load-bearing decisions, per the spec's fabrication-risk argument; vision's Users + v1-done-line are interview questions, not archaeology), confirm-or-correct, write (never overwriting an existing intent file; provenance headers name `/onboard`, not `/intake`). **Leg B — import:** source discovery (roadmap/`TODO.md`/`BACKLOG.md`/legacy `product_roadmap.md`; `gh issue list` count-then-fetch with a **truncation guard** — returned count == limit → raise/paginate, never proceed silently); agent-read reasoning not a parser (Phase 68/71/81); decompose-and-enrich per the decomposition rubric; **dedup with a hold-don't-drop list** (every B2 item lands in proposed-imports or held-with-reason — no silent caps); chunked emit (~15 tasks/phase per chunk, validator between chunks) following `/intake` Step 7's write contract verbatim; everything left uncommitted. Ends by handing off to `/intake` (which picks up against the new intent layer, or offers to establish one if Leg A was skipped). **Zero new permission rules** — Write/Edit are file-level, `validate_tasks.py` + `gh issue list` rules pre-exist (Phase 6/71), presence checks + `git log` are read-only per `_shared/permission-guard.md` § Notes.

**The provenance mechanism (the one code change).** The spec's open decision — `surfaced_by: [imported]` — came back **negative** when checked: `validate_tasks.py` Invariant 6 requires every `surfaced_by` entry to resolve to a known task ID, so the spec's leaning would have failed validation. Phase 88 teaches the validator a **surfaced_by-only** lowercase sentinel `imported` (structurally collision-proof: the task-ID grammar requires a leading uppercase letter), with the field-scoping explicit — `depends_on: [imported]` still errors. `core/companion/tasks/schema.md` documents it (field row + Invariant 6); **+3 tests** (accept-sentinel / still-reject-unknown-ID / reject-in-depends_on — mutation-verified non-tautological by the reviewer). Downstream consumption is honest about its narrowness: **`/auto-claim`** re-estimates an imported candidate's `effort`/`blast_radius` from the body at check time (the same single read solo-invariant 1b already budgets) and runs its rules on the **heavier** of recorded vs. re-estimated per field — the discount can only tighten the gate; changes render as `Medium→High (re-est)` in the Step-4 table; `index.yml` is never rewritten by the gate. Doc claims scoped to match (schema.md/GUIDE name `/auto-claim`, not "downstream skills" — `next_task.py` and `/roadmap` read recorded effort verbatim).

**Wiring + docs.** `/intake` Step 0: fresh-guard and adopting branches route to `/onboard`; the Phase-87 "planned but not built" deferral note rewritten to describe the built capability (Phase-62 discipline — repo-wide grep confirms no stale claim survives; the remaining "planned separate module" lines correctly describe the still-unbuilt external-tracker module). `core/companion/tasks/README.md` (+`/onboard` row; the "authored only by `/intake`" exclusivity claim amended — it now contradicted the new row), `WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md` § 0 (adopting paragraph), `docs/workflow.html` minimal currency touch (hero "Twenty-one"/21 skills + 88 phases, an `/onboard` body paragraph scoped to "a roadmap file or open GitHub issues", colophon +`/onboard` + Phase-88 stamp — the colophon body-mention rule honored), `tools/ONBOARDING_SPEC.md` status flip + open-decisions resolutions, `tools/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` +an `/onboard` spotlight question (did the drafts read as *your* reasoning, or words in your mouth?).

**Gate.** **563 tests green** (was 560; +3 validator). Role guard green (source + installed); 13 manifests parse; leak-scan clean (no `tools/` path or internal identifier in shipped content); fresh-install smoke: skill ships **byte-identical** (Phase-69 resolver no-op), and the shipped validator accepts a real `/onboard`-shaped queue (`surfaced_by: [imported]` + `**Imported from:**` context line) with 0 errors — the end-to-end proof of the emit contract.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES, no blockers.** All 5 SHOULD-FIXES applied: **SF1** tasks/README's "authored only by `/intake`" newly self-contradicting → amended; **SF2** (real catch) the Step-0 consent template asked for "~N items" — obtainable only by the pre-consent read rule 1 forbids → count removed from the template, counts moved after the source-level yes, the `gh` call split count-then-fetch; **SF3** `--limit 200` silently truncates >200-issue repos, violating no-silent-caps at the fetch → truncation guard; **SF4** "downstream skills treat them as such" plural overclaim (only `/auto-claim` consumes the sentinel — verified `next_task.py` reads effort verbatim) → scoped in both docs; **SF5** the untracked `core/skills/onboard/` + missing PHASE_LOG entry as a landing-commit hazard → this entry + explicit `git add`. Nits applied: Leg-B-only handoff no longer misdescribed as "re-entry"; drafted files' provenance headers name `/onboard`; `/auto-claim`'s pre-existing loose "opened only for candidates being **added**" reconciled to *checked* (rule 1b reads skipped candidates' bodies too) + "heavier … per field" disambiguated; workflow.html "and/or imports … a roadmap file or open GitHub issues". Two nits declined with reasons: the WORKFLOW.md §8.2a gh-family enumeration is deliberately not-in-lockstep (Phase 85's ratified reframe); the re-estimate-overflow-hits-STOP edge is pre-existing Step-2 semantics, noted not changed.

**Follow-up (remaining legs, filed Low):** the external-tracker import module (Jira/Linear/Notion/GitHub Projects — new permission surfaces, the `/sitrep`↔`/roadmap` separate-module precedent) and the empty-queue *auto*-detection heuristics (the human-confirmed routing via `/intake`'s fresh-branch guard covers the case manually). Both now calibratable against real tester onboarding data. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`); tester mirror rebuilt + force-pushed after merge so the round gets Phases 87+88 together.

## Phase 89 (executed 2026-07-08 — `/add-task`: single-task quick capture, the lifecycle gap sweep's build item)

**Trigger.** A gap-analysis conversation the morning after the tester mirror went live: Wade asked whether any glaring lifecycle gaps would turn off a tester on an existing or new project. The sweep found that the highest-frequency planning event in real mid-project use — *"I just found a bug / had an idea — get it into the queue"* — had no named owner. The sanctioned paths were hand-editing `index.yml` against a strict validator (in a file whose own rules warn against hand-edits) or running the full `/intake` re-entry interview (a planning ceremony for one bug). Wade's own organic flow (paste a screenshot → "spec that as a task" → the agent writes the entry) works because he knows the schema cold — an emergent property of the author, not the product. It also creates a routing confusion: `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` looks like an issue tracker, so a tester plausibly dumps product bugs into the Sysop friction log. `/add-task` codifies the back half of the organic flow so a stranger's session behaves like Wade's — and since Claude Code skills trigger on description match, both entry points converge: the human types `/add-task`, or the agent routes there on its own when the conversation produces a task-shaped thought.

**What shipped.** `core/skills/add-task/SKILL.md` — the 22nd skill, `reasoning`-role (Phase-69 marker, opus default, resolver byte-for-byte no-op), auto-ships via the `install_skills()` dir-glob (no installer/manifest edit). Shape: **routing boundaries first** (fix-it-now vs capture — filing costs seconds and `/claim-task` needs a queue entry anyway; `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` = friction with Sysop vs the queue = your product's work; phase-shaped thought → `/intake`), then a **rubric-lite scope check** (the one-falsifiable-done-condition-sentence litmus from `_shared/decomposition-rubric.md`; up to ~3 independent siblings in one run; more → `/intake` — never creates `phases:` entries), a **decisions.md contradiction check** (tolerate-absent; detection-not-prevention, mirroring `/intake` Step 0), **dedup** vs open + deferred bodies (extend the existing task / surface the un-park decision / file-as-distinct), **draft** (queue's own ID-prefix vocabulary; `current_focus` phase default; both sizing fields even at v1; `user_action`/`on_hold_until`/`manual_smoke` per rubric semantics; body without `## Test decision` — that's a `/claim-task` plan-time artifact), **one-turn playback** (shown = emitted), **append-only emit** (never rewrite existing entries/`sprint_note`, never touch `phases:` or any `status:`, refuse ID collision) + the validator floor + **uncommitted hand-off** — `/intake`'s two-leg floor/ceiling contract, restated. **No new permission rules** (Write/Edit are file-tools; `validate_tasks.py` already allowed bare + `.venv` variants).

**Docs wiring.** WORKFLOW_GUIDE §0 paragraph (between `/onboard` and the rubric ¶) + the by-hand closing line; `tasks/README.md` skill-table row + rule 4 reworded to lead with the skill; `docs/workflow.html` minimal currency touch (hero 22 skills / 89 phases, a body ¶ in the Day-one section, colophon list entry + Phase-89 stamps); `tools/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` spotlight question (did mid-session capture land without ceremony?).

**The rest of the sweep — filed, not built.** "Backing out of Sysop" uninstall doc section (**Medium** — trust precondition for testers; every payload path is tracked so `git revert` + deleting the armed hooks fully backs out, but no doc says so; optional later `--uninstall` flag). Five **Low**: advertise where a consumer's e2e/QA suite plugs in (the hook point exists — `§ Pre-merge verification` `### Always` — but is unadvertised; deliberately no QA subsystem, populate-from-real-friction); consumer CI story (local hooks are `--no-verify`-bypassable; Phase 63's `pr` policy serves a protected `main` that needs a required check Sysop doesn't help create); Windows prereq line (WSL/Git Bash unstated); multi-human scope statement (solo-plus-agents is intent, not oversight — say so); un-claim owner (`in_progress → open` flip + lock release has none: rule 2 forbids hand-edits, `claim_task.sh` has no `--release`, `/sitrep` detects abandoned claims but `--cleanup-stale` is deferred — decide the owner when tester data shows frequency).

**Gate.** **563 tests green** (unchanged — markdown-only; the role-guard CI test accepts the new roled skill); role guard green source + installed; scratch fresh-install ships the skill byte-identical (Phase-69 resolver no-op) and the installed tree passes the guard; leak-scan clean.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES, no blockers.** **SF1** — Step 3's field enumeration omitted the two validator-hard-required basics, `title` and `status: open`; on the empty-seed path (install → `/add-task` before any `/intake`) there is no sibling entry to mimic, so the enumeration is the only guide — an avoidable validate-fail-refix loop in exactly the skill that promises deterministic capture → full required-set preamble + a `title` bullet. **SF2** — Step 5.1's "append under the existing list" mis-describes the installer-seeded literal `tasks: []` (nothing to append under; `/intake` explicitly branches Write-vs-Edit on this exact state) → author-the-first-entry sentence. **N1** — vestigial helper-names blockquote (the file cites no helper names) deleted. **N2 (bundled Phase-62-class, pre-existing)** — `schema.md` § "What NOT to put here" still said "use `/claim-task`, `/document-work`, `/review-close`", predating `/intake` (P60) and `/onboard` (P88) and now contradicting the README rule-4 rewrite → reworded to the add-vs-advance skill split. Reviewer verified clean: field-by-field schema fidelity against the real `validate_tasks.py`, the `/intake` Step 7–8 mirror (add-task appropriately stricter), the permission claim vs the settings template, every rubric §-ref, role marker + guard exit 0, colophon count 22 = hero stat with all 22 body-mentioned, phase-assignment validator-safety, no exclusivity contradiction, zero identifier leaks. One pre-review self-fix: the fix-it-now bullet originally said "route to `/claim-task`," which can't claim unfiled work — reworded to file-then-claim.

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 88's `_PR pending_` cells (`a5fccea` #47) in both phase-log tables.

## Phase 90 (executed 2026-07-08 — tester-trust doc bundle: Backing out, e2e plug-in, Windows prereq, multi-human scope)

**Trigger.** The four clean documentation items from Phase 89's lifecycle-gap sweep, taken as one bundle ahead of the private tester round. Wade picked the doc bundle (via `AskUserQuestion`) over building `claim_task.sh --release` — the un-claim flag / a-b-c owner decision stays deferred as filed. Each of the four answers a question a tester asks before or during evaluation, and each answer was already worked out in its filing — the Phase-85 "polish bundle" pattern, markdown/HTML only.

**What shipped.** **(#1, Medium — the trust item) `## Backing out` section** in `README.md` + a short pointer in `docs/getting-started.md`. Two scales: **reversing a single `/claim-task`** (find the worktree via `git worktree list`, `git worktree remove`, optional `git branch -D`, `rm .locks/<TASK-ID>.lock`, flip `status:` back to `open` in the *same pass* as the lock removal — the one sanctioned exception to `tasks/README.md` rule 2 because it re-syncs rather than desyncs — `validate_tasks.py`, then commit) and **removing Sysop from the whole project** (revert the install commit for a fresh install; else delete the `managed_paths` — Sysop installs `scripts/` flat and merges into any existing `.claude/`, so `.claude/sysop.lock`'s `managed_paths` is the source of truth for selective removal, not a blunt `rm -r`; then disarm the two armed hooks `.git/hooks/pre-commit` + `pre-merge-commit`). **(#6 folded in) manual un-claim guidance** is that section's first half — the stopgap while the `--release` flag stays deferred (item remains open, now cross-referenced to the doc). **(#2, Low) e2e/QA plug-in point** — a note in `WORKFLOW.md` §6.1 after the Pre-merge verification template + a tip in `getting-started` step 5: a Playwright/Cypress/integration suite is one more `### Always` command `/review-close` runs on every merge, no Sysop-side wiring; Sysop ships no QA subsystem (populate-from-friction, an e2e pack the eventual shape). **(#4, Low) Windows prereq** — a WSL-primary line (Git Bash flakier/unverified) in the README install bullet + `getting-started` prereqs. **(#5, Low) multi-human scope** — an honesty sentence in `docs/workflow.html`'s Audience "team" paragraph: Sysop coordinates parallel *sessions* under one reviewer; two humans sharing one queue (assignment, review handoff, who runs `/review-close`) is a deliberate non-goal today, not an oversight — placed where a team-shaped evaluator forms the impression. No colophon re-stamp (a one-sentence honesty add, not a currency pass; the Phase-86 stamp stands).

**Gate.** **563 tests green** (unchanged — markdown/HTML only; no executable surface touched); leak-scan clean on the new prose (the `BeanRider`/ISSUE grep hits are pre-existing WORKFLOW.md provenance, not additions); the `workflow.html` edit sits inside the existing `<p>` with balanced `<em>`/`<code>`; four files changed — `README.md`, `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md`, `docs/getting-started.md`, `docs/workflow.html`.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose, zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES, no blockers.** The reviewer verified every load-bearing claim against the repo (claim-task's three-step claim; the lock path resolved under the main repo via git-common-dir + the uppercase `TASK_ID` filename; the reversal ordering vs `validate_tasks.py` invariant 9; `sysop.lock` as the manifest; the payload list vs the install commit; all anchors/cross-refs incl. the GitHub `#backing-out` slug; "no Sysop-side wiring" for e2e; HTML well-formedness; the multi-human boundary). **SF (S1)** — `git rm -r .claude scripts` undercut the "clean git operation" promise (Sysop installs `scripts/` flat and merges into any pre-existing `.claude/`, so a blunt `rm -r` deletes a consumer's own content) → added the selective-removal caveat pointing at `sysop.lock`'s `managed_paths`. **N1** (real correctness) — the disarm command listed `pre-push`, which Sysop **never ships or arms** (verified: only `pre-commit`/`pre-merge-commit` exist under `core/companion/git-hooks/`; `install_hooks.sh`'s allowlist names `pre-push` but skips it for want of a source file), so `rm -f …pre-push` would delete a consumer's *own* untracked, unrecoverable hook → dropped it + noted the `.bak.<ts>` backup `install_hooks.sh` leaves. **N2** (`tasks/` holds Sysop scaffold + your content), **N3** (revert conflicts on any *used* project — sharpened "intact" to the fresh-install-only case), **N4** (commit the status flip), **N5** (venv-python hedge for PyYAML), **N6** (WSL-primary, Git Bash caveated) all applied. **N7** (`### Ratchet` a stretch for e2e) left — already hedged and reviewer-deemed defensible.

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 89's `_PR pending_` cells (`f1846d2` #49) in both phase-log tables.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 91 (executed 2026-07-08 — `claim_task.sh --release`: the un-claim owner; first of the two remaining lifecycle-gap-sweep items)

**Trigger.** The lifecycle-gap-sweep item filed by Phase 89 and given a *manual* stopgap by Phase 90: **"Un-claim has no owner — the `in_progress → open` flip + lock release."** A human who claims a task and changes their mind had no sanctioned path back — `tasks/README.md` rule 2 forbids hand-editing `status:`, `claim_task.sh` had no un-claim flag, and `/sitrep --cleanup-stale` (option b) stays deferred. Wade chose (via `AskUserQuestion`) to build **both** remaining sweep items, **un-claim first**, then Consumer CI as a follow-up. The item listed three owners — (a) `claim_task.sh --release` (smallest), (b) `/sitrep --cleanup-stale` (heavier stale-*detection*), (c) a future queue-hygiene skill; option (a) is a strict subset of b/c (doesn't foreclose them) and is the *voluntary* un-claim a tester most likely trips (claim → change mind), so it was the low-regret build.

**Design (measure-twice).** The claim flow **splits responsibilities**: the `/claim-task` skill does the `index.yml` status flip (Step 4a, PyYAML round-trip) and `claim_task.sh` does the worktree+branch+lock (4b). The filed gap names **both** halves as ownerless, so a `--release` that closes it must reverse **both** — not just the script's half. Hence `claim_task.sh --release <TASK_ID>` owns the full reversal:
- **Reads `branch:`/`workspace:` from the lock**, so the operator supplies only the task ID.
- **Mutations ordered so any early exit lands on a validator-consistent state** (the safety claim): pre-flight the flip (if `index.yml` exists but PyYAML is absent, mutate **nothing** and print the manual reversal to run in the consumer's venv — removing the lock alone would create exactly the `in_progress`-without-lock desync `validate_tasks.py` invariant 9 flags) → remove the worktree (a dirty worktree without `--force` aborts with the **whole claim intact**) → flip `status: in_progress → open` (PyYAML round-trip mirroring Step 4a *in reverse*, params `sort_keys=False, default_flow_style=False, allow_unicode=True, width=120` matched byte-for-byte so a claim→release round-trip reformats identically; **refuses to clobber** a `done`/`deferred` task) → remove the lock. The only `in_progress`-preserving branch is the genuine-crash guard, which keeps the lock → still consistent.
- **Crown-jewel safety:** never removes the main worktree (mirrors Phase 84's `cleanup_worktrees.sh` invariant); refuses to run from inside the target worktree (git would refuse anyway); both guards precede `--force` so it can't bypass them.
- **Never commits** — prints the `chore: release <TASK-ID>` commit, matching the claim path's separation (the skill's 4d commits). `--delete-branch` and `--force` are opt-ins.
- **Bare `python3`** for the flip (symmetric with Step 4a, which also uses bare `python3`): if the consumer's `python3` can do the claim flip, it can do the un-claim flip; the degradation points at `.venv/bin/python3`.

**What shipped.** `core/companion/scripts/claim_task.sh` — the `--release`/`--delete-branch`/`--force` flags + the release block (header/usage updated). Docs: `README.md` § Backing out (replaced "there is no `--release` flag yet" with the one-command path, keeping the by-hand steps as the no-PyYAML fallback), `core/companion/tasks/README.md` rule 2 (points at `--release` as the sanctioned un-claim), `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md` (§4.1 "How it works" bullet + §8.4 script table row), `docs/getting-started.md` (named the one command inline for tester discoverability). Tests: `tests/test_claim_task_sh.py` new `TestRelease` class — **+13 tests** covering full reversal, `--delete-branch`, unlocked-refusal, **never-removes-main-worktree**, **dirty-abort-then-`--force`**, refuse-from-inside-worktree, **no-PyYAML-degrades-without-mutation**, no-index still releases, already-open clears stale lock, **leaves-validator-consistent-state** (the no-desync proof via a real `validate_tasks.py` run), don't-clobber-`done`, `NOT_FOUND` still clears lock, trailing-flag guard.

**Gate.** `bash -n` clean; end-to-end scratch-repo smoke (claim → release → clean state; and the PyYAML-degradation path verified to mutate nothing). **576 tests green** (was 563, +13). Auto-ships via the existing companion-scripts install loop (no installer/manifest edit); **no new permission rules** (`Bash(bash scripts/claim_task.sh:*)` already covers it).

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES, no blockers.** The reviewer empirically **mutation-tested all three crown-jewel tests** (each reddens under an obvious break — non-tautological), confirmed the **flip params match Step 4a exactly**, ran a **full reversal end-to-end under bash 3.2** (the `set +e`/`set -e` fence around the heredoc-in-`$()` is correct; path canonicalization handled the `/../` in the recorded workspace), and traced **every path to `rm "$LOCK_FILE"`** against `validate_tasks.py` invariant 9 → **no path removes the lock while leaving `in_progress`** (verified `done`-task-not-clobbered and malformed-`index.yml`-keeps-lock empirically). **SF (S1)** — no test pinned the `done`/`deferred` non-clobber guard, so a future refactor to an unconditional `t["status"]="open"` would revive completed work with every test still green → added `test_does_not_clobber_done_task` (+ `test_task_not_in_index_still_clears_lock`). **N1** (trailing-flag footgun — `--release FEAT-X --force` silently drops `--force`) → reject a trailing flag loudly + a locking test. **N2** (bare `git worktree remove --force` died under `set -e` without the graceful "claim is intact" message the non-force branch prints) → wrapped it symmetrically. **N3** (`REPO_ROOT` used only as the in-repo guard) + **N4** (verbose traceback on the crash path) left as cosmetic/honest per the reviewer.

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 90's `_PR pending_` cells (`e1ca79f` #50) in both phase-log tables.

**Follow-up (per Wade's "un-claim first"):** Consumer CI story (the second remaining sweep item) is the next phase. The un-claim owner decision's options (b) `/sitrep --cleanup-stale` and (c) queue-hygiene skill stay deferred — (a) `--release` closes the *voluntary* un-claim; stale-*detection* cleanup is a distinct owner.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 92 (executed 2026-07-08 — Consumer CI template: the second and last lifecycle-gap-sweep item)

**Trigger.** The other remaining lifecycle-gap-sweep item filed by Phase 89: **"Consumer CI story."** Sysop ships local git hooks only, and an agent can bypass them with `--no-verify`, so a consumer wanting a *protected* `main` — the exact thing Phase 63's `pr` merge policy exists to serve — needs a required **CI** check Sysop didn't help create. Second half of Wade's "**both, un-claim first**" (`AskUserQuestion`), after Phase 91's `--release`. Appetite was filed *undecided* ("a tester with existing CI feels nothing → greenfield-consumer polish"), so the shape was ratified via a second `AskUserQuestion` before building: **shipped hardened `.example` + docs** (recommended), over doc-only-recipe and over shipped-plus-auto-arm (rejected — auto-arming CI on a consumer's repo burns their Actions minutes without consent, and contradicts the item's "template-not-armed" framing).

**Design.** A **hardened, unarmed GitHub Actions workflow**, `core/companion/ci/sysop-checks.yml.example`, mirroring Sysop's own `.github/workflows/tests.yml` shape (SHA-pinned actions — the exact `actions/checkout` v6.0.2 / `actions/setup-python` v6.2.0 pins Sysop dogfoods; `concurrency` + `cancel-in-progress`; `permissions: contents: read`; scoped `pull_request.types`). It runs the Sysop gate `run_checks.sh --fail-on-blocking` (inert-but-valid on a fresh install — placeholder check globs are no-ops; meaningful as the consumer configures `checks.yml`) plus a **placeholder `Tests` step that `exit 1`s on purpose** — so an unedited copy can never become a green-but-meaningless required check. The `.example` suffix keeps GitHub from running it; **shipped like the git-hook templates** (`install_git_hooks()`'s model — delivered to the consumer's tree but *not* activated): a new `install_ci_template()` copies it to the consumer's `scripts/ci/`, recorded in the lock's `managed_paths`, **never into `.github/workflows/`**. The consumer copies it there, fills the two `TODO` steps (their deps; their real test command), and marks the `sysop-checks` check required in branch protection — then `/review-close`'s `pr` route lands through a PR GitHub won't merge until the gate is green.

**What shipped.** `core/companion/ci/sysop-checks.yml.example` (new); `install.sh` (`install_ci_template()` + pipeline wiring after `install_git_hooks`); `tests/test_ci_template.py` (**+7 tests** — template shape: valid YAML, the `run_checks` gate step, SHA-pinned actions, least-privilege permissions, the `exit 1` placeholder, the `.yml.example` inertness; plus a real fresh-install test asserting the template lands in `scripts/ci/`, is in the lock, parses after shipping, and **nothing is armed into `.github/workflows/`**). Docs: `WORKFLOW.md` §6.1 "Protecting `main` with CI" (enable steps) + the `scripts/ci/` addition to the `managed_paths` parenthetical; `docs/getting-started.md` (a CI pointer under the merge-policy block).

**Gate.** `bash -n install.sh` clean; real fresh install + `--update` round-trip both ship the template unarmed; **583 tests green** (was 576, +7); auto-ships; **no new permission rules**.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES, no blockers.** The reviewer mutation-tested the load-bearing locks (unpin an action → `test_actions_are_sha_pinned` reddens; arm into `.github/workflows/` → `test_ships_unarmed_…` reddens), ran real fresh + `--update` installs (template lands, in-lock, `.github/` stays absent), and **ran the actual gate step** `bash scripts/run_checks.sh --fail-on-blocking` in a scratch consumer with only python3+PyYAML → **exit 0** (`run_checks` resolves `python3` off PATH when there's no repo `.venv`; absent tools FileNotFoundError-skip), confirming the template works out-of-the-box. **SF1** (the real one) — `core/skills/security-audit/SKILL.md:320` still referenced the non-shipped `.github/workflows/security.yml`, the **identical false-claim class** this phase set out to eliminate (it repointed WORKFLOW.md's "CI integration" para away from that exact file), and it's a **shipped** skill so every consumer got the dangling reference → repointed to the real template `scripts/ci/sysop-checks.yml.example` (pip-audit noted as the consumer's TODO). **N1** (the `.example` is out of the Phase-24b preserve-consumer-edits scope — defensible, since the consumer's live file is the unmanaged `.github/workflows/` copy and the `.example` *should* refresh on update → documented that intent in the `install_ci_template` comment) and **N3** (`push:` hardcodes `main` → added an "adjust if your default branch differs" note) applied; **N2** (the §6.1 cross-ref names a bold lead-in, not a heading — findable by search, no functional impact) left.

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 91's `_PR pending_` cells (`327053d` #51) in both phase-log tables. Also (SF1 above) closes a pre-existing dangling `.github/workflows/security.yml` reference in a shipped skill.

**Both lifecycle-gap-sweep items now closed** (un-claim = Phase 91, Consumer CI = Phase 92); Phase 89's sweep is fully resolved.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 93 (executed 2026-07-08 — `/test-audit` Tier-2b calibration ledger: the mechanism for Phase 80's open calibration follow-up)

**Trigger.** Phase 80 shipped `/test-audit` + `_shared/test-assessment-rubric.md` **provisional**, and filed a Medium follow-up to calibrate the rubric out of provisional across real suites. That item scoped the work correctly — only the **Tier-2b** judgment dimensions (redundant / brittle / hollow) calibrate over runs; Tier 1 (recommend a test) and Tier 2a (provably dead) fire correctly on the first run — but it left the *how* implicit: "run real audits and observe accept/veto." A conversation this session pulled on that thread and surfaced that there was **no mechanism to accumulate the accept/veto signal** — it relied on unaided memory across audit sessions. Phase 93 builds that mechanism (it does **not** close the calibration item — the mechanism now exists; the real runs that promote dimensions still have to happen).

**A design question resolved first (the "whose ledger" fork).** A natural instinct is that each *consumer* should get a local ledger that tunes their own `/test-audit` from their own choices. Worked through honestly and ratified via `AskUserQuestion` (**global now, local later**):
- **The calibration that matters is global, and its corpus is the maintainer's own repos.** The §5.1 promotion gate wants a dimension to survive across three suites — and the three named in the spec's Dogfood plan (Sysop's own suite, BeanRider, GDP) are all Wade's. So the accumulator is sysop-side, fed primarily by Wade's own audit runs; no cross-user transport is required for the core calibration.
- **External-user signal, when it comes, rides the existing opt-in friction pipe — no new telemetry.** A tester who disagrees with a Tier-2b recommendation logs it as friction; `/report-issues` transports it upstream as a consented issue. This is consistent with the no-telemetry posture Phase 65a set (it *declined* GDP's `task_outcome` emit). Nothing is collected silently.
- **A per-user "confidence-learning" loop was explicitly rejected**, not deferred: it overfits on thin single-user data and can *silently suppress genuinely-new findings*; the safe way to encode a project-wide "we do X on purpose" preference is an explicit `.project.*` overlay convention, not inferred veto-history. The one *safe* per-user feature — a local "don't re-nag me about tests I already kept" **suppress-list** (a `run_checks`-baseline analog) — was deferred to be shaped by the first real audits (dogfood-before-build) and filed Low.

**Design.** Three moving parts, split cleanly by ship-vs-internal:
- **`tools/TEST_AUDIT_VERDICT_LEDGER.md` (new, maintainer-internal — never ships).** The accept/veto accumulator. It lives in `tools/`, which `make_public_mirror.sh` deletes (`rm -rf "$TARGET/tools"`), so it reaches neither the tester nor the public mirror. Modeled on the Phase 67 **convention fire ledger** (accumulate-verdicts-then-adjudicate), with two honest adaptations: the **axis** is cross-*suite* survival, not cross-*round* (the §5.1 gate, as `decomposition-rubric.md` in 60b); and it is **bidirectional** in one place (`accept` rows feed promotion, `veto` rows feed tighten/demote) whereas the Phase-67 fire ledger is demotion-only. Rows are grouped by dimension; a roll-up procedure reads each dimension and decides **promote / tighten / demote-to-flag-only / keep-watching**, clearing an adjudicated dimension's rows (keep-watching does not clear). Every promote/tighten/demote is an edit to the *shipped* rubric that reaches consumers on their next `sysop-update`.
- **`core/skills/test-audit/SKILL.md` — new Step 4b (shipped; portable).** Only when the report carries Tier-2b findings, it emits each as a copy-pasteable ledger row (verdict/note blank). Framed portably for **two opt-in uses**: track your own accept/veto, or — the higher-value signal — *report a disagreement* upstream via `/report-issues` so the shared rubric's labels sharpen. **It references no maintainer-internal path** (a consumer has no `tools/`); it emits to no disk. Tier 1 and Tier 2a are never emitted. The output-shape reference gained a matching CALIBRATION block, and Deferred features gained the `--suppress` local-decision-memory entry.
- **`core/skills/_shared/test-assessment-rubric.md` — a portable "report a wrong Tier-2b call" pointer** in the provisional blockquote (routes only through `/report-issues` + cites Step 4b), closing the loop for consumers.

**What shipped.** The three files above + `tools/TEST_AUDIT_SPEC.md` (status: Phase 93 "mechanised that follow-up — it did not close it") + `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` (the calibration item annotated with the mechanism, **stays open**; a new Low item for the deferred per-user suppress-list) + the CLAUDE.md / REVIEW_CHECKLIST phase-log rows.

**Gate.** Markdown + internal-doc only → **583 tests green** (unchanged); no skill model-pin/marker touched (role-guard CI unaffected); the ledger is `tools/`-scoped so no shipped-content leak.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero context): SHIP**, no blockers, no should-fixes. The reviewer verified all 9 invariants against the actual files — most load-bearingly, **zero internal-path leak in shipped content** (grepped `core/` for the ledger filename and `tools/`; the only `tools/` hits in `core/` are unrelated example/grep strings), the ledger is **double-protected from shipping** (`rm -rf tools/` *and* `git archive HEAD` never seeing an untracked file), the four calibration surfaces are consistent, Tier-1/2a exclusion is enforced in both the skill and the ledger, the no-telemetry claim holds, and the two phase-log cells correctly read `06052b7` (#52). Three NITs, all in the internal ledger doc (no shipped impact), all applied: **NIT-1/NIT-2** — the Phase-67 analogy was imprecise (the fire ledger is demotion-only; promotion reads a separate record — and Phase 67 clears rows for every adjudicated disposition whereas Phase 93's *keep-watching* is an un-adjudicated hold that shouldn't clear) → reworded to "modeled on… with two adaptations (axis + bidirectional)" and "dispositions parallel… adapted"; **NIT-3** — the emitted row is 7-column (carries `Dimension`) but the destination tables are 6-column (dimension = section header) → made the drop-the-column reshape explicit in "How rows arrive."

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 92's `_PR pending_` cells (`06052b7` #52) in both phase-log tables.

**The Phase-80 calibration item stays open** (mechanism ✓ Phase 93; the real cross-suite runs are the remaining leg — recommended, non-blocking). Per-user suppress-list filed Low.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 94 (executed 2026-07-11 — GDP review-data July snapshot refresh + bundled doc fixes)

**Why.** The launch-facing severity chart and headline counts in `docs/workflow.html` (and their sources under `docs/analysis/`) were a June-8 *partial* snapshot — 69 rounds / 3,217 findings, "February through June," a five-point Fig. 7 with June marked partial. Wade ran GDP's final pre-launch `/codebase-review` + `/security-audit` rounds on 2026-07-10 — exactly the trigger the parked refresh item (filed 2026-07-10) was waiting on: bring the public data current and earn the "July" label before the tester round.

**The mine (read-only against GDP).** `docs/analysis/mine_gdp_reviews.py` re-read `~/Projects/gdp-query-system` (file reads + read-only `git log`/`show`/`rev-list`; it writes only sysop's JSON). Two new rounds since the committed snapshot: **Round 73** (2026-06-30, Code Quality, 45 findings, 0 critical) and **Round 74** (2026-07-10, 37 findings, 2🔴/11🟡/24🟢). Last night's security audit was committed *under the same `## Round 74` header* (`b31923cb docs: add Round 74 security audit tasks`) rather than as a separate `## Round 75 — OWASP Security Audit`, so the miner types Round 74 `quality` but counts all 37 findings — nothing dropped; the only effect is there is no distinct July "security round" in the type split (irrelevant to the severity-share chart, which counts findings regardless of type). New totals: **71 rounds / 3,298 findings / 78 conventions**. No new promotions — the forecast plateau, confirmed. The +81 net (not +82) reconciles cleanly: R73 +45, R74 +37, and R72 −1 (its lone 2026-06-08 critical was reclassified out of the archive during a later consolidation, 24→23 findings / 1→0 crit), which also flips June's critical share to 0.0%.

**Five number sites, moved together.** `gdp_review_metrics.json` (miner output) · `docs/analysis/REPORT.md` (source window `2026-02-23 → 2026-07-10`, verdict numbers, the monthly table with a full two-round June row and a partial-July row, a July revision note) · `docs/workflow.html` (body "nearly 3,300 findings", the §"Does it actually get quieter?" prose, the Fig. 7 caption, and a **hand-redrawn SVG**) · `README.md` · `CLAUDE.md:3` (internal, doesn't ship).

**The SVG redraw.** Fig. 7 is hand-plotted, so it was redrawn rather than find-replaced: 5→6 month groups at 140px spacing (from 165) to fit the sixth inside the 1000-wide viewBox; June **de-partialed** (it is now a complete two-round month) and drawn with a 0%-crit bar (no bar; "0%" at the baseline); **July added** as the new partial. Crit bars keep the 11.5px/point scale, the low-severity line keeps 2.5px/percent; every coordinate was arithmetic-verified in-bounds and the aria-label rewritten to describe the six-point series. New points: crit share 21→10→5→17\*→0→5, low share 22→29→59→43→75→65.

**Narrative reworded — "fell then held low" (ratified via `AskUserQuestion`).** July's critical share (5.4%) ticks *up* from June's 0%, so the old "severity falls" arc is no longer literally monotonic. Wade chose the honest framing over keeping the falling arc: severity fell sharply Feb→Apr (21%→5%) and then *held* in the low single digits for five more months (17% May during the Round 70 sweep, 0% June, 5% July) while the rubric kept growing — the sustained low plateau *is* the claim. The `REPORT.md` verdict and the workflow.html paragraph were reworded to match; the "measured, not asserted" bar is preserved (the reword also corrected `~6×`→`~5×` commit-size shrinkage and `65→11`→`65→13` to match the fresh medians).

**Bundled per the parked item.** (a) `core/skills/report-issues/SKILL.md` — dropped the dangling `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` ref (mirror-excluded → 404s for a public reader) *and* corrected the now-false "tracked as a follow-up": those `install.sh` closing-summary + `/intake`-completion friction nudges actually **shipped in Phase 73b** (`install.sh:2663`, `intake/SKILL.md:172`), so the sentence now states they exist. (b) Phase-count currency bump — README "94 phases", workflow.html hero stat + colophon "Phase 94 · 2026-07-11" — plus a bundled Phase-62-class fix: the hero prose said "Twenty-one skills" while the stat + colophon list **22** (Phase 89 added `/add-task` and bumped the stat but not the word), corrected to "Twenty-two."

**Gate.** Markdown + data only; zero test/code files touched → **581 tests green** (unchanged, and equal to the clean-`main` baseline — verified by running the suite on both the branch and a stashed `main`, so the 581-vs-the-log's-583 is a pre-existing baseline, not a regression from this phase). JSON valid, HTML tags balanced, no stale numbers left behind, no test depends on the refreshed values.

**Note on scope.** The parked item's "ALREADY DONE this session — uncommitted `tools/` edits (BeanRider accept ratification + `make_public_mirror.sh` Pass 2b)" tail is moot: those landed in the launch-prep commit `204cae1` (#59) before this session; the working tree was clean at branch time and this refresh touches no `tools/` file.

**May-outlier deepened during review (LSP amplification).** Wade's review of the PR surfaced that the May/Round-70 severity bump had a *review-process* cause he'd made in gdp but never documented anywhere: `TECH-LSP-REVIEW` (gdp `2f3c5497`, 2026-04-17) made `/codebase-review` language-server-aware — a `pyright`/`tsc` diagnostic stage plus, load-bearing here, Step 9 convention **sweeps routed through `LSP.findReferences`** that amplify one promoted convention into one-task-per-call-site (where grep only approximated). It landed the same day as `TECH-SEMGREP-CHECKS` (`b9984ac7`) and three days before `53764e3f` retired the noisy `audit-trail-gaps` / `state-mutation-logging` greps into the `/security-audit` LLM agents. Round 70 (2026-05-12) was the first *broad* sweep to exploit the amplification, which is why its 45 criticals are dominated by one-🔴-per-call-site logging/audit enforcement while the incremental (changed-files-only) Round 69 (2026-04-25) stayed at 10 — the instrument got sharper, the code did not get worse. Captured as: a **self-contained** Fig. 7 chart note (spells out "language-server-driven (LSP)" so no monograph LSP-intro is required), a `REPORT.md` § "May outlier" paragraph + a confound-#2 mechanism note (both with commit refs), and a **Low-priority follow-up** to surface the multi-tool pre-scan as a monograph *feature* later — Wade chose that (Option A) over bundling it here, since the operational docs already document it (WORKFLOW.md §5.4 "Sibling amplification" / §6.5; `codebase-review` Step 2b-2).

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Rename round 2 (executed 2026-07-11 — `jig` → `sysop`, org flip `wade-cms` → `getsysop`)

**What & why.** The 2026-06-26 rename landed `jig` (wade-flow → jig, `tools/RENAME_PLAN.md` Batches A–E). On 2026-07-11, a launch-prep scout found [`duronext/jig`](https://github.com/duronext/jig) — public since 2026-03-29, an AI engineering workflow framework distributed as a Claude Code marketplace with the plugin literally named `jig`, occupying the exact same `/jig:*` command namespace, with the same manufacturing-jig metaphor. Parallel invention, but we would ship second into a shared plugin-namespace collision. The name was re-decided the same day: **`sysop`** passed the full clearance dive (zero bare-name AI-niche adopters; USPTO 0 live marks, first-party confirmed; PyPI/crates/RubyGems free) — the brand story names the human's ROLE (responsible operator of the agent fleet), not the tool. Handles claimed 2026-07-11: GitHub org `getsysop`, domains getsysop.com/.dev, usesysop.com, sysop.run. The public repo becomes **`getsysop/sysop`**, so this sweep folds in the org flip — consumers migrate once.

**What changed.** Re-executed the RENAME_PLAN batch structure with the ten post-June deltas enumerated in `tools/RENAME_SYSOP_PROMPT.md` (internal — `tools/` never ships). Token forms: `jig`→`sysop`, `Jig`→`Sysop`, `JIG`→`SYSOP`, `wade-cms/jig`→`getsysop/sysop`. Concretely: manifests (marketplace + 12 plugin.json names/deps/homepages, owner `getsysop`), install.sh (`.claude/sysop.lock`, `sysop_commit`, `SYSOP_SRC`, `SYSOP_ISSUES.md`, `get_sysop_commit`, `references_sysop`, pack-prefix logic, detection/served-models/CI-template installers, `--help`), three history-preserving `git mv`s (`jig-update.sh`→`sysop-update.sh`, `jig-checks.yml.example`→`sysop-checks.yml.example`, `test_jig_update_sh.py`→`test_sysop_update_sh.py`), the Phase-69 model-role marker prefix (`<!-- sysop:model-roles … -->` / `<!-- sysop:role=… -->`) renamed in the parser (`_model_roles.py`) + all 20 roled skills + tests in the same commit, the friction-log Status enum (`Filed to Sysop`) in lockstep between the install.sh seed and `/report-issues`' read/write sites, the `--repo` defaults in `/report-issues` + `/contribute-convention`, the Discussions URL, the full monograph brand sweep (title, masthead, hero, colophon, OG/Twitter meta), and every shipped prose surface. This entry's own history convention: the June entry facts above keep saying wade-flow → jig — true history; everything live says sysop.

**Unchanged on purpose.** The `wade-flow-extract-base` git tag (protected provenance). Tier-4 history files (`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`, `*_HANDOFF.md`, `HANDOVER.md`, `PHASE_47_SPEC.md`) — "wade-flow"/"jig" there is historically correct. The tester mirror repo slug `wade-cms/jig-tester` in Phase 77's entry above — the name that repo carried at the time (renamed to `wade-cms/sysop-tester` + refreshed with a sysop-branded snapshot later the same day).

**Gate.** 581 tests green (= main baseline); JSON valid on all 13 manifests; `bash -n` clean; role guard green on source + a scratch install; scratch install round-trip (fresh/update/adopt) produces `.claude/sysop.lock` + `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` + `scripts/sysop-update.sh`; resolver byte-identical no-op under the default mapping; residue grep returns only Tier-4 history + rename-history lines + the extract-base tag; public-mirror dry-run clean.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 95 (executed 2026-07-11 — model-role Fable currency + the consumer-customization story)

**Trigger.** Wade's two launch-window questions: (1) should we be specifying models anywhere we're currently not — or less often than we are — and is Fable missing as a role? (2) how easy is it for a user to customize shipped skills *and keep the changes* when they pick up the latest Sysop?

**Assessment (1) — the role system already answers Fable.** Census: 19 of 22 skills carry a role (17 × frontmatter `reasoning`→opus; `/next-task` the sole `quick`→haiku; `/auto-review` inline-`reasoning` with the one per-pin `mechanical`→sonnet override); `/document-work`, `/sitrep`, `/triage` deliberately carry no pin and inherit the session model (Phase 86's corrected framing — the role guard governs pinned skills only). Roles name *kinds of work*, not models — Fable is a mapping target, not a missing role. Harness facts verified against the official docs via a claude-code-guide probe (not guessed, per the house rule): `fable` is a valid frontmatter alias; `best` now means "Fable 5 where the org has access, else latest Opus"; a pinned-but-unavailable model **silently keeps the session model**; Fable needs Claude Code ≥ 2.1.170 and is excluded under zero-data-retention. Declined on that evidence: flipping the `reasoning` default to fable (cost changes materially for every consumer with access; the silent-fallback degrade on older/ZDR consumers falls back to the *session* model, not opus; every phase of dogfood evidence is on opus), a fourth role tier (speculative — the indirection exists precisely so a tier can be added later without a sweep), and pinning `/sitrep`/`/triage` to `quick` (inheriting rides better session models for free; `/sitrep`'s RECOMMENDED NEXT routing carries some judgment).

**Shipped (1).** `served_models.yml`: **`fable` pre-listed in the default `served:`**. The design win is subtle: a consumer remap (`roles: reasoning: fable` in `served_models.local.yml`) becomes ONE key — and because the *default* list is Sysop-managed (refreshed every update), a future fable sunset still goes loud for that consumer, whereas the pre-Phase-95 route (consumer extends their local `served:` with fable) would have muted the loud-sunset guard forever (local `served:` entries union in and never leave). Override example rewritten: the one-key fable case first, then the extend-`served:` case for `best`/`inherit`, with the ≥ 2.1.170 silent-fallback caveat. The stale `/sitrep`-as-`quick` example fixed (Phase-62-class rot — the comment predated Phase 86's inherit framing) plus an explicit "un-pinned skills inherit; roles govern pinned skills only" note. Default mapping untouched → the install-time resolver stays a byte-for-byte no-op.

**Assessment (2) — easy to edit, deliberately non-persistent.** Skills are tier-1 fully-managed: `_phase_24b_in_scope` (install.sh:640) scopes preservation to `scripts/*` + `scripts/hooks/*` only, with the anti-prompt-fork rationale written into the code (a silently-preserved skill edit accumulates divergence from upstream indefinitely with no pressure to reconcile). A committed skill edit gets the Phase-8 pre-overwrite divergence warning; an uncommitted one is captured by the Phase-7 snapshot commit; both recoverable from git history, neither preserved. The persistent surfaces that DO exist: CLAUDE.md prose (always loaded — the guided-mode stanza proves the pattern governs skill behavior without touching skill files), the never-managed overlays (`.project.*` maps/checks, `substitutions.project.yml`, `served_models.local.yml`), preserved scripts/hooks, and the fork-under-an-unshipped-name escape hatch (paths outside `managed_paths` are never touched by `--update`). The real gap was **discoverability**: `served_models.local.yml` appeared in NO consumer-facing doc (README/getting-started zero hits — only WORKFLOW §8.4 + the monograph) and the fork pattern was documented nowhere.

**Shipped (2).** New **README § Customizing Sysop** (between Required permissions and Backing out): the three-tier update taxonomy recap, the rule of thumb (*behavior in CLAUDE.md, config in an overlay, skill bodies stay upstream-owned*), the overlay table, the one-key fable example, and the honest skills paragraph (overwritten-with-warning by design + the rationale + the fork escape hatch + the plugin-path caveat — marketplace-cache skills have no in-place customization at all). `docs/getting-started.md` gains a "Make it yours — without losing updates" paragraph pointing at it.

**Filed, not built.** The skill-body overlay mechanism (a per-skill `SKILL.project.md` appendix mirroring the map overlays) → § Decisions to revisit later, demand-gated (REVISIT: tester/consumer demand beyond what CLAUDE.md prose expresses; if it fires alongside the 2026-07-10 tuning-knobs entry, build one shared overlay shape, not two). The 2026-07-11 model-role *utilization* item stays open, annotated partial: this phase landed its Fable/discoverability half; the per-step economy audit ("are we making enough use of haiku and sonnet?") + the recommended-economy preset remain its scope.

**Gate.** Markdown + config only (the one YAML-visible change is the inert `served:` entry — nothing maps to fable by default, so guard semantics are unchanged): **581 tests green** (= main baseline); role guard green on source; resolver dry-run under the default mapping = 0 rewrites (still byte-for-byte no-op); **one-key override proven end-to-end on a scratch fresh install** — shipped `served_models.yml` carries fable, a two-line `served_models.local.yml` (`roles: reasoning: fable`) passes the guard (`reasoning=fable`) and the resolver reports it would rewrite all 29 pins across 19 files; leak-scan on the diff clean (shipped surfaces mention no internal identifiers).

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers. The reviewer empirically proved the loud-sunset design win with a three-scenario guard run (one-key override → green; fable dropped from the default `served:` with the same override → RED, all 29 pins flagged; the pre-Phase-95 route where the consumer extends local `served:` → **silently green** after the same drop, confirming the muted-guard claim) and verified every README claim against `install.sh` (the Phase-8 divergence net and Phase-7 snapshot both cover `.claude/skills/**` — only `settings.json` is excluded; the obsolete-deletion loop iterates only recorded `managed_paths`, so a fork name is structurally safe). Both findings applied: **SF1** — the docs told a consumer to create `served_models.local.yml` but never said the override applies at install/update time via the resolver (a mid-session edit does nothing until the next update — the most likely friction report) → added "run `scripts/sysop-update.sh` to apply" to README + getting-started; **NIT** — the fork paragraph's "never touched by updates" was slightly overstated: the Phase-69 resolver walks the whole skills tree, so a fork keeping its `<!-- sysop:model-roles … -->` marker still gets its `model:` line synced to the role mapping (body prose untouched — empirically verified) → reworded to "never overwritten or deleted" + a strip-the-marker note.

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled rename 2's stale `_PR pending_` cells (`cf861e8` #67) in both phase-log tables.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 96 (executed 2026-07-11 — skill renames `/auto-claim` → `/auto-build` + `/auto-review` → `/auto-fix`, monograph currency, fable-override doc polish)

**Trigger.** Wade's pre-public question: "are any of the skill names really bad? I made them up as I went in the GDP project." Census of all 22 names against their frontmatter descriptions: ~19 are good-to-excellent; two are genuinely misleading, and the pre-public window is the once-ever cheap moment (consumers are BeanRider + GDP, both Wade's; the tester mirror gets rebuilt anyway; permission rules reference zero skill names — verified).

**The two renames.** **`/auto-review` → `/auto-fix`** (13 files, the strongest case): its own description reads "Automatically **fix** mechanical review batches" — it never reviews anything, and the old name collided with the review family (`/codebase-review`, `/plan-review` *find* issues), so a newcomer would read it as "automated code review," exactly wrong. **`/auto-claim` → `/auto-build`** (26 files): the old name described its first mechanical step (claiming), not its value — the flagship parallel batch builder (plan → adversarial review → execute per task) was invisible in a skill listing. The `auto-*` family now reads as a coherent set: `/triage` routes each review batch to `/auto-fix` (mechanical) or `/auto-judge` (judgment); `/auto-build` builds new work — and `/auto-judge`, opaque alone, becomes self-explanatory beside `/auto-fix`. **Kept deliberately:** `/auto-judge` (fixed by the sibling rename), `/review-close` (odd compound but 38 files deep, learnable, and the brand of the human gate), `/report-issues` (mild direction ambiguity, but `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` + the `Filed to Sysop` enum + the issue templates all share the "issues" vocabulary — renaming would orphan or cascade it), `/document-work` (bland but accurate), `/sitrep` (jargon as a feature), and the rest.

**Mechanics.** Two history-preserving `git mv`s; frontmatter `name:` fields; a scoped sed sweep over **live surfaces only**: all `core/skills/**/*.md` (incl. the 8 `_shared/` partials), WORKFLOW.md (×50), WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md, `tasks/schema.md`, `served_models.yml`'s `mechanical` example, `sitrep_survey.py` (`_AUTO_CLAIM_MAX_BATCH` → `_AUTO_BUILD_MAX_BATCH` + the Phase-73a routing strings, with `tests/test_sitrep_survey.py` renamed in the same commit), the `parse_subagent_envelope.py`/`next_task.py`/`_model_roles.py` docstrings, `batch_work.sh`'s skip-messages (with its test), workflow.html (×16), getting-started, and `.gitignore`. **Runtime-dir contract renamed:** `.auto-claim/` (per-worktree scratch + the Phase-65a `parked/` central archive) → `.auto-build/`.
