Consumer migration is `mv .auto-claim .auto-build` plus updating any consumer-side `.gitignore` entry — an un-migrated dir would become un-ignored and trip `/review-close` Step 1a's dirty classification — and rides along with the pending rename-2 BeanRider/GDP migration. **Deliberately NOT renamed:** the dev-repo-only research miners (`auto_claim_miner.py`/`_v2.py` + `tests/test_auto_claim_miner.py` + every reference to those *filenames* in `make_public_mirror.sh`, `tests/README.md`, and the tools docs) — they mine historical GDP `/auto-claim` batches and renaming would falsify their subject; all Tier-4 history (PHASE_LOG.md, both phase-log tables' historical rows, REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md, `tests/PORT_LOG.md`) keeps the old names as true history. Open REVIEW_CHECKLIST items — future work instructions, not history — DID rename: the sed was line-range-scoped to stop at the `## Phase completion log` header (0 residue above it, 18 historical mentions preserved below it).

**Bundled doc currency (the same conversation's other question).** workflow.html hero "Shipped phases" 94→96 + colophon "Phase 96 · 2026-07-11" + README "96 phases shipped"; the monograph's §VI "Model roles, not model pins" block and WORKFLOW.md §8.4 each gain the one-key `reasoning: fable` override sentence (Phase 95's mechanism, now discoverable in the explanation tier); `tools/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md` gains a "Making it yours" paragraph (model remap example + README § Customizing Sysop pointer, with an explicit "friction with the customization story is itself feedback" nudge).

**Gate.** **581 tests green** (= main baseline; the sitrep constant + routing-string tests renamed in lockstep, so the count is unchanged); role guard green on source (`auto-fix/SKILL.md` keeps its file-level marker and the one per-pin `mechanical` override — the mixed-role file survives the move); resolver 0-rewrite no-op under the default mapping; `bash -n` clean on `batch_work.sh`; 13 manifests JSON-valid (none name skills); scratch fresh install ships `.claude/skills/auto-build/` + `auto-fix/` and **neither** old dir; repo-wide residue grep = miner filenames + Tier-4 history only.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — 4 should-fixes, all applied. **SF1**: three Title-Case output banners the lowercase-scoped sed missed (`## Auto-Review Plan` / `## Auto-Review Complete` / `## Auto-Claim Complete` in the skills' own printed report templates — a user running `/auto-fix` would have seen it announce "Auto-Review Plan") → renamed. **SF2** (the real catch): the open-item sed **over-renamed** GDP-upstream and preserved-miner references in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` — "gdp's `/auto-build`" is factually wrong (GDP's skill dir is still `auto-claim/`, un-renamed until Wade migrates), `auto_claim_miner.py` got renamed in the very item that tracks promoting it (violating this phase's own miner-preservation rule), and `GDP_AUTO_CLAIM_GATE_REDESIGN_HANDOFF.md` became a dangling pointer → surgically reverted the gdp-possessive skill refs (×7) + the three filenames (`auto_claim_miner` ×6, `analyze_auto_claim.py` ×4, the handoff doc ×1), keeping wade-flow-side refs renamed. **SF3**: `batch_work.sh`'s "Skipping auto-build" was wrong on *both* counts — the script serves `/auto-fix`/`/auto-judge`/`/claim-task` (not `/auto-build`, which uses `claim_task.sh`), and its action is *claiming a review batch*; the old "auto-claim" was an accurate action verb the sed destroyed → genericized to "Skipping batch claim" (×5 + the test assertion in lockstep). **SF4**: the colophon *body* still said "as of *Phase 94*" (the currency pass caught the list entry but missed the prose line) → 96. Two NITs accepted as-is (living-doc convention of describing historical events by current names — e.g. "Phase 44 split this out of `/auto-fix`" — reviewer agreed it's the doc's standing convention; the coined "auto-buildable"). Post-fix re-gate: **581 green**, `bash -n` clean, residue re-grep 0.

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 95's `_PR pending_` cells (`2bd0a00` #70) in both phase-log tables.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 97 (executed 2026-07-11 — `/auto-build` explicit task-ID subset + `/roadmap` `Run it:` executable orderings)

**Trigger.** Wade's pre-public gap: "the disconnect between roadmap and auto-build. Roadmap tries to give me a couple of proposed paths, but auto-build has a choice algorithm that doesn't accept subsets of tasks yet… maybe it's because I have a certain deadline." His own follow-up instinct — "put all your important tasks into the current focus section" — framed the doc-vs-build question this phase answers.

**The assessment (doc-only was rejected).** `current_focus` is *phase*-granularity: it cleanly handles the case where a deadline is a genuine **lane shift** (reshape `phases:` via `/intake` re-entry, flip the flag), but the common deadline case is "these 5 of the 15 ready tasks in the *current* phase" — expressing that via `current_focus` means restructuring launch lanes for an ephemeral execution preference (phases are lanes with history, not sprint buckets), and the inversion (`on_hold_until` on everything else) is worse. Meanwhile `/roadmap`'s orderings had no executor: `/claim-task <ID>` is serial (loses the parallel plan→adversarial→execute machinery) and bare `/auto-build` picks its own front-of-sort batch. Documenting `current_focus` as *the* answer would either over-claim or sanction phase abuse — so Wade ratified **build** via `AskUserQuestion` (over doc-only and file-as-deferred).

**The mechanism.** `/auto-build` now accepts task-ID arguments (`/auto-build FEAT-0012 TECH-0004`): Step 0 classifies any token matching the schema ID grammar (`^[A-Z][A-Z0-9-]{2,80}$` — `validate_tasks.py`'s `_TASK_ID_RE`; structurally collision-free with the bare-integer N and `--flags`) into `SUBSET_IDS`; Step 1 narrows the candidate pool by **intersection** with the already-filtered frontier — never a bypass. Every eligibility rule (open status, no `user_action`/`on_hold_until`/lock, current-focus lane, met `depends_on`) still applies to a named task; **out-of-lane IDs stay excluded** (the lane filter guards which lane is being prosecuted; the reason line points at the real knob, `current_focus`). Requested IDs that don't survive print as `EXCLUDED <id> <reason>` lines — the reason ladder mirrors `ready()`'s short-circuit order exactly — and reappear under the Step 4 confirmation table, alongside subset tasks the Step 2 walk cut (named with the *rule* that cut them: solo invariant / cross-module cap / K=6-N ceilings). Step 2 is explicitly unchanged: "the invariants and ceilings never loosen because a task was named; a subset can shrink a batch, never inflate one." A subset-specific zero-survivor stop replaces the generic no-claimable message with the per-ID reasons. **`/roadmap` becomes executable:** each ordering closes with a copy-pasteable `Run it:` line built from its leading ✅-ready IDs (`/auto-build <IDs>` when ≥2 lead; `/claim-task <ID>` when one does; a 🔒 leader is named as the human's move with the agent-ready remainder handed to `/auto-build`) — a handoff, not a guarantee: `/auto-build` re-validates and still stops at its own confirmation gate, so `/roadmap`'s read-only contract is intact. The "Honesty about the ceiling" paragraph gains the subset-vs-lane-shift routing rule.

**Design detail worth keeping (shell-portability catch, found live).** The subset was first passed to the Step 1 heredoc as unquoted argv (`python3 - <<'PY' $SUBSET_IDS`) — and the build session's own zsh shell delivered all IDs as **one** argv entry: unquoted `$var` word-splitting is shell-dependent (bash splits, zsh doesn't). Fixed to environment passing (`SUBSET_IDS="$SUBSET_IDS" .venv/bin/python3 - <<'PY'` + `os.environ.get(...).split()`), which is shell-agnostic; the invocation shape stays inside the existing `Bash(python3 -:*)`-class permission rules (no new rules — the skill's Pre-flight guard is unchanged).

**Surfaces.** `auto-build/SKILL.md` (description + `argument-hint`, Step 0 parse + usage, Step 1 subset paragraph + subset-vs-lane-shift blockquote + heredoc + EXCLUDED relay + dual zero-survivor stops, Step 2 anti-loosening sentence, Step 4 "Requested but not batched" list), `roadmap/SKILL.md` (Step 4 `Run it:` instruction + subset-vs-lane-shift sentence, Step 5 actuator bullet, example block ×3 `Run it:` lines, Design-notes "Executable orderings" entry), `WORKFLOW.md` (§2.4b step 1 + skill-table row), `WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md` (`/auto-build` + `/roadmap` paragraphs). `tasks/README.md`/getting-started/sitrep enumerate no `/auto-build` args — verified, no edit.

**Gate.** Markdown-only → **581 tests green** (= main baseline, unchanged); role guard green (`reasoning=opus` markers untouched); leak-scan clean. The Step 1 heredoc is pytest-unreachable (inline markdown — the Phase 74 precedent), so it was hand-verified by extraction against a scratch 9-task/3-phase `index.yml`: no-subset parity with pre-change output (unblocker-first order intact, empty **and** unset `SUBSET_IDS`), clean narrowing (sort preserved), all seven exclusion reasons firing with actionable messages (not-in-index / done / user_action / on-hold / locked / out-of-lane / unmet-dep), and the zero-survivor path.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — reviewer compiled + functionally simulated the heredoc against its own 7-task fixture (all rejection kinds reproduced; confirmed the intersection *structurally cannot* bypass eligibility, the reason ladder mirrors `ready()` exactly with no unreachable branch, `unlock_count` still computes over the full phase so subset rows show true `unlocks`, and the env-var prefix-assignment claim is accurate), verified every arg-enumerating cross-ref repo-wide (nothing still implies `[N] [--dry-run]` only), and called the anti-rationalization seeding "unusually strong." **SF1** (real catch, reachable via the diff's own roadmap example): the Step 4 not-batched template named only the K=6/N ceilings, so a subset task cut by the **architectural-solo** invariant (exactly what `TECH-DB-BOOTSTRAP` hits in the example) would be mislabeled → broadened to name the cutting *rule* + added an architectural-solo example line. **N1**: orderings 1 and 2 handed the identical command with inconsistent caveats → solo caveat mirrored onto ordering 1. **N2**: `<ready IDs, in order>` over-implied argument order is honored (`/auto-build` re-sorts unblocker-first and fans out in parallel) → "list them in the ordering's sequence for readability — `/auto-build` re-sorts internally."

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 96's `_PR pending_` cells (`a26135e` #71) in both phase-log tables.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 98 (executed 2026-07-12 — evidence-claim limitations pass: § II + monograph falsifiers + the covered-class test spec)

**Trigger.** Wade received an external critique of the § II / Fig. 7 evidence claim ("As the convention map grew, the reviews got calmer") arguing it is unfalsifiable as presented: critical-finding rates fall in every young codebase (the **maturation confound** — nothing published separated the loop's contribution from ordinary hardening), n=1 with the loop's author as reviewer and severity grader, small-n volatility in the tail (June 68 findings, July 37), unexamined severity drift, and an unstated finding-counting policy. The critique demanded a "decisive test" (partition findings into convention-covered vs uncovered classes over time), a methods memo, and revised copy with a prominent limitations paragraph — "the limitations section is not a liability, it is the differentiator."

**The assessment (accepted, with corrections).** The maturation objection is real and was unaddressed in the *public* copy — but about half the critique's analysis program already existed in `docs/analysis/REPORT.md`, which the critic evidently never saw: the diff-size denominator (`critical_per_10k_lines`) is already the report's corroborating check, the counting policy is the report's process-induced-findings section, and the demotion pipeline exists (Phases 62/67 — zero retirements adjudicated to date, disclosed as such). The severity-drift concern is *stronger* than the critic knew: Phase 94's own notes record June's lone critical being reclassified out during an archive consolidation. And the critique's decisive test has a design flaw the repo's own May-outlier analysis documents: post-promotion enforcement sweeps file covered-class findings **by design** (Round 70: ~25 of 45 criticals were per-call-site enforcement), so a naive covered-class series *rises* after promotion and falsely falsifies.

**What shipped (copy, not analysis — the analysis is specified-not-run).** (1) **`docs/index.html` § II:** lede now names the correlation-on-one-project status; new prominent `.limits` block ("What this chart doesn't prove") covering one-grader/self-graded severity + the June reclassification (counted, June reads ~1.5%, not 0%), maturation as a live rival, the thin tail, and the falsifier ("if covered classes recur in new code at the uncovered rate, the claim is wrong"); figcap's denominator reasoning corrected from the "codebase grew" non-sequitur to the real rubric-tracking reason; § III loop-note's causal "which is why the reviews get calmer" softened to the mechanism ("has to get past a standing check, not a memory"). Bundled: `<figcap>` element → `<p class="figcap">` (the custom element never matched the `.figcap` class selector — pre-existing unstyled caption, found while rewriting it). (2) **`docs/workflow.html`** "Does it actually get quieter?": two new paragraphs — the limits plainly (n=1 self-graded, label movement, thin tail, maturation as the strongest rival: "Nothing in Fig. 7 separates the two hypotheses") and the covered-class test spec with its falsifiers; Fig. 7 cap "Severity falls…" → "Severity fell, then held low… a correlation on one self-graded project; limits in the text"; § Preamble "what that bought, measured" → "what the archive measures, and, just as carefully, what it can't". (3) **`docs/analysis/REPORT.md`** (ships in the mirror): new revision-notes section = the critique's methods memo — the four accepted points, the covered-class test **with three required amendments over the critique's own spec** (separate new-code recurrence from retro-application backfill; split by enforcement tier — mechanized conventions are blocked pre-review so archive recurrence is ~zero by construction, prose-only conventions are the informative subset; event-study recurrence of the specific promoted pattern as primary, since promotion selects on recurrence bursts → regression to the mean), plus the honest "say so" notes (second codebase = same author/smaller/different domain, not an independent control; zero demotions adjudicated). (4) **`REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`**: new Medium item to actually run the covered-class analysis (needs per-finding re-mining of the private gdp archive, ~3,300 findings against 78 dated convention states; not launch-blocking — the limitations block was the launch-blocking half).

**Gate.** Markdown/HTML-only → **581 tests green** (= main baseline, unchanged); HTML tag balance clean on both pages; diff leak-scan clean (no internal identifiers in shipped content; the one self-caught leak-class issue — the new REPORT.md text pointing readers at the mirror-excluded `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` — reworded to "queued as a follow-up analysis" before review).

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — reviewer recomputed every number from `gdp_review_metrics.json` (all ✓: Feb 285/21.4%, June 68/0, July 37/5.4%, 71/3,298/78, the ~1.5% counterfactual = 1/69) and confirmed the completeness matrix (every critique point lands on all claimed surfaces; every not-run analysis consistently marked not-run). All three SHOULD-FIXES applied: **SF1** the figcap said May's sweep criticals were "one already-promoted rule" — it was three rule families (REPORT.md's own breakdown; the monograph annotation says the plural) → "already-promoted rules… one-per-call-site"; **SF2** the unconditional "machine check" mechanism claim contradicted the same diff's enforcement-tier amendment (only *mechanized* conventions have machines) → scoped to "where a convention is mechanized… a prose-only convention's gate is the reviewer re-armed with the map" (×3 sites) and the loop-note to "standing check"; **SF3** the "held low for **five** more months" count (a pre-existing Phase-94 favorable overcount at two sites, repeated by the new limits copy) doesn't survive arithmetic — the hold is three quiet months plus one excused sweep → recounted at all three sites + the lede's ambiguous "over five months" window replaced with the explicit "between February and July 2026". NITs applied: per-line-rates claim anchored to the March peak (the Feb→Mar per-line rate *rises*); dangling relative clause fixed; "per-call-site filing *began with* LSP" → "became precise and tree-wide with" (grep-approximate per-site filing predates it); ~1% → ~1.5% (tighter, and the error direction now runs against the claim). NIT 4 (the hard `getsysop/sysop` REPORT.md link 404s until the public cut) accepted as a context flag — same class as every other link on the page.

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 97's `_PR pending_` cells (`eb277c6` #74) in both phase-log tables.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Public cut (executed 2026-07-13 — the open-source flip to `getsysop/sysop`, and the install.sh hook-arm bug the launch verification caught)

**What & why.** The one-time public cut per `tools/PUBLIC_RELEASE_SPEC.md` §4: the sterilized fresh-history snapshot becomes the go-forward **source of truth** at **`getsysop/sysop`**, and the private repo becomes the frozen notebook. All prep was already done (rename 2; the OSS starter kit; the landing page + monograph; `tools/cut_public_release.sh` built and tested green; the `wade@gdpquery.ai` email gate cleared; the mirror dry-run clean at `ef61f2e`). This session ran the flip and stood up the site.

**The flip.** `bash tools/cut_public_release.sh` cut from private `ef61f2e` → **GATE GREEN** (Pass 1a/1b/3/4 empty; Pass 2 = 38 kept Option-A provenance; Pass 2b = 128 BeanRider, no swing; 194 tracked files; snapshot `5f01c96`). SSH push was a stated prereq but **no GitHub SSH key existed** on the machine — generated a fresh ed25519 key (`gh auth refresh -s admin:public_key`, then `gh ssh-key add`; the gh token's HTTPS credential helper is a working fallback). Created **`getsysop/sysop`** (public but **quiet** — unannounced) and pushed the snapshot as commit #1.

**Repo settings (gh/API).** Squash-merge only (merge + rebase off, delete-branch-on-merge on); wiki + projects off; issues + Discussions on; Dependabot alerts + security-fixes on; About = the hero-line description + homepage `https://getsysop.com` + topics `claude-code`/`developer-workflow`/`ai-agents`. **Branch protection mirrors the private repo exactly** — required `pytest` check (strict) + `enforce_admins`, and *no* required reviews. That last is a deliberate solo-maintainer call surfaced via `AskUserQuestion`: a required approving review *with* `enforce_admins` would lock the sole maintainer out of self-merging their own `pr`-policy PRs (GitHub won't let you approve your own PR), so the config gates every merge on CI without a review gate the maintainer can't satisfy. **Pages** enabled from `main`/`docs`, custom domain `getsysop.com` picked up from the committed `docs/CNAME`, built clean; Enforce-HTTPS left off pending DNS + cert.

**The cut script committed (PR #79, `d1f223f`).** `tools/cut_public_release.sh` had been an uncommitted working-tree utility; ratified via `AskUserQuestion` to land it in the notebook via branch → PR → squash-merge — done *after* the flip so HEAD stayed at `ef61f2e` for the cut, and `tools/` never ships, so it doesn't reach the public repo.

**The bug the cold-clone verification caught (step 6 earned its keep).** A cold clone of the public repo plus a real `install.sh` run surfaced a HIGH, silent, launch-blocking bug on the *documented* install path: `arm_git_hooks` (and its twin `check_armed_hooks_divergence`) resolved the hooks dir with `git -C "$TARGET" rev-parse --git-path hooks`, which returns a path **relative to `$TARGET`** (`.git/hooks`). install.sh then used that relative path from its **own CWD** — not `$TARGET`. On the README/getting-started quickstart (`git clone …; bash sysop/install.sh /path/to/project`, where CWD is the clone's parent, not the target), the hooks armed into a **stray `.git/hooks` under the launch dir** and the target project got **none** — silently: install exited 0, printed "armed", and the post-install divergence check shared the same relative-path flaw so it never warned. Reproduced end-to-end from a non-repo CWD. Pre-existing (baked into the snapshot); the suite never caught it because every install integration test inherits pytest's CWD (the repo root, itself a git repo) and none asserted arming landed in the *target*.

**The fix (PR #80, `020d478`).** New `resolve_hook_dst()` helper anchors a relative `--git-path hooks` result to `$TARGET` (already-absolute worktree results pass through — worktree-safe; `$TARGET` is canonicalized to absolute before use), used by both `arm_git_hooks` and `check_armed_hooks_divergence`. No behavior change for `--update` (arming still skipped), dry-run, or non-git targets — and it *repairs* the divergence check, which under the old relative path silently no-op'd. +3 regression tests (`tests/test_install_arm_hooks_sh.py`) drive the real install.sh from a non-target CWD: hooks land in the target, none stray in the launch dir, an unrelated launch-dir git repo is untouched. **Mutation-verified non-tautological** (all 3 redden when the bug is reintroduced).

**Re-cut + force-push.** Per Wade's `AskUserQuestion` choice (fix-now → re-cut, over public-PR or file-for-later): re-ran the cut `--force` from the corrected HEAD `020d478` → GATE GREEN (Pass 2/2b steady; 195 tracked files, +1 = the new test), snapshot `1760d61`; then force-pushed public `main` `5f01c96`→`1760d61`. The branch protection blocks force-pushes and the auto-mode classifier (correctly) gates protection edits, so Wade ran the protection `DELETE` + force-push via the `!` prefix; the identical protection was re-applied immediately after (window safe at 0 forks / 0 stars, unannounced). Public CI green on `1760d61`; hook-arm **re-verified from a fresh public clone** (both hooks armed into the target, no stray `.git`).

**Gate.** Full suite **584 green** (581 baseline + 3 new). `bash -n` clean. Fresh-eyes adversarial pass on the fix (general-purpose Opus, zero context): **SHIP WITH FIXES** — the product fix confirmed correct across standard-repo / worktree / CWD==target / dry-run / `--update` / non-git; the one should-fix (test hermeticity — a contributor's global `core.hooksPath` is honored by `git rev-parse --git-path hooks`, so an un-isolated test could trigger a *destructive write* into their real hooks dir) applied by setting `GIT_CONFIG_GLOBAL`/`SYSTEM=/dev/null` in the test's git env (the reviewer verified this preserves the relative-default branch, keeping the tests non-tautological, and warned against pinning `core.hooksPath`, which would defeat the regression). Two NITs left as cosmetic/pre-existing.

**Remaining — pure click-ops (no repo access needed).** Apex DNS (4×A `185.199.108-111.153` + 4×AAAA `2606:50c0:800x::153` + `www` CNAME `getsysop.github.io.`); three 301 redirects (getsysop.dev / usesysop.com / sysop.run → getsysop.com); optional Cloudflare Email Routing (`wade@gdpquery.ai` already works — no swap needed); flip Enforce-HTTPS once the cert provisions; then a cold-clone re-check and **announce last**. Runbook in `tools/DOMAINS.md`. Frozen-notebook model now in effect: product development moves to the public repo; the private repo keeps receiving tracking-only commits (this entry among them).

## Phase 99 (executed 2026-07-14 — tester round 1 fixes: Dia's six `wade-cms/sysop-tester` issues)

**Context.** First external-tester feedback round on public Sysop. Dia (`diametropolis`) filed six issues on the tester mirror (`wade-cms/sysop-tester` #3–#8) via the `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` → `/report-issues` pipeline. Triaged by severity — two High (#3, #7), one Medium (#4), three Low (#5, #6, #8); all auto-labeled `bug` by `/report-issues` v1, but only #7 was a genuine code defect (the rest split doc / decision / enhancement). Two design calls were Wade's: #4 → allow-list the one-shot `--yes`; #3 → the updater fallback, then "go with your recommendation" = also do the Discussion-doc change.

**#3 — updater fallback (the headline fix).** `install.sh --update` reconstructs the OLD install (via the lock's `sysop_commit`) to detect committed consumer edits to managed scripts (Phase-24b preservation). When that commit is unreachable — exactly the tester snapshot-mirror case, where every refresh is a force-pushed single-commit rebuild that orphans the prior commit — it hard-aborted, and the abort's own `git fetch` remedy couldn't work post-force-push. The fallback (Dia's option 2): when `reconstruct_old_install` fails AND the pre-update snapshot found no dirty managed paths (`snapshot_hash` empty — clean working tree), proceed instead of aborting; a dirty tree still aborts (the ISSUE-0024/0025 preservation guarantee holds). Safety analysis: the snapshot detects only UNCOMMITTED edits, so the one axis lost when the ancestor is gone is a COMMITTED edit to a managed script (clean tree). Rather than silently overwrite it, the fallback proceeds with a loud `⚠` header naming the by-SHA recovery — chosen over silent-proceed (re-opens the data-loss hole) and over keep-aborting (breaks the documented flow). `copy_file`'s `[[ -f "$_ancestor" ]]` guard means the empty shadow dir cleanly falls through to a normal overwrite (same as `--force`). The fallback self-heals the lock (rewrites to the valid commit on success). The dirty-abort error's `git fetch` remedy was corrected to by-SHA (flagged best-effort — a by-SHA fetch works only while the host still serves the orphaned object, which is why Dia's workaround was "fragile"). Also (Dia's option 1) Discussion #1 on the tester mirror was rewritten to `git fetch && git reset --hard origin/main` in place — keeping the prior snapshot commit reachable so preservation keeps working, not just tolerating its loss.

**#4 — allow-list the one-shot update.** In a no-TTY agent session `sysop-update.sh` → `install.sh --update` refuses at `confirm()` without `--yes`, but `--yes` wasn't in the shipped allow-list, so the permission system (correctly) denied the agent's attempt to add it — every agent-driven update dead-ended. Fix (Wade's call, Dia's option b): added `Bash(bash scripts/sysop-update.sh)` + `:*` to the `settings.json` template. The `:*` also covers `--force` — accepted as consistent with every other `:*` rule and the trusted-update-agent model.

**#7 — the gitignore append that never existed.** `parse_subagent_envelope.py` documented that `install.sh § install_tasks_scaffold` gitignores `.subagent-envelopes/` on fresh install; a grep proved there was NO gitignore handling in `install.sh` at all — a dangling reference, worse than Dia's "didn't run / regressed" diagnosis. New `ensure_runtime_gitignore()` (wired into `run_install_pipeline`) appends `.subagent-envelopes/` + `.auto-build/` append-if-missing on every install AND `--update`, scoped append-only (a consumer-owned `.gitignore` is never rewritten), with no-trailing-newline handling and a one-time section header. The dangling comment was corrected.

**#6 / #8 — doc one-liners.** `/intake` Step 8 now binds "the roadmap" to `tasks/index.yml` (+ `/roadmap`, `tasks/README.md`, `tasks/open/`). README Quickstart gained the macOS bash-3.2 caveat (`brew install bash`).

**#5 — positive-signal capture (transport → Phase 100).** Dia's meta-observation: the feedback pipeline is friction-shaped end-to-end and drops positives. Shipped the capture half — a `[good]` entry convention + template in the `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` seed (option 1), and a `/review-close` Step 7 "anything that worked notably well?" prompt + a Step 8 `Signal:` line (option 2). The transport half (batch `[good]` entries into one Discussion comment per round) stays open as a Phase 100 candidate; Wade ratified a **dedicated `/share-wins` skill** for it (over folding a `--good` mode into `/report-issues`, and over capture-only). OSS context: most projects have no structured "protect this behavior" signal (stars/reactions/Show-and-tell/ADOPTERS are the norm; the closest engineering analog is a characterization test), so the transport is kept lightweight.

**Gate + review.** 592 tests green (584 baseline + 8 new: 4 gitignore, 2 fallback, 2 settings). Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (Opus, zero context): **SHIP**, no blockers/should-fixes — verified all six fixes empirically (scratch installs, dry-run branch behavior, the unquoted-heredoc backtick escaping, gitignore edge cases, a non-tautological revert test) + a leak scan. Three NITs: applied two (the by-SHA remedy over-promised → honest best-effort wording; the clean-tree warning was a quiet `note` → promoted to a `⚠` header), left one (`:*` covers `--force` — acceptable). Shipped-code references cite "Phase 99 (tester round)" not the `jig-tester` slug (leak-clean for the public mirror). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`); replies to the six issues posted after merge.

## Phase 99.1 (executed 2026-07-14 — tester round 1 follow-up: complete the runtime-dir gitignore set + `/report-issues` disclosure wording)

Two issues Dia filed minutes after the original six (`wade-cms/sysop-tester` #9, #10), the second directly extending Phase 99's #7 fix.

**#10 — the gitignore set was incomplete.** Phase 99's `ensure_runtime_gitignore()` covered `.subagent-envelopes/` + `.auto-build/` (exactly what #7 reported), but Dia found during a later cycle that the full set of Sysop runtime dirs is four — `.pending-docs/` (`/document-work` Step 3 drafts) and `.locks/` (`claim_task.sh` task locks; Phase 32) are also un-ignored. The impact is a real blocker, not clutter: `/review-close` Step 2a derives its `dirty` verdict from `git status --porcelain`, so an un-ignored `.locks/<TASK>.lock` or `.pending-docs/<branch>.md` makes a clean branch read dirty → auto-SKIP → the close silently refuses (the skills at `review-close` SKILL.md:94/:601 + `document-work` Step 4 assert these dirs are gitignored and depend on it). Fix: extended the `want` list to all four. Plus a **drift-guard test** (Dia's suggestion) — greps every shipped skill/script for `.dir/` tokens on gitignore-mentioning lines and asserts `ensure_runtime_gitignore()` covers each (denylisting `.github/` etc.), so the set can't silently drift again; verified non-tautological (the grep independently surfaces all four, incl. the two new).

**#9 — `/report-issues` disclosure wording.** Step 2's redaction reminder hardcoded "filed **publicly**," inaccurate when `--repo` targets a private repo (the private tester round itself, which the skill's own Step 0 supports). Reworded to track the resolved target ("filed to `<target>` — visible to anyone who can see that repo"), accurate whether the target is public `getsysop/sysop` or a private fork/tester repo.

**Gate.** 594 tests green (592 + 2 new: the 4-dir lock + the drift guard); scratch install confirms all four dirs append exactly once; role guard clean; `bash -n` clean. Completeness relied on the automated drift-guard rather than a fresh-eyes cold pass — it structurally checks the exact "is this set complete?" failure mode that #10 itself was, which is a stronger guarantee than an eyeball for this class. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge; replies posted + #9/#10 closed after merge.

## Phase 100 (executed 2026-07-14 — concurrency-model documentation + collision-aware-claiming filings)

The tester round surfaced a gap that was never a bug, only an undocumented feature: Sysop's parallel-work model (worktrees + locks) is sound, but nowhere in the shipped docs did it explain *where* work physically happens or *what you can safely do beside a running build*. Dia asked, in plain words — while `/auto-build` is building two tasks in parallel, can I open another session and brainstorm? add tasks? start a new task, and how do I know it's okay to claim given what's already in flight? The answer was "yes, and here's how," but we'd only ever assumed worktree fluency. This phase writes it down (**C**), files the two enhancements the "how do I know it's okay to claim?" half of the question exposed (**A/B**), and parks the heavier schema change (**D**).

**C — the concurrency model, three homes.**
- `WORKFLOW.md` **§4.4 "Working alongside a running build"** — the authoritative reference, anchored to the existing §4.1 worktree section. The three-places model (primary checkout on `main` holding the orchestrator + `.locks/` + `tasks/index.yml`; one worktree per task where agents actually edit; the two coordination files every session reads); a "what's safe while a build runs" table (brainstorm · `/add-task` · `/claim-task` · a second `/auto-build` · `/review-close`); the one hazard to avoid (freehand edits or `git checkout` on `main` in the primary checkout — the HEAD-hijack race, and why `_shared/main-push-guard.md` Rule A makes it fail *loud* rather than *prevent* it); the honest "is this safe to claim right now?" answer (partly automated today — `/claim-task` checks the task's own lock, not cross-overlap; the collision advisory is A/B); and the real parallelism ceilings (review-close is the throughput gate; shared verification state → flaky FAILs; semantic coupling that isn't file-overlap; index.yml write races; machine + supervision; dependency ordering).
- `docs/getting-started.md` **"Working alongside a build"** — the tutorial-tier callout: worktrees in a paragraph, the three safe moves, the "start via `/claim-task`, never edit `main` by hand" rule, and a pointer to §4.4.
- `docs/workflow.html` **Fig. 8 "Where the work lives"** — a new monograph figure placed right after Fig. 3 (Fig. 3 is the auto-build *process*; Fig. 8 is the *place* — the filesystem reality Fig. 3 omits). Primary-checkout plate (holding `.locks/` + the task index) on the left, two worktree boxes on the right, a `/claim-task · /auto-build` create-arrow out and a `/review-close` merge-arrow back, a bottom band with the "from another session, while a build runs" guidance. **Render-verified in a real browser (Playwright, HTTP-served) in both light and dark themes** before trusting the hand-authored SVG coordinates — the first render caught two real defects (a bare `<text>` outside a `.node` group is left-anchored not middle, so the band text overflowed; and `.small` uppercases its content, wrong for sentence-length guidance) → fixed to explicit `text-anchor="middle"` + normal-case `.smallserif`, re-verified clean. Render scaffolding (HTTP server + screenshots + `.playwright-mcp/`) torn down; none of it is in the tree.

**A / B — collision-aware claiming, filed for fresh-context sessions.** The "how do I know a task is okay to claim?" question has no automated answer today: `/claim-task` checks only whether the named task is itself locked, and `/auto-build`'s batch-sizing collision heuristics (`blast_radius` cross-module cap, solo invariants, K=6) reason only *within one batch* — neither compares a candidate against the *in-flight* set for scope overlap. New internal spec `tools/COLLISION_AWARENESS_SPEC.md` (never ships — `make_public_mirror.sh` `rm -rf`s `tools/`) designs one shared **scope-overlap primitive** (`scripts/scope_overlap.py`) with two consumers: **Leg A**, a non-blocking claim-time advisory in `/claim-task` (+ `/next-task`/`/roadmap` enrichment — the half that answers Wade's "surface me better tasks to batch"); **Leg B**, in-flight overlap awareness in `/auto-build`'s batch-sizing. The load-bearing design insight: an in-flight task's scope is a *fact* (read its live worktree diff, `git -C <worktree> diff --name-only main...HEAD`), while the candidate's is a pre-plan *guess* (`## Key files` + `blast_radius`) — the primitive matches guess-against-fact and advises, never blocks (worktree isolation makes overlap recoverable rework at `/review-close`, not corruption). Strong prior art the spec reuses: `review_tasks.md`'s `Overlap:` field already drives `/auto-fix`'s parallel-vs-sequential decision — B brings that same awareness to roadmap-task batching. Both filed to `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md § Medium` with the shared-primitive-first dependency named (the first session builds the primitive; the second waits for it on `main` — building it twice would itself be a collision). Advisory-not-blocking, a `scripts/`-tier helper (not skill prose), and B's soft-flag-not-hard-exclude are the recommended defaults; the remaining open decisions are left for the building sessions.

**D — parked.** A structured `scope:`/`files:` schema field (an explicit per-task glob list) would make overlap detection reliable rather than heuristic, but it's a schema change rippling to `validate_tasks.py` + `schema.md` + every author surface (`/intake`, `/add-task`, `/onboard`) for a signal the heuristic approximates. → `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md § Decisions to revisit later`, demand-gated on the heuristic proving too imprecise in real use.

**Phase-number note.** Phase 99's close-out earmarked "Phase 100 `/share-wins`" for the positive-signal transport skill; that item stays open (§ Low) and will land under a later number — this Phase 100 is the concurrency work that arose in the same tester-round conversation. The `/share-wins` item's live forward-reference was de-staled to drop the now-taken number (the historical Phase 99/99.1 rows are left as an accurate record of what those phases intended).

**Gate.** Markdown + HTML + one internal spec only, no executable surface touched → **594 tests green** (unchanged from Phase 99.1); role guard untouched; `docs/workflow.html` tag balance verified (8/8 `<figure>`, 9/9 `<svg>`); leak-scan clean on the three shipped files (the pre-existing BeanRider references the scan surfaced are in unrelated existing prose, not the new §4.4 / callout / figure). **Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 99's + Phase 99.1's stale `_PR pending_` cells (`67e4394` #82; `df35007` #83) in both phase-log tables. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 101 (executed 2026-07-14 — prune REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md to a live-only active queue)

Wade filed a maintainer-workflow friction item on 2026-07-14: reading `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` for routine work repeatedly overflowed the read-token budget — he'd had to `awk`-slice the file just to append new entries. The file had grown to 315 lines, but the *active open items* were a minority of it; the bulk was three classes of non-active content that Phase 56 (which established the `REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md` convention) never swept, because Phase 56 moved only *resolved item entries*, not the accreting header material. This phase finishes that sweep.

**What was bloating the file.**
- **The ~74 KB line-6 "Last updated" running narrative** — a single physical line carrying a per-phase prose log that duplicates `PHASE_LOG.md` (the canonical prose home since Phase 38/39). It is the post-Phase-56 continuation of exactly the narrative Phase 56 had already split once (the archive's "Pre-split … running narrative (through Phase 55)" section).
- **Two stale status lines** — the old "Open review batch: none…" line (a 2026-05-12 review-batch status) and a ~2.7 KB 2026-05-22 BeanRider issue-triage log (a close-out ledger of resolved `ISSUE-00NN` entries).
- **The 124-row "## Phase completion log" table** (Phase / Commit / Date / Notes) — a fourth copy of the phase index: it duplicates CLAUDE.md's canonical 3-col Phase log table plus PHASE_LOG.md's prose, differing only by a git-derivable Date column and one-line Notes summaries subsumed by the prose.

**What was done — move, not drop (nothing lost; git-history-safe).** All three classes moved *verbatim* into `REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md` (which never ships — it is Tier-4 internal, excluded by `make_public_mirror.sh`), each under a labeled section grouped with the existing pre-split narrative at the archive's top: a **"post-split continuation (Phases 56–100)"** narrative section, a **"Pre-prune status snapshot"** section, and a **"Phase completion log (full table — Phases 1–100, frozen)"** section. The moved table is byte-identical to the source save one intended change: Phase 100's `_PR pending_` Commit cell was filled with `165e4d9` (#84) during the move (the standard next-phase Phase-62-class bundled fix). A new `## Resolved — Phase 101` entry leads the archive's Resolved list. In the checklist, lines 6/8/10 collapsed to a single **"Status — live-only active queue"** pointer paragraph naming the three homes (this archive = history, `PHASE_LOG.md` = prose, the CLAUDE.md Phase log table = canonical index), and the `## Phase completion log` section (the `---` separator through the Phase-39 "Update protocol" note) was removed.

**Convention consequence, handled in the same commit.** Removing the checklist's phase table strands the Phase-38/39 going-forward convention, which had instructed each phase to *append a one-line Notes row to that table*. Left unfixed, the next phase author would look for a table that no longer exists. So CLAUDE.md's "Going-forward convention" statement was amended: the running narrative and the checklist phase-table are **retired**; a phase now closes by updating `PHASE_LOG.md` + the CLAUDE.md Phase log row and ticking/moving any resolved checklist item to the archive — no more running narrative, no more checklist phase-table row. This phase is itself the first to follow the amended convention (no checklist table row was written for it).

**Scope item (4) — "confirm no resolved items linger above the fold" — verified.** The only `- [x]` marks remaining in the active queue are shipped-sub-idea markers *inside* still-open audit items: the Caliper "three ideas" item (idea #2 shipped in Phase 75; ideas #1/#3 open) and the "Pack split discoveries" item (two Phase-5 sub-findings resolved; the `mcp-server`-pack sub-finding open). These are a deliberate "already done, don't re-propose" signal within open items, not standalone resolved entries, and were intentionally retained.

**Gate.** Markdown-only, no executable surface touched → **594 tests green** (unchanged from Phase 100). Verified: the moved 124-row table is an identical row-set to the source (diff-clean but for the Phase-100 cell fill); no `## Phase completion log` header remains in the checklist; no double-blank seams; the checklist ends cleanly on its last Planned-phases item; `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` dropped 315 → 164 lines. Inline close-out; the Medium maintainer-friction item moved to `REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 102 (executed 2026-07-14 — collision-aware claiming: the shared scope-overlap primitive + Leg A, the claim-time advisory)

Builds the first two-thirds of the collision-aware-claiming feature Phase 100 filed (from Dia's tester round — "how do I know the task I want to claim is okay to claim given what's being worked on now?"): the **shared scope-overlap primitive** every leg depends on, and **Leg A**, its first consumer — a non-blocking overlap advisory in `/claim-task`. Chosen by Wade this session (via `AskUserQuestion`, over the Tier-1 coverage backfill and the covered-class recurrence analysis) as the freshest, tester-driven, fully-in-session item he'd already flagged "wanted." Scoped per `tools/COLLISION_AWARENESS_SPEC.md`'s own recommendation — **claim-task first, so the primitive gets one real consumer before the ranking work** — leaving Leg B (`/auto-build` in-flight awareness) and the `/next-task`/`/roadmap` enrichment as the fast-follows the now-landed primitive unblocks.

**The gap it closes.** `/claim-task`'s lock check (Step 2) only asks "is *this* task claimed?" — it says nothing about whether the task's *files* collide with work already in flight in another worktree. Two claims touching the same files sail through and surface as a merge conflict at `/review-close` — recoverable rework (the worktrees kept the builds isolated), but wasted work the system could have warned about.

**The primitive — `core/companion/scripts/scope_overlap.py`.** A deterministic `scripts/`-tier helper mirroring the `next_task.py` idioms (module-scope compiled regex, `None`-default monkeypatchable path constants, inline `_sanitize_log` / `_resolve_canonical_locks_dir` duplicated for standalone-runnability, `__file__`-relative `_REPO_ROOT` = the installed `<consumer>/scripts/` layout). Auto-ships via the existing `install_companion_scripts` depth-1 loop (no installer/manifest edit). The load-bearing design is the **two asymmetric scope sources**: the candidate's scope is a *guess* (inferred lowest-effort-first from the body's `## Key files`, then `blast_radius`; **never fabricated**, Phase-58a discipline), while an in-flight task's scope is a *fact* (its live worktree's real changed set — `git -C <ws> diff --name-only main...HEAD` + uncommitted — falling back to the lock's `files_impacted:`, then the in-flight task's own body `## Key files`). It grades guess-against-fact — exact path match → `likely`, same directory or glob intersection → `possible`, disjoint → `none` — and emits a text advisory or `--json`. **Advisory, non-blocking by construction:** overlap is recoverable rework, not corruption, so the tool *warns and lets the human decide* (the guided-mode "genuine tradeoff → human owns it" branch, in deliberate contrast to the lock collision the same step correctly hard-fails). Critically it **can never break the claim flow** — every degrade path (missing index, absent PyYAML, no in-flight work, an unreadable worktree, a candidate not in the index) exits 0 with a note; only an unexpected crash exits 2 (the deliberate contrast with `next_task.py`, which exits 1 on invariant violations because it *is* the operation, not an advisory feeding one). A `none` verdict means "no declared overlap," not "provably safe" — stated in the docstring and every surface.

**Leg A — the claim-time advisory.** Wired into `/claim-task` Step 2 after the lock check (roadmap tasks only — review-batch overlap is Leg B / the existing `Overlap:` field's territory): run `.venv/bin/python3 scripts/scope_overlap.py <TASK_ID>`, surface any overlap verbatim, then continue. Framed explicitly as advisory-not-a-gate; the skill instructs that *any* non-zero exit means "advisory unavailable — proceed," never halt. **Four permission rules** for the script land in the `settings.json` template (mirroring `next_task.py`'s `python3` + `.venv/bin/python3` × bare/`:*` set); the `git -C <ws> diff` the script shells out to needs **no** rule (it's a subprocess of the permitted python call, and read-only `git` auto-passes per `_shared/permission-guard.md` § Notes) — and the rule isn't even load-bearing, since a missing rule just skips the advisory.

**Bundled Phase-62-class staleness fix.** `WORKFLOW.md` §4.4's "is this safe to claim right now?" paragraph said the collision advisory was "a planned enhancement" — now partly built, so it was rewritten to describe Leg A as shipped (`scripts/scope_overlap.py`, the guess-vs-fact mechanism, the `likely`/`possible`/`none` grading) while naming Leg B (`/auto-build` batch-sizing) and the `/next-task`/`/roadmap` enrichment as still planned. A §8.4 scripts-table row documents the helper.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — the reviewer confirmed the non-blocking contract holds under adversarial input (exit 0 on missing/malformed index, malformed lock YAML, PyYAML absent, candidate-not-found, unreadable/non-git workspace; exit 2 only on a genuine crash, message sanitized), that the grading is correct on the common cases, that the root-file false-match guard is genuinely locked, and — by mutating the same-dir guard, the heading-reset, and the exact-match branch — that the three load-bearing tests are non-tautological (each reddens). One real **SHOULD-FIX** applied: the intake heuristic `_looks_like_path` silently dropped extensionless / dotfile **config** names (`Makefile`, `Dockerfile`, `.env`, `.gitignore`) — precisely the high-collision shared-infra / build-config files the advisory most wants to catch, so a candidate whose only `## Key file` was a `Makefile` graded a false `none` → fixed two ways: a config-basename allowlist on the candidate side, and the *factual* `files_impacted:` list is now **trusted verbatim** (only placeholder-shaped / spaced entries dropped) rather than shape-filtered, with the misleading "drops the placeholder" docstring corrected to say what it really does (filter-by-shape). **NIT** applied: the Step 2 example command switched from bare `python3` to `.venv/bin/python3` (Phase-45b convention) so the advisory fires for consumers whose PyYAML lives only in the venv instead of silently no-op'ing. Two NITs accepted-and-documented (low impact): `fnmatch` doesn't respect `/` boundaries so a bare-glob candidate bullet can soft-over-warn `possible` (never a false-clean, never `likely`; only fires on the uncommon glob-in-Key-files case), and a directory token written without a trailing slash under-matches its subfiles (documented trailing-slash convention).

**Gate.** **637 tests green** (was 594; **+43** in `tests/test_scope_overlap.py` — pure grading, Key-files extraction, config-basename intake, the `files_impacted:` placeholder/trust logic, the git-boundary porcelain/rename parse + main→origin/main fallback, and `assess`/`main` integration with an injected `worktree_reader` and monkeypatched paths). Role guard green (source; no skill marker touched — the `/claim-task` edit is prose). Install round-trip clean: `scope_overlap.py` ships to `scripts/`, all four permission rules land, and the installed script runs exit-0 with a graceful note on the fresh install's seeded-empty queue (the tester's first experience). Real-git worktree smokes confirm the full pipeline: a committed-in-a-worktree change to `src/api/routes.py` → `likely` from the main checkout AND from inside the worktree (git-common-dir lock resolution), a disjoint candidate → clean, and the SF1 `Makefile` case → `likely` end-to-end. Inline close-out. The Medium **Leg A** item is partially resolved (the primitive + the `/claim-task` advisory ship; the `/next-task`/`/roadmap` enrichment remains) so it stays open in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` with an update note; the **Leg B** item's shared-primitive `depends_on` is now satisfied on `main`. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 103 (executed 2026-07-14 — collision-aware selection: Leg A enrichment + Leg B, the two remaining consumers of the Phase-102 primitive)

Builds the last third of the collision-aware-claiming feature Phase 100 filed. Phase 102 shipped the shared `scripts/scope_overlap.py` primitive + **Leg A's floor** (the `/claim-task` Step 2 advisory); this phase builds the two remaining consumers the now-landed primitive unblocks — the **Leg A enrichment** (`/next-task` + `/roadmap` candidate ranking, "surface me better tasks to batch") and **Leg B** (`/auto-build` in-flight overlap awareness). Both items were filed 2026-07-14 by Phase 100 and marked "Wade wants — for a fresh-context session"; their shared `depends_on` (the primitive) was satisfied on `main`. Wade chose **"Both, one phase"** via `AskUserQuestion` over taking either leg alone. All four surfaces reuse the *same* tested primitive rather than re-deriving the inference — the Phase-68 `_log.py` single-sourcing lesson applied to scope inference.

**Leg A — `/next-task --avoid-inflight` (the one real-code leg).** A new opt-in flag. `pick_next_task` gains an `overlap_fn: Callable[[str], int] | None` parameter; when supplied, a **two-tier** collision-avoidance key is layered onto the existing unblocker-first sort. The two-tier shape is the load-bearing design decision (and an adversarial-review refinement — see below): a **`likely`** overlap is an *exact-path* match, a near-certain conflict, so it is the **PRIMARY** key — it steers around the collision even ahead of a foundational unblocker; a **`possible`** overlap is *same-directory/glob*, a guess on a guess (the candidate's own scope is inferred), so it is only a **SECONDARY** nudge applied *after* unblocker-first — a weak same-dir hit never buries a foundational task. A clear task still wins at equal standing. The resulting key is `(likely, -unlock, possible, effort, id)`; with `overlap_fn=None` (the default and every non-flag path) the sort is byte-for-byte unchanged, so the 48 pre-existing selection tests stay authoritative. `format_task_output` gained an `overlap_note` param that renders an `**In-flight overlap:**` line for the chosen task (omitted entirely when empty). `main()` lazily imports the primitive only under the flag (`_build_avoid_inflight`), soft-degrading to the ordinary ranking on `ImportError`; it builds a **memoized worktree reader + per-task assessment cache** so ranking N candidates costs at most one `git diff` per in-flight worktree, and reuses the cached assessment to render the note. `--avoid-inflight` combined with `--review` prints an informative NOTE and is a no-op (review batches are `/auto-fix`'s territory, gated by `review_tasks.md`'s `Overlap:` field). `/next-task` SKILL.md's `argument-hint` + argument-forwarding prose now advertise the flag.

**Leg A enrichment — `/roadmap` collision annotation (prose).** Folded into the existing `--in-flight` overlay rather than a new flag: the overlay already reconciles the strategy view against what's actually running, and collision risk is exactly that reconciliation at the file level. A new **Step 2b** runs `scope_overlap.py --json <ID>` per ✅-ready candidate, reads `max_verdict` / `overlaps` / `broad_radius_note`, and drives two annotations — a **💥 marker** on ready tasks whose scope collides with an in-flight worktree, and a **collision caveat** on the `Run it:` actuator lines (`heads up: FEAT-A 💥 overlaps in-flight TECH-B … — expect a /review-close conflict`). Advisory only: the 💥 marker warns, it never removes a task from an ordering (the read-only contract holds; overlap is recoverable rework). The base path (no `--in-flight`) stays pure `Read` file access with no git/script dependency, so `/roadmap`'s any-agent portability is unchanged. This is the read-only, portfolio-level companion to `/claim-task`'s single-task advisory — "of everything I *could* batch, which won't fight what's already running?" — the half that answers Wade's "surface me better tasks to batch."

**Leg B — `/auto-build` in-flight overlap awareness (prose + Step 1 heredoc).** The Step 1 selection heredoc imports the primitive in-process (`sys.path.insert(0, "scripts")` at repo root, where `/auto-build` runs on `main`), grades each candidate against the in-flight set via a memoized worktree reader, and folds the **full 0/1/2 collision rank into the sort as a secondary key after unblocker-first** — soft: a foundational unblocker is never buried, and with nothing in flight every rank is 0 so the sort *order* reduces to the pre-Phase-103 result exactly (only an added `inflight=none` field differs on each line). It emits `inflight=<verdict>` per candidate plus human-readable `# overlap` / `# inflight-set` detail lines; **Step 4** gains an **In-flight overlap** annotation block (shown-equals-claimed, the sibling of Phase 97's "requested but not batched" list) so the human sees the collision before confirming. **Soft-flag, not hard-exclude**, per `tools/COLLISION_AWARENESS_SPEC.md § Leg B`: the aggressive option (extending the cross-module cap to hard-exclude against the in-flight set) would silently drop legitimately-claimable work, so it stays deferred until the soft flag proves too weak. The whole `except Exception` block degrades to no annotation (the batch math is untouched) if the primitive can't be imported.

**The deliberate asymmetry** (`/next-task` overlap-can-be-PRIMARY vs `/auto-build` overlap-always-SECONDARY) is not an inconsistency: `--avoid-inflight` is an **explicit opt-in flag** — the human *asked* to avoid in-flight collisions, so an exact-path `likely` conflict may take precedence — whereas `/auto-build`'s awareness is **always-on**, so it must never bury a foundational unblocker on its own initiative. Documented in both skills and both scripts.

**No new permission rules.** Leg A imports the primitive in-process (covered by the existing `next_task.py` rule); `/roadmap --in-flight` shells `scope_overlap.py --json` (covered by the Phase-102 `Bash(python3 scripts/scope_overlap.py:*)` rule); Leg B's heredoc imports in-process inside the already-permitted `.venv/bin/python3 -` call, and its `git -C <ws> diff` reads are read-only subprocesses. The reviewer verified the template carries every rule the claim relies on.

**Verification.** `+8` `next_task` unit tests inject a fake `overlap_fn` to lock the ranking contract without any git repo (the primitive itself is covered by its own 43 tests): `likely` prefers a clear task and outranks a foundational unblocker; `possible` does *not* bury an unblocker but still nudges a clear task ahead at equal standing; a uniform overlap tier falls through to unblocker-first; `overlap_fn=None` is inert; the note renders and is omitted-when-empty. The `main()` wiring was hand-verified on a scratch repo with a real in-flight worktree (default picks the colliding task; `--avoid-inflight` flips to the clear one and annotates `none detected`; with the clear task locked it selects the colliding one with a `⚠ likely conflict … shared: src/api/routes.py` note). The `/auto-build` Step 1 heredoc — pytest-unreachable, so hand-verified by extraction (Phase 74/97 discipline) — was run against a scratch in-flight collision: the clear candidate sorts ahead of the colliding one at equal unlock (secondary key working), `# overlap` / `# inflight-set` lines appear, and the control run (lock removed) reduces to the pre-Phase-103 order with no `# overlap` lines.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers. The reviewer built its own scratch repo with a real in-flight worktree + lock, extracted and ran the actual Step 1 heredoc, ran the real `next_task.py` CLI, and **mutated the sort key** to confirm the load-bearing tests redden (verified non-tautological), then reverted. It confirmed both legs' code correct, every degrade path safe, the permission claim accurate, and no gdp leaks. All four findings applied: **SHOULD-FIX 1** — the `/roadmap` output-shape *example* edited to demo the annotation self-contradicted the skill's own rules three ways (a task labeled both `✅ ready` and "in flight," `Run it:` lines batching that now-in-flight task, and a 💥-marked ID with no caveat) → the base example was reverted to a coherent no-flag version and a separate, internally-consistent `--in-flight` illustration added below it; **NIT 2** — adopted the two-tier `likely`-primary / `possible`-secondary refinement described above (the reviewer flagged that a weak same-dir `possible` hit shouldn't demote a foundational unblocker below a trivial clear leaf; the naive single 0/1/2 primary key did exactly that), plus two new tests locking it; **NIT 3** — `/next-task` SKILL.md now advertises `--avoid-inflight`; **NIT 4** — strengthened the uniform-tier test and fixed an awkward comment. One out-of-scope note the reviewer surfaced (the auto-build heredoc is invoked as `.venv/bin/python3 -` while `settings.json` lists `Bash(python3 -:*)`, not a `.venv` variant — this predates Phase 97 and is not a Phase-103 regression; the heredoc has run in production since) was left untouched.

**Gate.** **645 tests green** (was 637; **+8** in `tests/test_next_task.py`). Role guard green (source; no skill model marker touched — the skill edits are prose, and `/next-task`'s `frontmatter=quick` / `model: haiku` pin is unchanged). No installer/manifest edit (the primitive already ships; the skill/doc edits ride existing globs). `tools/COLLISION_AWARENESS_SPEC.md` status flipped to **BUILT** (except the deferred structured `scope:` field, **D**, which stays demand-gated in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md § Decisions to revisit later` — its "ships" precondition is now met, so its trigger narrows to "the heuristic proves too imprecise in real use"). Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 102's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`00ff860` #86). Inline close-out; both Medium collision items → [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Deliberately skipped a `docs/workflow.html` counter bump — Phase 103 adds no new skill or monograph surface (it enhances existing skills), so a currency touch would be churn better batched into an intentional doc phase. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 104 (executed 2026-07-14 — Tier-1 test-coverage backfill: the security / data-integrity slice)

Takes the "do first" slice of the standing Tier-1 coverage-gap item the first `/test-audit` run on Sysop's own suite filed (2026-07-08): the load-bearing **security / data-integrity guards that work today but were pinned by no regression test**, so a future refactor could silently ship them broken and green. Chosen by Wade this session via `AskUserQuestion` — over `/share-wins`, the covered-class recurrence analysis, and the outbound Ideas surface — as the highest-certainty, fully-in-session work that directly de-risks the lifecycle scripts the live tester round exercises, and the natural continuation of the Phase 82/84/91 coverage cadence. **Purely additive: no source file was touched**, so it is behavior-preserving by construction; the whole risk surface is "are these tests real, or do they pass for the wrong reason?" — which is why every guard was mutation-verified.

**The gap it closes.** Four controls on the queue-safety floor had zero direct coverage (only `next_task.py`'s *parallel* path-containment copy was tested):
- `validate_tasks.py` body/`archive_summary` **path-traversal containment** (realpath-rejects a body/summary path that escapes the `tasks/` base) — the guard whose whole point is that a string reading as a legitimate `tasks/open/<id>.md` can secretly (`..` or a symlink) point elsewhere on disk.
- `validate_tasks.py` Invariant-11 **secret scanner** (`_scan_secrets` / `_check_secret_line` — AWS `AKIA…`, `sk-` tokens, long-hex runs), a warn-only defense-in-depth backstop against a credential pasted into a committed `.md`.
- `run_checks/grep.py:run_check`'s **symlink-escape realpath guard** (skips a scanned path whose realpath lands outside `repo_root` before opening it) plus its three finding-emitting branches (`invert_file_check`, per-line `negative_pattern` filter, simple match).
- `_log.py:_sanitize_log`'s **truncation (DoS-mitigation) and newline/CR/NUL-collapse (log-injection defense) branches** — only the ANSI/control strip had been exercised.

**+23 tests across three files.** `tests/test_log.py` (new, 9) drives `_sanitize_log` directly — ANSI/control strip, the CR/LF/NUL→space collapse that stops an embedded newline forging a second log line, the truncation branch and its exact `> max_len` boundary, custom `max_len`, non-str coercion (an exception object is the primary real input), and strip-before-truncate ordering. `tests/test_run_checks_grep.py` (new, 6) drives the real `grep` binary against `tmp_path` trees for the three finding branches + the containment guard, via the `run_checks_impl` shim. `tests/test_validate_tasks.py` (+8) adds a path-traversal section (dot-dot body escape, **symlink** body escape — the case only realpath catches — `archive_summary` escape, and a legitimate-path negative that proves the guard doesn't over-fire) and a secret-scan section (one test per pattern + a clean-body no-false-positive control).

**Every guard mutation-verified non-tautological.** A coverage test that stays green when its guard is deleted is worthless, so each was broken in the source, confirmed to redden the right test(s), and reverted: disabling `_log`'s truncation reddened the truncation tests (and `>`→`>=` reddened the boundary test); neutering the `validate_tasks` escape guards reddened the traversal tests while forcing them always-on reddened the legitimate-path negative (proving it reaches the guard, not passing vacuously); disabling `_scan_secrets` reddened all three detection tests while the clean-body control stayed green — and the fresh-eyes reviewer went finer, confirming **per-regex attribution** (neutering each of the three secret regexes reddened *only* its own test); disabling the grep containment guard reddened the symlink test while its control stayed green.

**The tautological-test catch (the instructive part).** The first cut of the symlink-guard test was **itself tautological** and I caught it via the mutation pass: it passed even with the guard deleted. Root cause — BSD grep (macOS) does not dereference a command-line symlink-to-directory *unless the path ends in `/`*, so `paths=["linked_src"]` meant grep never emitted the escaping file, the guard was never reached, and the empty result came from grep, not the guard (it would only have meant anything on GNU grep in CI). Fixed by switching to a `"linked_src/"` path (dereferences reliably on **both** BSD and GNU grep), adding a paired **control test** that proves grep surfaces an in-repo file reached the same way, documenting the trailing-slash requirement inline so no one "cleans it up," and re-verifying it now reddens. The fresh-eyes reviewer then sharpened this into the one applied NIT: the control proves grep reaches a *real* dir but not that it *dereferences a symlinked* dir — different grep behaviors — so a hypothetical grep doing the former but not the latter could still let the symlink test pass vacuously. Hardened in-suite by asserting the **precondition** (raw `run_grep(...)` must surface `evil.py`) so a future platform regression fails *loudly* instead of silently going green — converting the exact silent-false-green class this phase exists to prevent into a loud failure.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP**, no blockers, no should-fixes. The reviewer independently mutation-tested every guard (including both directions of the invert neg-check and the per-regex secret attribution above), confirmed the working tree stayed clean throughout, and raised one NIT (the symlink precondition), which was applied. Two low-value notes left as-is: `test_coerces_non_string_values` harmlessly doubles as a newline-collapse assertion, and a stale-`__pycache__` artifact was in the reviewer's own mutation harness, not the tests.

**Gate.** **668 tests green** (was 645; **+23**). No source, installer, manifest, skill, or permission edit → role guard untouched, no leak surface, behavior-preserving by construction. Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 103's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`13eefd1` #87). Inline close-out; the Tier-1 coverage item **stays open** in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` — the entire "Security / data-integrity (do first)" bucket is now covered, but the Data-loss, Whole-stage/classifier, and Medium/low buckets remain (annotated with a Phase-104 progress note). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).


## Phase 105 (executed 2026-07-14 — Tier-1 test-coverage backfill: the remaining three buckets — Data-loss / Whole-stage-classifier / Medium-low)

Finishes the standing Tier-1 coverage item the first `/test-audit` run filed 2026-07-08. Phase 104 covered the "Security / data-integrity (do first)" bucket; Phase 105 covers the other three (Data-loss, Whole-stage/classifier, Medium/low), so the whole item now closes and moves to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Wade directed it in one word ("finish the backfill"); it continues the Phase 82/84/91/104 coverage cadence and de-risks the lifecycle scripts the live tester round exercises. **Purely additive — no source, installer, manifest, skill, or permission file touched → behavior-preserving by construction**; the entire risk surface is "are these tests real, or green for the wrong reason?", so every guard was mutation-verified non-tautological.

**+66 tests → 734 green (was 668).** Five new files, eight extended.

**Recon-first (three parallel read-only agents, one per bucket).** Each mapped its targets against the *current* source — exact line, guard behavior, the existing test pattern to reuse, a concrete test, and the exact mutation that would redden it. Two tautology traps were caught at the map stage, before a line of test was written: (1) `cleanup_worktrees.sh`'s `--clean` unmerged-branch guard (L176) is **unreachable by a genuinely-unmerged branch** — the classifier routes a clean-but-unmerged worktree to ACTIVE, which `--clean` skips before the branch delete; the mutation-verifiable path is `--force` (L216), which deletes every non-main worktree's branch regardless of class. Testing L176 would have been a silent tautology (for a *merged* branch `-d` and `-D` behave identically). (2) `sitrep_survey._recommended_next`'s P4 `/auto-fix` sub-branches are **dead code** — `untagged` and `auto` are defined by the identical `not rb.has_flag` predicate, so once the `if untagged:` return fires, `auto` is always empty; only `/triage` and `/auto-judge` are reachable P4 outcomes, and the tests assert only those.

**Data-loss bucket (6 tests).** `cleanup_worktrees.sh` `--force` keeps an unmerged branch (worktree removed, branch survives via the safe `-d`); `install.sh:validate_target` refuses a dirty target tree on fresh install (+ a `--force` companion proving it's the dirty/no-force branch, not a blanket failure); `install.sh:copy_file` Phase-24b preservation — a real fresh-install → modify-managed-script → `--update` round-trip (which reconstructs a shadow worktree of the actual repo) proves a consumer-modified `scripts/*` file is **preserved**, `--accept-upstream <path>` **overwrites** it, and an out-of-scope managed path (`WORKFLOW.md`) is overwritten regardless (preservation is scoped, not universal). All key on a `#SENTINEL` string that genuinely distinguishes preserve from overwrite, robust to any REPO_ROOT working-tree drift.

**Whole-stage / classifier bucket (43 tests).** `run_checks/lsp.py` (15) — the whole ingest stage had zero coverage while feeding `--fail-on-blocking`: the pyright parser (the load-bearing 0→1-indexed line conversion, rule→check_id mapping, severity), the tsc parser (line-not-column, continuation-line collapse), the `included_ids` filter, and every graceful skip (binary-missing via `FileNotFoundError` not rc, timeout, non-JSON, empty, the two tsc guard-file skips), plus dispatcher routing. `run_checks/semgrep.py` (10) — the parser was only ever mocked to `[]`; now the results parser (last-dotted-segment rule id, the deliberately-1-indexed line — no `+1`, unlike pyright, severity map) + the six skip paths. `pr_dependabot.execute` (6) — the merge-actuation safety gate: it re-resolves CI + mergeable *fresh* before `gh pr merge`, and skips a non-green or non-mergeable PR; both boundaries mocked so no real `gh` runs. `sitrep_survey._recommended_next` (12) — P1–P4 and P6 were unreachable because the test `_survey` helper hardcoded `review_batches=[]`; it gained a `review_batches` param, and the new tests cover each of those priorities plus five cascade-precedence pairs (each activates *both* adjacent priorities so the higher genuinely wins — not a winner-wins-regardless tautology).

**Medium / low bucket (17 tests).** `run_checks/grep.run_grep` empty-`valid_paths` guard — verified with a **subprocess spy** (`assert calls == []`), deliberately *not* the empty result, because BSD grep with no path operand reads empty stdin and returns `[]` even without the guard (the Phase-104 BSD/GNU-flavor lesson applied preemptively). `validate_tasks` Invariant-10 (effort + user_action required on open/in_progress, with a positive control guarding the opposite mutation), `_check_manual_smoke` non-bool type guard, `_validate_orphans` Inv-4 (both previously reached only by the never-run embedded `--self-test`). `pr_dependabot.ci_state` legacy-`state` fallback (FAILURE is the mutation-catcher — a SUCCESS-via-state case stays green even if the fallback is dropped) + terminal-`pending`. `_model_roles.resolve_text` — a new test for the defined-but-unconfigured-role branch, and the **misnamed** `test_resolve_leaves_unroled_and_undefined_untouched` renamed to `..._unroled_pin_untouched` (its data only ever exercised the `role is None` half → false safety). `install.sh:detect_packs` non-postgres-compose (a redis-only `compose.yaml` must not false-select postgres), `batch_work.sh:claim_batch` dirty-`review_tasks.md` skip (unstaged, so removing the guard's leading `!` is the clean mutation), `run_checks/baseline.load_baseline` `#`-header round-trip, `install.sh:cmd_adopt` double-adopt refusal.

**Mutation pass (author-side, 26 mutations, all killed).** A literal-string-replace harness broke each guard in the source, ran only the target test (expected RED), and reverted via `git checkout`. All 26 reddened. One methodology gotcha surfaced and is worth recording: a *same-length* mutation (`+ 1`→`+ 0`) defeated Python's mtime+size bytecode cache, so after the fast `git checkout` a stale `.pyc` briefly made the lsp test read `:41` — the on-disk source was correct; clearing `__pycache__` restored green. (Fix for future mutation harnesses: clear pycache, or trust the isolated/CI run.)

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP**, no blockers, no should-fixes. The reviewer independently mutation-tested 12 high-risk targets — all reddened — and explicitly cleared every wrong-reason-green concern: the grep spy sidesteps the BSD/GNU ambiguity; the copy_file tests key on a sentinel that distinguishes preserve vs overwrite, not repo drift; the cascade tests activate both priorities so the winner is genuine; the three positive-controls (`ci_state` green, `manual_smoke` true-bool, effort/user_action present) correctly guard the *opposite* mutation and are good practice, not weak tests. It confirmed the tree stayed clean (only test files changed, no stray worktrees).

**Byproduct, re-filed not buried.** The `/test-audit` run's two production-side source-hygiene notes — `migrate_skill_model.py:extract_model_pins` is dead code with a stale docstring (still claims `check_skill_models.py` uses it, false since Phase 69's `analyze_text`), and `run_checks/config.py:filter_checks` is a re-exported public helper reached in-repo only from tests — are source changes, out of scope for a test-only phase, so they were re-filed as their own Low-priority `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` item rather than lost in the archived coverage entry.

**Gate.** **734 tests green** (was 668; +66). `git status` = test files only; `git diff` on `core/` + `install.sh` empty. No role-guard/manifest/leak surface. Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 104's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`2a873ef` #88). Inline close-out; the Tier-1 coverage item is fully resolved (all four buckets) and moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 106 (executed 2026-07-15 — `/review-close` `.venv`-symlink classifier refinement: BeanRider ISSUE-0043)

Closes the Medium correctness item BeanRider filed 2026-05-27. A `/claim-task` worktree can carry a `.venv` **symlink** pointing at the main repo's own `.venv` (a tooling convenience — direnv, IDE plugins, or anything that hard-codes `.venv/bin/python`). `.gitignore`'s `.venv/` is a *directory* pattern and never matches a symlink, so `git status --porcelain` surfaces `?? .venv`, and `/review-close` Step 1a's mechanical "any porcelain line → `dirty`" rule mis-classified the whole worktree as **paused mid-implementation work** — forcing a false SKIP at Step 2a and an unforced-`git worktree remove` refusal at Step 3b, on a branch with zero reviewable work. BeanRider unblocked once via `AskUserQuestion` → hand-`rm` the symlink → retry; the fix puts the intelligence at the classifier boundary where it belongs. Chosen by Wade via `AskUserQuestion` over `/share-wins` / the atomic-rewrite backport / the covered-class analysis, as the strongest correctness item fully in-session while the live tester round runs.

**The fix spans two steps, because the classifier fix alone is incomplete — a design point verified empirically, not assumed.** Option 1 from the filing (downgrade the symlink in Step 1a's scan) correctly lets the branch be *reviewed*, but a downgraded-yet-physically-present symlink still makes Step 3b's **unforced** `git worktree remove` refuse (`contains modified or untracked files`, rc=128) — so classifier-only just *relocates* the false-SKIP into cleanup. Complete fix:
- **Step 1a** computes a *significant* set: from `git status --porcelain`, drop each untracked (`?? `) line that is a **symlink whose target is gitignored in the main repo**, then classify (`dirty`/`clean-ahead`/`clean-merged`) on the significant set. Everything with reviewable content — modified tracked files, real untracked files, untracked directories, and any symlink whose target is *not* provably ignored — stays significant, so the ISSUE-0016 silent-data-loss guard is unweakened.
- **Step 3b** re-applies the same downgrade rule and `rm`s just those symlinks *before* the unforced remove — deleting a symlink removes only the pointer, never its (gitignored) target, and we stay unforced, so any real leftover file still blocks the remove and triggers the existing became-dirty → SKIP fallback.

**Empirically driven throughout (CLAUDE.md's "don't guess git behavior" rule).** A scratch repo + worktrees confirmed each hinge before a line shipped: (a) the canonical bug reproduces (`?? .venv`); (b) the elegant `check-ignore '.venv/'` (trailing-slash) shortcut I considered is **invalid** — git errors `fatal: pathspec … is beyond a symbolic link` — so BR's target-based `check-ignore` is the only correct incantation; (c) `check-ignore` exit codes drive the filter correctly (rc=0 ignored → drop; rc=1 not-ignored and rc=128 error/out-of-repo → keep); (d) a worktree with genuine uncommitted work + a `.venv` symlink still classifies `dirty` (guard intact); (e) Step 3b's `rm` removes only the pointer — the main repo's `.venv` survives — and a real leftover file still refuses the unforced remove. The shipped bytes were re-extracted from the file and re-run (`bash -n` clean).

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers. The reviewer built a 9-worktree scratch and independently confirmed no data-loss regression under bash, then caught a real portability defect I'd missed and even half-observed: **`path` is a special array variable in zsh (bound to `$PATH`)**, so `path=${line#'??
