'}` silently clobbers `PATH` under zsh — and the agent's default shell on macOS (BeanRider's platform) *is* zsh, so under the real runner the downgrade no-ops (`readlink: command not found`) and reproduces the exact ISSUE-0043 symptom, while Step 3b's `git worktree remove` itself becomes `command not found` (rc=127) → the worktree is silently not removed. (This was the root cause of the "zsh subshell quirk" I'd worked around by forcing `bash` mid-build — the reviewer correctly diagnosed it as a shipping defect, not a test artifact.) **SHOULD-FIX applied:** renamed `path` → `entry` at both call sites; the fix now runs identically under bash and zsh. **NIT-1 applied (strengthens the fix against a genuine no-op):** the reviewer flagged that a *relative* symlink target (`.venv → ../main/.venv`) fails `check-ignore` (`outside repository`) and stays falsely dirty — and BeanRider's real symlink form can't be confirmed (the batch worktree is long cleaned up), so an absolute-only fix might not actually resolve the filed case. Added a `case`-based canonicalization that resolves a relative target against the symlink's own directory before `check-ignore`; verified the abs, rel, and broken-target cases all downgrade correctly under **both** bash and zsh while the guard-intact case still classifies dirty. **NITs 2–3 left as-is (both fail-safe, reviewer-confirmed):** a spaced-name symlink (`?? "my venv"`, git-quoted) conservatively stays `dirty` — no data loss, irrelevant for `.venv`; and Step 3b's `rm`-before-a-rare-still-refuses race only removes a regenerable ignored-target pointer, matching intent.

**Markdown-only** (skill prose + two heredocs) → no executable Python path → **734 tests green** (unchanged). The heredocs aren't pytest-reachable (the established pattern for skill blocks, per Phases 74/97) → verified via the scratch smoke above under both shells instead. No installer/manifest/role-guard/permission edit; leak surface none. **Deferred coordination note preserved:** the filing's Phase-32.x tie-in still stands — if the deferred `.venv`-symlink-into-worktrees feature (ISSUE-0031) ever ships and auto-creates these symlinks in *every* worktree, this classifier refinement is its hard precondition; that item stays open in `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`. Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 105's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`15a5a03` #89). Inline close-out; the ISSUE-0043 item ticked and moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 107 (executed 2026-07-15 — `/share-wins`: the positive-signal transport half of the give-back loop)

Closes the transport leg of the positive-signal channel Dia's tester round filed (`wade-cms/sysop-tester#5`). Phase 99 shipped *capture* — a `[good]` entry convention in the `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` seed + a `/review-close` Step 7 prompt ("anything that worked notably well?") — but the wins died in a local file: a tester round told the maintainer what to **fix** (via `/report-issues`) but not what to **protect** from a future "fix." Wade ratified the shape 2026-07-14: a **dedicated skill `/share-wins`** (over folding a `--good` mode into `/report-issues`, and over capture-only), because Discussions-transport is a genuinely different operation than issue-filing and a give-back feature earns its own discoverable name.

**The skill** (`core/skills/share-wins/SKILL.md`, 23rd skill, `reasoning`-role, Phase-69 marker → resolver byte-for-byte no-op) is the **third give-back skill** after `/report-issues` (friction) and `/contribute-convention` (conventions), mirroring their spine: permission guard → `gh auth` → resolve upstream repo → render → per-entry consent → post → annotate source → report. It reads the `[good]` entries (`## GOOD-NNNN … [good]`, `Status: Good — keep`), renders each win plus the full assembled comment (shown-equals-posted), takes **per-entry** consent (`AskUserQuestion`, ≤4/question), then transports **one aggregated comment per round** into a standing "Wins" Discussion and flips each shared entry to `Status: Shared` with a `**Shared:** <url>` back-ref so re-runs never double-post. Dry-run default / `--execute`.

**Why a Discussion, not an Issue.** A win has no open/close lifecycle and creates no work item — it's social proof plus a durable "don't regress this" registry. So it belongs in GitHub Discussions, and a round's wins **aggregate into one comment** (the deliberate contrast with `/report-issues`, one issue per entry). This is the family's one Discussions poster, via the GraphQL API (`gh api graphql`) rather than `gh issue`.

**Transport-model fork (resolved this session via `AskUserQuestion`).** The ratified scope said "one comment per round via `addDiscussionComment`," but that mutation needs an *existing* discussion — and `getsysop/sysop` has **zero** discussions today. Three models were weighed: *(A) standing thread, resolve-or-create* — find the thread by title in `Show and tell`, create it once if absent, then comment; *(B) new discussion per round* (`createDiscussion` each time; deviates from "comment," scatters wins); *(C) maintainer-seeded thread with a baked number* (off-repo prerequisite + a fragile hardcoded number that 404s until seeded). Wade chose **(A)**: no maintainer-seeding prerequisite, no fragile number — the "constant" is the category (`Show and tell`, a GitHub default present in both repos) plus the canonical title (`Wins — what Sysop did well`), and it self-heals (the first tester establishes the thread; an oldest-match rule converges a rare create race onto one thread).

**Empirically grounded** (CLAUDE.md "don't guess tool behavior"). Both GraphQL **read** queries were validated against the real `getsysop/sysop` before shipping the prose that instructs an agent to run them: repoId resolves, `Show and tell` is present (id captured), and the discussions query returns zero → confirming the first `--execute` takes the create path. The **RCE-safe body path was proven**, not assumed: `-F body=@<file>` binds a hazard-char markdown body (`$(whoami)`, backticks, single+double quotes) as a clean GraphQL `String!` variable — `$(whoami)` did **not** execute, no `-F` type-coercion error — matching the exact `/report-issues` Step-4 fix. `-f` (raw string) is used for every other GraphQL variable so an all-numeric `owner`/`name` (legal on GitHub) can't be integer-coerced. No mutation was run during the build (that's an outward-facing side effect; the skill creates the thread at runtime under `--execute`).

**Delivery.** `+1` permission rule `Bash(gh api graphql:*)` in the `settings.json` template — one rule covers both the read resolve-queries and the write mutations because they are the same command prefix (the classifier can't tell a query from a mutation). Auto-ships via `install_skills()` (no manifest/installer edit). The give-back trilogy is now consistent across the living docs: `/review-close` Step 7 tail (its "transport is in-progress" note repointed to `/share-wins`), WORKFLOW.md (SYSOP_ISSUES row / gh-CLI family / friction narrative), WORKFLOW_GUIDE helper list, CONTRIBUTING, README.

**Gate.** 734 tests green (unchanged — markdown+JSON only); role guard green source + installed; resolver no-op (`model: opus`); all 14 manifests + settings.json valid JSON; install round-trip ships the skill + the rule; leak-scan clean.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, one real **BLOCKER**. **B1** — the `createDiscussion` intro body (a fixed constant) contained `one project's wins`: an apostrophe **inside** a single-quoted `-F body='…'` terminates the quote early and breaks the command — and this fires on the *guaranteed first-run create path* (zero discussions on `getsysop/sysop` today), so the skill's headline capability was dead on arrival. The irony (the one skill whose thesis is "never inline a hazard-char body" broke on its own inline constant) was noted. Fixed per the reviewer's option 1: reworded to `one Sysop project` and switched the create fields to `-f`; bash-parse-verified. Two **SHOULD-FIXES**: **SF1** — Step 4.1 hard-stopped on a missing discussion category even when only a *comment* was needed (a category is needed only on the create path); made non-fatal in step 1, hard-stop deferred into the create step that actually needs it. **SF2** — the post and the per-entry flips aren't atomic, and unlike `/report-issues` there's no discussion-side dedup, so a post-succeeds-then-flip-fails state would let a naive re-run re-post a win; added a loud Step-5 branch that names the un-flipped `GOOD-NNNN` id(s), states they're **already upstream at `<comment url>`**, and instructs the human to hand-add the `**Shared:**` backstop before re-running. Two NITs applied: **N1** `-f` (raw string) over `-F` for all non-file GraphQL fields to dodge integer coercion (empirically re-verified `-f` binds String variables); **N2** dropped a vestigial `gh repo view` mention from the permission-guard note (the skill resolves via `gh api graphql`, not `gh repo view`). N3 (Phase-107 attribution) confirmed correct; N4 (the title-contains-`Wins` fallback heuristic) is acknowledged design intent — the exact-title match takes precedence once the canonical thread exists. Post-fix re-gate green (role guard source; install ships the fixed body).

**Deliberately deferred + filed (Low).** The `docs/workflow.html` monograph is stamped "as of Phase 96" and is 11 phases stale by design (Phases 97–106 all left it alone, since monograph currency is a *dedicated*-pass concern — Phases 86, 94). A piecemeal skill-count bump ("Twenty-two → Twenty-three") under an unchanged "as of Phase 96" stamp would be internally contradictory, so the next currency pass owes the skill-count bump + a `/share-wins` mention + the 97–106 feature delta together. The *living* docs (README/WORKFLOW/GUIDE/CONTRIBUTING) were updated. Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 106's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`20e4e48` #90). Inline close-out; the positive-signal channel item ticked and moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 108 (executed 2026-07-15 — durability backport: atomic-rewrite + defensive-parse for `archive_review_tasks.py` + `backfill_completed_dates.py`)

Closes the Medium "durability axis" item filed 2026-05-27 by Phase 51 (its `_log.py` half was resolved by Phase 68, leaving the atomic-rewrite + defensive-parse wins). Chosen by Wade this session via `AskUserQuestion` over the covered-class evidence analysis / the monograph currency pass / source-hygiene cleanup, as the highest-certainty fully-in-session work de-risking the two once-per-cycle helper scripts a live tester exercises through `/review-close`. Both scripts run **only in consumers** (installed at `<consumer-root>/scripts/`) — Sysop-the-meta-repo closes phases inline and has no `review_tasks.md` — so the backport source is BeanRider's hardened copies, **adapted** (not verbatim-cp'd): BR identifiers stripped, cross-refs re-verified against Sysop's own files. Continues the Phase 82/84/91/104/105 hardening cadence.

**`backfill_completed_dates.py`.** The migration helper's plain `open(index,"w") + safe_dump` becomes an **atomic rewrite** — write `<index>.tmp`, `flush()` + `os.fsync(fd)`, `os.replace()`, then `os.fsync()` the parent-dir fd (so the post-crash directory entry points at the new inode), with best-effort tmp cleanup on failure. `errors="replace"` on the read tolerates a stray non-UTF-8 byte instead of an *uncaught* `UnicodeDecodeError` (a `ValueError`, not caught by the existing `OSError`/`YAMLError` handler). Error messages use basename-only (`index_path.name`) — the path is operator-controlled but an absolute path leaks home-dir layout into shared paste-backs. `_sanitize_log(e)` replaces `_sanitize_log(str(e)[:200])` (the helper already coerces + caps). Two docstring caveats added: the `git log -S` pickaxe false-positive mode, and the basename-in-messages rationale.

**`archive_review_tasks.py`** already carried the single-file `_atomic_write_text` (Phase 48); this phase adds:
- **Repo-root path resolution** — `REVIEW_FILE`/`ARCHIVE_FILE` anchor to `Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent` (the consumer root, since the script installs at `<root>/scripts/`) instead of bare CWD-relative paths a worktree-subdir or non-`cd`'d invocation would open against the wrong dir. BR's `review_index.py:38-40` cross-ref was **not** ported — Sysop's `review_index.py` uses a git-root walk-up (a different pattern), so the comment was generalized rather than pointed at a wrong line (Phase-62 discipline).
- **`_atomic_write_pair()`** — the archive flow rewrites *both* markdown files; two separate `_atomic_write_text` calls leave a wide crash window (write+fsync+replace ×2) in which a crash duplicates state (archive has the new rows AND review still has the un-archived ones). The pair writes both tmp files first, then issues the two `os.replace` calls back-to-back, narrowing the window to two consecutive syscalls (documented as *not* transactional, with a `git checkout` recovery note). `main()` reorders to build `review_lines` before the write; behavior-preserving (final file contents identical).
- **Defensive `update_archive_total` parsing** — a hand-edited `Archive Total` row with `<5` pipe cells (IndexError on `parts[4]`) or a non-numeric cell (AttributeError on `re.search(...).group()`) now returns `(None, None)` with a `WARN` instead of crashing the whole archive flow on one typo; a `(None, None)` sentinel guard on the `main()` "Updated" print avoids a literal "None -> None tasks".
- **`_log` migration** — `_sanitize_log` (from the sibling `_log` module) sanitizes the `review_index` rebuild error message.

**The one adaptation that diverged from BR — reverted the narrowed `except`.** BR narrowed the post-write `rebuild_index()` catch from `except Exception` to `except ImportError` ("surface bugs in rebuild_index"). The **on-disk smoke caught why that's wrong for Sysop**: `review_index.py` resolves `review_tasks.md` via a *git-root walk-up* while this script now resolves it via *parent-of-scripts* — in any layout where those disagree (or with no `.git`, as in the scratch smoke), `rebuild_index()` raises a `FileNotFoundError` that BR's narrow catch would let **crash the run — after the durable writes already succeeded**, making a correct archive look failed. The rebuild is explicitly best-effort ("auto-rebuilds on next read"), so the broad `except Exception` (reported-not-silent, never fatal) is the right posture; kept it, added `_sanitize_log`, and locked it with a regression test.

**Deliberate scope calls.** Kept Sysop's existing 5-arg `update_review_tasks` signature (did **not** port BR's dead-param drop — avoids churning the 5 tests that call it; the dead `total_round_tasks` stays, pre-existing). Kept `_atomic_write_text` even though `main()` no longer calls it (the single-file primitive is exercised directly by two tests and mirrors the pair).

**Verified.** The writes produce byte-identical final files on the happy path, so the change is **behavior-preserving by construction** for well-formed inputs; the whole risk surface was the new guards + tests being "green for the wrong reason," so every guard was **mutation-verified**: the un-guarded `update_archive_total` genuinely IndexErrors (too-few-cells) / AttributeErrors (non-numeric); strict `\xff` decode genuinely raises (so `errors="replace"` is load-bearing); the write-failure path leaves the original byte-for-byte intact (injected `os.replace` → OSError); and the two adversarial-pass fixes redden their own tests when reverted. **On-disk smoke** ran both scripts in a replicated installed layout from a *different* CWD (proving CWD-independence) — the archive moved a round + bumped the total atomically with no leftover `.tmp`, and (post-fix) degraded the `review_index` FileNotFoundError to a printed note. **+12 tests → 746 green** (was 734); no installer/manifest/skill/permission/role-guard edit.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero context): SHIP** — no blockers, no hard should-fixes; the reviewer independently mutation-verified every guard and confirmed the broad-`except` revert is load-bearing. Three of six NITs applied: **N1** the ported pickaxe docstring wrongly implied `git log -S` searches commit messages (it pickaxes file-diff content only; commit messages are `--grep`) → reworded; **N2** the malformed/missing-`Archive Total` degrade path wrote a literal "(None tasks)" into `review_tasks.md` (pre-existing for the missing-row case; the new defensive guard newly routed malformed rows here too) → `update_review_tasks` now preserves the prior count when `new_archived_total is None`, plus a `main()`-level malformed-row integration test; **N3** `_atomic_write_pair` orphaned a `.tmp` at repo root on a write failure — the exact untracked-file class that trips `/review-close` Step 1a dirty-classification (Phases 65a/106) → best-effort tmp cleanup mirroring backfill, plus a mutation-verified cleanup test. Three skipped with reasons: **N4** (dir-fsync false-report — can't-happen on the supported platforms, reviewer-agreed), **N5** (basename-only on the not-found message — basename-only is the item's *specified* requirement, kept uniform), **N6** (`See CLAUDE.md § Data integrity` is a correct consumer-convention pointer — a documented `## Data integrity` subsection consumers author, per `test-assessment-rubric.md` — pre-existing, not dangling).

Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 107's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`aff195b` #92). Inline close-out; the Medium durability item ticked and moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 110 (executed 2026-07-15 — commons-framing docs pass + contribution trust policy + model-provenance rider; the first Fable-authored phase)

Closes two items filed 2026-07-15: the Medium **commons-framing docs pass + published contribution trust policy** and the Low **model-provenance-on-contributed-conventions** rider (bundled per its own trigger — "bundle with the commons-framing docs pass"). Wade routed the build to **Fable 5** deliberately — the same day's model-suitability assessment marked this the one genuinely Fable-shaped item in the queue (near-zero mechanical bulk; judgment-dense public writing + threat-model articulation) — and the fresh-eyes adversarial pass ran on **Opus** for cross-model independence, the stronger form of the independence discipline the checklist's own standing model-reviewer entry names (builder and reviewer are different models, so correlated-error risk drops rather than sharpens).

**The gap.** The give-back trilogy (`/report-issues` P71, `/contribute-convention` P81, `/share-wins` P107) + CONTRIBUTING presented contribution as *mechanics*; no shipped doc stated the thesis — **every pack convention is a documented, generalized, mechanized failure mode of AI coding agents, and contributing yours raises everyone's floor** — the commons claim a closed competitor structurally can't make (the Caliper positioning, one level up). And nothing published the curation/security rules that make an open convention corpus safe to accept strangers' contributions into — needed *before* announce, because announce is the moment contribution invitations start arriving.

**Framing half.** `README.md` gains a differentiator paragraph after the lifecycle lede: corpus-is-the-point, the give-back route, a pointer to the trust policy, and the optional positioning fold-in — the floor matters most for cheaper-generation-model setups (lighter coder + `reasoning`-tier reviewer via Phase 69's role indirection), worded as design intent ("designed to catch"), never as a measured result. `docs/workflow.html`'s differentiator section gains a second paragraph in the monograph register (closer: "The floor is shared; the curation is not crowdsourced."). `CONTRIBUTING.md`'s lede states the thesis and points at the policy.

**Trust-policy half — new `CONTRIBUTING.md § Contribution trust policy`, each rule named load-bearing, not etiquette.** (1) **Convention contributions land as issues; a maintainer authors the actual pack change** — convention prose is read by review agents in privileged contexts (the map is the reviewer's rubric), so contributed convention text is a prompt-injection surface; an issue keeps it inert, convention PRs are never auto-merged, and a convention PR is usually closed in favor of a maintainer-authored commit that credits the contributor. (2) **No contributed git hooks, period** — a hook is arbitrary code execution on every consumer's commit; templates ship from the maintainer only. (3) **Mechanized rules are reviewed like code, because they are code** — review looks for inverse logic (a rule that blesses the pattern it claims to block) and ReDoS-shaped regexes that would run on every consumer's CI path. (4) **The merge gate is cross-consumer survival** — WORKFLOW §5.1's cross-round gate one level up: a convention merges once >1 project has independently hit it; a singleton waits as an open, credited issue. (5) **You can't leak your codebase by accident, and that's advertised** — generalize-to-placeholders + shown-equals-filed + per-pack consent + dry-run default; the property that makes contributing compatible with a corporate "no proprietary code leaves the building" policy.

**Model-provenance rider (the Low item).** `/contribute-convention` Step 3 gains one optional question in the existing attestation turn — which model/agent family generated the strays these conventions kept catching, and roughly when — **never required, never inferred from git history, never pressed; absence is honest**. The answer is project text like the attestation: it flows through Step 4 generalization and lands in the Step 6 body, so shown-equals-filed holds end-to-end. Step 6 gains the optional `**Model provenance:**` body line (omitted entirely when unknown); the `pack_or_convention` issue template gains the symmetric optional hint for hand-authored proposals; CONTRIBUTING explains the why in one paragraph. Dataset value: separates durable engineering discipline (model-agnostic — the corpus's core value) from model-era tics, which become natural retire candidates for the demotion path (P62/P67) when a model generation ages out — and makes the "do cheaper-model users contribute noisier conventions?" question empirically answerable.

**Phase-stat currency (rides along, per the Phases 94/96/109 number-sites-move-together discipline).** The monograph content edit obligates the stamp move (it's a point-in-time artifact): hero shipped-phases `109 → 110`, both colophon stamps → `Phase 110 · 2026-07-15`, `docs/index.html` stat tile `109 → 110`, README "109 phases shipped → 110".

**Gate.** Markdown/HTML-only → **746 tests green** (unchanged); tag balance even on both edited HTML files; role guard green (the SKILL.md edit touches neither pin nor marker); leak-scan clean — the new prose introduces zero internal identifiers (the scan's only hits are pre-existing sanctioned named-provenance).

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — the reviewer verified every factual claim in the new prose against the real machinery (shown-equals-filed / per-pack consent / dry-run / excluded-and-handed-back all real in the skill; the §5.1 citation accurate; anchors resolve; stat = 110 at all four sites; HTML balanced; no new leaks; the provenance rider optional, non-inferring, and shown-equals-filed-preserving end-to-end). **SF1 (the real catch):** the new trust policy contradicted the *pre-existing* pack-authoring guidance — "Ways to contribute", "Before you start" ("a new pack" as the worked example of a large *PR*), and the pack-skeleton section still walked a first-time contributor down build-it-and-PR-it, only for the policy to say the PR "will usually be closed" → reconciled all five sites: the packs + conventions bullets now route to the issue path explicitly, "Before you start" gains "the issue *is* the contribution", the skeleton is reframed as what a proposal sketches / what a maintainer-authored pack contains, the new-pack bullet's marketplace/README registration moved into the maintainer-authored commit, and the licensing section extends inbound=outbound MIT to issue-proposed content (the reviewer's related lower-weight note). **NITs applied:** "compounds across consumers" → "**can** compound" (design-intent hedge — no external consumer has contributed yet); "nothing merges unreviewed" → "no **contribution** merges unreviewed" (the repo auto-merges green Dependabot patches via `/pr-dependabot`; scope the claim); blank line before the template's `**Model provenance:**` line (CommonMark-safe). **NIT accepted, no change:** the issue template's inline `Model provenance:` hint vs the skill's bold body line — same field, two presentations, template is a human hint.

Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 109.1's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`3e307a7` #95) in the CLAUDE.md phase-log table. The sibling supply-chain Medium item's scope (d) — "name the contributions-land-as-issues property load-bearing" — is discharged by this phase's trust policy; annotated there rather than closed (its (a)/(b)/(c) versioning + pinned-install legs remain). Inline close-out; both items → [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 111 (executed 2026-07-15 — supply-chain hardening: release-tag-pinned bash installs, `install.sh --ref <tag>`)

Closes the Medium **plugin/pack supply-chain hardening** item filed 2026-07-15 — the "staying unversioned" revisit trigger having fired (the public cut `getsysop/sysop` on 2026-07-13 + the live tester round mean external consumers track repo HEAD on *both* install paths, so the packs were a supply chain with no pin: a compromised maintainer account or a malicious merge propagates to every consumer on their next update, and nothing let a cautious consumer say "give me the last reviewed release"). Scope + first version ratified via `AskUserQuestion`: **tags + bash `--ref`**, first release **v0.1.0**.

**The pivotal recon reframe (the item's literal leg (a) was counterproductive).** The filing said "add `version` to the 12 `plugin.json` manifests + cut releases." A `claude-code-guide` probe of the official docs (per the CLAUDE.md "don't guess the plugin manifest schema" rule) found that adding a `version` field to a plugin manifest **freezes** Claude Code plugin auto-updates — consumers then update *only when the maintainer bumps the field* ("pushing new commits alone is not enough"), so we'd bump ~13 version strings every phase or plugin-path consumers silently stop receiving updates — **and it still gives no consumer-side pin** (there is no `install sysop@x.y.z` syntax; version is maintainer-controlled only). The docs' idiomatic answer for "ship frequently *and* offer a stable pin" is a **dual-marketplace release channel** (a `sysop-stable` marketplace pointing at a tag), not version fields on the default marketplace. So the reframe: **keep `plugin.json` unversioned** (commit-SHA auto-update stays), deliver pinning where it's actually controllable — the **bash path** — and treat a stable-channel marketplace as a documented *future* option. The recon saved us from an actively-harmful change; the value of cutting git tags/releases is that they're the thing a `--ref` pin (and any future stable channel) points *at*.

**Mechanism — `install.sh --ref <tag>` (fresh install or `--update`).** The installer's "source" is simply its own clone's working tree (`$REPO_ROOT = $SCRIPT_DIR`), copied directly by every `install_*` with **no checkout step** anywhere in the copy path. So `--ref` materialises the rev into a temp `git worktree add --detach` (the exact `reconstruct_old_install` pattern — the in-repo precedent that satisfies the Phase-58a source-verification bar) and **re-points `$REPO_ROOT` at it for the whole pipeline**; `get_sysop_commit` then records the *rev's* commit in the lock (so a later `--check` correctly reports the consumer N commits behind HEAD). Nested-`git worktree add` from a linked worktree (needed because `--update --ref` runs `reconstruct_old_install` with `$REPO_ROOT` re-pointed) was **empirically verified** before building (CLAUDE.md "don't guess git behavior"). `SYSOP_SRC_CLONE` holds the original clone for two jobs: removing the ref worktree on exit (a worktree can't cleanly remove itself) and standing in for `$REPO_ROOT` in every consumer-facing recovery/onboarding hint (which must name the durable clone, not the ephemeral worktree). A **unified `_cleanup_install_temp` EXIT trap** (set once in `main()`) replaces the old per-site divergence-shadow trap and cleans **both** temp resources — bash has one EXIT trap, so a single guarded cleanup avoids the two sites clobbering each other. `--ref` is **rejected for `--adopt`/`--check`** (record a rev in an adopt lock with `--anchor`; `--check` reads HEAD via `--source`), fails gracefully on an unresolvable rev (exit 1 + `git fetch --tags` hint, nothing written), and carries a value guard (missing or flag-shaped value → exit 2, friendlier than the silent `shift 2` its `--anchor`/`--source` siblings inherit; safe because git refs never start with `-`).

**Decision — opt-in `--ref`, keep HEAD as the default** (not flip `--update` to a tag default). The tester mirror (`wade-cms/sysop-tester`) is a force-pushed **snapshot** with *no tag objects*, so a tag-default would fail to resolve any tag there and **break the live tester round** (and `--check` would need parallel tag-resolution rework). Opt-in `--ref` is purely additive → **zero regression** for the HEAD-tracking consumers (BeanRider, GDP, the tester mirror), confirmed by the unchanged default-path suite. `sysop-update.sh` needs **no code change** — `--ref` rides its existing `"$@"` passthrough (doc-only). **Sticky pinning** (a lock field keeping subsequent updates on a release track) was deliberately *not* built — per-invocation `--ref` for v1 is simpler and *safer* (an update never silently stays on a stale, possibly-vulnerable release); noted as a future option.

**Docs (leg c + the amendments the item mandated).** `SECURITY.md` reframed: "Supported versions" now names rolling `main` + tagged reviewed releases, a new "How updates reach you — and how to pin" section (bash `--ref` is the real pin; the plugin path tracks HEAD by commit-SHA and pins only by disabling marketplace auto-update, with the stable-channel marketplace as a future option), and a "Maintainer posture" note (2FA, protected `main`, contributions-land-as-issues) pointing at Phase 110's `CONTRIBUTING.md § Contribution trust policy`. `README.md`'s "Version pinning is not officially supported" point → "Pinning the plugin path" (why unversioned is deliberate + the bash `--ref` hard pin); the support-expectations line reworded. `CLAUDE.md § Things NOT to do` amended (the item's explicit ask): keep manifests unversioned *on purpose* — versioning would freeze plugin auto-update without buying a pin; release pinning is via tags + `--ref`, and the "revisit after the first external user" trigger is now resolved to tags-not-versions. `/release` SKILL.md's "Sysop is deliberately unversioned so it wouldn't exercise the write path" corrected (Sysop now cuts *tags*, but its manifests stay unversioned, so it exercises the tag path, never the manifest-rewrite path). `WORKFLOW.md` §8.2b gains `--ref` in the forwarded-flags list + a dedicated `--ref` paragraph. **Cutting the first release itself** (`v0.1.0` tag + GitHub Release + `CHANGELOG.md`) is a human-gated `/release --execute --github-release` run Wade does from merged `main` — this phase ships the pinning *machinery* + docs; the tag is the follow-through (no `CHANGELOG.md` pre-created, since `/release` owns it).

**Deliberately NOT built** (documented): `version` fields on any manifest (freezes plugin auto-update, no consumer pin); the dual-marketplace stable channel (a real plugin-path pin, but heavier infra — a future item); sticky-pin lock state.

**Gate.** +8 integration tests (`tests/test_install_ref_sh.py`, driving the real `install.sh` against a self-contained scratch **source clone** tagged one commit behind its HEAD) → **754 tests green** (was 746). **Mutation-verified non-tautological:** neutering the `REPO_ROOT` re-point reddens the tag-commit + content-from-tag + update-repin tests (pinning becomes a no-op → lock records HEAD, sentinel leaks into the pinned tree), and reverting the SF1 footer fix reddens the footer assertion. `bash -n` clean; 13/13 manifests valid; role guard green (no skill pins touched); leak-scan clean on shipped content; `SECURITY.md → CONTRIBUTING.md § Contribution trust policy` anchor resolves.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — the reviewer exercised all eight risk areas against a real tagged source clone and verified the core claim empirically (content genuinely from the tag's tree not just the recorded sha; lock records the tag's commit; worktrees always cleaned from the original clone; `reconstruct_old_install` correctly ran *through* the linked ref worktree and preserved a committed local edit; the unified trap dropped no path and is `set -u`-safe; the default no-`--ref` path unchanged) and **confirmed both plugin-versioning doc claims TRUE against the official docs** (a `version` field freezes per-commit auto-update; no consumer-side version-pin syntax). **SF1 (the real catch):** the fresh-install footer printed `$REPO_ROOT` — the *ephemeral, deleted-on-exit* worktree path — as the `export SYSOP_SRC=…` line and the lower-level `bash …/install.sh` command, so a pinned consumer's very first `sysop-update.sh` would fail the shim's `SYSOP_SRC` precondition (fails loud, not silent, but actively-wrong onboarding for exactly the cautious audience the feature targets) → fixed with `${SYSOP_SRC_CLONE:-$REPO_ROOT}` at both footer lines, and the same fallback swept across every other consumer-facing recovery hint that prints the source path (the `reconstruct_old_install` skip hint + both `--update` fail-closed recovery hints — NIT 3, same root cause), regression-locked by a footer assertion in the fresh-`--ref` test. **NIT 1 + NIT 2** (trailing `--ref` with no value died on a silent `shift 2` exit 1; `--ref=` empty silently tracked HEAD) → the value guard above (+ a test). My own `--ref` error messages (the git-clone / cannot-resolve checks) were verified correct as-is — they fire *before* the re-point, so `$REPO_ROOT` is still the clone there.

Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 110's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`98c3d53` #97) in the CLAUDE.md phase-log table. Inline close-out; the Medium supply-chain item ticked and moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md) — its (a) legwork resolved as "cut tags, not version fields," (b) shipped as `--ref`, (c) shipped in `SECURITY.md`, (d) already done by Phase 110; the plugin-path stable-channel marketplace refiled as a demand-gated future option. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 112 (executed 2026-07-15 — covered-class recurrence analysis: the falsifier that tries to separate the convention loop from ordinary maturation)

Closes the Medium § II-evidence item filed 2026-07-12 by the external critique, chosen by Wade this session. The critic's point: "the reviews get quieter as the convention map grows" is, on the shipped round-level dataset, a **correlation that ordinary code maturation would also produce** — young codebases get less critical over time regardless of any convention loop, and nothing published separated the two hypotheses. Phase 98 accepted the critique, weakened the public copy to correlation-plus-mechanism, and shipped an explicit limitations block, leaving the decisive test — the **covered-class test** — specified in `docs/analysis/REPORT.md` but **not run**. Phase 112 ran it.

**The test.** Partition every finding into **(A)** a class already covered by a promoted convention at the time of its round, versus **(B)** a class nothing covered. Maturation depresses A and B together; a working enforcement loop selectively suppresses A. Three amendments (all from REPORT.md's own earlier findings) shaped the method: (1) separate new-code recurrence from **retro-application backfill** — when a new instrument is turned on it files covered-class findings across the whole tree *by design*; (2) split by **enforcement tier** — a mechanized convention's archive recurrence is ~0 after its gate by construction, so the informative subset is the prose-only window; (3) prefer the **event-study** form — promotion selects on a recurrence burst, so regression-to-the-mean guarantees some post-promotion decline even with zero enforcement.

**Method.** All 3,298 gdp findings were classified against the 79 dated conventions with a transparent **signature classifier** (distinctive helper/option identifiers that recur verbatim in findings, plus a documented prose-keyword layer). Each convention's *promotion* date (first CLAUDE.md git appearance) and its *mechanization* date (first appearance of a real machine gate — semgrep rule / `checks.yml` check / eslint error rule) were dated independently from git history. The classifier was **validated blind** by an independent fresh-agent labeler on a 100-finding stratified (early/late) sample: **precision 0.80, recall 0.66, exact-class agreement 0.82**. Low recall is *conservative* for the A/B contrast — missed covered findings fall into B, diluting the difference the test looks for. Reproducible via `docs/analysis/covered_class_analysis.py` (a **dev-repo research artifact**, excluded from the public mirror like `auto_claim_miner.py` because it hardcodes gdp-specific convention signatures the leak-greps do not catch; re-running it needs the private archive).

**Result — mixed, and honest.** The **rate-normalized test is inconclusive.** gdp's review instrument changed twice mid-history — a grep check registry (2026-03-20) and then semgrep + language-server review (2026-04-17, the "spike" Wade flagged mid-session) — each surfacing a whole-tree backlog across *every* finding class, covered and novel alike, then collapsing as the tree was swept clean. The truly-novel (uncovered) baseline **itself swings 161 → 169 → 445 → 13 per 100k effective lines** across the four instrument eras, so per-window recurrence *rates* are dominated by the instrument, not by code health or enforcement — for A and B classes alike. The one signal robust to this is within-convention and **denominator-free: 14 of 26 mechanized conventions have zero post-gate new-code recurrence (21 of 26 have ≤ 2)** — for 13 of those 14 the class had been recurring in the review before the gate (1–14 prior findings) and then stops; the fourteenth (an abort-cleanup rule) appeared only in the activation sweep, so it is not evidence of a reduced recurrence. Prose-only and novel classes keep recurring. **Load-bearing caveat:** this is partly true *by construction* — a machine gate catches the class before the review runs, so it stops appearing as a review finding whether or not fewer are written. It proves the gate works; it does not independently prove the code is healthier absent the gate. **Prose-only conventions show no separable effect from maturation** — their covered-class recurrence tracks the novel-class baseline.

**Decision (ratified via `AskUserQuestion`, option 1 of 4, then a follow-up on the public HTML).** The result **confirms the mechanization-specific clause** already in the § II / monograph copy ("where a convention is mechanized its machine check makes silent recurrence of that finding class structurally harder"), finds **no separable effect for the prose-only clause** (inconclusive, not a proven null), and confirms **maturation is entangled and large**. It does *not* support a blanket "the loop suppresses covered classes beyond maturation" claim. So the **Phase-98 weakened *claim* stands unchanged** and the falsifier is recorded as *run, with a mixed result* rather than buried — more credible than the aggregate chart alone. Promoting the mechanization finding to lead § II evidence was **considered and declined** (the by-construction caveat + n=1 + classifier error bars make it too thin to headline — exactly the over-claim the critique warned against). **The one public-copy change** (surfaced by the fresh-eyes review, ratified separately via `AskUserQuestion`): the landing page (`docs/index.html`) and monograph (`docs/workflow.html`) both said the test "has not been run" — now false — so that stale *status* was corrected to "run, mixed result" while the claim itself stays put; a pure factual correction, not the "promote to lead evidence" option (which was declined).

**Delivery.** New `docs/analysis/covered_class_analysis.py` (reproducible, self-contained, read-only against the private gdp clone) + its emitted `covered_class_metrics.json`, both added to `tools/make_public_mirror.sh`'s exclusion list (`rm -f` + a header note explaining the leak-scan-drift risk: unlike `mine_gdp_reviews.py`, which extracts everything at runtime with zero hardcoded identifiers, this script hardcodes gdp convention signatures). `REPORT.md` § "The covered-class test" flipped from *(specified, not run)* to *(run — Phase 112)* with the full method / result / verdict, plus a dated revision note and an updated header Date line.

**Gate.** Docs + a mirror-excluded research script only → **754 tests green** (unchanged from the Phase-111 baseline — no shipped code, skill, manifest, or test file was touched; the analysis is behavior-preserving for the product by construction). `bash -n` clean on the edited mirror script; the consolidated script reproduces every number cited in REPORT.md and the phase log.

**Fresh-eyes adversarial pass (general-purpose Opus, zero authoring context): SHIP WITH FIXES.** The reviewer independently reproduced every headline number (byte-identical `covered_class_metrics.json`), confirmed the A/B split / mechanization gating / event-study logic sound with no verdict-flipping bug, and verified the leak surface clean (script + metrics correctly mirror-excluded; REPORT.md introduces no new private gdp identifiers beyond the sanctioned `_sanitize_log` example + generic library options). **One real BLOCKER (a genuine catch):** the shipped landing page (`docs/index.html`) and monograph (`docs/workflow.html`) both still stated the covered-class test "has not been run" — now false, and a direct contradiction with the REPORT.md "run" update shipping beside them in the public mirror. My option-1 decision ("no public change") had assumed the public copy was silent on run-status; it wasn't, so "no change" would ship a falsehood. Resolved via a follow-up `AskUserQuestion` (disclose vs keep-private): **disclose** — both HTML surfaces corrected from "has not been run" to "has now been run (Phase 112); mixed result — rate comparison inconclusive, mechanization clause confirmed but partly by construction, prose-only no separable effect" while the *claim itself* stays the narrow, defensible one (not promoted to lead evidence). **All four SHOULD-FIXES applied:** (2) reconciled the 78-vs-79 convention count in the shipped report (the 78 is the 2026-07-11 snapshot; the map gained one entry by the 07-15 run); (3) the mechanization sentence over-smoothed — the two *highest-volume* mechanized classes (Logging, Engine selection) did NOT collapse post-gate, now disclosed as exceptions cutting against the signal; (4) added that the classifier's 0.66 recall runs *anti-conservative* for the "zero post-gate" count (a missed post-gate finding inflates "14 of 26 to zero"), where for the A/B contrast it's conservative; (5) softened "returns a null on the prose-only clause" → "no separable effect detectable (inconclusive)" AND backed it with a committed, reproducible prose-only era-split (covered-prose 24→45→48→3 vs novel 161→169→445→13 per 100k; both instrument-dominated, covered-prose share of novel bounces with no trend). **NITs applied:** the "14 of 26" denominator now notes it is 26 of 28 gated conventions the classifier saw; dropped the dubious `covered_fraction_recall_adjusted_pct` estimator from the JSON; added boundary-day-overlap and validation-reproducibility caveats to the script. **One error I caught in self-verification before the review:** the "classes that provably recurred before the gate (6–56 findings each)" claim was wrong — the 14 zero-post-gate conventions' pre-gate range is 0–14, and one (an abort-cleanup rule) had zero pre-gate findings (activation-sweep-only) — corrected across REPORT.md / PHASE_LOG / CLAUDE.md to "13 of the 14 recurred before (1–14 prior findings); the fourteenth was sweep-only."

Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 111's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`bb087a6` #98) in the CLAUDE.md phase-log table. Inline close-out; the Medium covered-class evidence item ticked and moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 113 (executed 2026-07-15 — README progressive-disclosure restructure + the audience story: who Sysop is for, and who it isn't)

Triggered by external feedback relayed by Wade: a colleague read the README as "a federal data science supervisor writing an immutable technical standard" — the wrong filter for a GitHub front page, where a visitor is looking for a reason to stay, not a specification. The in-session assessment confirmed the diagnosis quantitatively (304 lines, ~150 of them update/reconciliation mechanics — Phase 24a/24b/25, plugin-update reconciliation, stale-token reports, pyyaml notes — accreted phase-by-phase with no reader-first pass ever taken) and added a second, related finding: the **audience** answer already existed and was good ("Three readers, and one who should close the tab," `workflow.html`), but it lived at the *bottom* of the funnel while the front page carried zero qualification — and the "who shouldn't use this" story (cost, Claude-Code requirement, team non-fit, project-size non-fit) was scattered or absent entirely. Wade directed both fixes as one phase.

**The restructure (progressive disclosure — colleague's shape, adapted to this repo's constraints):**

- **`README.md` → a ~100-line landing page.** Hero tagline + first paragraph kept verbatim. New **Mermaid loop figure** (finding → convention → deterministic check → back into review, with the FP-ledger demotion edge) — Mermaid over a lifted monograph SVG on purpose: GitHub renders it natively, it's theme-safe, and it doesn't mint a new hand-drawn currency surface (the monograph figures are theme-aware inline SVG that wouldn't transplant). Render-verified via Playwright against real mermaid 11 (the one artifact of that check — `·` separators showing as `Â·` — was proven to be the *test page's* missing charset declaration, not a diagram defect; re-render with UTF-8 declared came back clean). The paragraph-2 lifecycle wall was replaced by **"What you get"** bullets; the Phase-110 commons/differentiator paragraph was **condensed, not cut** (corpus thesis + trust-policy link + the cheaper-generation clause all survive — it was deliberate announce-prep framing). Quickstart slimmed to the `--packs auto` golden path with the two load-bearing details explicitly preserved: the **full-payload `git add`** (byte-identical across README / getting-started / install-and-update — Phase 79/85 established that a worktree only sees committed files) and the **macOS bash-4+ caveat**; the Claude Code plugin kept exactly one sentence (matching the architecture — a plugin-only install is explicitly insufficient), with its mechanics moved. New **Documentation index**; slim Status; **Backing out kept in the README** (the trust anchor) in compressed form with the full walkthrough moved.
- **Two new public docs** (both ship in the mirrors; content **moved near-verbatim, not rewritten**, to keep the diff reviewable and avoid minting a drift axis): [`docs/install-and-update.md`](./docs/install-and-update.md) — both install paths in full, the update contract (shim, `--update` snapshot/divergence/delta behavior, `--adopt`/`--check`, the lower-level invocation, a new `--ref` release-pinning paragraph), Phase 24b preserve-if-modified, the plugin path's four numbered points + reconciliation, required permissions, the repo-layout tree, and the complete Backing out (including the no-PyYAML manual reversal) — and [`docs/configuration.md`](./docs/configuration.md) — the three management tiers, CLAUDE.md-prose behavior overrides, the never-managed overlay table, Phase 24a append-point pattern with both worked examples, Phase 25 placeholder substitution + stale-token report, model roles (`#models` anchor), skills-don't-persist-by-design, and the optional `/simplify` note. Where the old README *restated* WORKFLOW.md § 8.2b/c, the pointers were kept rather than a third copy grown.
- **The audience story (`## Is this for you?`)** — the new README section distills the monograph's Three Readers to the front door **with evidentiary honesty** (the repo's own design-intent-vs-earned-record discipline, applied to positioning): *built for* (1) the solo engineer shipping a real product — named as the case the workflow was extracted from and the one with dogfood evidence; (2) the agentic team — with the single-human-reviewer boundary stated up front (two-people-one-queue = deliberate non-goal, Phase 90's honesty sentence promoted from one buried monograph line); (3) the builder growing into the judgment — guided mode described faithfully (opt-in, gates restated, bar unmoved) and labeled *newer and less proven*. *Probably not for you:* the project fits in your head (the monograph's not-a-fit, front-paged); you're not in Claude Code yet (portability = design intent, not yet an earned record — matching getting-started's framing verbatim in spirit); **you're on a tight token budget** — the first place any Sysop doc states the cost expectation (deep skills default to Opus-class on purpose; Max plan or API budget is the comfortable fit; the one-key `served_models.local.yml` remap linked as the knob). The cost gap was ranked the highest-damage silent omission in the assessment: a Pro-plan user hitting limits mid-cycle was the most predictable negative first impression, and the remap was documented only as *customization*, never as *expectation-setting*.
- **Cross-refs repointed (5 sites):** `docs/getting-started.md:246` (Customizing Sysop → `configuration.md`; the `#backing-out` link verified still valid against the kept README section), `tools/TESTER_ONBOARDING.md:76`, `WORKFLOW.md` ×2 (the pyyaml worked-example pointer and the model-roles § pointer), `core/companion/scripts/sysop-update.sh:36` (error hint README "Installation" → README "Quickstart"). `SECURITY.md`'s "README § Support expectations" pointer needed no change (section kept).
- **Stat currency 110 → 113** across all four sites per the move-together discipline (README Status, monograph hero + "as of Phase" + colophon, index tile); 71 rounds / 3,298 findings / 78 conventions verified unchanged.

**Gate.** Markdown/HTML + one shell-string edit only → **754 tests green** (unchanged; no skill/manifest/permission/role-guard surface touched); leak-scan clean on both new mirror-shipping files; HTML tag-balance even on both edited pages; `bash -n` clean on the shim; every link/anchor hand-verified; the Mermaid figure render-verified in a real browser.

Content preservation was verified claim-by-claim (pyyaml notes ×2, stale-token report, `--adopt`/`--check`, contract-files framing, `SYSOP_SRC` setup, the plugin path's four points — all located in the new homes; the only condensation found lossless). Links/anchors all resolve (20+ checked, GitHub anchor rules); repo-wide stale-ref grep zero; every audience-section claim verified against the real machinery (guided-mode stanza + "bar doesn't move," `served_models.yml` `reasoning: opus`, `workflow.html`'s single-reviewer wording, getting-started's portability framing); Mermaid constructs all GitHub-valid; stats consistent; the `git add` payload shell-compared **byte-identical** across the three files; leak surface zero. ## Phase 114 (executed 2026-07-15 — production-side hygiene: resolve the Phase-105 `/test-audit` byproduct notes; both documented keeps)

Closes the Low-priority item filed 2026-07-14 by Phase 105 — the two production-side hygiene notes the first `/test-audit` run surfaced and kept out of that test-only diff so they wouldn't be buried: `migrate_skill_model.py:extract_model_pins` (flagged "dead production code with a stale docstring — decide delete-or-keep") and `run_checks/config.py:filter_checks` (test-only reach — "leave public or mark internal"). Chosen by Wade as one of two parallel worktree concerns this session (the other is the `/test-audit` rubric-calibration run), each done in its own `git worktree` off `origin/main` to stay clear of a concurrent documentation session on `phase-113-readme-restructure` — the two sessions share one `.git` on the case-insensitive filesystem, so a worktree is the isolation primitive.

**Measure twice: both filed premises did not survive inspection.** (1) `extract_model_pins`'s docstring was **already accurate** — the "still claims `check_skill_models.py` uses it" premise was void; that path was rewritten onto `_model_roles.analyze_text` back at Phase 69 and the docstring already reflected it (the fix predates the Phase-105 filing). (2) The "dead code → delete" framing is **contradicted by a deliberate design note**: `_model_roles.py`'s module docstring designates `migrate_skill_model.py` "the home of the bare-alias pin regexes" and states "the migrator's API (and its tests) are untouched" — a Phase-69 decision. So `extract_model_pins` and its bare-alias regexes (`_ALIAS` / `_FRONTMATTER_RE` / `_INLINE_RE` / the `ModelPin` dataclass) are a **retained canonical primitive, not accidental dead code**: deleting them would falsify that note and strip the canonical bare-alias pin-shape. Verified with grep — the only callers are the migrator's own 4 tests plus one comment self-reference; `_model_roles.py` imports only `REPO_ROOT` and `iter_skill_files` from the migrator and deliberately uses its *own* broader value-matching regexes (a resolved value can be a full id / ARN / `inherit`, not just a bare alias), so the migrator's regexes are pointed-at-as-canonical, not imported. Per CLAUDE.md's "if what you find contradicts how it was described, surface it rather than proceeding," the near-deletion was rejected.

**`filter_checks` — legit re-export surface, kept.** Confirmed the in-package run path filters via `cli._classify_checks` (a single pass over both mode and baseline); `filter_checks` is reached only by tests and the `run_checks_impl` back-compat re-export (`from run_checks_impl import filter_checks`). "Mark internal" would mean a rename that breaks that re-export — the exact public-surface break the item's own conservative wording ("leave as-is (public surface)") guards against — so it stays public.

**Resolution — doc-only hardening.** Both docstrings were strengthened so the deliberate retention is self-documenting and neither is re-flagged as dead a third time (Phase 69 kept them; Phase 105 re-flagged them; the retention rationale simply wasn't legible at the symbol). `extract_model_pins` now names itself the canonical bare-alias pin-shape and cross-references `_model_roles.py`'s "home of the regexes" design note with a "do not prune without reconciling that note" caveat; `filter_checks` now states it is retained on the `run_checks_impl` re-export surface with the run path filtering via `cli._classify_checks`. No symbol renamed or deleted → no behavior change, no shipped-public-surface break.

**Gate.** Doc-only → **754 tests green** (unchanged — the count held precisely *because* nothing was deleted; a deletion would have dropped the 4 `extract_model_pins` tests). No installer / manifest / skill / permission / role-guard edit; role guard untouched (no pin or marker changed); leak surface none. A full zero-context fresh-eyes adversarial agent was judged **unwarranted** for a doc-only, behavior-preserving change whose one substantive risk — the deletion — was *rejected* rather than taken (the Phase-109.1 precedent for proportionate self-verification): both new docstrings were self-verified accurate against the real `_model_roles.py` design note and `cli._classify_checks`, imports confirmed intact, suite green (Wade's-own-eyes review ceiling still applies via the PR).

Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 113's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`67a4c24` #101) in the CLAUDE.md phase-log table — the concurrent Phase-113 documentation session merged first (it filled Phase 112's cell), so per the prior-phase-fills convention this phase fills Phase 113's; Phase 114 was rebased onto Phase 113 before landing. Inline close-out; the Low-priority hygiene item ticked and moved to [`REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`](./REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 115 (executed 2026-07-15 — `docs/workflow.html` dark-mode legibility: the Fig. 8 callout band + the masthead toggle clip)

Two dark-mode rendering bugs in the launch monograph — the first artifact the tester onboarding points at — surfaced by Wade from a dark-mode screenshot ("some text isn't showing up well"). Both were real defects, not dim-by-design, and both were **dark-mode-only** (dark is the default theme, so they shipped broken to every default viewer while reading fine in the opt-in light theme — which is why they slipped past authoring).

**Bug 1 — the Fig. 8 "Where the work lives" callout band rendered in invisible black.** The three lines in the bottom band (`From another session…` / `/add-task appends…` / `never edit main by hand…`) carry `class="smallserif"`, but the only rule that fills that class is scoped `.node text.smallserif`, and those `<text>` elements sit at the top level of the `<svg>`, *outside* any `<g class="node">` group. No catch-all `svg text { fill }` rule exists and no ancestor sets an inheritable `fill` (`figure.fig svg` sets only layout properties; body `color` doesn't paint SVG `fill`), so they fell through to SVG's initial `fill: black` — ~1:1 contrast on the near-black `--paper` (#0e0d0a), effectively invisible. The tell that it was an oversight, not intent: every *other* out-of-`node` smallserif in the file (Fig. 1's arc lists) carries an explicit inline `style="…fill:var(--ink)"` for exactly this reason; the Fig. 8 band, added later, was written without it. Fix: gave the three lines an explicit fill — the two framing lines `var(--ink-dim)`, and the caution line (`never edit main by hand — it skips the lock and can hijack a running build's HEAD`) `var(--ink)`, so the actual warning reads as the emphasis it is. Left the inherited size as-is (a prominent band suits the note); only the paint was broken.

**Bug 2 — the "◐ Light" masthead toggle clipped off the right edge at intermediate widths.** `.masthead-inner` was a no-wrap flex row; between ~700px and the 1180px container cap, the nine nav links plus the toggle overflowed past the container's right padding, and because at those widths the viewport ≈ the container, the overflow spilled off the screen edge and clipped the toggle's `◐` glyph. Fix: let the masthead wrap (`flex-wrap: wrap` on `.masthead-inner`, with a tight `gap: 10px 32px` so a wrapped line stays vertically compact) and promoted `margin-left: auto` from the ≤700px media query up into the base `.masthead-toggle` rule (removed there as now-redundant) so the toggle right-aligns as a proper top-right control on whatever line it lands — instead of orphaning at the left of a wrapped line. The nav is genuinely full at the 1180 cap, so at desktop widths the toggle now tucks right-aligned onto a second line under "V · Hooks"; it shares line one only where there's room, and below 700px the nav hides and the toggle sits top-right as before.

**Gate.** HTML/CSS only, no logic surface. Verified in a **real browser** rather than by reasoning about the cascade: Playwright against a local `http.server` (Chromium blocks `file://`), rendered in **both themes** at **1440 / 1120 / 1000 / 560px**. Confirmed the band is legible in dark *and* light with the intended two-tier hierarchy (caution line brighter), and the toggle never clips at any width — one line at desktop with the toggle right-aligned under the nav, a clean wrap at ~1000px, and nav-hidden/toggle-top-right below 700px. Tag balance came back even across every container (svg 9/9, text 155/155, figure 8/8, …). The **759-test suite** (Phase 114's 754 + 5 from the `#103` second `/test-audit` run) is invariant by construction — no test references `docs/workflow.html` (grep-verified) — and CI's required pytest check confirms green on the PR. A full zero-context fresh-eyes agent was judged **unwarranted** (the Phase-109.1 / Phase-114 proportionality precedent): the one meaningful verification for a visual fix is the rendered result across themes and widths, which a text-only reviewer cannot see better than the browser screenshots did, and the human-eyeball ceiling still applies via Wade's PR review. This phase deliberately does **not** bump the monograph's own hero/colophon phase stats — those move only in dedicated currency passes (Phase 109), not on a bugfix.

**Getting it online (Wade's `!` steps).** Merging to private `wade-cms/sysop` `main` does not update getsysop.com — the apex is served from the public `getsysop/sysop` mirror's Pages. Once this PR is squash-merged, refresh the public mirror the usual way (`make_public_mirror.sh` snapshot of the new HEAD → force-push to the protected public `main`, i.e. the delete-protection → force-push → re-apply dance the classifier gates behind the `!` prefix) so the getsysop.com monograph picks up the fix.

Bundled Phase-62-class fix: filled Phase 114's stale `_PR pending_` cell (`0672644` #102) in the CLAUDE.md phase-log table. Inline close-out; no checklist item attached (externally triggered — a design-review catch, like Phase 113). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 116 (executed 2026-07-16 — prune the CLAUDE.md Phase log table to a one-liner index)

**What & why.** The always-loaded `CLAUDE.md` had regrown to **235 KB, 95% of it the `## Phase log` table** — everything above the table (the actual instructions, project shape, conventions, things-not-to-do) was ~12 KB. The cause: from roughly Phase 50 onward each inline close-out wrote the full phase summary into the table row *as well as* into `PHASE_LOG.md`, so the "3-col index" rows averaged ~2 KB (Phases 50–79) → ~3.4 KB (80–99) → ~4.1 KB (100–115), worst single rows ~6 KB (Phases 111, 108, 112), while Phases 1–49 averaged 88 bytes — the intended shape. This is the exact bloat class the repo had already fixed twice elsewhere: Phase 38 extracted phase prose out of `CLAUDE.md` into `PHASE_LOG.md` ("~49% smaller"), and Phase 101 pruned `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`'s duplicate narrative + phase table for the same token-budget reason. But "standard 3-col row" never carried a length discipline, so summaries re-accreted in the description cell. Externally triggered (Wade asked what the bloat was from, then directed the fix as a phase).

**What changed.**
1. **The full-prose table is frozen verbatim in `REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md`** (new § "CLAUDE.md Phase log — original full-prose rows (Phases 1–115, frozen by Phase 116)") — nothing dropped, the Phase 56/101 verbatim-move discipline. Phase 115's `_PR pending_` commit cell was filled (`a91ea1b` #104) during the move, the standard prior-phase fill.
2. **Every summary-length row rewritten as a one-liner** — 74 rows > 300 chars (the whole post-Phase-50 accretion) got a hand-authored title-plus-one-clause description; the Commit and Done cells are byte-identical (script-verified), label order preserved, no remaining row > 320 chars. `CLAUDE.md`: **235 KB → ~33 KB**.
3. **The going-forward convention now carries the cap** (amended in place, § Status): the table row is a one-liner index entry — title + one clause, aim ≤ ~200 characters, never the phase summary — so the class can't silently re-accrete a third time.
4. **Gap found and fixed while verifying zero loss:** rename round 1 (`wade-flow` → `jig`, 2026-06-26, `969a4cc` #9) had **no `PHASE_LOG.md` section** — the only phase-class event whose prose lived solely in the table row (rename round 2 and the public cut both have sections). A `## Rename round 1` section was added (row prose moved verbatim) so this file's "single source of truth" claim actually holds before the row shrank.
5. **Bundled Phase-62-class fixes:** the § Status line still read "**Phases 1 through 38 are done**" — written by Phase 38 and never advanced, 78 phases stale — now current (and notes the repo has been public since 2026-07-13); plus the Phase 115 cell fill above.

**Verification.** The rewrite ran as a script with built-in checks, not hand edits: every original row's label present in the same order; every Commit/Done cell byte-identical (except the deliberate 115 fill); every original row byte-identical inside the new archive section; no long rows remain; the mapping fully consumed (74/74 applied). Zero-loss also cross-checked semantically: every phase 26–115 (bar 27, whose row was already a 92-byte one-liner) has a fuller `PHASE_LOG.md` section than its row (sampled: Phase 111 row 6.0 KB vs section 9.8 KB; Phase 108 5.9 vs 7.7; Phase 112 5.4 vs 10.0), Phases 1–25/27 rows were already one-liners, and the one true gap (rename 1) was closed by (4). Markdown-only — no test parses `CLAUDE.md` (grep-verified; the one hit is a filename string in the miner test) — **759 tests green** (unchanged baseline). **Fresh-eyes zero-context fidelity review (general-purpose agent): SHIP WITH FIXES**, no blockers — it independently re-verified the mechanical integrity (all 148 original rows byte-identical in the archive but for the sanctioned 115 cell fill; label order + Commit/Done cells preserved; the rewritten set exactly the 74 rows > 300 chars; every size/percentage claim in this section recomputed ✓; 759 tests re-run green) and read all 74 one-liners against their frozen originals. Both SHOULD-FIXES applied: the 116 row's own size claim said ~25 KB where the real result is ~33 KB (contradicting this very section), and row 107 credited `/share-wins` with `--body-file` — that flag is `/report-issues`' (`gh issue create`); share-wins' actual RCE-safe mechanism is `gh api graphql -F body=@<file>`. Four NITs applied (rename-1 opening stutter from the prepended label; row 101 "conventions retired" collided with the demotion-pipeline term; row 89 implied Phase 89 shipped the uninstall doc it only *filed* — Phase 90 built it; this section's "every phase 26–115" needed the Phase-27 carve-out). One NIT left knowingly: the frozen archive table inherits HEAD's pre-existing unescaped `\|\|` in the Phase-72 row (mis-renders that one row on GitHub) — byte-identical verbatim preservation wins over rendering in a never-shipped archive file. Inline close-out; no checklist item attached (externally triggered, like Phases 113/115). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

## Phase 117 (executed 2026-07-16 — cold-read gap fixes: doc-currency drift promoted to a check + adopter-facing completeness)

**Provenance — a zero-context cold-read exercise, not a review round.** Wade asked whether a stranger could paste the public links (getsysop.com, `github.com/getsysop/sysop`) into any web-enabled LLM session and get both an accurate summary and an adoption decision. Tested empirically: two zero-context general-purpose agents simulated exactly that — one reading the landing page as a solo Next.js + Postgres builder, one reading the GitHub repo as a Python/FastAPI team dev — with instructions to use no prior knowledge and report what they could and couldn't determine. Both produced accurate first-pass descriptions (the surfaces fetch cleanly: no JS shell, no auth wall, zero dead links) and **converged independently on the same verdict** — "safe to try; can't tell if worth adopting" — and on the same gaps. This phase fixes the four fixable ones.

**Fix 1 — the stat drift, promoted to a deterministic check instead of re-bumped.** `README.md`, `docs/index.html`, and `docs/workflow.html` all said 113 phases with the repo at 116 — the *second* recurrence of this drift class (Phase 109.1 fixed the first). Per the workflow's own promotion semantics (cross-round recurrence → mechanical enforcement), the fix is a check, not another bump: new `tests/test_doc_currency.py` anchors on `PHASE_LOG.md`'s `## Phase N` headings (the canonical public history, present in every distribution — CLAUDE.md's table is not) and enforces a **two-tier policy** decided by Wade via `AskUserQuestion`: README + `docs/index.html` are current-state surfaces and must equal the max phase; `docs/workflow.html` is a dated snapshot ("as of Phase N", refreshed by deliberate currency passes — Phases 86, 109) whose own phase stamps must agree with each other and never run *ahead*, but may lag. Strict-everywhere was rejected because forcing a monograph bump every phase without a content pass would make its "as of" claim quietly false. **The self-referential wrinkle:** appending this very entry makes 117 the max phase, so the same commit sets README and the index tile to 117 — the test now makes phase-close bump the two current-state numbers or fail CI, which is the designed friction (two numbers, one commit, named lines).

**Fix 2 — the reframe half of the same decision.** Both cold readers independently called the raw phase count a non-signal ("measures the author's process, not adoption or stability") when placed in maturity-claim position. README's Status now leads with "In daily use by its first consumers…" and demotes the count to provenance framing ("Development history is public in PHASE_LOG.md — 117 phases so far, one entry each").

**Fix 3 — pack visibility.** "Populated from real projects" was the most load-bearing, least verifiable phrase on both surfaces (both readers ranked it their #1 gap: "a pack could be nearly empty and the wording would read identically"). The Status section now links each populated pack's `convention_map.md` directly — the maps are compact (44–108 lines), already public, and turn the claim into something a prospective adopter can read before installing. No counts in the README (counts would be a new drift surface the currency test would then have to own).

**Fix 4 — hooks day-one behavior + the missing prereq.** The highest-blast-radius unknown both readers flagged ("hooks that reject commits, named but never specified") has a reassuring answer that was written nowhere adopter-visible: both hooks ship as skeletons — every check a commented-out example, blocking nothing until the project populates them, with documented escape hatches (`PRE_COMMIT_ADVISORY_ONLY=1`, `git merge --no-verify`) and pre-merge firing only on the protected branch. New `docs/install-and-update.md § What the git hooks do` states all of it; README's "Reversible by design" bullet gains the one-clause version + link. The README quickstart callout also becomes a real **Prerequisites** line (git, bash 4+, Python 3 + PyYAML) with the one-clause *why* — "Sysop's own check runner and task validator are Python scripts, whatever your project's stack" — closing the README-vs-`getting-started.md` prereq inconsistency and the "why does my Next.js repo need PyYAML?" question one reader hit.

**No-action, deliberately:** (a) the multi-human-semantics gap the FastAPI reader hit is a fetch artifact, not a doc gap — README § "Is this for you?" already states the single-human-reviewer boundary verbatim; that reader received a model-summarized fetch that dropped it; (b) a dollars-per-month cost figure — too variable to state honestly; the token-budget paragraph already sets the expectation. **Filed, not fixed:** the public surfaces stay at 113 until the next mirror push (which requires the full leak-scan dry-run per the runbook) — filed as a Medium checklist item so the refreshed copy actually ships.

**Bundled Phase-62-class fix:** filled Phase 116's `_PR pending_` commit cell (`063a49b` #106) per the prior-phase-fills convention.

**Gate.** All three new tests mutation-verified (author-side: README count 117→999, index tile 117→999, monograph hero 113→999 breaking self-consistency — each kills its test). **762 tests green** (759 + 3). Docs + one test file otherwise — no installer / manifest / skill / permission / role-guard edit; leak surface checked: the shipped test names no private tooling (docstring reworded before commit). Inline close-out; no checklist item resolved (externally triggered, like Phases 113/115/116); one new Medium item filed (mirror push). Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge (Phase 63 `pr` path on protected `main`).

**Update (same day, 2026-07-16 — the filed mirror push executed, Wade-directed).** Full gate run: Pass 1a/1b/3 empty, Pass 2's 40 hits all accepted-class with zero new from 116–117, Pass 2b delta = 1, suite green inside the mirror tree (741). One discovery en route: the public repo's branch protection declines **all** direct pushes to `main` (force and fast-forward alike), so the runbook's force-push refresh model no longer applies to the public slug — the snapshot landed as the public repo's **first PR** (getsysop/sysop#1, pytest green there, squash-merged `e15e794`). The de-facto public refresh model is now **append-snapshot-via-PR**; `make_public_mirror.sh`'s printed publish instructions updated to match, tester-repo force-push flow unaffected. The Medium checklist item this phase filed is ticked and archived with the full record.

## Phase 118 (executed 2026-07-16 — retire the phase count from current-state public surfaces; the currency guard inverts to a ratchet)

**Provenance — the round-2 cold read.** After Phase 117 shipped publicly, Wade re-ran the zero-context cold-read exercise with two Opus agents against the refreshed surfaces (same personas as round 1). Verdicts moved from 2× "genuinely can't tell" to 2× "try it on a branch/side repo first" with the core loop independently called sound by both — and the round-1 gaps confirmed closed (hooks fear gone, prereqs plain, pack contents actually fetched and critiqued on substance). Two residual signals drove this phase: (a) with the count demoted to provenance framing, both readers **stopped using it entirely** — they anchored maturity on the v0.1.0 release date and consumer count instead, so the number informs nobody and only carries drift risk; (b) one reader experienced the README's "117" next to the monograph's "as of Phase 113" as version drift. Wade chose full retirement over single-sourcing via `AskUserQuestion` (true single-sourcing isn't available anyway — GitHub markdown and static Pages HTML have no include mechanism, and a build step to stamp two integers is machinery without a payoff).

**The change.** README's Status drops the number ("Development history is public in `PHASE_LOG.md` — one entry per phase"); the landing page's stat band drops the "Documented phases" tile and goes to `repeat(3, 1fr)` — the three remaining tiles (71 rounds / 3,298 findings / 78 conventions) are now uniformly evidence-corpus stats with one shared provenance, which is a cleaner story than three evidence stats plus one self-referential process stat. The mobile 2-column grid gains a `:last-child { grid-column: 1 / -1 }` rule so three tiles don't strand an empty cell showing the band background. Playwright-verified at 1200px (three even tiles) and 400px (2 + full-width third).

**The guard inverts — demotion, per the loop's own pattern.** `tests/test_doc_currency.py` keeps its name and its monograph leg (the dated "as of Phase N" stamp is different in kind — it dates a document rather than counting progress; still checked self-consistent and never ahead of `PHASE_LOG.md`), but the two current-state legs flip from "count must be current" to "a count must NOT exist" (`\d+ (documented|shipped)? phases`, case-insensitive, README + index.html). Same shape as Phase 116's row-length convention: prune the accretion AND install the thing that stops the third recurrence. All three tests mutation-verified post-inversion (re-adding "117 phases so far" to README, re-adding the tile to index.html, desyncing the monograph hero — each kills its test).

**Gate.** 762 tests green (count unchanged — 3 tests rewritten in place). Docs + one test file + CSS; no installer / manifest / skill / permission edit; leak surface none (no new names). Round-2's other findings (6-phases/4-commands/3-arcs framing spread, portability-wording tension, pack placeholder-expectations) are **not** filed yet — offered to Wade, pending his call. Inline close-out; no checklist item resolved. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge, then the public snapshot appends via the PR route Phase 117 established.

## Phase 119 (executed 2026-07-16 — workflow-framing coherence: the public surfaces state their altitude and share one frame)

**Provenance — the round-2 cold read's framing finding.** The 2026-07-16 zero-context cold-read round (Opus, website persona, post-Phase-117 surfaces) found the three public surfaces describing the lifecycle at three granularities with no stated relationship: the landing page § III shows **six** lifecycle moves, `docs/getting-started.md` walks **four** commands, the monograph's arc is **three** phases — "not contradictory, but confusing on first read." Filed 2026-07-16 (#110) with a **Fable-tier model note** (multi-surface narrative coherence holding the monograph's authored voice); this phase is that item executed, by Fable. Cross-ref precedents: Phase 86 (three-readers Audience pass), Phase 109 (monograph currency).

**The frame, made canonical.** Per the filed recommendation: the monograph's arc — *plan · execute · maintain* — is the top-level mental model; the landing page's six moves nest inside it; the four tutorial commands are the concrete path. The nesting is stated per the monograph's own arc boxes, so it's honest rather than tidy: landing move 1 (Intake) = *plan*; moves 2–4 (adversarial plan review · isolated worktrees · deferred docs) = *execute* — move 2's "Plan" chip is **task-level** planning, which lives inside execution, and the new prose says so ("the task's own plan attacked") rather than forcing a symmetric 2-2-2 split that would contradict Fig. 1; moves 5–6 (dual-mode review · promotion loop) = *maintain*. The four commands = plan (`/intake`) + execute (`/claim-task` → `/document-work` → `/review-close`); the tutorial meets *maintain* only at the end, and now names it there.

**The change — one orienting addition per surface, no rewrite.** (1) **Monograph** (frame owner): a paragraph after the arc lede — "The arc is also the map" — mapping the document's own sections onto the phases (Day one = plan; § I–II = execute; § III–IV = maintain; § V = plumbing) and nesting the other two surfaces explicitly; incidentally the monograph's first link to the tutorial (it had none) and to the landing page.
