Stamp untouched — this is a framing sentence, not a currency pass; no phase-current facts added. (2) **Landing § III**: two sentences appended to the lede — the strip states its altitude ("one pass around that loop") and the three-phase nesting, with the tutorial named as the four-command concrete path. Chips (`Plan/Plan/Build/Record/Review/Learn`) deliberately unchanged. (3) **Tutorial**: one intro sentence ("this walkthrough is the first two phases…") plus a matching clause in *What just happened* so *maintain* lands exactly where the reader first meets `/codebase-review`/`/security-audit`.

**Gate.** 762 tests green (no new tests — prose-only; the Phase-118 no-count ratchet holds because no phase count was introduced anywhere); HTML tag-balance verified on both edited pages. Docs only; no installer / manifest / skill / permission edit; leak surface none. Checklist item (§ Medium, filed 2026-07-16) resolved → archive. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge; the public snapshot follows via the append-via-PR route (Phase 117 model) whenever Wade next refreshes the mirror.

## Phase 120 — `docs/packs.md`: anatomy of a pack rule (round-2 cold read, finding 2 of 3)

**Why.** The round-2 cold read filed three findings; Phase 119 closed the framing one. This closes the pack-expectations one: the reader followed the Phase-117 README pack links (working as designed), found rules written in placeholder vocabulary (`<api module>`, `<auth module>`), and concluded "these aren't concrete rules you get for free — you'd have to map them to your codebase." They also read the python pack as payments/tier-gating-shaped and noted no framework-specific rules exist.

**The filed premise was wrong, and executing it as written would have shipped a false claim.** The checklist entry asserted the reader was merely under-informed — that install-time substitution *already exists* (Phases 24a/25) and the only gap was that no adopter-facing doc shows a pack rule's post-install substituted form. Verification against the code says otherwise. `install.sh:1218-1221` hard-gates substitution to one filename:

```bash
case "$dst" in
  */checks.yml) ;;
  *) return 0 ;;
esac
```

Convention and security maps return early — never substituted, deliberately. The comment at `install.sh:1206-1212` records why: Phase 55 narrowed this *because* byte-substituting the markdown rewrote section headers into junk (`## __disabled_no_op__/*.py — Auth`), and the placeholder tokens are accurate documentation as they stand. So there is no "post-install substituted form" of a convention-map rule to show. **The cold reader was right, not under-informed.** The page was written against the corrected premise; the archived entry records the correction so the wrong page isn't rebuilt from the old text.

**A second, sharper correction — caught mid-draft by verifying my own claim.** The first draft asserted "a pack's rules are live from the moment you install; the mapping happens in the agent's head." That is true for `/security-audit` (`SKILL.md:11` instructs agents to substitute project equivalents while reading) but **false for `/codebase-review`**, which glob-matches section headers to scope which bullets reach a review agent (`SKILL.md:52`, `239-240`). A section still in `<api module>` form matches no tracked file, so it delivers **no rules** until localized — which the skill itself half-acknowledges at Step 2b(a), declining to flag placeholder globs as stale ("an install artifact, not staleness"). The two map consumers behave differently; the page now says so explicitly rather than flattening them into one reassuring sentence.

**The page.** `docs/packs.md`, linked from the README beside the pack links (where the reader actually lands). Its spine is that the concrete "before" the reader wanted **already ships** — `WORKFLOW.md` § 6.2 preserves GDP's original unredacted map (`agent/server.py`, `require_studio_access`, `firebase_uid`, `stripe_customer_id`), and the python pack carries the same section generalized (`<api module>`, `require_<tier>_access`, "auth-provider UID", "payment-provider customer ID"). Shown side by side, the generalization is legible and the placeholder vocabulary stops reading as vagueness and starts reading as the portability mechanism — the same property. The page also notes the shipped form *gained* a clause the original didn't need ("at the route layer; do NOT remove from data-access functions"), because generalizing forces a rule to explain itself. Then: the two-layer split (checks concretized mechanically from `substitutions.project.yml`; maps localized through use), where localization durably lands (the `.project.*` overlay — **not** the regenerated base map), and the honest consequence that an upstream placeholder section and your localized one coexist.

**Provenance (finding b), stated per pack rather than centrally.** The reader was reading the pack file, so the sentence belongs there: one `> **Provenance:**` line in each of the five populated packs naming what it was mined from and how far it travels — python/postgres/nextjs-react/llm from the extraction source (a hosted multi-user subscription web app: FastAPI + Postgres, LLM-backed, third-party auth and payments), beancount from BeanRider. `docs/packs.md` carries the same as a transfer table and states the real limitation plainly: four of five come from one product and share its shape. Nothing invented — the shape is read off content already public in `WORKFLOW.md` § 6.2. Finding (c) (no framework-specific rules) is named as a real gap that closes only the way everything else here does.

**One dead-end instruction fixed.** `packs/python/companion/convention_map.md:7` told adopters glob patterns "should be replaced with your project's actual paths" — pointing at the assembled `.claude/convention_map.md`, a managed path regenerated on every `--update`. Doing as instructed gets silently reverted. Reworded to name the overlay as the durable home; the other four packs never carried the line.

**Riders.** README portability bullet (the wording half of the 2026-06-24 any-agent item, reopened by the same cold read): the two statements — "designed to run under any capable agent" and "probably not for you if you're not in Claude Code (yet)" — read as a contradiction because the logical connective was missing. The bullet now makes the design *the reason* it's a "not yet" rather than a "no", then states the limit ("every real run so far has been Claude Code, so on another agent you would be the first"). Validation leg unchanged and still open — that's the real resolution. Also: `CLAUDE.md`'s Phase 119 row still read `_PR pending_`; corrected to `5f820f3` (#111).

**Parked, not built.** The verification exposed a genuine design gap: `/codebase-review`'s glob-scoped rules are inert on a fresh install until localized, the base map can't durably hold the localization, and the overlay appends rather than supersedes — so the emergent path is "run `/codebase-review` and let its coverage sweep propose overlay sections," which is coherent but slow and leaves permanent dead sections. Three options sketched (localization assist reusing the `substitutions.project.yml` collection point; narrowing the reverted substitution to glob *headers* only; letting `/codebase-review` suppress superseded upstream sections). Filed demand-gated rather than built: no real adopter has been bitten — this came from a cold-read persona plus a code audit, and both live consumers hand-authored their maps. Build on evidence, not inference.

**Gate.** 762 tests green (docs + pack-header prose only; no new tests — no runtime surface). The Phase-118 no-count ratchet holds (no phase count introduced; `docs/packs.md` carries none). No installer / manifest / skill / permission edit.

**Update (same day, 2026-07-16 — mirror push executed, Wade-directed; covers Phases 119 + 120).** The public mirror was two phases stale (public `4aa49db` = private `d769247` = Phase 118) while both unmirrored phases had edited *public* surfaces — so getsysop.com was serving pre-119 content and the work was invisible to readers. Full gate run on private `72591f9`: Pass 1a/1b/3 empty, exclusions confirmed absent (`tools/`, the miner, the covered-class artifact), suite green inside the mirror tree (741, matching Phase 117's baseline). **Pass 2 = 43 sites (+3 vs published), Pass 2b = 144 (+3 vs published, all accepted-class BeanRider provenance.)** The +3 on Pass 2 is exactly what the leak-surface note below predicted: the two deliberate `docs/packs.md` / PHASE_LOG sites, plus PHASE_LOG's record of the decision itself. Landed as `getsysop/sysop#3` (pytest green there, squash-merged **`3e70d15`**) via the Phase-117 append-via-PR model.

**The maintainer's-eye call below was given the eye, and ratified.** The note asks whoever runs the cut to adjudicate an attributed quote of the § 6.2 worked example against `CLAUDE.md`'s "no gdp-specific identifiers in newly-authored content." The premise was checked empirically rather than reasoned about: `## `agent/server.py`, `agent/routes/*.py` — API Endpoints` **already ships publicly** at `core/companion/docs/WORKFLOW.md:953` in the live public repo, so `docs/packs.md` quotes content that is already public and introduces no identifier that is not. In-policy under Option A; shipped as-is (Wade's call, `AskUserQuestion`). The reversal path in that note stays valid if the § 6.2 exception is ever narrowed.

**Method fix to the gate itself (the drift trap this cut nearly walked into).** Pass 2b's comment named a frozen absolute baseline — "~125 sites at ratification (private `9e7bd52`)" — but accepted-class provenance grows with every phase that writes BeanRider-mentioning prose, so published had already drifted to 141. Read against the frozen number this cut looked like a **+19 swing**; read against the *published snapshot* it is **+3**. The absolute baseline was a false-alarm generator with a shelf life, so `tools/make_public_mirror.sh`'s Pass 2/2b comments now name the diff-against-published method (clone the public repo, `comm` the hit lists) — self-updating, and it isolates exactly what the unmirrored phases introduced instead of re-litigating the whole accepted set. This is the `project_mirror_leak_scan_drift` class turned on the gate rather than the content.

**Fully live — but the Pages build took three tries, and the failure was transient, not content.** Final state: **both HTML surfaces verified byte-identical to local** (`diff` against a live `curl`, not a substring grep), both HTTP 200; everything markdown-shaped went live on GitHub immediately (README, `docs/packs.md`, `docs/getting-started.md`, the five convention maps). Build tally, all on `3e70d15`: **`errored` 22:35 → `errored` 22:50 → `built` 02:07**. Both failures fell inside a window where GitHub's Actions API was returning `HTTP 503` behind an "All Systems Operational" status page; the first retry *after* that window closed succeeded with no content change. Note `docs/packs.md` is a *relative markdown link from the README*, not a Pages page — it needs no build, and a `getsysop.com/packs.html` 404 is correct, not a defect.

**The gotcha worth keeping: `pages/builds/latest` lied.** It reported `building — err: none` for ~25 minutes while the **history list** (`gh api repos/getsysop/sysop/pages/builds`) showed the build had **errored** ("Page build failed.", the legacy builder's only message). Diagnosing off `latest` alone reads "slow queue" when the truth is "failed build" — this session recorded exactly that wrong diagnosis here on the strength of `latest`, and had to correct it in a follow-up commit (`673e4bc`). **Always read `pages/builds`, not `pages/builds/latest`.** Retry with `gh api -X POST repos/getsysop/sysop/pages/builds`.

**And the second lesson: two consecutive same-commit failures did *not* mean a content bug.** The honest mid-session prior was damning — 2-for-2 errors on `3e70d15` while `4aa49db` and `e15e794` had built fine, which points straight at the 119+120 delta. What actually held was the degradation-window overlap plus a recovered identical failure on 2026-07-14 (`75b2dc2`). **Ruled out along the way, so nobody re-runs it:** Liquid syntax in Phase 120's *new* markdown breaking Jekyll (`grep -rn '{{\|{%' docs/` clean across every `.md` and `.html`), and front-matter shape (no `docs/*.md` carries front matter — `packs.md` is structurally identical to the pre-existing `configuration.md`/`install-and-update.md`, and Jekyll copies front-matter-less files as static rather than rendering them). Pages config: `main//docs`, legacy build type, no `_config.yml`, no `.nojekyll`. **The rule for next time: retry once the Actions API is healthy before hunting content; only a fresh error against a green API is evidence of a real bug.** Verify live with `curl -s https://getsysop.com/ | grep -c "six moves below are one pass"` (expects 1; the page has five `class="lede"` elements and Phase 119 edited the third, so grep the sentence, not the class).

**Leak surface — read this before the next mirror cut.** Passes 1a + 1b clean (verified against the changed set). **This phase adds two new Pass-2 sites, deliberately:** `docs/packs.md`'s "How a rule is born" block quotes the § 6.2 worked example verbatim (`agent/server.py`, `require_studio_access`, `firebase_uid`, `stripe_customer_id`), and the Phase-120 entry above restates it. Pass 2 marks this class "EXPECTED under Option A — eyeball each as intended provenance/worked-example, not a new leak," and both sites are attributed quotes of content `WORKFLOW.md` § 6.2 already ships — so they are in-policy, but they are **new sites on the eyeball list**, not a no-op. The per-pack provenance sentences carry no identifiers (they describe the source project's *shape* only). Note the tension worth a maintainer's eye: `CLAUDE.md` § Conventions says "no gdp-specific identifiers in newly-authored content" and names `agent/server.py` explicitly, while the § 6.2 worked example is a ratified exception (2I.2 + Option A, 2026-06-22); Phase 120 read an attributed quote of that exception as falling inside it. If that call is ever reversed, the fix is to paraphrase the block's paths — the page's argument (concrete → generalized) survives paraphrase, though it loses the "this is real, not invented" force that made it worth writing.

Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge.

## Phase 121 (executed 2026-07-16 — the outbound Ideas surface: the demand gate becomes reachable by the people it gates on)

**Why now — the blocker discharged itself.** The item (§ Medium, filed 2026-07-10, ratified 2026-07-11 as the outbound half of the frozen-repo-as-notebook disposition) was explicitly **sequenced behind enabling Discussions** — "can't seed before the channel exists." Discussions is now live on `getsysop/sysop`, the default **Ideas** category already exists, and it was **empty**. So the one stated blocker was gone and the phase was purely the curation it always was. The structural argument for doing it *now* rather than after: roughly a dozen parking-lot entries set their REVISIT TRIGGER as "external tester/OSS demand counts (watch Discussions + `/report-issues`)", while `make_public_mirror.sh:61` `rm -f`s `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md` — so the parking lot never ships and a visitor can file a *new* idea but cannot see or upvote an *existing parked one*. The demand gate was **structurally unreachable by the people it gates on**. Timing also argued for pre-announce: announce is the remaining launch step, and announce is what brings the audience whose votes these triggers key on — seeding afterward wastes the one wave of attention.

**The curation rule (the actual work, and the reusable part).** Seed only entries whose disposition is **parked pending demand**; never an entry whose disposition is **ratified out-of-scope**. Seeding something already decided against doesn't *measure* demand — it *manufactures* the signal it claims to read, and publicly contradicts a settled boundary. Two entries fell to this rule: the **`/intake` discovery front-end** (2026-07-12 — ratified out-of-scope at `/intake` Step 4 boundary 1; its own trigger is *repeated independent* demand arriving organically, which seeding would fabricate) and the **standing model-reviewer** (2026-07-09 — half ratified against, and named competitively sensitive in the queue). The discovery boundary is instead **stated plainly in the pinned post** as a decision that is not up for a vote, with an invitation to argue it in a *new* Idea — which preserves the organic-arrival trigger intact rather than pre-empting it. Also excluded: `--surfaced-by` (deep-internal; its own adversarial review found the framing oversold), the telemetry/K-ramp/`touches:`/nesting/test-audit-calibration cluster (internal measurement, GDP-shaped, not user-legible), distribution/subscription + provenance + rename (business/internal), and campaign/wave orchestration (explicitly downstream of fast-path merge — seeding it invites votes on the wrong link in the chain).

**Trimmed to six, deliberately.** The draft carried ten. Wade trimmed it: an empty category dilutes votes across a long list, and the held four (pack-rule localization, per-turn convention checks, economy preset, stable plugin channel) lose nothing by waiting for an audience — the parking lot still holds them. The shipped six, each stating what it is, **why it isn't built**, and what a 👍 would signal: **#5** guided mode (trigger *is* tester demand), **#6** unattended build-leg mode, **#7** fast-path merge (the good half of the excluded model-reviewer entry — it carries the anti-rubber-stamp reasoning explicitly, so the seeded version can't be misread as the rejected one), **#8** populate-a-pack (purely demand-gated; doubles as the contribution flywheel's request line), **#9** durable customization overlay (one seed measuring **two** parked entries — tuning knobs + skill-body overlay — which the queue says should be built as one shared shape if they fire together), **#10** external-tracker import (its calibration explicitly wants "which trackers real adopters arrive with"; a vote answers it directly). Pinned framing post: **#4**, carrying the "signal, not commitment" reconciliation with the README's no-roadmap stance and stating that planning is maintained privately and this list is a curated projection of it. Every body rewritten to the leak-scan bar to stand alone for a reader who has never seen the private queue — no GDP, no BeanRider, no Caliper, no tester names, no telemetry numbers, no `tools/*` paths.

**Honest framing carried into the copy, not just the policy.** Each seed states its real reason for not existing, including the unflattering ones: #7 names the survivorship confound in "we've never had a bad merge" as the reason the predicate must come from data; #6 concedes it buys *attention*, not pipeline speed, because the review sitting is the real ceiling; #9 admits the appendix mechanism is unbuilt because "your text wins" and "our text wins" are both wrong answers to a contradicted safety gate. This is the same discipline as Phase 98's limits block — a parked idea's honest "why not" is what makes the vote informative rather than a wish poll.

**A premise I got wrong, mid-phase, one step after invoking the lesson.** I flagged `packs/mcp-server`'s manifest as the lone placeholder pack missing the `(placeholder — populates from real-project use)` marker, and Wade approved folding in the fix. **The marker was there** — my check truncated descriptions at 70 chars and cut it off. Reported as a correction rather than quietly substituted. What the full read *did* surface is smaller and real: the description named **BeanRider** in marketplace-picker copy ("populates from real-project use, starting with BeanRider's MCP server") — in-policy per Decision 2 (2026-06-22 accepts BeanRider references in shipped content) but meaningless to a reader who has never heard of it, and no sibling pack does it. Trimmed that clause only. **The lesson is Phase 120's, re-learned from the other side:** Phase 120 caught a false *filed* premise; this caught a false premise **I authored myself, from a truncated read**, while writing the phase that cites it. A `[:70]` slice is not a verification.

**The CONTRIBUTING follow-through** the 2026-07-11 ratification owed: § Questions dropped the now-stale `(if enabled)` hedge on Discussions (it's enabled) and gained the one-liner — planning is maintained privately, no public backlog, the Ideas category is where parked things live with honest why-nots, 👍 is prioritization signal not a promise, and a real use case beats a vote.

**Gate.** 762 tests green (no new tests — Discussions content + docs; no installer/skill/permission surface touched). Manifest JSON re-parsed. Two shipped-content edits (`CONTRIBUTING.md`, `packs/mcp-server/.claude-plugin/plugin.json`) need the mirror; the Discussions posts are live already and are not mirror content. **Pinning #4 is click-ops** — GitHub's public GraphQL API has no discussion-pin mutation (`pinIssue`/`unpinIssue` only; introspected, not guessed), so the pin is a one-click manual step. Checklist item (§ Medium, filed 2026-07-10) resolved → archive. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge.

**Addendum (same day, Wade-directed — the README's own claim had drifted).** Pre-mirror check found the README's `- **A feedback loop you control**` bullet describing only the *inbound* half (`SYSOP_ISSUES.md` + `/report-issues` + `/share-wins`) — as of this phase that's two-thirds of the loop it names, and the outbound leg appeared nowhere in the README (nor on the landing page, which has no Discussions link at all). Same shape as Phase 120's portability fix: not false, just narrower than its own claim. Resolved as **one clause on the existing bullet**, deliberately not a new bullet and not a landing-page change — the README was pruned to a ~100-line landing surface by Phase 113, and its § Support expectations "no roadmap commitment" (`:81`) is load-bearing, so the clause is worded to *agree* with it ("👍 is prioritization signal, not a promise") rather than re-litigate the framing in a surface with no room for the caveat. The landing page stays untouched on purpose: its job is conversion, and the Discussions tab is one click from every link it already carries. **Verified in the same pass, because it would have bitten a tester before it bit us:** `/share-wins` resolves its standing-thread category at runtime, preferring `Show and tell` and falling back to `General` — both exist on `getsysop/sysop`, so a first `/share-wins` works against the live repo (the skill stops with a clear ask if neither exists; it doesn't need a "Wins" *category*). Global pin on #4 confirmed via `pinnedDiscussions`; the category pin is unverifiable by API (GitHub exposes no pinned field on `Discussion` and no pin mutation at all — eleven discussion mutations, none of them pin), so it rests on the maintainer's word. Bundled: the Phase-121 row's `_hash pending_` cell filled (`14af39f`).

**Update (same day, 2026-07-16 — mirror push executed; public `3e70d15` → `3e505ec`, private `bbc399b`).** Full gate on the exact pushed tree: **Pass 1a / 1b / 3 empty**, exclusions confirmed absent (`tools/`, the miner, the covered-class artifact), suite green **inside the mirror tree (741** — matching the established baseline exactly; the private 762 minus the excluded miner tests). **Pass 2 = 44 (+1 vs published), Pass 2b = 147 (+3 net vs published)** — every new site is `PHASE_LOG.md` changelog prose in an already-ratified class (the Pass-2 addition is Phase 120's own record of the ratified maintainer's-eye call, which quotes `agent/server.py` — already public at `WORKFLOW.md:953`; the Pass-2b additions are this phase's entries plus Phase 120's mirror record naming BeanRider as provenance, accepted tree-wide under Decision 2b). **No new leak class, no new file class.** Pass 2b's four *new lines* net to **+3** because `673e4bc` rewrote a line rather than adding one — a reminder that the line-diff and the count answer different questions, and the diff is the gate. Reader-visible delta is three files (README bullet clause, CONTRIBUTING § Questions, the mcp-server manifest); everything else is changelog prose. Landed as `getsysop/sysop#11` (pytest green there, squash-merged **`3e505ec`**) via the Phase-117 append-via-PR model. **Pages: `built` on the first attempt** — no Pages-served surface changed (`docs/index.html` / `docs/workflow.html` untouched), so the build was a no-op re-render; verified via the *builds history* per Phase 120's lesson (`builds/latest` lies), plus a live `curl` confirming getsysop.com still 200s and still serves the Phase-119 framing sentence. That clean first build is also mild corroboration of Phase 120's transient diagnosis: same repo, same builder, no content change, no failure.

## Phase 122 (executed 2026-07-17 — the provenance-verifiability close: one rule traced end to end, the snapshot policy stated as policy, and the round-3 copy bundle)

**Trigger.** The two Fable-tagged Medium items from the round-3 cold read (filed 2026-07-17, verbatim reports in `tools/COLD_READ_ROUND3_FABLE.md`), executed in one Fable session per each item's model note: (1) the provenance-verifiability gap — both readers independently called the "history is the evidence" footer a slogan against a five-squash-commit public history, and both proposed the same fix (one auditable walkthrough + a visible snapshot-cadence note, neither requiring private history to be published); (2) the landing + README copy bundle (History link target, May-endpoint framing, "self-improving" oversell, plugin-vs-bash two-step).

**The archaeology, and the pivot it forced.** Exemplar selection ran against Phase 112's covered-class metrics rather than narrative instinct — and the obvious candidate lost. The SQL f-string class has the richest recurrence history in the archive (TASK-122 through TASK-1454, a dozen-plus findings across months) but shows **6 post-gate recurrences** (join-built SQL and other shape variants the AST pattern doesn't match); building the flagship walkthrough on it would have re-committed exactly the endpoint-cherry-picking sin the copy bundle's item (b) exists to fix. The chosen exemplar is **Outbound HTTP security → `http-client-redirect`** (ships in the python pack): Round 28 (OWASP, 2026-03-16) found five call sites of unguarded `httpx.Client()`/`AsyncClient()` constructors in one sitting (TASK-883/884); the prose prevention convention was promoted the same day (private `b5d615a7`); **Rounds 29–30 hand-found four more findings the very next day** (TASK-897/898/899/982 — the walkthrough's "prose doesn't hold" beat); mechanized as a grep check in the new shared registry 2026-03-20 (`8f29037f`); ported to a Semgrep AST rule 2026-04-20 (`53764e3f`) after a single round's pre-scan emitted ~43 false positives across six text-local greps — the rule-maintenance beat; and the class then shows **7 findings before mechanization, 0 after** across the rest of the archive (covered-class row), with the by-construction caveat carried from `docs/analysis/REPORT.md` rather than hidden.

**The fire-evidence sweep, and the honest gap it set in the artifact.** A dedicated read-only sweep of the gdp record (commits, changelog, task archive, baselines, suppressions) established what a "no model in the loop" fire actually looks like there — and what the record does *not* contain: **no instance of a custom rule catching post-gate-authored code in CI** (the source project runs the custom rules edit-time + review-prescan; they are `blocking: false` in CI). What is on record, dated: the 2026-04-22 edit-time scan **blocking every edit** to a module until an incomplete suppression was fixed (an incident that itself got promoted into a new deterministic check, `nosemgrep-sqlalchemy-pair`); registry secret-scan rules firing on newly-written JWT-shaped test fixtures (2026-05-13, adjudicated as documented suppressions); and the `json-loads-broad-except` lifecycle (2026-05-18/19: six first-scan fires → one real fix + five FPs → rule V2 with five `pattern-not` blocks and a negative fixture → baseline emptied). The walkthrough states the gap in its own § 5 instead of papering over it — the candor register is the point of the document — and closes with the leg no historical record can supply: **a reader-runnable check** (`semgrep --config packs/python/companion/semgrep/http_client_redirect.yaml` against the shipped fixtures — verified live this session: three findings on the positive fixture, silence on the negative), plus the coda that `recompile-inside-def` caught the checks runner's own memoization helper, whose reasoned `nosemgrep` suppression ships publicly at `core/companion/scripts/run_checks/grep.py:120`.

**What shipped.** (1) **`docs/one-rule.md`** — the walkthrough, six sections + a "what this page doesn't prove" close; private anchors carry dates and hashes and are labeled non-verifiable, everything in the last two sections is checkable in the shipped tree. (2) **`docs/history.md`** — the ~15-line outsider-legible timeline (copy item a), now the landing History tile's target (PHASE_LOG demoted to the "unabridged log" link inside it). (3) **README § Provenance** gains the snapshot-cadence paragraph (item 1b): squash snapshots as policy, the `sysop public snapshot (private <hash>)` naming contract, the leak-scan discipline as what the granularity is traded for, and pointers to PHASE_LOG + the walkthrough. (4) **The footer line has a referent now** (item 1c): "provenance is the evidence, not a slogan" → the squash-mirror policy named inline + a link to the walkthrough. (5) Copy item (b): the § II lede's "one language-server sweep aside, held there" pre-excuse rewritten to name the May spike as data ("fell, then held low, spike included; the full table is below"), and the SVG `figdesc` un-glossed to match. (6) Copy item (c): "self-improving" qualified once, up front, in all three first-contact surfaces — hero lede clause ("you ratify every rule it promotes — nothing learns autonomously"), meta description, README lede. (7) Copy item (d): the plugin-vs-bash pair stated plainly at both top-of-doc sites (README install paragraph + `install-and-update.md`'s plugin bullet, which now cross-anchors its own § Plugin path detail). Cross-links: README Documentation list (history + one-rule rows), `docs/packs.md` § provenance → one-rule.

**Verification.** Full suite green (762, incl. the Phase-117 doc-currency guard); leak-scan pre-check clean on every new/edited file (no strip-class identifiers — the one internal constant name in a quoted exploit scenario was paraphrased to "a revalidation secret as a Bearer token"); the walkthrough's reproducible command executed against the shipped rule + fixtures before being printed in the doc.

**Checklist.** Both Fable-tagged Medium items → `REVIEW_ARCHIVE.md § Resolved — Phase 122`. The announce sequencing note inside item 1 (Show HN etc.) remains user-owned click-ops and was not absorbed into this phase.

**Update (same day, 2026-07-17 — mirror push executed; public `3e505ec` → `27b3f2c`, private `2f2c6ff`).** Full gate on the exact pushed tree: **Pass 1a / 1b / 3 empty**, suite green **inside the mirror tree (741** — matching the established baseline; private 762 minus the excluded miner tests). **Pass 2 = 47 (+3 vs published), Pass 2b = 148 (+1)** — the Pass-2 additions are the two new docs pages naming GDP Query System as intended Option-A provenance (`docs/one-rule.md`, `docs/history.md`) plus Phase 121's own mirror-record paragraph (changelog prose, ratified class); the footer and README lines in the diff are rewrites of already-matching lines, not new sites; the Pass-2b +1 is the same Phase-121 paragraph (accepted tree-wide under Decision 2b). **No new leak class, no new file class.** Landed as `getsysop/sysop#12` (pytest green there, squash-merged **`27b3f2c`**) via the Phase-117 append-via-PR model. **Pages: `built` on the first attempt** — and unlike the Phase-121 no-op re-render, this one carried real Pages-served changes (`docs/index.html`); verified via the builds history (per Phase 120's lesson) *and* two live-content probes: getsysop.com now serves the § II honest-arc lede ("spike included") and the new footer ("one rule traced end to end"). Reader-visible delta: the two new docs pages, the README provenance/lede/install edits, the landing lede/figdesc/hero/meta/footer/History-tile edits, the install-and-update plugin bullet, the packs.md cross-link.

## Phase 123 (executed 2026-07-17 — loop-only install mode: `--mode loop`, the graduated on-ramp — legs 1–4 of 5)

**Trigger.** The round-3 cold read's #1 item (filed 2026-07-17, Medium; `tools/COLD_READ_ROUND3_FABLE.md` + `tools/LOOP_ONLY_SPEC.md`): two independent zero-context readers both verdicted "maybe-later," both named adoption weight as the bounce ("I want the rules compiler, not a new religion" / "I'm being handed a whole operating system"), and both named a loop-only mode — install the convention loop *without* the lifecycle — as the single change that tips them to yes. The sequencing argument is that announce is the one shot at the funnel, so the on-ramp ships before it. The spec's task-coupling audit had already established this is a **carving, not a build**: the promotion/demotion machinery lives entirely in the standing audit skills + `review_tasks.md`, not the merge gate, and the installer decomposes along exactly the needed seam.

**Leg 1 — the decision-free build-time audit (resolved every unknown the spec flagged, and corrected one spec error).** The `_shared/` closure is **four** partials, not the three the spec's "known" list carried — it had omitted `adversarial-review.md`, which both `codebase-review` and `security-audit` reference; the transitive walk is otherwise clean, and `guided-mode.md` (CLAUDE.md-activated, not skill-referenced) stays out. The two ambiguous scripts: `review_index.py` **ships** (a hard `from review_index import rebuild_index` in the bundled `archive_review_tasks.py`, and it parses the loop's own `review_tasks.md` ledger), `permission_denied_hook.py` **drops** (its sole trigger is the `/review-close` protected-branch classifier-override, which loop mode excludes). The permission subset came out to **14 allow-rules** from the master 55, and — the finding that surprised the audit — **both hooks drop**: `SubagentStop`'s `parse_subagent_envelope.py` only parses the `TASK_ID`-keyed `/claim-task`+`/auto-build` envelopes, and the audit skills' adversarial pass returns findings inline (confirmed against `adversarial-review.md:76-78`), so loop-mode `settings.json` is permissions-only. A scratch-repo run confirmed `review_index.py` + `archive_review_tasks.py` execute green with no `tasks/` directory present.

**Leg 2 — the installer (`--mode loop|full`, +286 lines across 12 sites in `install.sh`).** Deny-list filters (`LOOP_EXCLUDE_SKILLS`/`_SHARED`/`_SCRIPTS`) drive `install_skills`/`install_companion_scripts`; `install_permissions` feeds a filtered temp template (14-rule allow-subset, no hooks block) through the existing copy/merge paths unchanged; `run_install_pipeline` skips `install_workflow_docs` + `install_tasks_scaffold`; the lock records `mode`; and the mode/update state machine gives loop→full an additive upgrade (`--update --mode full`) with full→loop rejected (reinstall fresh). A fresh `--mode loop` install produces the intended shape, verified end-to-end: root footprint is `.claude/`, `scripts/`, `.gitignore`, `CLAUDE.md` only — no `WORKFLOW.md`/`WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md`/`SYSOP_ISSUES.md`/`tasks/`; 5 skills + `_shared` (4 partials); 11 loop scripts + `run_checks/`; 14-rule hookless `settings.json`; lock `mode: loop`. **Name resolved → `loop`** (over `lite`: names the crown-jewel mechanism rather than a shortfall, avoids the freemium/second-class connotation that clashes with MIT/free + loop-only being a complete product, and matches the existing `review_tasks.md`/"the loop" vocabulary; `lite`'s one edge — instant "this is small" — is carried by the picker *description* instead of the token).

**Two adopter-facing decisions, put to Wade and resolved.** (1) The audit skills read three `<project>/CLAUDE.md` scope sections that no lifecycle bootstrap writes in loop mode; the installer **seeds them section-level append-if-absent** (create the file with all three if absent; append only the missing sections to an existing file, never rewriting authored content — the `ensure_runtime_gitignore` contract) rather than the more-conservative note-only, because the loop audience is by definition an existing repo. (2) `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` **stays lazy** in loop mode (created on first friction capture, not at install), which the footprint gripe named directly and which `/report-issues` already tolerates.

**Leg 3 — the drift-guard test (`tests/test_install_loop_mode.py`, 22 tests).** Two layers: a static classification guard (every source skill / `_shared` partial / companion script must be bucketed loop-or-lifecycle, and the buckets must equal `install.sh`'s `LOOP_EXCLUDE_*` lists — so a new upstream lifecycle file that nobody classified fails the suite loudly rather than leaking into the "smallest install") and an end-to-end layer (exact bundle, 14-rule hookless settings, clean footprint, lock mode, the full mode/update state machine, and the CLAUDE.md append-if-absent behavior against an authored file). The dangling-ref check is scoped to *invocations*, not prose mentions — which surfaced that `adversarial-review.md` ships inert lifecycle prose in loop mode (a shared partial's sections about the reviewer-executor / `/auto-build` / the SubagentStop hook); parked ship-as-is v1 in the spec's open questions, analogous to `ensure_runtime_gitignore`'s dead lifecycle entries.

**Leg 4 — docs.** `docs/install-and-update.md` gained an authoritative § "Install modes: full and loop"; README § "Is this for you?" gained a "Want less than all of it?" door at the decision point plus a Quickstart `--mode loop` variant clause; `docs/index.html` § Start gained a "smallest install" line. `getting-started.md` stays full-mode by design.

**Gate.** 791 tests green (762 prior + 29 loop-mode tests; no full-mode regression — the 80 existing install tests pass unchanged, and a manual full install is byte-unchanged). Doc-currency guard green.

**Adversarial review (Wade-requested, pre-merge — the discipline the build had skipped).** Three independent fresh-context reviewers (not forks) attacked the built legs 1–4 along distinct lenses: install.sh correctness, test rigor, docs/integration accuracy. **No HIGH-severity breakage** — they confirmed the deny-list filtering, the `LOOP_SETTINGS_TMP` lifetime/cleanup, the full mode/update state machine, `run_checks` self-sufficiency, exact settings, and anchor links all work — but they found real defects the green PR was hiding, all fixed on-branch (full record in `tools/LOOP_ONLY_SPEC.md` § "Adversarial review"). The two that mattered most were **test-coverage holes, not code bugs**: the 14-rule allow-list was asserted by *count only* (a reviewer mutated install.sh to swap a dropped `gh release create` in for a loop rule — count stayed 14, suite stayed green), and the enforcement payload (checks.yml/maps/semgrep) was never asserted *present* (only lifecycle-absence was). Both closed with exact-set assertions + an install.sh `LOOP_ALLOW` cross-check + payload-presence checks, and the allow-set guard was **mutation-verified to bite**. Code fixes: the settings fallback was **fail-open** (a filter error shipped the full 55-rule master + hooks pointing at unshipped scripts) → made fail-closed; loop mode wrote a `.gitignore` of four lifecycle-dead entries → `ensure_runtime_gitignore` skipped in loop mode (the footprint claim "just `.claude/`, `scripts/`, `CLAUDE.md`" is now literally true, superseding leg-2 finding #6); a dangling `WORKFLOW.md` in the install summary → mode-gated; lock-`mode` corruption now normalizes to full; the dry-run no longer creates a temp; the companion-scripts subdir branch is mode-filtered. Docs: `review_tasks.md` reworded as lazy (bootstrapped on first audit, not installed), hook-arming reworded (auto-armed). The lesson is the repo's own: a green suite is not a reviewed one — the count-only assertion would have shipped a permission regression, and only an adversary looking to *break* it found the crack.

**Leg 5 — dogfood — deferred as a tracked before-announce validation** (Wade's call: PR legs 1–4 now, dogfood as follow-up). The scratch tests exercise the *installer*; nobody has yet run the actual audit skills in a loop-mode install end-to-end (install → fill the CLAUDE.md scope sections → run a round → promote a convention → confirm a compiled check fires), which is where UX bugs the tests can't see would surface. Non-blocking for the code landing; the checklist item stays open on this leg. Landing via branch → PR → squash-merge to protected `main`.

**Update (2026-07-17 — merged + tester-mirror dry-run).** Legs 1–4 squash-merged to dev `main` as **`4886f62` (#122)** after the adversarial-review fixes (CI green). Loop mode is on the **dev repo only** — the tester mirror (`wade-cms/sysop-tester`) sits at Phase 115 (`a91ea1b`, no loop mode) and the public repo (`getsysop/sysop`) at Phase 122 (`27b3f2c`), so neither exposes `--mode loop` yet. A **tester-mirror dry-run + full leak-scan ran clean** on the `4886f62` snapshot (`tools/make_public_mirror.sh`): Pass 1a/1b/3 empty, Pass 2 = one accepted GDP-provenance changelog line (Phase-122 mirror-record prose, Option-A class), Pass 2b = 0; loop content confirmed in the snapshot (4 `--mode loop` refs + the test), internal files (`tools/`, `CLAUDE.md`, `REVIEW_CHECKLIST.md`) excluded. **Snapshot is ready to push but deliberately held** pending Wade's go — the tester refresh is a force-push to `wade-cms/sysop-tester` (each build is a new root commit; testers re-clone). **Remaining open:** leg-5 dogfood (a tester's loop-mode run would be the natural vehicle) + the tester/public mirror pushes whenever Wade next refreshes them.

## Phase 124 (executed 2026-07-17 — TECH-0007 sysop-side High fixes: BeanRider ISSUE-0048/0049/0050, the three lifecycle-flow blockers surfaced by BeanRider's sysop migration)

**Trigger.** BeanRider's TECH-0007 migration (its jig→sysop adoption) exercised the documented `/claim-task` → `/document-work` → `/review-close` cycle end-to-end and hit five upstream defects, filed to `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` as ISSUE-0046..0050. A builder-session triage confirmed all five present in this repo's source and untracked; 0044/0045 (2026-05-27) were already resolved upstream (Phases 50/68) and correctly skipped. This phase lands the **three High** (0048/0049/0050) — each a flow-breaking or silent-safety defect on the primary worktree path; the two Medium (0047 installer force-degradation, 0046 pip-audit `--strict` dead stage) and a discovered sibling class (B#3) stay filed.

**ISSUE-0048 — `git push` blocked from every worktree; the fix must land in three copies.** `_resolve_canonical_locks_dir`'s `git -C <root> rev-parse --git-common-dir` probe (Phase 32) inherited git's ambient `GIT_DIR`/`GIT_WORK_TREE`, which outrank `-C` and are exported into every hook — so `validate_tasks.py --self-test`'s tmpdir fixtures resolved to the *invoking* repo's `.locks/`, failing Invariant 9 inside the pre-push pytest gate. Reproduces only from a worktree (git sets `GIT_DIR` relative on `main`, absolute in a worktree), so it was invisible on `main`. Fix: a `_git_discovery_env()` helper (os.environ minus `GIT_DIR`/`GIT_WORK_TREE`/`GIT_COMMON_DIR`/`GIT_INDEX_FILE`) passed as `env=` to the probe — added to **all three** deliberate zero-dependency duplicates (`validate_tasks.py`, `next_task.py`, `scope_overlap.py`; BR's own fix reached only the first, and the duplication is itself the root cause). The env-strip restores the documented tmpdir fallback without changing the answer for real callers; Phase-32's cross-worktree guarantee is preserved. New `tests/test_git_env_hermeticity.py` parametrizes the guard over all three modules (unit: env-strip + fallback-under-ambient-`GIT_DIR`; e2e: the `--self-test` guard lifted from BR) — red against pre-fix, green after.

**ISSUE-0049 — `/review-close` heredocs died on `import yaml` for venv-only consumers.** Step 4c's `tasks/index.yml` status-flip heredoc ran a bare `python3` (no PyYAML on e.g. macOS system python 3.9.6), one line above a `.venv/bin/python3` validator call — internally inconsistent. Step 3c's smoke-gate heredoc carried the same latent shape. Both fixed with a conditional `PATH=.venv/bin:$PATH` prefix that keeps the command word a **literal `python3`**, so the existing `Bash(python3 -:*)` allow-rule still matches. (The issue — and my first attempt — used a `$PY_BIN="$(… )"` variable; the adversarial review below showed a variable command word binds to *no* static allow-rule and routes to the auto-mode classifier, and the `.venv/bin/python3 -:*` rule it would need was never in the shipped template. Reverting to the literal-`python3` idiom the rest of the skills already use resolves both.)

**ISSUE-0050 — the manual-smoke gate silently no-op'd on the worktree flow.** Step 3c scanned only main's `.pending-docs/`, but `/claim-task` authors each branch's pending-doc *inside its worktree*, and those aren't copied to main until Step 3b — which runs **after** the gate. So on the primary flow the gate read an empty directory and returned `NO_SMOKE_REQUIRED`, defeating itself; any `manual_smoke:true` task built in a worktree would merge without the human being asked. The filed fix (hoist collection into a new "Step 3a" before the gate) was **rejected** after analysis: collecting early breaks the load-bearing invariant "everything in main's `.pending-docs/` belongs to a just-merged branch" that Steps 4c/6 depend on, letting a Step-3b-SKIP'd branch's doc get consolidated and its task marked `done` with code never merged. Wade chose the safer option: the gate now maps this run's approved branches to their worktree dirs (`git worktree list --porcelain`) and scans each worktree's `.pending-docs/` **in place** alongside main's, deduped by basename — collection stays in Step 3b at merge time, invariant intact. The issue's secondary "scan `index.yml` for `manual_smoke:true` directly" suggestion was also declined (over-flags unrelated open tasks — the issue's own FEAT-0044). New `tests/test_review_close_smoke_gate.py` (4 tests) extracts + runs the detection heredoc against synthetic worktree fixtures.

**Adversarial review (self-imposed, pre-merge — green tests confirm, they don't break).** Two independent fresh-context reviewers (not forks) attacked the review-close changes along distinct lenses (smoke-gate correctness; interpreter + bash 3.2 robustness). The bash mechanics (awk offsets, `+=`, `$'\n'`, nested heredocs, worktree-path space-safety) were confirmed clean by execution, but five real defects the green suite was hiding were found and fixed on-branch: **(1)** the `$PY_BIN` permission-match regression + missing template rule (→ literal-`python3` + `PATH` prefix, above); **(2)** the smoke gate would **silently regress to the ISSUE-0050 bug** if the agent left the `APPROVED_BRANCHES` placeholder unsubstituted (empty worktree set → scan only main → false `NO_SMOKE_REQUIRED`) → added a hard guard (unsubstituted placeholder exits 3; empty allowed only when set deliberately for a main-only close); **(3)** dedup was **main-first**, so a stale main copy could shadow a fresher worktree doc carrying a newly-added smoke heading (re-run-after-halt path) → flipped to worktree-first, now test-guarded; **(4, pre-existing)** Step 3b copies a branch's pending-docs *before* the unforced worktree remove, so a remove-refusal SKIP stranded the doc for a later Step 4c to consolidate — the same "done-though-unmerged" hazard the 0050 fix avoided introducing in 3c, living natively in 3b → added a rollback of the copied docs on the SKIP path; **(5)** the smoke-gate heredoc had zero CI coverage → the new test file closes it. The repeat lesson: the count-only/prose-only paths a green suite never exercises are exactly where the adversary looking to *break* it finds the crack.

**Discovered + filed, not fixed here.** The ISSUE-0049 class is not confined to `/review-close`: `claim-task/SKILL.md:57,162` and `document-work/SKILL.md:210` carry the same bare-`python3`-imports-yaml shape and want the same one-line `PATH`-prefix sweep (filed Medium — out of these three issues' scope, each site wants its own smoke-check). The two Medium TECH-0007 items (0047, 0046) also remain filed.

**Gate.** 802 tests green (791 prior + 7 hermeticity + 4 smoke-gate; no regression). Both new guards red-green verified; the 0048 reproduction and the Step 3c gate exercised end-to-end against real/synthetic worktrees. Landed via branch → PR #124 → squash-merge to protected `main`. Sysop-side only — BeanRider carries local workarounds until it next runs `--update`.

## Phase 125 (executed 2026-07-17 — the TECH-0007 tail: the three BeanRider SYSOP_ISSUES items Phase 124 filed rather than fixed — ISSUE-0047 installer force-degradation, ISSUE-0046 pip-audit dead stage, ISSUE-0049 sweep)

**Trigger.** Phase 124 landed the three *High* TECH-0007 defects and explicitly left three filed: the two *Medium* installer/checks defects (0047, 0046) and the discovered sibling class — the ISSUE-0049 venv-only-`import yaml` shape recurring outside `/review-close`. This phase clears all three; each was confirmed sysop-side with line numbers when filed. Bundled as one PR (shared "BR-migration-surfaced, sysop-side, no external gate" shape).

**ISSUE-0047 — `--update` silently degraded to `--force` on a no-anchor lock, overwriting hardened consumer scripts.** A lock whose `sysop_commit` is empty/`"unknown"` cannot anchor Phase-24b 3-way divergence detection: `reconstruct_old_install()` returns 1 (its no-anchor branch), and the Phase-99 clean-tree fallback treated that identically to a *legitimately-unreachable* ancestor — proceeding to overwrite in-scope `scripts/*` + `scripts/hooks/*` with exit 0 and only a blank `was:` field as signal. The asymmetry was self-evident in the same file: the read-only `--check` path **hard-errors** on exactly this, while the *destructive* `--update` fell open — backwards, and it bit BeanRider's migration (three hardened scripts, incl. the mandatory `bean-check` gate, overwritten). **Fix — the load-guard, not the exit-code refactor.** The issue offered two shapes (reserve exit `2` from `reconstruct_old_install` and route it to a fail-closed caller branch, or — the "minimally" clause — validate the anchor at `--update`'s lock load). Chose the load-guard: right after `old_commit="$(lock_field sysop_commit)"`, `err` + `exit 1` with two-option remediation. It is strictly stronger and simpler than threading a new exit code through a single-caller function — it stops before any temp-worktree work and makes the no-anchor case unreachable at the fallback. **The adversarial review (below) reshaped it twice:** **(1) git-source gate.** The guard now fires only when `get_sysop_commit != "unknown"` (a *git* source, where a real anchor was possible → an empty/`"unknown"` lock anchor is corruption). A **non-git source** (unpacked tarball/zip — a first-class "any agent or none" path) can *only* ever yield `"unknown"`, so a `"unknown"` lock anchor there is **normal, not corruption**; failing closed would break the documented tarball update flow AND advertise a `--adopt` recovery that provably can't help. That population stays on the existing Phase-99 fallback (proceed-if-clean, abort-if-dirty), unchanged. **(2) `cmd_adopt` re-adopt.** The headline remediation (`--adopt`) was a *circular dead-end* — `cmd_adopt` refused when a lock already exists ("use `--update`"), and the no-anchor case always has a lock, so `--update`↔`--adopt` looped the user. Taught `cmd_adopt` to **re-adopt in place** when the existing lock's anchor is empty/`"unknown"` (rebuild the anchor, recover the recorded packs so there's no re-prompt) — adopt's job is to (re)establish tracking, and a no-anchor lock has none. A valid-anchor lock still routes to `--update`. `--force` remains the deliberate preservation opt-out (exempt), and the summary now prints `was: (unknown — lock had no anchor)` instead of a blank. New `tests/test_install_no_anchor.py` (6 items) drives the real installer: git-source no-anchor `--update` fails closed on a **clean tree** (the non-tautological contrast with Phase-99's clean-tree-proceeds), parametrized over `""`/`"unknown"`; `--force` proceeds + labels the summary (both anchors); a **non-git source** with a `"unknown"` anchor does NOT fire the guard (proceeds via Phase-99); and `--adopt` **rebuilds** a no-anchor lock with a real 40-hex anchor + preserved packs, after which `--update` proceeds.

**ISSUE-0046 — the pip-audit A06 stage silently reported zero findings on every editable consumer.** `pip_audit.py:47` ran `pip-audit --strict --format json`; pip-audit treats `--strict` as fatal on *any* skipped dependency, and an editable install (`pip install -e .`, the documented Python-pack shape) always leaves one unresolvable local package — so the audit aborted **before emitting JSON**, and `if not r.stdout: return out` returned an empty (== "all clear") list, indistinguishable from a genuinely-clean run. A security scan that reports nothing looked exactly like one that found nothing, for months. **Fix:** drop `--strict`, add `--skip-editable` (`--strict --skip-editable` is *also* broken — a skip is still a skip that `--strict` fails on — so `--strict` had to go entirely, a claim the review confirmed against a real pip-audit flag matrix); rewrite the docstring rationale; and close the silent path — on a non-zero exit with empty stdout, `warn: pip-audit exited N with no output — dependency audit did NOT run: <stderr tail>` so a broken invocation announces itself. The warn branch is reachable *only* on a genuine no-output abort: pip-audit exits non-zero when it *finds* vulns too, but then stdout carries the JSON, so `if not r.stdout` is False and that run parses normally. +3 mutation-verified tests (invocation uses `--skip-editable` not `--strict`; non-zero+empty warns; exit-0+empty stays silent — guard-the-guard).

**ISSUE-0049 sweep — the venv-only-`import yaml` class, three siblings outside `/review-close`.** Phase 124 fixed `/review-close` Step 3c/4c; the issue named it a *class*. `claim-task/SKILL.md` Step 2 (index.yml lookup) + Step 4a (status flip) and `document-work/SKILL.md` Step 3b (pending-doc validator) carry the identical bare-`python3`-imports-yaml shape and `ModuleNotFoundError` on a venv-only consumer. Each got the Phase-124 idiom **verbatim** (byte-identical, by design — consistency with the shipped, adversarially-reviewed form): a `[ -x .venv/bin/python3 ] && PATH=".venv/bin:$PATH"` prefix immediately before the heredoc, keeping the command word a **literal `python3`** so the shipped `Bash(python3 -:*)` allow-rule still matches. Smoke-verified: the prefix resolves `python3` to `.venv/bin/python3` and the heredoc body runs under it.

**Adversarial review (self-imposed, pre-merge — two independent fresh-context reviewers, not forks; green tests confirm, they don't break).** Reviewer A (install.sh / ISSUE-0047) drove the real installer through every path and confirmed the core guard + test sound and non-tautological, but found two real defects the green suite hid — a **HIGH** (the `--adopt` remediation dead-ended in a circular `--update`↔`--adopt` loop; adopt refuses an existing lock) and a **MEDIUM** (non-git/tarball installs, where `"unknown"` is legitimate, were wrongly failed-closed with no working recovery). Both fixed on-branch: the git-source gate + the `cmd_adopt` re-adopt path, each with a new regression test (the two additions that took the file 3→6 tests). Reviewer B (pip_audit / heredocs) **fully verified pip_audit.py sound** against a real pip-audit (editable-consumer flag matrix + a known-vulnerable run + 3-way mutation testing — "ship it"), verified the heredoc PATH-persistence + arg-passing, and surfaced two **pre-existing** items *filed, not fixed here*: (Concern 4) the `[ … ] && PATH=` prefix splits into three permission-subcommands and two match no allow-rule — but the form is **byte-identical to the shipped Phase-124 sites**, so the sweep introduces **no new divergence**; it's a cross-cutting Phase-124-level question wanting one empirically-grounded pass across all 5 sites (also flags the competing `VAR=value python3` form at `review-close:387`); and (Concern 6) `auto-build/SKILL.md:68,346` use a hardcoded `.venv/bin/python3` that breaks on *non-venv* consumers and whose declared `Bash(python3 -:*)` rule can't match its command word. Both filed Medium. The repeat lesson holds: the config-dependent / prose-only paths a green suite never exercises are exactly where an adversary finds the crack — here, the recovery UX the tests asserted was *printed* but never that following it *works*.

**Gate.** 811 tests green (802 prior + 6 no-anchor + 3 pip-audit; no regression). All three fixes behaviorally verified (0047 end-to-end against scratch git *and* non-git consumers + the re-adopt recovery; 0046 via mocked-subprocess + the reviewer's real-pip-audit matrix; 0049 via a PATH-prefix resolution smoke). Landed via branch → PR → squash-merge to protected `main`. Sysop-side only — BeanRider carries local workarounds until it next runs `--update`.

## Phase 126 (executed 2026-07-17 — Tier C python-heredoc permission convergence: resolves the two pre-existing siblings the Phase 125 review filed — Concern 4 + Concern 6)

**Trigger.** Phase 125's adversarial review filed two Medium items it declined to fix in-scope: **Concern 4** — the venv-aware heredoc idiom Phases 124/125 shipped (`[ -x .venv/bin/python3 ] && PATH=".venv/bin:$PATH"` immediately before a `python3 - <<` heredoc) splits into three permission-*subcommands*, two of which (`[`/`test` and the bare `PATH=` assignment) match no allow-rule and aren't in the documented read-only set — a potential silent halt under `auto + skipAutoPermissionPrompt`; and it flagged a competing `VAR=value python3 - <<` form at `review-close:387` resting on the same unverified assumption. **Concern 6** — `auto-build/SKILL.md:68,346` used a hardcoded `.venv/bin/python3 - <<`, the *inverse* bug: matches no rule **and** breaks non-venv consumers. Both wanted "one empirically-grounded pass" keyed on a Claude-Code permission-matcher fact the Phase-125 session couldn't verify. This phase runs that pass.

**The empirical probe inverted the item's own candidate.** A `claude-code-guide` agent read the official permissions doc and settled the load-bearing facts: (1) env-var **assignment prefixes are NOT stripped** by the matcher — so `VAR=… python3 -` and `PATH="…" python3 -` do **not** match `Bash(python3 -:*)`. This *kills Concern 4's own proposed candidate* (the `PATH="…" python3` single-command form) and confirms `review-close:387` was **broken**, not merely unverified. (2) Compound commands split on `&&`/`||`/`;`/`|`/newlines, each subcommand matched independently; `[`/`test` is **not** in the documented read-only set — so the shipped `[ … ] && PATH=` idiom's safety was genuinely uncited, exactly as Concern 4 worried. (3) `.venv/bin/python3 -` matches no rule either. Net: the *only* inference-free idiom is a single plain `python3 - <<` command — literal command word first, no prefix, no sibling subcommand.

**Tier C (Wade-selected from three options: keep-the-idiom-on-inference / one-benign-inference / zero-inference).** Converged **all 7** inline heredocs (claim-task ×2, document-work ×1, review-close ×2, auto-build ×2) onto: command word literally `python3` (matches `Bash(python3 -:*)` as a single simple command — **zero new settings.json rules**); shell values passed as **positional args**, never env prefixes (document-work's `PENDING=` and review-close's `REPO_ROOT=` shell computations folded into Python via `git branch --show-current` / `Path.cwd()`, so every block is genuinely one command); and PyYAML resolved for venv-only consumers by an in-heredoc `try: import yaml / except ImportError: sys.path[:0] = glob.glob(".venv/lib/python*/site-packages"); import yaml` bootstrap. Verified behavior-identical to the old idiom across all four consumer shapes (system-yaml / venv-at-cwd / venv-not-at-cwd / no-yaml) — no regression. This also makes auto-build's *already-declared* `Bash(python3 -:*)` rule accurate (it had been declaring it while invoking `.venv/bin/python3`). The Phase-124/125 PATH-prefix idiom — the right call under the then-unverified assumption — is now retired everywhere in favor of the verified inference-free form.

**Adversarial review (self-imposed, pre-merge — three independent fresh-context reviewers, not forks; distinct lenses: permission-correctness, Python-behavior, completeness/docs).** The permission claim **held** (reviewer 1: every converged heredoc auto-approves via the single rule, inference removed not relocated) and the Python was **behavior-identical** across consumer shapes (reviewer 2, empirically, against a system python3 that happens to lack yaml). One **CONFIRMED moderate regression** surfaced and was fixed on-branch: I had changed review-close's Step 4c validator line — which *rode on the removed conditional PATH prefix* — to a hardcoded `.venv/bin/python3 scripts/validate_tasks.py`, dropping the non-venv fallback; a no-venv consumer would abort *after* the status-flip + `git mv` already ran, with a false "validator rejected the index" message (a half-applied close). The reviewer's suggested `PY=…; [ -x ] || PY=python3; "$PY" …` conditional was **rejected** — a variable command word (`$PY`) binds to no static rule, reintroducing the exact `$PY_BIN` inference this phase eliminates. Fixed instead by giving `validate_tasks.py` its **own** `sys.path` PyYAML bootstrap and reverting the line to bare `python3 scripts/validate_tasks.py` — permission-clean (matches `Bash(python3 scripts/validate_tasks.py:*)`) and serving **both** consumer shapes; verified end-to-end (system python3 without yaml resolves it from `.venv`, honestly fails with no venv). Two non-blocking notes, both handled: review-close Step 3c's repo-root now derives from `Path.cwd()` rather than `git rev-parse --show-toplevel` — kept **deliberately** (coherent with the venv-glob's identical CWD-is-root assumption; a subdir run was already unsupported; worktree-robust git-common-dir resolution stays the parked Phase-32.x item), with the assumption noted inline; and a **pre-existing** auto-build step-label nit (the heredoc is under Step 1, not "Step 2's batch-sizing math") was corrected in the skill and its `WORKFLOW.md` mirror.

**Out of scope, verified not a bug.** `claim_task.sh:187` is the same bare-`python3`-imports-yaml shape but a **permission-exempt** bash-script heredoc (runs under `bash scripts/claim_task.sh`), and it **fails safe** — the `--release` path pre-guards at `claim_task.sh:135-146` (`command -v python3 && python3 -c "import yaml"`) and exits 1 with actionable manual-reversal guidance, mutating nothing, *before* reaching line 187. No follow-up filed. It is the only python heredoc under `core/companion/scripts/`.

**Gate.** 908 tests green (811 prior + 97 from the new `tests/test_heredoc_permission_idiom.py` drift guard; the smoke-gate test was updated in place for the env→positional-arg change). The drift guard was **mutation-verified non-vacuous** (6 forbidden-idiom mutations each detected by its predicates) and asserts: no `.venv/bin/python3 -`/assignment-prefix/`[ -x ]`/compound-before-opener heredoc form, every yaml-importing heredoc carries the bootstrap, all 7 bodies compile, `validate_tasks.py` keeps its bootstrap (the Finding-1 guard), and the load-bearing `Bash(python3 -:*)` rule ships. Landed via branch → PR → squash-merge to protected `main`. Sysop-side only.

## Phase 127 (executed 2026-07-17 — gdp backport sweep: `/auto-build` K=6→K=12 sum ceiling + cross-module cap 1→2, adopted from gdp's settled loosen experiment)

**The sweep.** The recurring upstream practice — read gdp's workflow-layer changes since the last sweep (baseline `ffdd2811`, 2026-06-24) and port anything Sysop-relevant. Traced every gdp skill/script/doc change and found **six no-ops** and **one live candidate**. No-ops, recorded so the sweep isn't re-run: gdp's `run_grep` "no valid paths" hardening — Sysop's `grep.py` already carries the robust `valid_paths` form (Phase 5), cleaner than gdp's new counter and with an added rc≥2 warn (gdp caught up to Sysop); gdp's pyright warning-gate (parse `--outputjson` errorCount/warningCount instead of the exit code, which is 0 on warning-severity diagnostics) — the underlying insight is **already handled** in Sysop's `lsp.py`, which parses the JSON and maps warning-severity rules, and the ratchet script it lives in (`run_ratchet_lint.sh`/`pyright_gate.py`) is gdp-specific infra Sysop doesn't ship; gdp's `review-close` pyright-path prose — same gdp-specific machinery; gdp's +100-line `security-audit` convention-demotion apparatus — **reverse direction**, gdp importing Sysop's own Phase 62/67 demotion work (Sysop's lazy-create fire-ledger is the cleaner variant); gdp's `_shared/` rubric additions — gdp receiving the #309 jig-skills port; and the author-declared `touches:` field (a standing Sysop parked item) — **still not shipped** by gdp, which uses post-hoc `touched_files` from `git diff`, so that item stays correctly parked.

**The one candidate — the loosen experiment settled.** gdp's `TECH-AUTO-CLAIM-LOOSEN-GATE-EXPERIMENT` reached a **permanent "keep" 2026-07-13**: K=12 sum ceiling + cross-module cap 2, validated over 23 K=12 cycles against a 61-cycle K=8 baseline — executed/cycle **+78%** (1.34 → 2.39), $/executed down ($6.40 → $5.14), **zero reopened/abandoned merges** in either bucket, and the conflict-rate rise (2.82% → 7.89%) statistically indistinguishable from baseline (Fisher two-sided p = 0.28). This fired the data gate **three** Sysop items were parked on: the throughput-ceiling Decisions entry's "two `--compare` buckets + ~10 reason-captured parks" trigger (gdp's `.auto-claim/parked/` now holds ~28 entries), the 2026-05-27 telemetry+K-ramp backport's "buckets resolve" gate, and the stale K=6→K=8 ramp entry. **Wade selected full-parity K=12 + cap 2** (over the conservative K=8-or-document-only alternatives) — the checklist's item-(i) action, tracking gdp's tuned endpoint.

**What shipped.** Sysop was at **K=6**, prose-only — the value lives in no script (`next_task.py`'s weight math and `sitrep_survey.py`'s `_AUTO_BUILD_MAX_BATCH=4` are the *N* count ceiling, not K). Raised K=6→K=12 + cross-module cap 1→2 across **every shipped site describing the current gate**: `auto-build/SKILL.md` — a provenance blockquote carrying gdp's data + the revert trigger, rules 1c/2/3, the Step 4 batch-table denominator, the re-run error string, with **Examples A/B/D/F/G regenerated** for K=12 math (C/E are K-independent solos; H already used the symbol `K`); plus `roadmap/SKILL.md`, `WORKFLOW.md` (×3), `WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md`, `sitrep_survey.py`, the public monograph `docs/workflow.html`, and the two internal `tools/` specs that describe current behavior. **Key structural consequence:** at K=12 the heavy-solo invariant `c.` (weight > K) goes **dormant for all non-architectural tasks** — max non-architectural weight is High×cross-module = 10.0 ≤ 12, so `c.` is only reachable by a High-effort architectural task (weight 16), which already solos via `a.`; it's retained for correctness/headroom and re-arms if K is ever reverted. History was left intact (the Phase 42a log row, the dated `*_HANDOFF.md` docs, PHASE_LOG/REVIEW_ARCHIVE all keep their original K=6). **No telemetry stack ported** — Sysop has no consumer running `/auto-build` at gdp's cadence, so the figures are gdp's and the values are adopted on that evidence; the telemetry-stack leg of the 2026-05-27 backport item stays deferred.

**Adversarial review (self-imposed, pre-merge — two independent fresh-context reviewers, not forks; lenses: example-arithmetic recomputation, and rule-consistency + cross-file sweep completeness).** All **eight** worked examples were independently recomputed from first principles and **confirmed correct**; the rules block, the 1c dormancy claim, and the revert trigger were confirmed internally consistent, and the cross-file sweep confirmed no shipped current-behavior site was left at K=6. Both reviewers converged on the same real miss the `K=6` grep couldn't see — the Step 4 batch-table template printed the ceiling as `Total: <sum> / 6.0` (live tool output, → `12.0`) — plus a non-behavioral precision nit (rule 1c's "(weight ≥ 16)" characterized *all* architectural tasks, but architectural weights are {Low 4.0, Medium 8.0, High 16.0} — only High-effort reaches 16). Both fixed on-branch.

**Gate.** 908 tests green (no new tests — K is prose, not asserted in the suite; the change is worked-example arithmetic + doc prose, covered by the doc-currency guard, which stayed green). Landed via branch → PR → squash-merge to protected `main`. Sysop-side only; gdp is already at K=12, so the mirror is a no-op.

## Phase 128 (executed 2026-07-18 — the `sysop/` vendor-namespace migration: Sysop's consumer footprint moves out of shared namespaces into one labelled dir)

**The decision this executes.** Both round-3 cold readers named repo footprint as a bounce point — the installer wrote `WORKFLOW.md`/`WORKFLOW_GUIDE.md`/`SYSOP_ISSUES.md` at the consumer's root and `scripts/` *flat* ("every mature repo already has a `scripts/`"; "vendor files colonizing my repo root is a visceral no"). The decision session (Wade + Fable, effort explicitly excluded as a criterion) resolved to a **visible `sysop/` vendor namespace** ("option E") governed by one **ownership test**: *would the consumer keep this file if they removed Sysop?* No → under `sysop/`; yes → outside. Applied: `scripts/` → `sysop/scripts/`, `WORKFLOW*.md` → `sysop/docs/`, `SYSOP_ISSUES.md` → `sysop/`; **outside stay** `.claude/` (harness contract), `tasks/` (the consumer's backlog), and the `CLAUDE.md` / `.gitignore` appends. The teachable boundary collapses to one sentence: **"`sysop/` is Sysop's; everything else is yours."** Build-ready spec: `tools/SYSOP_NAMESPACE_SPEC.md` (v2, two-reviewer adversarial pass). One separable leg — consolidating the four gitignored runtime dirs under `sysop/runtime/` — was **deliberately cut** (Wade's call: keep the one-way-door diff focused on the user-facing win; the dirs are gitignored so the gain is small) and **filed** as a Low follow-up carrying the T7-worktree-guard precondition.

**Built in four layers.** *(1a)* every fresh-install dst in `install.sh` (scripts/docs/issues), `_phase_24b_in_scope` rekeyed to `sysop/scripts/*`, the full 27-rule + loop 14-rule settings templates and both hook `command` strings migrated in lockstep. *(1b) — the one behavior-changing part (§3.1, authorized exception):* the script self-location anchors. Five Python definers moved `parent.parent` → `parents[2]` (which resolves to the **same directory** at the new depth — preserving main-checkout / worktree / source-tree behavior); the model-role importers inherit it; `review_index.py`'s git-walk is depth-independent and needed **no** change. Five shell scripts' `${REPO_ROOT}/scripts` → `sysop/scripts` (git-resolved roots stay correct; only the sub-path moves). Functionally smoke-verified on a synthetic new-layout tree — every anchor resolves to root, all scripts run. *(1c)* source sweep: 117 skill refs + the `auto-build` `sys.path` anchor, companion docs, pack `checks.yml.fragment` comments (modernized off the Phase-49-stale `run_checks_impl.py` to the `run_checks/` package modules), `TESTER_ONBOARDING`. **Deliberate keeps** verified: `convention_map.md`/`security_map.md` `scripts/*.sh` globs stay `scripts/` (they target the *consumer's own* scripts, and maps are out of scope per spec §11); source `companion/scripts` refs protected by a fixed-width lookbehind throughout. *(4)* repo docs — README + `docs/{install-and-update,configuration,getting-started}` + the HTML monograph tree diagram (restructured under `sysop/`) + WORKFLOW.md port-checklist/managed-path rows; the "Backing out" hedge became its payoff line (removal is now `rm -rf sysop/` — nothing of yours mingled in to pick apart).

**The `--update` migration machinery (Layer 2, §5 algorithm + traps T1–T7) — the delicate core.** A delta on the existing update flow: divergence detection still runs on OLD paths, then **both** the working tree and the reconstructed shadow move to the new layout, then the standard pipeline runs layout-blind so `copy_file`'s Phase-24b preservation (keyed on the moved shadow ancestor) and the obsolete sweep operate on new paths with **zero special-casing**. Detection is **tree-probed, not lock-keyed** (T3 — `cmd_adopt` writes current-pipeline locks, so a lock-spelling trigger would silently miss real old-layout trees), which also makes a crashed migration re-entrant. The move list is derived from a **DRY_RUN precompute of the NEW managed set** (captures upstream add/drop) intersected with on-disk presence; the precompute's global-state mutation (KNOWN_DIRS/MANAGED_PATHS/DIVERGENCE_SHADOW) is saved/restored so the real pipeline isn't corrupted. The obsolete sweep normalizes each old-managed entry to its **new** spelling before the "still managed" test — so a *moved* path is never mistaken for a *dropped* one under either lock spelling (an early self-caught bug: a naive forward-map fallback would have deleted a live moved file), and a genuinely-dropped file is resolved to whichever spelling survives on disk. T2 migrates **both** `settings.json` and `settings.local.json` (3-tier old-rule source: shadow → `git show OLD:` → tertiary inverse-map). T7 refuses migration on extra worktrees / active `.locks/*.lock` claims / a foreign `sysop/` (fresh-install refuses a non-lock-tracked `sysop/`, no `--force`). T6 arms `sysop-update.sh` with a source-freshness guard so a stale pre-namespace source clone can't reinstall the flat layout and un-migrate the consumer. Dry-run shows the true plan (⚠preserved preview against old spellings, numstat table suppressed) without writing. **End-to-end validated** by installing with the pre-namespace installer, then migrating: 40 paths moved, a consumer-diverged `claim_task.sh` **preserved byte-identical** at its new path, 0 wrongly swept, settings rewritten, idempotent re-update = normal no-op.

**Two Layer-1 completeness gaps the migration smoke caught** (the slash-anchored sweep missed non-slash forms): `install_companion_scripts`' bare `dst="$TARGET/scripts"` (no trailing slash — so a *fresh* install had been writing the main scripts to `scripts/`, not `sysop/scripts/`; the earlier hand-built Layer-1 smoke had copied them manually and so didn't catch it), and user-facing message/usage-comment `scripts/` strings inside the shell scripts (e.g. `install_hooks.sh`'s "No hooks found in scripts/hooks/"). Both fixed and re-verified.

**Tests (Layer 3).** New `tests/test_install_namespace_migration.py` (17 tests): a synthetic old-layout fixture builder — old tree + a **JSON** version-1 lock with old-spelled `managed_paths` and an unreachable anchor — exercising the degraded/clean-tree migration path (detection, move, settings-tertiary, sweep, T7 ×3, T6, dry-run, idempotency, SYSOP_ISSUES move + lazy-absent no-op, loop-mode subset, §3.1 anchor smokes), plus a T1 preservation test that locates a real pre-namespace `install.sh` commit in history and drives the true two-step upgrade. Updated **22 install-path drift guards** to the new layout + 3 downstream tests (settings.local, the update-fallback path, the shim T6 stub marker).

**Adversarial review (self-imposed, pre-merge — three independent fresh-context reviewers, not forks; the spec put "the strongest reviewer on the `--update` diff"). It earned its keep — the review found a HIGH data-loss bug the suite could not, because every fixture used the one lock spelling that is safe.** Reviewer 2 (anchors + source-sweep completeness) came back **CLEAN** — verified by building main-checkout *and* git-worktree fixtures and running the §3.1 smokes; two LOW cosmetic doc-staleness items (one comment miss fixed). Reviewer 1 (data-loss lens) found a **CONFIRMED HIGH**: `cmd_adopt` records the *current* (NEW-spelled) `managed_paths` even against an old-layout tree — the exact **adopt-bridge** route the spec routes GDP through — so the pre-update snapshot, the Phase-99 clean-tree check, T2's settings-removal, and committed-divergence detection all keyed on a lock spelling that didn't match the on-disk files. On that route, with an unreachable anchor, an *uncommitted* managed-script edit was silently, unrecoverably overwritten (the reviewer reproduced it; my fixtures all used OLD-spelled locks — the one safe spelling — so the suite shipped green over it). Fixed at all four spelling-blind sites (snapshot candidates now union the on-disk `NS_MOVE_OLD`; settings-removal always unions the inverse-mapped template; divergence detection normalizes to on-disk spelling), each verified by reproducing the exact scenario (the edit now survives in the snapshot commit / the dead flat rules are removed), the HIGH regression test **mutation-verified** non-vacuous, and two adopt-bridge regression tests added. Reviewer 3 (guard-rail lens) confirmed T6/T7/dry-run/idempotency/resume/malformed-JSON all correct, and found the **T4 stale-reference report** structurally broken two ways — a leading `ls` of an absent `settings.local.json` aborted the scan's `set -e` subshell before it reached `.git/hooks`/`.github/workflows` (the common case), and `\bscripts/` is unsupported by `git grep -E` (dead tracked-file scan) *and* boundary-matches `sysop/scripts/` (flooded the report with the file it just migrated). Both fixed with one POSIX-ERE boundary `(^|[^/[:alnum:]_])scripts/` that both engines honor, plus an `if`-guarded producer; the spec-§8-required T4 test (never written — the reason these shipped green) added, plus fixes for a doubled plan-summary (unsaved `PLAN_SUMMARY` across the precompute), a too-global hook-command re-path, an unrealistic fixture, and a defensive sweep guard so no lock can ever `git rm` the consumer's `tasks/` backlog.

**Gate.** 928 tests green (908 prior − 22 drift guards updated in place + 20 new migration tests). Lands via branch → PR → squash-merge to protected `main`. Sysop-side, dev-repo only — the tester and public mirrors, and the live-consumer (GDP, BeanRider) migrations, are the deliberate downstream sequence recorded in the checklist decision + spec §7 (GDP first via the adopt-bridge, since it has no lock).

**Post-open review round (2026-07-18, on PR #134 pre-merge — a second, independent multi-agent pass over the full branch diff after the phase's own 3-reviewer review).** Four finder agents produced 29 candidates; independent verifiers confirmed 21 and refuted 0; merged to 16 distinct findings.
